in the mirror of your eyes

by beethernuts

Summary

“Oh, and one more thing.” Her tone shifts almost instantly. “I loved Dawn, but let's be real—you were a terrible crier.”

Agatha’s mouth falls open.

“Like, really terrible. Your tears weren’t even and your sobs sounded awful. I didn't know if you were acting or having a stroke. It was honestly painful to watch.”

This little shit.

“I’ve always wondered how you won that Emmy.. Was it a pity prize?” She blinks at Agatha with feigned innocence as if she did not just verbally eviscerated the older woman before her.

“Anyway,” She continues breezily without missing a beat, “I’m Rae.”

Agatha snaps and grabs the opportunity by clearing her throat, desperate to redeem herself. “Right. Rae.” She lets the name roll on her tongue. “Is it short for.. 'Rae-who-should-really-watch-her-mouth-around-adults,' that Rae?”

“No.” Rae smirks. “It’s short for.. 'Rae-the-daughter-you-gave-up-for-adoption-sixteen years-ago,' that Rae.”

OR

Agatha’s world turns upside down when a young girl named Rae claims to be the daughter she abandoned—all unbeknownst to Rio, Rae’s adoptive mother.

Chapter 1: Chapter 1

Chapter Notes

fic title is from abba's my love, my life 𑣲

RAE’S 16TH BIRTHDAY WISHLIST

Dearest, mami

As you consider my wishes, please keep in mind that I am consistent with having good grades at school. I am also a decent human being who is courteous, polite, and respectful.

All that thanks to you.

You have managed to singlehandedly raise me with good values. You molded me to become the woman that I am today (Yes, Mami.. woman, although we both know I am and will always be your baby no matter how old I get.)

With that said, also remember that I am the sweetest, kindest, cutest, and most loving angel in your life.

  1. New phone — A phone is a necessity in this time of day, and mine is an artifact. It's cracked all over the screen, laggy, and probably created during the time of Adam and Eve. It is outdated and it barely charges to 100%. I believe I have been patient for so long that I earned to have an upgrade now.
  2. A tattoo (The art can be negotiable, you're allowed to express your input or veto anything) — I know you said that I must wait until my frontal lobe develops, but I strongly believe that I have already entered the right age and mental capacity for a permanent ink anywhere in my body. Fuck the frontal lobe. Sorry. But really, I feel like I don’t need to wait any longer until it actually develops. I promise there will be no laser-removal requests anytime soon if you let me get one tattoo. Or two tattoos.
  3. Public social media accounts — All content will be kid friendly, wholesome, and Mami-approved. I'm more than equipped and ready to have followers on my accounts other than you, Aunt Wanda, the twins, and my best friends.
  4. Acting school or acting gig — You say that you'll never get tired of supporting my dreams and endeavors. This is one of them! You know I have always been passionate about acting and maybe, it's time to go beyond school plays. I left pamphlets in your left bedside drawer, you are free to browse them at your convenience.
  5. Other mother ??? The woman who gave birth to me — Mami, I love you with all my heart can give and more. You are the most important person in my life, and I wouldn’t change that for the world but sometimes.. sometimes I wonder.

And I want to stop wondering. I want to quiet those voices at the back of my mind once and for all.

When I was younger, I recall you telling me that I can ask anytime. I wasn’t ready then and frankly, I had no intentions of ever exploring or knowing that part of me.

But, something has shifted. I think.. I do now. Or I am now.

I am ready now.

I want to know who she is :)

 

Love, Rae

Chapter 2: Chapter 2

Chapter Notes

whaaat, you guys!!! thank you so much for taking the time to read this fic :)

mistakes are mine.. or whatever they say xx

See the end of the chapter for more notes

If you tell 25 year old Agatha Harkness that one day, she will be back at the hell hole she spent her entire youth running away from, she’d laugh straight in your face and probably call you an idiot for even suggesting that idea.

The loathing she has for Westview, New Jersey can be traced back to the evil doings of her cunt mother. Thanks to that woman’s endless litany of sins, Agatha would gladly participate in a modern day lobotomy if it means erasing all the trauma that has been endured over the years under her mother’s neglect.

She’d burn her Emmy statuette or send an audition tape rather than willingly set foot in the place she was born and raised in (Agatha has reached a point in her career where she never auditions. Roles are either handed to her or made for her.)

After losing a bet she barely remembers agreeing to, Agatha is forcibly hauled back to the hellhole she swore she’d never return to sixteen years later, courtesy of her mentor, Lilia Calderu. And as if that isn’t punishment enough, Agatha has to help run Lilia’s workshop, teaching their craft to a bunch of hormonal teenagers or spreading the word and art of the Lord, as Lilia insists on calling it.

Lilia retired from the industry years prior. She now prides herself by sliding into a role of an acting coach. She travels across the country to share her expertise, educate aspiring young performers, and scout talents for the next generation.

The fates must have realized that it has been too good to Agatha for a long while that it has promptly decided to make her life a little bit miserable to balance it out. Lilia’s next stop just happens to be in Westview, New Jersey.

Sure, Agatha can always refuse and back out from the bet. She knows she could do that without jeopardizing her relationship with Lilia yet her ego tells her otherwise. Afterall, she is not but a woman of principles.. even when following them means walking straight back to the place she swore she’d never return to.

“We’re going out for dinner at 6:30.” Lilia barges inside the room she’s staying in for the next couple of weeks, carrying bath towels and neatly placing them at the edge of Agatha’s bed. “Tell me if you need anything and I will have Kate or the staff handle it for you.”

Agatha bats her eyelashes, “Can they book me the earliest flight back to Los Angeles?”

“That’s funny, Harkness.” Lilia deadpans. “You’re not leaving until the workshop concludes, and you know it.”

“Damn right I do.” She whispers, more to herself. “Though I would like to stay in rather than go out tonight. It’s chilly outside and you know just how awful my skin reacts to such horrendous temperature!”

Lilia looks at her suspiciously as Agatha pulls up the sleeve of her sweater, showing her bare arms.

“I was there when you were filming a scene that gave you an Oscar nomination in Alaska. You were wearing a tube top. I’m pretty sure you’ll do just fine to survive Westview weather.”

“Well, Alaska is different.”

“Exactly. Westview is more similar to Los Angeles therefore you won’t be needing much adjusting, might I remind you.”

Agatha rolls her eyes with that response. She’s afraid there’s no winning with this one, but that doesn’t mean she can’t try. “I’ll survive eating Kraft mac & cheese. You can literally just leave me here to rot.”

“Bold of you to assume I’ll allow you to do that.” Lilia smiles, waving a dismissing hand. “Again, 6:30. Reservations are tough. We can’t miss it by being late.”

Agatha has never liked being told what to do. In truth, she never had the chance to develop a sense of what she wanted. Growing up, choices weren’t things she was allowed to make—they were things handed to her, already decided, already final. Her mother spoke, and Agatha followed. That was the rhythm of her childhood, obedience disguised as normalcy.

Her favorite color is purple, yet she could never wear it or own anything in that shade because her mother disliked it. She was pulled out of school at least twice a month to accompany her mother on out-of-town trips to visit friends—Agatha left waiting in the car with nothing but a bag of nuts. And when she begged to pursue law school, her mother refused without a second thought.

That’s just what it was for Agatha.

The moment she gained the liberty to speak for herself, Agatha made a vow: no one would ever dictate her life again. Anyone who tried would quickly learn just how difficult she could be when pushed.

Lilia is an exception to that rule. With her, Agatha’s defenses soften. She finds herself agreeing without hesitation, following requests without the usual bite or prickly resistance. It’s effortless in a way that should feel unsettling, but doesn’t.

Maybe it’s because Agatha’s entire career spiraled into motion after she appeared as a background extra in one of Lilia’s films all those years ago. Maybe because they have stayed close and kept in touch since then. Maybe because Lilia had no prejudices when Agatha was a nobody.

Or maybe it’s because Lilia offered Agatha kindness and gentleness she had never truly known.

Neither would ever dare say it aloud, but the truth lingers between them all the same. Lilia has become the mother Agatha never had, and Agatha the daughter Lilia never expected.

Two lives intertwined not by blood or obligation, but by choice.

A few hours passed and Agatha still shows up at 6:30 despite resenting the idea of being out and about in Westview. She warns Lilia that she can’t promise to be on her best behavior tonight, especially once drinks are served.

The town bore little resemblance to what she once knew. Buildings had shifted, old businesses had vanished, and new ones had materialized. Even the pavement she used to follow home had been replaced and rebuilt.

Still, Westview’s wrapped around her exactly as she remembered. Cold, sharp, and unsettingly familiar. Almost too familiar.

Agatha, Lilia, and Kate—Lilia’s ever-naive assistant, found themselves being led into Rayo del Sol, a restaurant dressed in soft terracotta walls and sun-washed golden accents. Sun emblems hung here and there, glowing like tiny halos.

Their table was tucked as far from the main crowd as possible, a courtesy extended whenever known people like them needed to eat in peace. It wasn’t actually a thing for celebrities but Kate managed to argue and prove her point when she made the reservation a couple of months ago. Meaning, she cried and pleaded her way to give utmost satisfaction to her boss’ dining experience. Or in this case, bosses.

Agatha gives the place one slow look and snorts. “Subtlety is clearly not the owner’s strong suit.”

“You think?” Kate asks, occupying the chair adjacent to her. “Fun fact: this place is one of Westview’s pride and joys! Their Puerto Rican menu is supposedly Michelin-star quality.”

Agatha lifts a brow, unimpressed. “Key word, supposedly.”

“I like it.” Lilia adds. “It’s.. home-y.”

“You like a lot of things. Frankly, your standards aren’t high to begin with.”

“And it’s that supposed to be a bad thing?”

“It is when your entire plan is to create an army of future Academy awardees with speeches that require at least a mention of your name.” Agatha points an accusing finger at her mentor. “If you want to avoid social media discourse or flop cinema weekends, you must recognize and sort through actual talents. Sydney Sweeney wannabees are definitely not one of those.”

Before Lilia can take offense at Agatha’s remark, a young girl approaches their table holding a handful of menus. The initial thing Agatha noticed is that the said girl isn't in uniform, unlike the other servers who greeted them earlier.

She’s dressed casually in a beige turtleneck, red pants, and worn-in Doc Martens. Agatha gives her a slow once-over, curiosity flickering in her eyes.

She doesn’t usually bother paying attention to.. well, normal people. But something about this girl tugs at her, draws her focus in a way she can’t put a name to.

Odd.

“Good evening!” She greets, her blue eyes landing on Agatha a second too long. It’s as if she recognizes her, which isn’t unheard of considering Agatha’s status. “Here are your menus. Please don’t hesitate to take your time and browse them one by one.”

Lilia and Kate graciously take theirs. Agatha does not.

She is suspicious of the girl, and she doesn’t even know why.

“Do you work here?”

The girl quickly responds, “I do.”

“Really?" Agatha attempts to press more. “Because everyone else is in uniform, and you’re not.” She even makes the show of gesturing to a staff serving a nearby table to prove her point.

“Well.. I was called in last-minute. Didn’t have time to change.” The girl doesn’t flinch despite Agatha’s attempt of intimidation.

“And how old are you? Twelve?”

“I just turned sixteen, actually.”

Agatha clicks her tongue. She’s not even trying to hide the disdain in her face as she continues to speak, “Still unprofessional. This place is supposed to be—Kate, what was it?”

“Uh.. Michelin star?”

"Right. Michelin star.”

“I’m sorry if you find my being unprofessional, Ms. Harkness.” The girl doesn’t break her posture. “Would you prefer a different server then?”

“Darling, that won’t be necessary.” Lilia finally butts in, giving Agatha a warning glare. “You’re fin–”

“No, she’s not fine.” Agatha cuts her off. “She’s out of uniform and menus can be easily stolen. For all we know, she’s a deranged fan who bribed someone to sneak in so that she can interact freely with celebrities.”

Truth is, no one can blame Agatha for being cautious. Sure, she’s rude to this young girl and maybe all her assumptions are incorrect but she can never be too careful. Especially one of her status. She has her fair share of crazy experiences with so-called fans, and those always ends up with someone overstepping a boundary she didn’t give them permission to cross.

The girl lets out a tiny laugh. “Deranged fan.. huh. That’s new.”

“Agatha.” Lilia hisses. “Please don’t make a scene. She’s just a child.”

“She’s a teen.” Agatha shoots back. “And excuse me for caring about our safety. Stalkers come in all shapes and sizes, they don’t exactly show up labeled.”

The girl’s expression shifts. If Agatha wasn’t intently looking at her, she would have missed it. Just for a second—hurt flashed in the girls expressive eyes, like she’d been bracing for those exact words to come since the moment she showed up tonight.

Again, odd.

“It’s not my intention to.. possibly ruin what should be a lovely night for all of you.” The girl says, her voice gentle but steady. She pointedly avoids looking at Agatha this time, turning instead to Lilia and Kate with an apologetic smile. “If you’ll excuse me, I’ll go fetch another server for your table. Have a good night ahead.”

She leaves without so much as a final glance at Agatha.

Once she’s out of earshot, Lilia exhales sharply and immediately begins to lecture Agatha about manners, decency, and respecting people who are literally offering you service. She said that Agatha’s scrutiny was unwarranted and she could’ve seriously frightened that poor girl.

Agatha ignores all of it, flipping open the menu with feigned disinterest as her free hand lift automatically to her silver pendant, pressing it between her thumb and forefinger. It is an action done out of habit.. or possibly, comfort.

The interaction had been brief, even dismissive. And yet.. The more she remembers the image of that girls’ piercing ocean eyes, something twinges deep in her chest—a feeling she refuses to acknowledge.

Despite the earlier tension brought by Agatha’s outburst, the rest of the night unfolded calmly. Work schedules were sorted, conversation flowed, and the much to Agatha’s surprise, the food was exceptional.

Who needs that damn Michelin star anyway?

The bistec encebollado, in particular, nearly brought her to tears. It was so good she briefly wondered what kind of drugs or preservatives they might’ve slipped to make it taste divine. But when she asked a server, they claimed everything was organic and “farm fresh.” Agatha was too enamored with the dish to call their bluff.

“May I personally give compliments to the Chef?” Agatha asks, all in good spirit.

“We’d love to arrange that,” The server says, “But unfortunately, Chef Vidal had to leave early for the night. We’ll make sure to pass your compliments along.”

Vidal.

Agatha knows that name, although she can’t remember why.

Or how.

“Well, make sure to send them my kisses too.” Agatha declares, waving her hand in a theatrical arc. “That steak was spectacular, I can practically see myself eating it forever.”

In the next few minutes, Agatha indulges in a rarity as someone who enjoys the spotlight the same way she ravishes her privacy. She allows herself be swarmed by eager staff and guests alike, letting them take selfies and receive autographs, mostly written in napkins.

She’s absolutely convinced they slipped something mystical into her dish for her to be this welcoming and approachable to a group of people.

In reality, it’s just the wine talking. A couple of glasses would do that to a person.

When it was finally time to leave, Agatha slipped away to the restroom to freshen up. She needs a moment alone before stepping into whatever chaos waited beyond the restaurant doors. With the buzz she’d gotten, she was sure paparazzi would be waiting outside. Her presence is apparently the hottest topic Westview had seen in years.

She reapplies her lipstick, watching her silhouette with practiced precision. The restroom is quiet, blissfully so—until the click of footsteps breaks the silence.

Agatha doesn’t look up at first. But when she catches the newcomer’s reflection in the mirror, her hand stills.

It’s the young girl from earlier. The one who unsettled her for reasons she refuses to name. Or, can’t name.

Of course. Just her luck.

Their gazes collide in the mirror—blue against blue, both unwilling to be the first to look away. The girl hesitates at the threshold, breath hitching subtly before lunging herself forward, coming to stand at the sink beside Agatha.

Bold kid, Agatha thinks. She’ll give her that.

From the corner of her eye, Agatha secretly observes as the girl turns on the faucet, letting the cold water pool into her hands. She’s still wearing the same clothes as earlier. No uniform. No apron. No attempt to blend in with the other staff.

Figures.

Even with the staff’s confirmation that the young girl indeed works there, Agatha’s suspicion hasn’t eased. Why wasn’t this girl in uniform like the others? Is it some rule about minors working part-time? Or is there something else going on that no one’s admitting?

“Dawn.”

Agatha freezes mid-motion, lipstick hovering near her mouth. “Excuse me?”

The girl lifts her gaze, meeting Agatha’s eyes through the mirror once again. “Dawn. It was the first film I ever saw you in.” She pauses, then adds, “Well, the first out of three. Your body of work isn’ really.. for children.”

Agatha is rendered speechless. A rare, almost alarming state.

There’s that unsettling feeling in her chest again. She doesn’t like it.

Agatha doesn’t get unsettled, most especially not by a random sixteen year old who doesn’t follow basic institutional policies.

The girl continues, mistaking Agatha’s silence for permission.

“I remember thinking how brave your character was. Fighting crimes, injustices, standing alone in a world against her with no support whatsoever.” She smiles, but it’s crooked. Sad. “You were strong. The kind of strong little girls cling to. You were the personification of dawn that appears first after darkness, giving way to the sun before it sets.”

“Above all, I admired how you loved.” Her voice softens. “How you held on to the people you cared about and never.. never..”

Her voice cracks.

Agatha seizes the opening. “Would you like an autograph, dear?” She interrupts, tone dripping condescension. “You don’t have to monologue. You can just ask.”

The girl lets out a laugh humorless laugh, and then, “Why do you hate me?”

Agatha blinks, taken aback. “What?”

“Why do you hate me?”

“I—I don’t hate you.”

“Then why do you treat me like this?”

Agatha has no answer to that question. She can be awful, sure. But she’s never this awful to some kid she just met. The way she’s reacted to this girl all night.. it’s defensive. 

It’s almost like she's mustering up the courage to build walls and use it to surround herself as a barrier for an emotion she refuses to feel.

She wants to defend herself. ‘I’m not like that.’ ‘I’m never like this.’ ‘You’re making something out of nothing.’

But none of it comes out, because she knows it isn’t nothing.

They both do.

This girl has been unsettling her since the moment she appeared with those menus. Something familiar, almost wrong, and most importantly something important she’s resisting to understand.

“I.. I..” Agatha’s voice is barely audible as she attempts to find the right words to say.

“Rays of the Sun.” The girl murmurs instead, averting her gaze from Agatha as she speak. “Rayo del Sol means rays of the sun.”

She moves to grab a napkin and used it to dry her hands. Then, she smooths her shirt, gives Agatha a small, heartbreaking smile, and turns toward the door. That should be the end of it.

Unfortunately, it isn’t.

She stops and looks back. This time, her face seems a little brighter, carrying a sense of newly found confidence.

“Oh, and one more thing.” Her tone shifts almost instantly. “I loved Dawn, but let's be real—you were a terrible crier.”

Agatha’s mouth falls open.

“Like, really terrible. Your tears weren’t even and your sobs sounded awful. I didn't know if you were acting or having a stroke. It was honestly painful to watch.”

This little shit.

“And don’t get me started on your early commercials.” Rae adds, warming up. “The shampoo one? Your hair wasn’t even that shiny to begin with, who were you fooling back then?”

At this point, Agatha’s jaw is practically on the floor.

Rae just shrugs, deadpan. “Honestly, you didn’t improve until, like.. I don’t know, a decade and two later? Again, I don’t really follow your Hollywood journey. You never piqued my attention.”

“How dare you?” Agatha sputters in disbelief.

“I’ve always wondered how you won that Emmy.. Was it a pity prize?” She blinks at
Agatha with feigned innocence as if she did not just verbally eviscerated the older woman before her.

Agatha is so stunned she actually forgets how to speak. Her brain simply flatlines

Rae finally steps toward the door, hand on the handle. Her eyes are gleaming with mischief and.. something softer beneath it.

“Anyway..” She continues breezily without missing a beat, “I’m Rae.”

Agatha snaps and grabs the opportunity by clearing her throat, desperate to redeem herself. “Right. Rae.” She lets the name roll on her tongue. “Is it short for.. 'Rae-who-should-really-watch-her-mouth-around-adults,' that Rae?”

“No.” Rae smirks. “It’s short for.. 'Rae-the-daughter-you-gave-up-for-adoption-sixteen years-ago,' that Rae.”

She opens the door.

Agatha stops breathing.

Rae slips out.

The door shuts.

Agatha’s knees nearly buckle. Her fingers were the first to surrender as her lipstick clatters into the sink, falling freely from her grip.

Her brain becomes a singular, echoing word that continues to yell all across her lobes.

Rae is.. her WHAT?!

Chapter 3: Chapter 3

Chapter Notes

i had fun making this update lol hope you enjoy <3

Agatha was 24 when she had Rae—no. 

Agatha was 24 when she had a daughter.

Well, she was actually a day away from turning 25 when she gave birth to Rae—again, not Rae. 

She was a day away from turning 25 when she gave birth to her daughter.

Daughter.

Agatha had a daughter.

Agatha has a daughter.

The word daughter has always tasted foreign in her mouth. She never dared saying it aloud after convincing herself it was something she was not meant to claim, something she lost the right to the moment she fled Westview.

It is something that is not hers.

Leaving her mother, leaving the life she knew, letting go of the version of herself she was raised to be—that was easy.

Leaving a part of herself, her own child, wasn’t.

Agatha learned that sometimes, the right choice is the most difficult to make.

The pregnancy was an accident, but the love she felt wasn’t. She yearned to keep the child. She wanted to keep the child. But all that couldn’t erase the fact that she is unable to.

Two things can be true at once: she loved the child with everything she had, yet she knew she couldn’t give her the life she deserved.

Above all, she couldn’t risk her child’s safety—not with the threats her own mother hissed into her ears every chance she got.

So, if letting go meant giving her child a chance at a life far better than the one she could offer, even if that life didn’t include her, then so be it.

Agatha barely remembered leaving the restaurant. Kate had to physically guide her out of the comfort room, muttering her name in gentle whispers as an attempt of comfort. Her sudden shift of demeanor didn’t go unnoticed by Lilia, who carefully asked if she was alright. Agatha dismissed her concern with the effortless, practiced confidence she’d perfected over the years.

Once they arrived home, Agatha quietly slipped into her room, carrying the air of someone who desperately did not want to be disturbed. She didn’t bother turning on the lights or changing into more comfortable clothes. She simply sank onto her bed, back pressed against the headboard, her pendant curled tightly in her palm it might as well just leave a mark.

She remained steady and still as the hours crawled past her, replaying the encounter with Rae in a relentless loop. Her eyes are void of tears, which is a cruel contradiction considering she had just met her daughter—or someone claiming to be her daughter.

She let the hollow quiet of the night swallow her whole, drifting in and out of sleep, until the first rays of dawn made itself known through the uncovered windows.

After a few minutes of contemplation, Agatha finally forced herself out of bed. She stumbled toward her suitcase, grabbed a matching Lululemon set, and headed straight for the bathroom. She splashed cold water on her face, went through the quickest version of her hygiene routine, and tied her long hair into a tight ponytail.

If she couldn’t quiet her thoughts, she figured maybe she could at least outrun them.

For the time being.

The house was quiet when she left, and so were the streets of Westview. Life was still for now, most people deep in sleep. Agatha preferred it this way. At least then no one would recognize her or disturb the peace she was once again trying to rebuild.

She kept running with no exact destination in mind. Even with all the growing changes in Westview, Agatha still prided herself on knowing the place, where alleys to turn, which blocks to avoid.

She’d been running for so long, lost in thought, that she didn’t realize her feet had carried her back to Rayo del Sol. How she managed to find her way here again, she didn’t know. Maybe out of instinct. Maybe out of something she refuses to name.

She stood outside, taking in the vast exterior of the restaurant. Its golden accents caught the early light, as if the whole place was waking up gently with the sun.

If Rae works here.. if Rae has to work at such a young age, does that mean she isn’t living a good life? Does that mean she’s struggling financially?

Or.. Agatha forced the thought, maybe Rae just wants extra income like many kids her age.

Agatha jumps in surprise when the doors suddenly swung open, revealing a woman dressed in athletic clothes—almost similar to Agatha’s. She wore a simple green bralette and black shorts, her skin glowing faintly with sweat as if she’d just finished a workout.

The woman stopped dead in her tracks. Her brown eyes widened the moment it locked against Agatha’s blues, shock flickered across her features as if she had seen a ghost.

The said woman had straight dark brows, deep-set eyes, and a mouth that seemed to be one second away from a smirk. Her long hair is braided neatly to one side, though a few strands had slipped free, carried lightly by the passing breeze.

Agatha swallowed the lump in her throat. Fantastic. Of all people she could run into looking like a sleep-deprived mess—why does it have to be this woman? If the circumstances were any different, Agatha would’ve absolutely made a move to flirt.

Well, that is—if she ever confirmed this woman was into women. Or single. Preferably both.

“Uh..” The woman tried to speak, but only an incoherent sound escaped her mouth.

“I was just passing by.” Agatha waves a hand, pretending at a cool she absolutely did not possess right now. “I’m Agatha, by the way.”

“I know who you are.” The woman quickly replies without hesitation. Too fast, too certain. She then held Agatha’s gaze for a moment too long, lips parting, then closing again—like she wanted to speak but couldn’t shape the right words.

Odd.

Agatha figured she might as well put the poor woman out of her misery, and walk directly into her own mess while she was at it.

“Hey, do you..” Agatha's voice falters, unsure how to keep the conversation going without giving away too much—without sounding like a complete creep asking about Rae. “Do you perhaps.. work here?” Her fingers automatically reached for her pendant, searching for something to hold onto, something to do when her nerves spiked.

The woman nods. “Sort of.” She winces at her own answer, as if it wasn’t the one she meant to give. “I’m Rio. I actually own the place.”

Agatha stared for a beat—just long enough for the realization to settle over her.

Rio, the owner.

Rio, the chef.

Rio, the hands behind that incredible dish last night, the one so divine Agatha would’ve kissed her as thanks only if she had been there to receive it.

“Rio Vidal.” Agatha remembers names the same way she remembers lines and cues—perfectly. “Pleasure to meet you.” She steps forward and extends a friendly hand.

Rio hesitates for a moment, yet she finds herself accepting the gesture anyway. “The pleasure is mine.” Their hands brush a moment too long before Agatha pulls away, offering her a small smile.

“I was born and raised here, you know.” Agatha says. For a moment, she forgets why she’s here as she allows herself to slip into casual conversation. “I always heard the Vidal name growing up. Shame we were never in the same part of town.”

The Vidals were known for being a prominent family with businesses spanning from culinary ventures to banks and investments. Agatha instantly knows Rio is some kind of quiet big-shot, probably with a hefty trust fund tucked under her name.

“Well..” Rio replies shyly, as if her wealth is something she’d rather pretend doesn’t exist. “You made quite a buzz last night. Reservations came flooding in when people found out the great Agatha Harkness deemed my restaurant worthy of her presence.”

“Oh, please.” Agatha waves her off again, dramatically this time. “I heard reservations are already difficult to begin with. You didn’t need me to boost your name.”

“I didn’t know you were this humble.”

“Well, I can tell you more about me if you ask me out.” Agatha, of course, has no shame. She will flirt at dawn, at dusk, and in the middle of a mental breakdown. Consistency is key, as she likes to say.

Rio blinks, surprised and amused. “Yeah?” She challenges, finally finding her footing. “And how exactly would you know I swing on the same team?”

“I don’t. I just open my mouth and hope for the best.” Agatha shrugs lightly. “Besides, it’s never too late to embrace who you truly are, or whatever motivational nonsense people put on mugs.”

Rio chuckles out loud and Agatha has to physically restrain herself from collapsing upon seeing her gap tooth in full view. “Agatha Harkness..” Rio says with a shake of her head, “We just met and you already amaze me.”

“I’m certain I can amaze you even more if we were to meet again.” Agatha winks at her to prove a point. “I’ll be in Westview for a while. Now’s the perfect opportunity to ask me out.”

“And what if I had a partner?”

“You wouldn’t have humored me this long if you did.” 

Rio studies her like she’s actually weighing the offer. “Then why don’t you ask me out?” She challenges. “Since you’re so bold.”

“Oh, I’d personally skip the date and drag you straight to my bed.” Agatha replies without flinching. “You look like the type who’d insist on dinner first before letting me in your bed, and since my new year's resolution is to become modest, I believe now is the perfect start..”

Rio pokes her cheek with her tongue, arms folding. “And what makes you think I wouldn’t go for that?”

Agatha grins. “Because I knew you’d like the anticipation. The build-up. The tension.”

She knew she’d hit the jackpot when Rio turns silent for a short while, her expression darkens into something more promising.

“Private dinner tonight. Cabeza.” Rio decides. “Will you text me your address so I can pick you up?”

“My, what a gentleman. Chivalry isn’t dead after all!” Agatha gaps theatrically, hands to her forehead to elevate the show she has put on. “You may reach me through social media, you know where to find me.”

“Amongst a thousand other people?”

“My phone number is sacred. I don’t give it out easily.”

“You were just proposing a sleepover like.. Two minutes ago.”

Agatha adjusts the hem of her shirt and smiles meaningfully, “What can I say? I’m a woman of multitudes.”

Her eyes suddenly drifted to the Rayo del Sol sign, and the reason she’d come here in the first place slammed back into her. Rae. For a moment, she’d forgotten. And she silently thanked Rio for giving her that brief escape.

Rio watched her expectantly, as if waiting for Agatha to say something other than another flirtatious line, but she didn’t. Instead, Agatha offered a quick goodbye and told Rio to message her elsewhere.

She must’ve been imagining things, but.. she could’ve sworn Rio looked a little disappointed. Agatha wasn’t sure why.

During her run back home, Agatha decided she’d deal with Rae another time. Her main priority as of now is to confirm whether Rae was actually her child before deciding how to move forward. That part was tricky since no one had known about her pregnancy, but she was certain her bitch (affectionately) of an assistant, Jenny Kale, could help her figure it out.

She sent Jen a brief, urgent message the moment she arrived home. Then she took a long bath to officially start her day. By the time she stepped out, both Lilia and Kate were already awake and to her benefit, neither seemed eager to revisit her behavior from the night before.

They followed the day’s schedule as Lilia’s acting workshop kicked off. The drive to the studio took them to the busier part of town, where morning chaos was already in full swing.

Agatha sank into her seat beside Lilia for the dreaded screening process. Not everyone could join the workshop—Lilia insisted on watching each child perform first, with Agatha sitting in like some reluctant judge on a very low-budget talent show. Agatha thought the whole thing was tacky and painfully unnecessary.. though she begrudgingly acknowledged that it somehow worked.

Kid after kid performed. Some spent their entire stage time squealing at Agatha, which she considered deeply unprofessional. Lilia, of course, defended them by saying they were just starstruck. A handful were so young they couldn’t even pronounce half the words in their monologues. Others were visibly bored, clearly abducted by their overenthusiastic mothers for a chance at 'character building.'

It was from a user riovidal on Instagram.

riovidal: found you

riovidal: technically, it wasn’t much of a challenge

agathaharkness: I have zero tolerance for unpunctuality.

riovidal: noted, my lady :p

She puts her phone down at the sound of footsteps, the next hopeful being guided into the room. Her smile vanished as quickly as it had appeared the moment she recognized who it was.

Rae.

Gone were the sweater and Doc Martens.

This time, she wore a simple white dress, her long hair loose and tucked behind her ears. She looked almost angelic—if Agatha didn’t know better.

This was the same kid who verbally gutted her last night and dropped a life-altering revelation in the same breath. How could Agatha ever forget her?

Because she might be my daughter.

“Respect begets respect.” Rae fires back, glaring right back at her. “And for your information, my mami taught me everything I needed to know.”

A Mami. She has a mami—and the way she said it almost sounded defensive. Protective. It hits Agatha harder than it should but she brushes the feeling off immediately.

Good. At least Rae has a parental figure in her life. At least she’s not alone.

Wait. Why does that matter to Agatha?

“Don’t mind her, sweetheart.” Lilia says kindly. “Go ahead with your lines, and Agatha will now shut up and act like a respectable adult with basic decency—” She cuts Agatha a pointed glare, “—and respect.” Agatha can only grunt before sinking back into her seat, resigned to see what Rae has to offer.

“Whenever you’re ready.” Lilia encourages her. “Although, I think you might’ve left your script outside. You should grab it first.”

“It’s okay. I won’t be needing it.” Rae says confidently. “I memorized my lines while waiting for my turn.”

What a show-off.

Lilia snickers and leans sideways to whisper to Agatha, “That’s exactly what you said when you auditioned for my film back then.” She giggles. “This kid is just like you.”

And while Lilia means nothing by it, Agatha shifts uncomfortably in her seat.

Just like her.

She held her pendant tightly and remained quiet as Rae prepared to perform l

Rae steps into the middle, her white dress glowing under the bright studio lights. From where she stands, she looks almost untouchable as if the universe wrapped her in god-lighting just to spite Agatha.

She inhales, squares her shoulders, and begins.

At first, her voice is gentle. “Isn’t it splendid to think of all the things there are to find out about?”

Agatha shifts in her chair once more, arms crossed, blatantly unimpressed.. or trying to be.

Rae continues, her eyes not on Lilia, but drifting purposefully to Agatha.

“It just makes me feel glad to be alive—it's such an interesting world.”

She says it like she means it. Like she’s talking about something bigger than the line. Bigger than the workshop. Like she’s talking about the life she’s been living without Agatha.

Rae continued her monologue, slipping into more Anne of Green Gables lines with an ease that made Agatha’s jaw clench. The kid easily shifted from whimsy to earnestness to heartbreak as if she had an emotional switch built into her.

By the time Rae finished, Lilia was openly crying—tears streaming, hands clasped to her chest like she had just witnessed the birth of a prodigy.

Agatha knew instantly: She lost.

There was no fighting this.

Rae was getting into the workshop whether Agatha liked it or not. And worse.. she was, by far, the most promising kid they’d seen all morning.

Agatha swallowed the truth like a bitter pill.

As much as it pained her, as much as she wished the universe would cut her open instead, she had to give credit where it was due.

Rae was good. Exceptionally good.

So good it almost felt unfaif, like cheating.

Like the talent wasn’t learned but rather.. inherited.

It was inherited from someone who was also terrifyingly good.

Someone who could command a room with nothing but a monologue and a stupid amount of dramatic flair.

Someone named Agatha Harkness.

Agatha’s entire body stiffened.

No. Absolutely not. She's not going there.

Not right now.

Not in front of her emotional mentor and this smug kid. Possibly, her smug kid.

She isn't going there, not if she could help it.

Lilia asked Rae to stay for a bit while she excused herself for a bathroom break. Agatha immediately tried to protest loudly, but Lilia shut her down with one firm look and vanished out the door.

So now it was just the two of them. Agatha and the kid who may or may not be her biological nightmare.

They share the painfully silent four-cornered room, pretending very hard not to look at each other.

Agatha hadn’t said a single word about Rae’s performance.

No compliments nor insults. Not even a sarcastic “huh.”

Instead, she glued her eyes to her phone, rereading her message thread with Rio for the seventh time just to divert her attention. The only thing stopping her from flinging herself out a window was the promise of tonight’s private dinner.

Two agonizing minutes passed until Rae cleared her throat deliberately, forcing Agatha to look up.

Agatha met her gaze with the weariness of someone who did not sign up for any of this.

“What do you think?” Rae asks. She tried to play it cool, even though deep inside she desperately longed for Agatha’s approval.

Agatha, of course, feigned complete nonchalance. “You were.. adequate.”

“Woah!” Rae gasps dramatically. “Careful, you might run out of compliments!”

“I’m rationing them,” Agatha says dryly.

“I know you think I’m good, you just won’t admit it.” Cocky little gremlin.

Again—just like Agatha.

“You think highly of yourself, don’t you?”

“Why not, if I can walk the talk?” Rae shrugs, then smiled as if a mischievous idea sparked in her head.

Agatha recognized that smile instantly, as if she was looking at her own reflection.. only years younger..

Hell, she invented that smile.

It was her signature 'I’m-about-to-be-a-problem-and-you-can't-stop-me' smile.

Rae steps forward so Agatha can see her more clearly. She innocently bats her eyelashes and says in the sweetest voice Agatha has ever heard, “I can’t wait to spend the next few weeks working with you, Mommy!”

Oh, for fuck’s sake.

The day went on with more kids coming in and out for auditions. In the end, the workshop accepted more or less thirty children, and Lilia simply would not shut up about Rae. The next big thing, a natural, a star in the making—you get the gist as she goes on and on about the kid she just met.

Agatha pretends to hate it, but there was a quiet, inconvenient pride curling in her chest. If Rae is indeed her daughter, then there was no denying how her genes had done spectacularly well. The kid not only resembled Agatha in a way that’s difficult to ignore, she’d clearly inherited her talent as well.

If this were a different situation, trust that Agatha would brag about it endlessly.

Like mother, like daughter.

Once everything was packed up and Agatha steps outside for a breath of fresh air, the universe naturally decided to be funny and make her suffer even more. She runs straight into Rae.

Of course she did.

Why was the kid still hanging around, anyway?

“If you’re planning some dramatic bit to get more attention from Lilia, save it.” Agatha says flatly. “I’m running on fumes.”

Rae raises a brow and crosses her arms. “I believe she already adores me. I’m not desperate to try that hard.”

“Then why haven’t you left?”

“Uber’s on the way.”

“You don’t own a car?”

“I just turned sixteen.” Rae shrugs. “I failed my driver’s test. My mom won’t let me retake it yet unless I sit through another safe-driving class for beginners.”

Agatha stares at her, equal parts relieved and annoyed. Good. No accidents involved, just pure teenage incompetence.

“Your mom..” Agatha murmurs, attempting to inquire more.

There are so many things she wants to ask about Rae’s life, about the woman who raised her, about everything she missed.

But the words refuse to come, so she doesn’t.

Not yet.

Instead, she settles for, “Why isn’t your mom picking you up? And why aren’t you with an adult today?”

“Why do you care?” Rae snaps, and before Agatha can respond, she speaks again, “She’s working and I’m almost an adult myself, I don’t need daytime supervision."

Agatha exhales. “What does she do?” To make it clear if it isn’t, she clarifies, “Your mom.”

“She’s a chef.” Rae replies. “I’m heading to see her, actually. She told me she’s going out to dinner tonight, and she asked me to help her pick what to wear.”

That alone said a lot. Rae must be really close with her mom.

“So.. you two are close.” Agatha concludes.

“We are. It’s always just been the two of us, anyway.” Rae replies.

Agatha plays it cool as she digs in for more, with whatever information she can possibly get. “No other parent?”

“No.” Rae looks at her straight in the eye. “I prefer it that way, tho.”

“What way?”

“To only have my mami. I don’t need anyone else.”

Agatha felt it straight through her ribs.

Instinctively, she reaches for her pendant, gripping it like an anchor to ground herself. “How long have you known?”

“Known what?” Rae frowns.

That you’re mine. Biologically. That you’re my daughter.

“That I’m the one who—”

“Gave me up?” Rae cuts in. “For adoption?”

Agatha exhales. “Yeah.”

“I asked.” Rae says quietly. “During my birthday earlier this month.”

She says it like Agatha doesn’t know her own child’s birthday. As if Agatha hadn’t counted the days once, hadn’t memorized a birthday she never got to celebrate.

“My mami had the file all this time.” Rae explains. “Your name and everything there is to know about the adoption. She never looked at it. She didn’t want to know anything about you then.”

Rae’s voice doesn’t waver. “She said that part of my life wasn’t hers to touch. That I should be the one to decide, should I want to know.”

Her gaze stays on Agatha. “So we opened it. Recently. That’s how we knew it was you.”

Agatha is conflicted. Part of her remains skeptical of Rae—of the timing, the circumstances, the unanswered questions. She needs certainty. She needs proof. She tells herself she can’t accept this until she’s absolutely sure.

And yet, despite her resistance, her heart betrays her.

There’s an ache. Almost a familiarity she never asked for.

She denies it, pushes it down.. but it’s there all the same beyond logic and reason.

She knows.

She knows.

Who else knows?

Her chest tightens as the implications crash in. The wheels in her head begin to spin, fast and unforgiving. It isn’t just her career that flashes before her eyes. The contracts, the scrutiny, the inevitable backlash—she’ll survive. She can handle the kind of life that she chose.

But Rae?

The public turns curiosity into condemnation, being too comfortable with snooping into celebrities’ lives. They would tear Rae apart just as easily. They would dig into her childhood, her adoption, her mami, searching for something scandalous to consume.

They wouldn’t see a kid. They’d see a headline.

“Who else knows?” She asks, keeping her voice even.

Rae blinks. “What?”

“That I’m your biological mother.” Agatha says. “Who else knows?”

Because if this gets out, it won’t just be her life that gets torn apart.

This little shit doesn’t deserve that.

Rae stares at her, those blue eyes wide and accusing, mirroring something in Agatha herself. And then she chuckles. Really chuckles. “You’re unbelievable.”

“Excuse me?” Agatha asks, her tone clipped.

“You only care about your career, don’t you?” Rae presses, defensive now. “You don’t want anyone to find out because it could ruin you.”

Of course she cares about her career. It’s her liberation, her life built brick by brick, each role and achievement carved out of sheer determination.

But beyond that, there’s Rae. Even though she only met Rae yesterday, she already cares about the kid. She cares enough that the thought of the world hurting her, or dragging her into scandal, makes Agatha’s chest tighten. She cares because Rae might be her daughter, because the possibility alone makes herself yearn for the child she lost in ways she didn’t expect.

Although she’ll never admit it out loud. That she cares. Not now, maybe not ever.

Her chest tightens, guilt and fear twisting together. If the world knew, the press, the public, her fans.. the scrutiny would be relentless. Headlines, rumors, questions about her morality, her choices, her past. And Rae, the menace that she is but innocent all the same, would be dragged into it. Agatha can’t let that happen.

“I—” Agatha starts, then stops. Words fail her once more.

Rae lets out a huff, disappointment and hurt almost evident in her expression. “Don’t worry. No one else knows other than me and mami.”

She brushes past Agatha, bumping into her shoulder forcefully, making Agatha stumble. She lets it pass. She deserved that anyway.

“No one will ever know.” Rae adds, her voice quieter now as she turns toward the exit.

Before she disappears completely, she glances back for the last time. “Besides, it’s not like I’m exactly proud to be Agatha Harkness’ daughter.”

She tries to hide the sting of emotion behind a tight smile, but Agatha notices. A flicker of something. Vulnerability slips through. Agatha recognizes it instantly because she has the same. It mirrors her own emotions, her own carefully hidden fears.

In that instant, she sees herself in Rae.

She doesn’t know what to do with that fact.

She locks the screen and sinks back into the couch at Lilia’s house, rubbing her thumb against the edge of her pendant.

She barely knows Rio. A few conversations, a lot of flirting, and a postponed dinner that somehow turned into soup delivery. It’s ridiculous, really. This is only going to be their second meeting—barely even that, if she’s being honest and yet Rio has already slipped past Agatha’s usual defenses with alarming ease. She doesn’t feel the need to bolt. No alarms going off. No urge to disappear.

That’s new. And suspicious.

Agatha Harkness does not do comfort without cost.

Get a grip, she tells herself. You like pretty women. You’ve always liked pretty women. This is nothing new, nothing mystical, nothing worth spiraling over. Rio is attractive—effortlessly so, which is frankly annoying. She carries herself with that quiet confidence Agatha has always been weak for. The kind that doesn’t need to announce itself. The kind that makes you lean in without realizing you’ve moved.

That’s all this is.

Probably.

Agatha exhales through her nose once again. She doesn’t like people who make things feel easy. Easy usually comes with strings.

She tells herself it’s just appreciation. Curiosity. Maybe boredom. Maybe the universe throwing a distraction at her when she desperately needs one.

It’s just soup. She convinces herself. It doesn’t mean anything.

Rio arrives twenty minutes later.

Agatha knows it without checking the clock because the house feels different before the knock even comes.

Agatha opens the door to the smell of garlic and ginger.

Rio doesn’t step inside. She stays just beyond the threshold, like she’s been very deliberately trained not to cross invisible lines without permission. She’s holding a paper bag in one hand and a soup container tucked under her arm, hair slightly damp as if she’d rushed straight from the kitchen. She looks.. domestic.

That should not be doing things to Agatha. 

“I brought soup.” Rio says, lifting the bag like evidence. “And bread. I didn’t know what kind you liked, so I went with neutral and inoffensive.”

Agatha huffs. “Bold strategy.”

Rio flashes a toothy grin, the one that looks like trouble and pokes her cheek with her tongue. “I’m excellent at being inoffensive when necessary.”

“Tragic.” Agatha deadpans. “You hide it well.”

They stand there for a beat, neither rushing the moment. Agatha notices the way Rio’s eyes flick past her shoulder, respectful and curious but not nosy. Still not stepping in.

“You don’t have to hover.” Agatha says. “I’m not contagious.”

Rio laughs, soft and brief. “I figured tonight was more of a soup drop-off than a dinner-and-flirting extravaganza.”

Agatha snorts despite herself. “Raincheck.” she says. “Dinner another time. When I’m less, well.. whatever this is.”

“Understood.” Rio says easily. No pressure. No disappointment—well, maybe a trace of it, hidden behind another grin. “I’ll hold you to that.”

She hands over the bag, their fingers brushing for half a second longer than necessary. Rio doesn’t pull away first. Neither does Agatha.

“Feel better.” Rio adds. “And,” She taps the container lightly, “Eat. That’s an order.”

Agatha raises a brow. “You're ordering me around already?”

“Orders from the chef.” Rio replies, tongue poking her cheek again, a habit Agatha is already filing under annoyingly endearing. “I’m very professional.”

Agatha watches her walk away before she closes the door, which is absolutely not something she plans on unpacking tonight.

Later, curled up with the soup balanced in her hands, Agatha takes one spoonful and pauses.

It’s good. Comfortingly so. 

She scowls at it, then at her phone, and finally types:

agathaharkness: Soup’s unfairly good.
agathaharkness: Thanks.

A reply comes almost instantly.

riovidal: told you.
riovidal: feel better

riovidal: i shall see you around

For the first time that day, Agatha's heart and mind felt at ease. A small smile sneaks in despite her best efforts as she takes another bite.

Little does she know, in one of Westview’s bigger estates, Rae notices that same smile and asks where it's from or why it's there. Rio deflects the question easily but later, alone, she wonders what it means to keep seeing Agatha without telling her daughter.

It goes the same for Rae who is silent about the restaurant and the workshop, basically about having already crossed paths with her biological mother.

For once, they are both holding things back, each unaware of just how close their truths already are.

The name Agatha Harkness lingers unspoken.

“Your reinforcement has arrived.”

Agatha startles awake when the lights in her room flip on, her body still heavy with sleep. The mattress dips immediately after as someone jumps straight onto her bed with zero regard for personal space. 

She squints and attempts to adjust her vision. Eventually, Jen comes into view. Her alarm hasn’t gone off and her room is still dark beyond the curtains. The unwelcome guest is clearly wide awake and painfully chirpy at this hour, far too pleased with herself for having interrupted Agatha’s carefully orchestrated beauty sleep.

Agatha groans, covering her eyes with the back of her palm. “Get the fuck out of here and come back after 8:00 am or I will hex you and your entire bloodline. You’ll never know peace and your descendants will feel it in their bones.”

Jen laughs, completely unthreatened. “Wow. That’s a lot of energy for someone who called me and demanded I take an urgent flight to Westview.” She reminds. “You’re being dramatic.”

“Not right now.” Agatha deadpans. “I am being reasonable.”

Jen flops more comfortably onto the bed, settling beside Agatha. “I brought you five just in case.. Or, I don’t know. Just to be sure, I guess?"

“Five what?”

“Pregnancy tests. Duh.” Jen says, like it’s the most obvious thing in the world. “I figured you couldn’t buy them here on your own, so—ow! What is wrong with you?” She hisses as Agatha bolts upright, her feet slamming straight into Jen’s thighs.

“What is wrong with you?” Agatha parrots, genuinely offended and visibly shuddering at the implication. “Why would you think I’m pregnant?”

“Why else would you ask me to come here ASAP?”

“I can think of a million other things, Jennifer. Jesus Christ.” If she were a devoted Catholic, she would’ve made the sign of the cross right then and there. “I am not pregnant.”

Jen’s expression softens as she reaches out for Agatha’s arms. “I know it won’t be easy, especially at your age and being an established woman whose career—”

“Shut the fuck up!” Agatha whispers screams, concerned that the walls might be thin enough to disturb other people in the household. All traces of sleep have removed itself from her body at this point due to the conversation they’re having. “I am not pregnant. Don’t make me repeat that a third time because I am this close to losing my mind.”

“Say sike right now.”

“What?”

“Never mind.” Jen waves a dismissive hand, realizing her friend slash boss isn’t exactly fluent in whatever trendy terms kids use these days. “If you’re not..” She stops herself from saying the word pregnant when she notices the vein in Agatha’s forehead threatening to burst. “Okay. Then why am I here? Why was I summoned?”

Agatha met Jen five years into her career. Hollywood was ruthless, and Agatha had just won her first Emmy, only to discover that her previous assistant had been sneaking off with her personal wardrobe (RIP to that one vintage Chanel bag she actually adored).

At first, Jen and Agatha weren’t exactly compatible. Both had strong personalities, and Agatha didn’t want an assistant she argues with constantly. But Lilia, who always seemed to know what was best for Agatha, suggested otherwise. Agatha listened despite herself and gave it a shot.

Jen proved herself worthy when a particularly aggressive paparazzi captured a moment out of context, Agatha was laughing politely while standing near a known corrupt politician. She knew how showbiz works that within hours, gossip columns would spin it into a full-blown scandal: Agatha Harkness dating a man under investigation.

Jen showed initiative, acting fast without being told. She shielded Agatha from the camera, guided her through a back exit, and quietly explained how they’d handle the rumors. Agatha would never associate herself with the man, let alone date one, but thanks to Jen’s careful and meticulous actions, they dodged a potential scandal entirely.

That particular moment sealed their partnership. Jen handles all the logistics, movies, schedules, and contracts. She’s Agatha’s manager, agent, and assistant all rolled into one.

And while they bicker endlessly, their friendship is unbreakable, tho neither of them would admit it out loud.

“Why am I here, Agatha?” Jen repeats, much gentler this time when Agatha failed to reply on her first try.

Agatha sighs. How could she even begin to explain what she’d been up to the past two days? Well, clearly, the past few years, if Jen was going to know the entire context.

Her fingers find the pendant again, rolling it between her thumb and forefinger. “There’s a kid..” She starts slowly. “A teenager.”

Jen waits. She’s learned not to interrupt when Agatha talks like this.

“She showed up on our first night here.” Agatha continues. “And now she won’t leave my head. Or my life, apparently.”

Jen’s brows knit together. “Okay..” She says cautiously. “And?”

Agatha lets it hang, waiting for Jen to realize what she’s been implying without having to spell it out. “And she looks like me. Talks like me. Acts like me.. She’s basically just like me, but younger.”

Jen blinks once. Twice. A third time.

“..Agatha.” She mutters her name carefully, “What exactly are you not telling me?”

Agatha stares at her friend as she adjusts her position, hugging her knees closer to her chest. “What I’m about to say is what I’ve done. You can judge me all you want, but whatever I did, I did with reason and what I thought was best at the time.”

Jen nods. “I’d judge the way you like your oatmeal, but never the decisions you made back then.” She says with a small smile, encouraging Agatha to continue. “Trust me.”

For the first time, Agatha told Jen what happened, or at least enough of it to make sense. She’d gotten pregnant at twenty-four, a one-night thing with a woman at a bar. She was still living under her mother’s cruelty with nothing to her name. Giving the baby up felt like the safest choice then. And now, sixteen years later, the child.. Rae—shows up.

Agatha tells her about their first interaction at the restaurant, about the way Rae looked at her like she already knew. She doesn’t miss the way Jen visibly winces when she mentions that Rae is also part of Lilia’s workshop.

She’s really here and she’s real.

Jen was quiet the entire time, just listening and letting out an occasional “hmm” here and there.

Once Agatha finished, Jen finally spoke. “So.. you have a kid.”

Agatha’s breath hitched at the admission she’d been trying to deny. “I have a kid.”

“And she’s just like you?”

“Painfully so..”

“Damn.” Jen offers a chuckle to somehow ease the tension in the room. “As if the world needed more variants of Agatha Harkness, may God help us all.”

They sit quietly for a while, both lost in their own thoughts, until Jen finally asks the question Agatha has been waiting for. “Are you one hundred percent sure she’s yours?”

“No.” Agatha admits. The word comes out rougher than she expects. “But I know I’m also not wrong with the thought that she’s possibly mine, and that’s the problem.”

Jen studies her for a moment, eyes sharp in the way that means she’s already thinking three steps ahead. “No one else knows, besides her and the adoptive mom, correct?”

“That’s what I’ve been told.”

Jen nods slowly. “Then you still have control. That matters.”

With that, her expression fully shifts. The softness doesn’t disappear, but it hardens into something purposeful. “Okay.” She says, already standing and slipping into manager mode. “We must verify.”

Agatha tries to protest,“Jen—”

“No.” Jen cuts in gently but firmly. “This isn’t about doubt, this is about certainty.”

She starts pacing, ticking things off on her fingers. “First: we do nothing publicly. No statements and no leaks. This strictly stays between us.”

Agatha nods.

“Second,” Jen continues, “We confirm the adoption records. Quietly, I must emphasize. I know a couple of lawyers who specialize in sealed and semi-open adoptions. One owes me a favor, the other dumped me on my birthday. Either way, we get access without making noise and that’s a priority.”

Agatha tries to discredit the one where her friend got dump on her birthday, noting that it should be a topic for another time. “Would that even be possible after sixteen years?”

“I don’t speak legal, but I assume everything is possible with a huge chunk of money.” Jen says easily. “Your name is already on the paperwork, anyway. That should be doable.”

She stops pacing and looks straight at Agatha. “Third, if and only if you want to, we can do a private DNA test. Not with the ones in clinics to avoid electronic database. There are doctors who handle this discreetly for public figures. I’ve dealt with one before, it’s surprisingly easy."

Agatha blinks but doesn’t question. Seems like Jen has an entire lifetime to herself before she met Agatha.

“And lastly,” Jen’s voice softens. “We protect the kid. You already have contact—fine. You’re simply her mentor. You keep it professional, appropriate, and exactly within the lines you already have. No emotional promises. No confessions you can’t take back. Again, we have to confirm first and give you plenty of time to decide what role, if any, you’re ready to play in that kid’s life.”

It’s too much to process, even for someone as brave and sharp-tongued as Agatha. Jen notices the shift in her demeanor and decides not to push. Instead, she settles back on the bed beside her friend and lets the silence do the work, offering comfort without a single word.

“Agatha?” She murmurs after a few minutes. “Be honest with me, do you want that kid to be yours?”

Agatha doesn't answer right away. It requires a lot of thought, and..

“I don’t know.” She whispers. “There’s maybe and possibly, and I already think of her as is. It’s.. complicated. I really don’t know.”

“That’s okay.” Jen accepts her answer without the need of pushing for more. “I’ll start making calls today and deal with what I can.”

A weight she hadn’t realized she was carrying lifts off her shoulders. “Thank you.”

Jen smirks. “Please don’t thank me yet. Wait until I invoice you for this, your bank account won’t take it lightly.”

A beat, then Jen bumps her elbow against Agatha’s playfully. “Bitch, I really thought you were pregnant.” She laughs. “Who would’ve thought you’d already given birth?”

“Seriously, Jenny?” Agatha glares at her, the emotions finally starting to feel lighter. “Again, why the fuck would you think that?”

“Don’t be offended, but for the run of my entire career working with you, I always assumed the biggest scandal I’d have to deal with was you accidentally getting yourself pregnant.”

That earns her a more sharper glare.

“I have always been prepared, I have plans ranging from A-Z.” Jen continues unapologetically. “And you can’t exactly blame me. I’ve got a pretty wide list of contacts from women you’ve engaged yourself with over the years.”

Agatha doesn’t take offense. She knows it’s mostly true.

Though, to be fair, not as bad as Jen makes it sound.

“I got really scared when a few months ago, you told me you were off birth control.” Jen adds. “We were in the middle of filming the Hill film, and you were fooling around with that Russian lady—which, by the way, was the hottest of them all, if you ask me.”

Agatha prides herself on that. Melina was hot, and it was fun while it lasted.

Little did Jen know, nothing ever happened between her and Agatha beyond a few steamy make-out sessions.

Agatha is exclusive, chooses carefully who she actually sleeps with and practices safe sex religiously, driven by a lingering fear of getting pregnant again. Birth control stayed part of the routine, even when there was no real action.

“I’ve obviously learned my lesson about sex right before I joined showbiz, hon.” Agatha says dryly. “Also, I’m in my early menopausal stage so you can definitely breath now. You won’t be needing your alphabet plan.”

Jen scoffs. “Whatever. The pregnancy tests I bought were pretty damn expensive, those were the best brands.” She says bitterly. “You’re paying me back.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “Worth it for your peace of mind.”

Agatha steps out of the rented car, the hazard lights ticking behind her impatiently. She shuts the door with more force than necessary and looks up just in time to see Rio push through the restaurant’s side entrance.

Breathless. Slightly flushed. And, annoyingly.. conveniently, dressed in a crisp white chef’s uniform.

Of course she is.

Her sleeves are rolled up just enough to show a fraction of her forearm. Agatha stares without shame and takes it all in. She observes the way the white catches the afternoon light, the way Rio wears that toothy grin even from a far, the way that the other woman looks entirely in her element.

Well. That’s unfair.

Rio spots her in no time as she jogs the last few steps over. “Hi,”

“Hi.” Agatha pretends to act cool. “You look like the place was on fire.”

“Soufflé emergency involving a couple of new sous chefs.” Rio replies, then she points at the hazard lights blinking behind Agatha. “I think your car is screaming for help.”

Agatha waves a dismissive hand. “It’ll live.”

Rio chuckles, then pauses, suddenly aware of her appearance. She tries to smoothen the fabric of her uniform consciously, “Sorry, I didn’t have time to change.”

“Don’t.” Agatha says without thinking.

“Don’t?”

“Apologize,” Agatha clarify, though her eyes linger anyway. “You look—” She stops herself before she says anything crossing the lines of initial flirting, so she settles with, “Appropriate.”

Rio’s grins again, wider this time. She pokes her tongue briefly into her cheek, like she’s holding something back. “That’s the nicest compliment I’ve gotten all day.”

“Don’t flatter yourself.”

“Should I not?”

They stand there for a beat, traffic humming past and the restaurant buzzing just behind Rio. Agatha becomes acutely aware of how close they are. How easy it would be to step closer, if she wanted to..

“You really should..” Rio points out, gesturing at the car again, breaking the thin ice. “Do something about that.”

“I wasn’t planning on staying.” Agatha replies. She lifts the plastic bag in her hand. “I told you I was around the area. And I happened to bring the container with me.”

That was a lie. Cue the acting when you naturally need them.

She hadn’t been anywhere near the area, and if there was one thing Agatha Harkness did not do, it was doing mundane errands such as returning food containers. She’s not equipped with that kind of morals and to develop it all of a sudden is highly unlikely.

It’s not even as if Rio is in desperate need of those containers. The woman clearly owns an obscene number of them, probably stashed in some massive kitchen warehouse somewhere in Westview.

She’s here on purpose.

To see Rio.

But as flirtatious as she can be, Agatha would rather choke than say that out loud.

She’d do a lot of other things rather than saying them aloud these days, unfortunately.

“I can whip something up.” Rio offers, shy but hopeful. “If you want.. and, um, if you don’t have other plans, maybe you could come in and—”

Agatha lets her pause hang. She’s curious to see her try, see her earn her attention a little because that’s just how Agatha is. She loves a little fun.

“And what exactly would you whip up for me?”

“You’re literally standing in a restaurant, Agatha. The options are endless.”

“And if I wanted, hmm.. some duck with caramel glaze? Can you make that happen?"

Rio quirks a brow, amused. “Not exactly on our usual menu, but yes, I can make it happen if that's what you really want.”

Agatha smirks, leaning back just slightly. “Then consider me a guest.”

Agatha stepped into the kitchen, letting herself be guided past the clatter of pots and pans. She recognized a few chefs and staff from previous visit, bracing herself for the worst in case she runs into Rae. She prays to whatever Gods will listen that she doesn’t.

Rio moved like she owned the place. Well, she does own the place.

Apron on, hair tucked back, knives in hand, chopping onions and stirring sauces with that quiet confidence Agatha didn’t even know she enjoyed watching. 

Their conversation flowed naturally. When was the restaurant established, how many award shows Agatha had survived slightly intoxicated.

All the while, Agatha kept stealing glances at Rio, realizing she was.. Completely charmed. 

More than charmed, if she was being honest to herself. She had never felt this kind of pull toward a woman. It was curious and flirtatious. It was easy and surprisingly pleasant.

She finds herself wanting for more.

She wanted to see where this could go.

Rayo del Sol doesn’t accept guests until six, which leaves the place quiet in a way Agatha isn’t used to. It feels like the space has been paused just for them. 

Rio leads Agatha toward the far end, where the lights are dimmer and softer. It was almost like an accidental dinner setup that was never meant to be romantic but kind of is anyway.

She’d traded the chef’s uniform for a sleeveless turtleneck and neutral trousers in no time. Agatha scowled at the loss, but stared anyway. Rio made even the simplest outfit look effortless.

And hot. Definitely hot, as simple as it is.

Is Agatha that desperate?

In her defense she hasn’t been with a woman in months so, yes. Maybe she is.

Rio sets down the dishes she made herself, the result of Agatha watching the entire time. She offered sarcastic commentary as Rio ignores most of it, hums through the rest. Agatha stays amused anyway.

No duck, in the end. Agatha had scrunched her nose at the idea, decided mid-thought that the word duck felt wrong in her mouth and promptly wanted nothing to do with it. Rio laughed and let it go without teasing her too much.

They eat slowly, talking between bites. The food container delivery agenda has turned into a dinner Agatha promised, and she's nowhere near complaining.

“Where did you go to high school?”

“Westview High.” Rio says, settling into the chair across from Agatha. “I had quite a reputation as a troublemaker.”

“Did you saran-wrap toilets or set someone’s hair on fire?”

“Neither, surprisingly.” Rio laughs. “But I did get caught making out with girls, one of them being the principal’s daughter.”

That gets Agatha’s attention. She lifts a brow. “So you weren’t a goody-two-shoes.”

“Far from it.” Rio says easily. “What about you? Where’d you go?”

Agatha takes a slow sip of the red wine Rio opened earlier. It was something she claimed was from the eighties. “St. Catherine’s.”

Rio waits for the punchline. When it doesn’t come, she blinks. “You’re kidding.”

Agatha Harkness and catholic school sounds completely on the opposite ends of a wavelength. 

“I don’t kid about trauma.” Agatha says flatly. “I think they used to pray for me more than they prayed for their own families.”

More conversation flows easily between them. Agatha asks Rio how many women she’s dated; Rio, unsurprisingly, turns the question right back on her.

Neither of them answers. Both numbers stay deliberately vague, tucked away behind smirks and raised brows, like a shared agreement not to ruin the mystery.

By the time they reach the end of the meal and with dessert somehow making its way to the table, Agatha realizes that she’s genuinely enjoying Rio’s company.

The ease of it. The quiet attention. The way Rio listens without prying.

She likes it more than she probably should.

And yet, no matter how comfortable the moment becomes, one thought refuses to leave her alone.

Or, one name.

Rae.

From what she’s observed, Rio seems distinctly close with the staff, which means it’s safe to assume she knows Rae. And as thankful as Agatha is that she hasn’t crossed paths with the kid today, that little menace still refuses to leave her mind.

She has questions. A few of them. And maybe, just maybe.. Rio can answer some.

“There’s a kid working here.” Agatha begins carefully. “And, uh.. I’m just—well. I’d really like to know anything about her..” She trails off, unable to find the right wording without sounding like a creep.

“My staff?” Rio asks, interest piqued. “I hope they didn’t trouble you, or sell your autograph on eBay for a thousand dollars or something.”

Agatha wishes it were that easy. “No.” She shrugs. “Her name’s Rae, actually. Do you—”

Rio’s expression shifts at the name. Her mouth parts, something unreadable flickering across her face before she clears her throat. Her posture stiffens, suddenly rigid, almost restless. “You met Rae?”

“I did. My first night here.” Agatha answers, not yet clocking the change in Rio’s behavior. “She’s a breath of fresh air, isn’t she?”

Rio stills completely.

“Agatha.” She says carefully, “What exactly has Rae told you?”

Agatha assumes Rae must have a reputation here. Mouthy, sharp, tends to cross one's boundaries. That would explain Rio's reaction, so she doesn’t dwell on it. “She didn’t do anything bad, if that’s what you’re thinking.” Agatha clarifies, attempting a chuckle that sounds brittle even to her own ears. 

Rio closes her eyes for a second. Just briefly. She needed to ground herself or perhaps, make the world stop spinning.

When she looks at Agatha again, something has shifted—something guarded and unreadable. “We really need to talk about Rae.”

Before Agatha can ask why, Rio’s phone vibrates sharply against the table. She ignores it, until she glances down. Agatha catches a brief glimpse of the caller ID. Sun emojis and a letter. Nothing useful to decipher.

Not that she wanted to. That would be eavesdropping, in a way.

Rio exhales a frustrated breath and stands abruptly, muttering a soft, “Excuse me.”

She steps away, voice lowered as she answers, leaving Agatha alone with her wine and the creeping sense that she’s just stepped into something far bigger than she meant to.

Rio said they needed to talk about Rae.

What was there to talk about that involved Agatha?

Her mind immediately runs through the worst possibilities, because of course it does.

Is Rae in trouble? Is she sick? Have she done something illegal?

What could possibly be wrong enough to warrant this kind of reaction?

“Dios mío.” Agatha overhears Rio mutter, loud enough that it cuts through the low hum of the restaurant.

Rio’s back is to her now, phone pressed to her ear, hands lifting to her forehead like she’s trying to physically contain whatever headache this conversation is giving her. She paces a few steps, agitation written into every movement.

“Raina.” Rio snaps into the phone, voice tight. “What exactly have you done?”

Whoever Rio was talking to on the phone, Agatha knew damn well it wasn’t her business to pry. She already had enough on her plate to begin with.

“You can’t just.. No, listen to me—” Rio’s voice cracked slightly this time, a sharp edge beneath the usual calm. “I’ll be heading home quick.”

Agatha tried to hide the disappointment flaring across her face. Rio had to leave making their early night was cut short. Not that she was expecting anything more, but maybe she had hoped for just a little.

“Until then..” Rio said, her eyes briefly meeting Agatha’s as she turned around, “Please don’t do anything stupid.” With that, she dropped the phone.

Agatha took her cue, standing as well to meet Rio at eye level. “Everything okay at home?”

“It should be.. there’s just a slight problem.” Rio admitted. “Listen, I have to leave now.”

“I get it.” Agatha forced a small smile. “Sounds important.”

“It is.” Rio confirmed.

They stand there, face to face, neither knowing what to do, neither wanting to cross a line.

Rio, polite as ever, leans forward slightly and gives Agatha a brief, almost awkward hug. Their bodies barely touch.

“I had fun tonight.” Rio says, soft but sure. “And I promise, we’ll talk about Rae next time.” Agatha nods, holding onto that promise.

Somehow, just knowing the conversation can wait eases the tightness in her chest. “I’m the one who owes you now.” Rio then murmurs, voice low.

Rio gestures for her to head out first, but Agatha shakes her head, claiming she needs to use the bathroom anyway. With a final wave, Rio smiles and makes her exit.

Agatha sighs once she’s gone.

The closest thing they got to physical contact tonight was a hug.

Agatha Harkness.. got a hug.

A hug.

Damn it. Does Rio have to be such a gentleman now that she’s older? Agatha would pay to see her being feral.

Fuck those lucky girls who got to make out with Rio during high-school, Agatha thinks. And maybe fuck her for wanting it too.
