Chapter 6: Chapter 6

Chapter Notes

i offer you rae's pov for my first update of the year :)

Rae was five years old when she learned the word adoption.

She was in kindergarten then, a time where she’d throw a fit if she’s asked to wear anything but princess dresses. She had chubby and rosy cheeks, and you’ll never see her without a big bow attached to her pigtails or a sparkly tiara on top of her braids.

School was her first real window into a world beyond her family tree. 

Her friends constantly talked about parents the way kids do, casually and without weight: two moms, two dads, a mom and a dad.

With that came along small observations. How many hands her friends held. How many voices called their names during pickup.

Rae watched and noticed.

While most of her friends had two parents, Rae had one.

She only had mami.

Mami is gentle, and kind, and patient.

She always tells Rae that she is smart and beautiful. She tells Rae that she’s the best thing that had ever happened to her. 

Mami gives her presents even when it isn’t her birthday or Christmas. She kisses her scraped knees, read her bedtime stories, and holds her hand a little longer than most whenever Rae needed it.

That had always been enough for Rae.

But the world had a way of teaching children to compare, and then to question. 

As Rae grew and stepped further outside the safety of what she knew, she began to notice that what she had was different.

Not wrong.

Not lacking.

Just different.

So when Rae finally asked mami about it, she can vividly remember the way mami’s breath hitched.

Mami didn’t answer right away. Instead, she led Rae into the kitchen and sat her on one of the tall stools by the island. She took Rae’s hands in hers before she spoke, holding them close together.

That day, mami told Rae she was adopted.

Rae didn’t know what that word meant yet. It might even be the first time she has heard of it at all.

To make her understand more, mami explained that Rae hadn’t come from her belly. She hadn’t been pregnant, she hadn’t given birth.

Rae frowned at that, the lines in her forehead becoming more visible by the second. At school, she’d learned that babies came from mommies’ bellies. That was how it always worked. Everyone said so.

So, if she didn’t come from mami’s belly.. where did she come from?

Mami squeezed her hands a little tighter, like she already knew the question Rae had in mind.

Mami told Rae that she had always wanted a child, even if it meant raising one alone. 

She didn’t have a partner, and she was unable to carry a baby herself.

She wanted to have a child to shower with affection, to raise, and to come home to every single day.

So when she was twenty-seven, she went to an orphanage in Westview. Mami told Rae that the moment she saw her, she knew. 

Not because one month old Rae cried the loudest or smiled the brightest, to the extent of her newborn capabilities. 

It’s because something in mami’s heart simply said, there you are.

And that was how Rae came to her.

That was how Rae came to be.

On top of that, mami also told Rae that she has another mom. 

The other mom was the one who carried her in her belly and brought her into the world.

Rae was able to comprehend the implications.

If she had another mom, then why was she here?

Why did she have to be.. adopted?

Why was she given away?

Mami chose every word carefully, not wanting to plant a negative narrative in Rae’s mind about her biological parent.

She said that sometimes, grown-ups know they can’t give their child the life they deserve. And when that happens, the bravest thing they can do is ask someone else to love and care for that child instead.

With that, Rae began crying, and mami’s heart broke the way it always did when she sees her little girl in tears.

Rae didn’t fully grasp what it meant to be given away. It sounded awful, sure—but it didn’t hurt the way mami seemed to think it would.

What hurt was the idea that there was someone else out there.

Another mom.

The fact felt heavy in her chest. She thought of it as unfamiliar and wrong.

Rae didn’t want another mom.

She only wanted mami.

The fear was strong enough that she said it out loud.

“What if she comes back?” Rae quivered. “What if she takes me away from you?”

Mami’s face softened immediately. She promised that it would never happen. No one would take Rae away from her. Not now, not ever.

And if anyone ever tried, mami would fight them the same way she fights nightmares and monsters under Rae’s bed at night.

They sealed it with a pinky swear.

Later, when Rae finally stopped crying, mami asked if being adopted made her feel sad. Or strange. Maybe different?

Rae shook her head.

She said she felt lucky because someone had chosen her on purpose.

At five, Rae accepted that easily.

At fifteen, it refused to be ignored.

The questions didn’t disappear, they simply learned how to wait.

She still believed she was chosen, that was never the question.

But she had started to wonder who had let her go.

Rio admitted that she doesn’t actually know who Rae’s other mom is, but she has the file that keeps her records and information safely secured. 

She wants Rae to make the decision when she’s older and vowed to give her full support once she makes the choice for herself.

On her sixteenth birthday, Rae finally opened the file with Rio by her side.

The folder was neat and thin, but the contents felt heavy in their hands. Every detail was there including dates, medical records, and adoption papers. Everything was kept safe all these years, just as Rio promised.

And then came the printed name with a signature scribbled on top. The one thing Rae yearns for.

Agatha Harkness.

A public figure. A renowned A-lister. A woman they had both seen in magazines, on screens, and in headlines. 

Who could have thought that the beloved Agatha Harkness of hollywood harbors this kind of secret?

Rae remembers looking up at Rio, searching for guidance and a hint of what this could possibly mean. It was deja vu when Rio squeezed her hand the same way she did when Rae first found out about being adopted.

“Remember, you get to decide what to do with this.” Rio reminded her softly. “It’s your choice. No one else’s.”

Rae’s mind raced, so did her heart. She was in shocked. Then she was in disbelief. After that, she was curios.

However, she had no sense of obligation to act neither does she had the drive to seek the woman out.

All Rae had ever wanted was a name, an identity. With that answered, the lingering question mark vanished into thin air. 

And for the first time, the face of the person who had left her in an orphanage was no longer a blur.

That was enough for Rae.

The life she has with Rio, with all that she needed and wanted handed freely with endless love and affection, was something Rae would never trade for anyone or anything.

Besides, even with Rio’s gentle reasoning over the years and her belief of always trying to see the good in people, grown-up Rae is now able to grasp the concept that being given away is just the nicer term for being abandoned.

Under no circumstances would she ever go looking for someone who had already given her away, no, abandoned her.

But the universe works in twisted ways. Imagine Rae’s surprise when Agatha Harkness appeared not at her doorstep, but at the restaurant named after her.

Initially, Rae had no intention of approaching her. Rio didn’t even know she was there that night, meaning Rae had no one to consult or rely on if things went sideways.

Something in her nudged her forward, and before she knew it, Rae was standing at Agatha Harkness’s table, menus in hand.

She spent countless nights reading articles and blogs about Agatha Harkness, of course she did. 

She consumed every detail of her life and filmography. She gnawed at everything she could reach for as far as the general audience could go.

Everyone knows Agatha has a sharp tongue, and she isn’t exactly the warm and approachable type. 

Her resting bitch face alone screams she doesn’t give out kindness freely, certainly not to a nobody like Rae.

It shouldn’t have been a shock when Agatha snapped at Rae the first time they met. Rae tried to keep it casual, to stay cool, but part of her still stung when Agatha treated her the way she did.

Her own daughter.

Then again, how could she have recognized her?

She had abandoned Rae as a baby. How was she supposed to know what her daughter would look like now? What her daughter would grow into?

Still, Rae had hoped for a connection. Something instinctive, per se. 

The kind Rio always has when Rae is sick, or when she needed something before she ever had to ask.

Agatha, it turned out, didn’t have that instinct.

To add insult to injury, it even seemed like she actively dislike Rae. 

A cruel way to meet the woman who gave you life.

It was never Rae’s intention to reveal who she was—but it happened anyway. She wasn’t expecting a reunion or tears, she wasn’t that naive, but she had hoped for more. 

For something, anything, that proved she had mattered.

Even once..

After that night, Rae half-expected Agatha to reach out. She figured she can now be accessible through social media, but Agatha didn’t. No call, no message. Not a peep at all.

The universe, apparently, wasn’t done with her. For its next big joke, Calderu Acting Workshop turned out to be a surprise collaboration with Agatha Harkness. Though, really, it shouldn’t have been a big reveal after seeing them have dinner together the night before.

If this was how things were going to be, Rae figured she might as well be difficult about it. 

She decided she wouldn’t shrink despite being forced into Agatha’s orbit.

She will stand out.

She will let Agatha see exactly who she’d become. Let her see how perfectly fine Rae is without her.

She didn’t need explanations or apologies, she had already lived a life without either. 

Rae wore her confidence like armor. It is polished and sharp. She wouldn’t ask for acknowledgment, wouldn’t beg for anything that should have been given freely. 

If Agatha saw her and felt nothing, then that’s on her. 

Rae will learn to live with it.

“You’re not going anywhere near a vicinity of a wheel ever again.”

Rae winces as Rio comes back inside, shutting the front door a little harder than usual. 

There’s a faint smell of oil and burned rubber still clinging to her, evidence of the crime scene she just inspected in the garage.

The Tesla survived. Barely. But at least it did.

“I swear I wasn’t going anywhere.” Rae says quickly, already backpedaling as she sets her hot cocoa down on the table and stands to face her mother. “I was literally just going to drive around the block.”

Rio arches a brow. Just one. “My love..” Rio says, her voice soft but with authority. “That does not make it less dangerous.”

Rae opens her mouth to explain, then she thinks better of it, so she closes it again instead.

Rio exhales through her nose and runs a hand through her hair, the earlier tension still sitting in her shoulders. “You don’t drive ‘around the block’ when you don’t have a license. You don’t test vehicles you can’t fully control. And you definitely don’t do it alone in a garage without conscious adults to guide you.”

“I do know how to drive.” Rae mutters.

“You know how to sit in a driver’s seat and feel brave.” Rio corrects gently. “That’s not the same thing.”

She moves closer, resting her hands on Rae’s shoulders. It is not to scold, but to anchor. 

Rae slumps immediately, her posture giving her away. She still smells faintly like cocoa, sugar, and 100% teenage recklessness.

“What if something went wrong?” Rio continues, quieter now. “What if the brakes didn’t respond? Or you panicked? Or someone else got hurt?”

Rae swallows. “I didn’t think—”

“Exactly.” Rio points out. “That’s why I’m thinking for you.”

There’s a beat.

Then Rio adds, “I’m cutting your credit card for a week.”

“A week?” Rae yelps. “That’s a cruel punishment, mother dearest! How could I ever survive my daily trips to the mall without your massive fortune?”

Rio snorts despite herself, poking her cheek with her tongue. “You’re lucky it’s only a week.”

Rae groans and drops back onto the couch dramatically. “You left me alone for one evening and suddenly my entire luxury living is over.”

Rio crosses her arms, watching her with an expression that’s equal parts unimpressed and fond. “I left you alone for one evening and you decided you’d audition for Fast & Furious. Not cool, kid.”

Rae cracks a smile despite herself.

Rio sighs, then leans down to press a kiss to the top of her daughter's head. “I love you too much to let you scare me like that.”

Rae softens instantly, curling into her side. “I know,” She pouts. “I’m sorry, mami.”

She makes way, moving to the side as Rio joins her on the couch.

Rio wraps an arm around her without hesitation, pulling her close. “You’re brilliant in about a hundred different ways.” She says, amused. “But, you’re an aggressively bad driver.”

Rae groans into her shoulder. “That’s what I don’t get. I’m smart. Like, objectively. I can do calculus, physics, and biology. I can easily memorize scripts and long monologues!” She complains with exaggerated hand gestures. “Why am I bad at cars?”

If being bad at something is genetic, Rae privately decides this one’s on Agatha. 

She’s blaming her.

Not that she knows if Agatha is bad at driving. She doesn’t know Agatha like that. She might never know Agatha like that. Which is fine. Totally fine. Probably for the best.

They sit in silence for a moment, the kind that isn’t uncomfortable but definitely isn’t empty either. Rio is watching Rae with that look—the one that means she already knows something and is deciding how to bring it up carefully.

“Rae?” Rio calls.

“Mhmm?”

“You haven’t been entirely honest with me lately, have you?”

Rae bolts upright like she’s been struck by lightning. Guilt flashes across her face at record speed. “Okay, listen. Before you say anything, I may or may not have misplaced the twenty grand ring you got me, but I swear it’s in my room. I’ve looked everywhere and I will continue looking until I find it. If worst comes to worst, I’ll pick up extra shifts and—”

“That’s not it.” Rio says calmly.

Rae pauses. “.. But we are still circling back to the ring later, right?”

“Oh, absolutely.” Rio replies. “But that’s not what I’m talking about right now.”

Rae squints. “Then what else? I think I’ve been pretty honest. Like.. real honest. Pinocchio level honesty, except I’m better than him.”

Rio doesn’t laugh.

She just looks at Rae directly and says, “You met her.”

Rae freezes.

“I met who?”

“Agatha.”

And there it is. The secret. The one Rae has been carefully folding up and stuffing into the back of her brain.

When Rae met Agatha at the restaurant, she made the staff swear to secrecy that she’d never been there that night. No slip-ups and accidental mentions. 

No, hey mami, guess who I met while serving tables.

Not because she wanted to lie to Rio, but because she didn’t want to hurt her. Because she didn’t want it to sound like she was searching. Or reaching. Or replacing.

Even if Rio said it wouldn’t hurt, Rae wasn’t willing to test that.

“How’d you know?” Rae asks quietly.

“She told me.” Rio admits.

Rae’s head snaps up instantly. “You met her?”

“Yes.”

“When?”

“The morning after you did.”

“What?” Rae squeaks. “Why didn’t you tell me?”

Rio sighs. “Because I didn’t know how. And because I didn’t want to hurt you.” She pauses. “I’m sorry.”

Rae swallows. “Does she know you’re my mom?”

“No.” Rio whispers. “She doesn’t.”

“But she brought me up, didn’t she?”

Rio hesitates, then nods. “At dinner.”

Rae’s eyes widened at the admission. “You had dinner with her?” Her voice rises a pitch higher once more. “Mami, respectfully.. why would you do that? She's an evil incarnate. You might combust being in the same room as her.”

“Don’t be dramatic.” Rio says, waving a hand. “We both have some explaining to do. You especially. So you’re up. Start talking.”

Rae groans but caves, recounting everything—her encounter with Agatha at the restaurant, revealing she’s the daughter, and seeing each other again at the workshop. 

When she gets to the part where she tells Rio she’ll be seeing Agatha four times a week, Rio is already rubbing her face in obvious distress.

“You’re telling me..” Rio says slowly, “That you’re voluntarily spending multiple days a week with Agatha Harkness?”

“I can handle myself.” Rae insists. “Now it’s your turn. Why are you seeing her?”

Rio explains honestly. The post run meetup, Instagram messages, and soup delivery. Rae looks personally offended when she tells her about the dinner as well.

“I wanted to meet her first, I wanted to know her.” Rio says softly, letting her hands rest on Rae’s. “Before she entered your life in any real way. Without bias. Tho, I should’ve told you sooner.”

Rae blinks, processing it. She appreciated the thought. She really did, but that didn’t stop her from rolling her eyes.

“So, what do you think of her?”

Rio hesitates at first, searching for words. “She’s.. quite the woman.”

Rae didn’t miss a beat. “She’s a bitch.”

“Language.” Rio’s eyebrows shot up. “And you say that, but you’re still going to her workshop.”

“It’s a good opportunity, mami.” Rae claims. “Besides, I told you I can handle myself. I can be meaner if I want to.”

Rio smiles, already knowing she can. “Just.. don’t be too mean. We don’t know the full story yet.”

Rae huffs but nods, relenting for her mom’s sake. “I can’t promise anything, but if she gets in my way—”

“Raina.” She knows Rio means business when she calls her that. “Tone down the threats.”

“Fine, fine! I’ll try to be nice.”

Rae rolls her eyes dramatically once more. “She’s still a bitch, though. Please don’t hang out with her.”

They sit quietly for a moment, then Rae says, “You know, she’s not as tall as she looks on TV.”

“Sure.” Rio suppresses a grin.

“And she’s really the same as on the news. The sarcastic interviews and press conferences…”

“I guess?” 

Rae sighs, exasperated but admitting defeat. “I can’t believe I’m saying this, but she’s.. way prettier in person. The camera doesn’t do her justice.” She feels her tongue burning by complimenting Agatha. “Still a bitch, though.”

Rio genuinely laughs this time, then shakes her head. “I agree.”

Rae arches a brow. “You agree that she’s a bitch?”

“No, silly.” Rio pokes Rae’s nose. “I agree that she’s really beautiful. On TV.. and certainly in person.”

Rae tries to ignore it, but the smile on Rio’s face was unmistakable. Rae has to fight the urge to roll her eyes again. “Yeah, okay.. you’re impossible, mami.”

Rio simply squeezes her hand. “And you love me for it.”

Chapter 7: Chapter 7

Chapter Notes

thank you for patiently waiting :p this is the longest chapter so i apologize for the mistakes you might see along the way (should there be any???) i'm in a daze i fear but i hope you enjoy this ride nonetheless

See the end of the chapter for more notes

riovidal: hey, can we talk?

riovidal: there’s something important i would like to discuss with you

riovidal: please let me know when you’re free 

Well, that was ominous.

Agatha raises a brow, lips curling slightly at the word important.

Her brain immediately starts drafting worst-case scenarios because, what exactly is there to talk about with Rio?

As far as Agatha could recall, dinner had been marvelous.. which obviously meant something terrible was coming next. The universe simply never allows her to enjoy things without consequences, doesn’t it?

Still, the other night was fantastic. It could’ve gone further too, if Rio hadn’t been summoned home early. Nothing bad had happened on her end. It was pleasant and fun and comfortable.

So, why did important sound like a threat?

Is it going to be a confession? A polite we should stop seeing each other speech? A surprise child she didn’t know about?

Surely it’s not that last one. She already knew about Rio’s kid.

Ironically, Rio is the one blissfully unaware she is hanging out with a woman who technically has a secret child of her own.

“I’m pretty sure our parents aren’t paying a ridiculous amount of money just for our so-called mentors to doomscroll through class.” Agatha bit her lower lip, dropping her phone onto the desk the second she hears that familiar voice, followed by her footsteps.

She looks up and watches as Rae breezes in as if she’s entering a runway rather than a classroom. Red turtleneck, plaid miniskirt, and a matching headband. The whole thing screams teen rom-com protagonist. 

Although knowing Rae, she might actually be more fitting for an antagonist role. Either way, Agatha believes she’s flexible.

Agatha squints her eyes and shamelessly asses Rae from head to toe. “Were you allowed to watch Clueless for the first time, or is this a cry for help?”

“Wouldn’t you like to know?”

Agatha dismisses her as she gestures vaguely at the clock. “Well, class doesn’t start until ten. It’s barely nine. You could’ve been sleeping or doing what is it that you do such as committing minor crimes.”

“What can I say?” Rae shrugs, smug as ever. “I’m a professional.”

“Professional what?” 

“Multitasker.” Rae grins, enunciating her words with her usual dramatic flare. “Obviously.”

Agatha knows exactly why the kid is early. This is her strategic masterplan beyond her ambition and dedication to learn. It gives Rae extra time to torture her, and she’s clearly clocked in for overtime today.

“Arriving an hour early isn’t as impressive as people think.”

“Sure it isn’t.” Rae says sweetly, pulling out a chair adjacent to Agatha’s. “But it gives me more time with my mommy, and that’s the real reward.”

Agatha groans, slumping dramatically. “My worst fear, actually.”

“Aren’t you a doll?” Rae deadpans.

“If I was,” Agatha quickly shoots back, “I’d be Annabelle.”

That pulls a genuine laugh out of Rae. “I admire your self-awareness. Good job.”

Agatha tries her best not to smile from the compliment, deciding to shift the conversation in a haze. “Did you terrorize an Uber driver on your way here?”

“My mami gave me a ride, actually.” Rae explains. “She wanted to stop by and meet you, but she had some meeting she couldn’t skip so, rain check, I guess.”

Agatha freezes for half a second.

“Oh,” She mutters, far too casually. “That’s.. great. Fantastic, even! I just love spontaneous parent introductions before lunch.”

She says that with pure sarcasm but deep inside, she’s already spiraling.

As much as she owes that woman everything, Agatha has absolutely no idea what she’d do if they actually met. Yet.

She forces a smirk to rebuild her snark and confidence, to show Rae that it didn’t affect her at all. “Tell your mami I’m devastatingly charming in person. Build the anticipation if you must.”

Rae snorts. “Yeah, no.”

“That’s rude.”

“You’re rude.”

Agatha places a hand over her chest in mock offense. “I am a cultural icon, do not disrespect me.”

Rae rolls her eyes so hard it’s a miracle they don’t get stuck. “Whatever helps you sleep at night, Harkness.”

Agatha was taken aback. It was the first time Rae uses her last name like that, as if she’s throwing darts and enjoying the aim. Agatha decides she liked it.

Silence settles between them, cautious but not uncomfortable. Rae takes out her kindle and starts reading, while Agatha scrolls through her phone some more, checking emails and replying to unread messages.

For a brief moment, everything almost feels normal, without either of them trying to start a verbal sparring to the other.

Eventually, the studio door swings open and Lilia claps her hands loudly as a group of kids follow behind.

“Alright, little thespians! Phones away, bags down, egos checked at the door.” She announces. “You too, Agatha.”

“Wow.” Agatha mutters. “Singled out again. Story of my life.”

Rae snickers and heads toward the circle of chairs forming in the middle of the room. Agatha follows, sliding into her usual seat like she owns the place. Technically, she kind of does. Her name on the new brochure definitely helps.

The room slowly fills with voices of kids of all ages. Awkward preteens, overconfident teens, and a six-year-old who looks like he wandered in by mistake. Everyone buzzes with nervous energy and excitement.

Lilia claps again. “Today, we’re doing monologues. Volunteers?”

Silence.

Agatha leans back with her hands under her chin, clearly enjoying the tension and the energy like it is premium entertainment.

A teen near the front timidly raises his hand. He’s probably around twelve with freckles across his nose.

“My man.” Agatha murmurs in approval.

The boy stands, hands shaking. “Uh.. this is from.. Um, a movie.”

“Groundbreaking.” Agatha receives an elbow and a glare from Lilia due to the comment.

He starts—stiff at first, voice cracking. It’s a dramatic scene about losing a friend. A few lines in, he falters.

Agatha straightens in her chair, her expression softening. “Breath, sweetheart.” She says. “Don’t rush yourself. Take your time.”

The boy looks at her, surprised, then nods and continues. His voice steadies as motion and adrenaline finally creeps in. His performance is not perfect, but it’s honest.

When he finishes, there’s a pause. Agatha made sure to clap first. It’s not even polite clapping. It is a full on unapologetic applause.

“Yes!” She says. “That was raw. You didn’t rush it like I told you to. You sat in the feeling which is hard to do at your age.”

The boy beams from her comment.

“Great feedback, Agatha.” Lilia smiles and continues to share her own thoughts with the entire class.

Behind it all, Rae stays quiet.

She doesn’t clap immediately. Not because she doesn’t think he did well. He did, but it’s more because Agatha’s attention feels.. a lot to that boy. It seems like there’s a spotlight Rae isn’t standing in.

She claps eventually when Lilia concludes with her statement.

The next volunteer goes up. A girl Rae’s age. She is confident and has a long red hair. She performs a comedic piece, a contrast from the first kid. Both mentors were laughing loudly at all the right moments during the entirety of her piece.

Rae watches Agatha instead of the girl.

It’s stupid, she knows. It’s petty. But something twists in her chest anyway.

Why does it bother her?

Agatha isn’t anyone to her. She’s just.. Agatha. A nobody in Rae’s life.

And yet, why is she feeling this way?

When the girl finishes, Agatha stands halfway out of her chair. “Phenomenal timing. You could do sitcoms, kid.”

The class went on until Rae’s name is called. “Okay.” Lilia says, “Rae, you’re up.”

Rae tenses in her chair before standing up.

Agatha turns, eyebrows raised. “What? Nervous now?”

“Shut up.” Rae hisses at her, pretending she's not absolutely worried about being judged by Agatha herself.

She starts her monologue, which is angrier and sharper. It's about betrayal, about not being chosen, which is almost intentional considering their situation.

During her piece, her eyes flick to Agatha without meaning to. Agatha’s face is unreadable, which makes it worse.

Rae powers through her performance and finishes strong. Agatha doesn’t clap immediately unlike she did when other kids performed, and that made Rae’s heart sink.

Finally, there it was. The applause came not only from Agatha and Lilia, but the other kids as well.

Rae could’ve sworn Agatha’s clap isn’t as loud, but who’s keeping score, honestly?

“Good.” Agatha says. “Really good. You’ve got bite, but don’t hide behind it.”

Rae nods at that comment, her jaw tight.

“Next time,” Agatha adds, “Don’t protect the character so much. Let her be messy, let her be hurt. Allow yourself to feel more.

Rae forces a shrug. “Yeah. Whatever.” She goes back to her seat and tries to remain invisible for the rest of the class, her enthusiasm for the day suddenly faded instantly.

The class continues. More kids, even more feedback, and tips along the way. Agatha keeps engaging and encouraging everyone, teaching them how to control their faces or what posture helps more. Rae remains quiet all through out.

During a short break, Agatha sneaks a glance at her phone and finally replies to Rio’s message.

agathaharkness: Define important.

Three dots appear immediately, as if Rio is waiting for her reply the entire time

riovidal: it’s nothing bad

riovidal: i think

riovidal: i just want to talk in person about it

Agatha frowns.

agathaharkness: That is somehow more terrifying.

This time, no response came from Rio.

Agatha sighs and slips the phone back into her pocket just as Lilia calls them back for the class to resume.

When it ended, Agatha noticed that Rae feels.. off.

She packs up quietly. She didn’t pester Agatha, she even went to join Lilia’s circle when they had a group activity earlier instead of Agatha’s.

This time, she doesn’t linger. She didn’t throw snarky comments like usual, which feels oddly not Rae.

“Hey.” Agatha approaches her before she leaves, and before she changes her mind about it. “You good?”

“Fine.”

“That’s convincing.”

Rae didn’t say more as she glares at Agatha before walking away.

Agatha watches her go, wondering what that kid’s problem is.

They were fine earlier, weren’t they? At least fine as they could be.

She replays the class in her head. The way she cheered for everyone, the way she focused on other kids. Now that she thinks about it, she barely interacted with Rae.

Did she somehow made Rae feel invisible?

Fuck. That thought hurts more than she expects.

Agatha thinks better of it and decides to run, following Rae. “You did great today.” She calls, walking behind the kid.

“You say that to everyone.” Rae mutters without looking back.

“Yeah, but I meant it more for you.”

Rae stops in her tracks and finally faces Agatha. “You don’t have to. I’m not asking for special treatment.”

Agatha swallows. “I know. I just.. care.”

Rae rolls her eyes once more as if that’s the most absurd thing she’s heard today, then leaves.

Agatha simply stands there, staring at her figure gradually disappearing from her sight.

For the first time, it really sinks in—she’s been treating Rae like just another student. Worst, she’s not paying attention at all. It’s like Rae is someone she has to keep distance from and stay careful around.

But Rae isn’t just a student.

She’s her daughter.

Albeit not confirmed, Agatha can’t think of her as anything but.

And the mere idea that Rae might feel overlooked by her sits heavy in her chest.

She vowed to never become the kind of mother she had growing up. 

Maybe some things are inevitable, no matter how hard you try to avoid it.

She feels sick to her stomach by just thinking about it.

Later that day, Agatha meets Jen at a café that looks like it was designed by someone who drinks celery juice before bed. Everything is beige, the menu is written in cursive, and the barista has a nose ring and an attitude.

She already hates it.

Jen is seated by the window, sunglasses still on despite being indoors, laptop open while aggressively typing like she’s arguing with trolls online. There’s an empty espresso cup beside her and three unopened sugar packets she clearly didn’t use.

“You should do a background-check on the barista, he looks suspicious.” Agatha tells her as she drops into the chair across from her friend.

Jen doesn’t miss a beat. “Give me five minutes.”

Agatha rolls her eyes and orders a black coffee because she is bitter, committed to it, and refuses to be perceived as someone who orders oat milk. When it arrives, she doesn’t touch it. 

She watches Jen type with her long nails. Seriously, how can anyone do anything with those?

“Why do you look like you’re about to tell me I’m banned from award shows?” Agatha asks.

Jen finally looks up. “That would actually make this easier.”

“Jenny Kale.” Agatha utters her name, almost a plea that she should get to the point.

Jen closes her laptop deliberately, preparing for impact. “Okay. So I went to the adoption agency.”

Agatha stiffens. She didn't expect it would be that fast. “What did you find?”

“I didn’t break in, if you’re wondering.” Jen says quickly. “I went legally with lawyers I told you about. They were sworn to secrecy, literally.”

“Of course they are.”

“They still had archived records.” Jen continues. “Not public, obviously. But once we presented documentation such as birth year, location, hospital—you’d be surprised how cooperative people get when they see legal letterhead.”

Agatha stares. “You’re terrifying.”

“Thank you.” Then, Jen exhales. “We had to go through sealed files, court approvals, old social worker records. It took a while, but..”

She pauses.

Agatha’s heart starts slapping her ribs with the revelation about to unfold.

“But,” Jen repeats, softer this time. “It’s her.”

Agatha freezes. Her fingers curl around her pendant immediately to ground herself.

Jen meets her eyes, and something in her expression shifts. The usual sarcasm fades, replaced by something careful. Gentle as she can be like she’s about to step on glass.

“Her name is Raina.” Jen says quietly. “She was born sixteen years ago. Her adoption is finalized in Westview.”

Agatha’s pulse starts to roar in her ears, loud and fast. Her body already knows what’s coming before her brain catches up.

“Biological mother—Agatha Harkness.”

Of course it is her. It has always been her, no matter how hard she tried to deny it, no matter how many excuses she built around the truth.

Rae really is hers.

Her blood and flesh.

Her daughter.

Her’s.

“You’re sure?” Agatha asks, even though she already knows the answer. Even though her heart has accepted it long before her mind did.

Jen nods. “I triple-checked.”

Of course she did, Agatha thinks. Of course the universe wouldn’t leave her room to pretend.

Agatha lets out a shaky breath, the kind that feels like it’s been trapped in her lungs for years. “So.. it’s real. She’s really my daughter.”

The word tastes strange in her mouth after saying it aloud.

“Very real.” Jen confirms.

Agatha stares at the table. Her reflection in the polished wood looks younger. She almost looks scared. Gone are the confidence and her usual bite. Right now, she looks human in a way she doesn’t like.

“She hates me.” Agatha whispers.

“She doesn’t know you.”

“Even worse. Teenagers smell cowardly weakness, it’s their specialty.”

Jen stays quiet, letting the space fill with Agatha’s thoughts. With every sarcastic remark, every eye roll, every unnecessary jab she threw at Rae without thinking, it all flashes in her mind at this very moment.

Agatha breathes slowly. “I deserved the way she treats me.” She admits, staring at nothing in particular. “I was.. awful to her. I was genuinely unpleasant to my own child.”

Jen hums. “You’re mean to everyone.”

“Mean is generous.”

“Well then you’re a bitch, sure.” Jen says matter-of-factly, “But I don’t think it came from nowhere.”

Agatha’s lips twitch. “Oh? Enlighten me.”

“I think you were scared.” Jen assumes. “You're terrified. So you did what you always do, you turned it into a personality.”

Agatha swallows. In a way, Jen's not wrong.

“At first I didn’t want to do anything with her.” Agatha murmurs. “I didn’t want to see myself in her, I didn’t want to care.”

“But you did.” Jen supplies.

Agatha closes her eyes. God help her, she did.

“Yeah,” She whispers. “I really did.”

Then came more worries. What if she ruin her? What if she already messed it up?”

Jen reaches across the table and squeezes her hand. “You were twenty-five living under your cunt of a mother’s roof. You made the choice you thought would protect her.”

Agatha smiles, but it's a sad one. “I don’t even remember her face as a baby. Isn’t that horrible?”

“No.” Jen shrugs. “It’s honest.”

This time, she lets out a breathy laugh. “She rolls her eyes exactly like me. Clearly, it’s genetic. God forbid I pass on something useful like my memorization skills.” Though she wouldn't know if Rae is good at something. 

How could she?

“She’s smart.”

“Of course she is. The universe wouldn’t let me have a dumb kid.” Then, to try ease the heavy tension in her chest, she blurts, “Can you imagine me at a PTA meeting?” 

Jen cackles. “You’d definitely start a feud with the bake sale lady.”

“She used boxed mix. That is unforgivable and punishable by law.”

They laugh at that.

Agatha wipes her eyes. It’s tears from confirming who Rae really is masked by something else. “So it’s really her. Huh.”

“Yeah.” Jen smiles. “It’s really your kid.”

Agatha presses a hand to her chest. “I made a human who is now a hormonal teenager.”

“Terrifying.”

Agatha chuckles, then goes quiet. “I don’t know how to be her mom.” She admits.

“You’re already her mom in other ways, Agatha.”

“I’m gonna screw this up.”

“Probably.”

“Thanks for the encouragement, you bitch.”

“But you’ll try.”

“Yeah..” Agatha finds herself nodding absentmindedly with that statement. She doesn’t know how, but she knows she’ll do it. “I will.”

They drifted into conversation of what Agatha should do next, though the truth was she had no plan at all. 

Moreso, she has no idea what to do next so Jen didn’t push. Until then, they can settle for what they know for now and what they have.

They circled back to Rae, and Agatha found herself dwelling there, talking about her daughter with a mix of awe, guilt, and the tiniest bit of hope tucked between her words, savoring the fact that for once she could think of and speak of Rae without immediately flinching.

At one point, Jen hesitates, clearly about to mention Rae’s adoptive parents, but Agatha shakes her head before the words can land. She’s not ready to put another face to the ache yet. 

Again, Jen didn’t want to push so reaches into her bag and hands her an envelope instead. 

Agatha takes it carefully, like it might break or break her, and tucks it under her arm without opening it, deciding she can survive one truth at a time.

Night came, and the town moved on like nothing had shattered inside Agatha’s chest. 

The world didn’t pause for anyone, not even for someone who felt she is entitled for a pause after everything that she’s been through.

Agatha finds herself in the Westview outlet. She’s wrapped in a long black coat despite the mild weather, oversized scarf hiding half her face, and a dark sunglasses to cover her eyes. 

She keeps her head down, weaving through tourists and bored teenagers, praying no one recognizes her.

She just wanted to walk and to breath air without paparazzis following her around.

She almost never gets to do that when she’s in LA.

Then of course, essentially the universe throws a joke at her as if it isn’t enough yet.

She freezes mid-step when she spots a familiar posture near the jewelry kiosk. She would recognize that stiff shoulders and the sharp profile anywhere. Additionally, there’s a black smoke following her around and a pair of horns on top of her head that only Agatha can see.

Evanora.

Her mother.

Agatha’s soul leaves her body for a full second. She hasn’t seen her or got in contact with Evanora in the past decade and she would gladly like to keep it that way.

“Absolutely not.” She mutters under her breath.

She ducks behind a taco stand so fast she nearly bump her head. Her heart pounds while she peeks through the display. 

Evanora looks the same as ever—meaning, she looks like an old hag with wrinkles no amount of botox can fix.

Agatha waits until she disappears into a boutique before moving again. She won’t deal with that cunt unless she absolutely has to which translates to: never.

For now, the crisis has been successfully avoided. Agatha exhales in relief and abruptly, she nearly walks straight into Rae.

Fucking hell. Is there some sort of Harkness reunion happening that she doesn’t know of tonight?

The kid is holding several shopping bags with designer logos. She’s changed her clothes too because apparently, one outfit a day is not enough for her.

Agatha can relate, so she takes note of that.

“Well, damn.” She murmurs to herself. “My daughter is loaded.”

She watches from a distance as Rae scrolls through her phone, chewing gum while walking.

Agatha’s brain spirals immediately upon realizing what she’s doing.

Here she is sneaking around like a raccoon, observing her daughter who is casually carrying bags on a random thursday which is probably worth more than a car.

“Guess the adoption agency really upgraded you.” 

She considers leaving. She should leave—must leave, but guilt is louder than common sense.

She figures she might apologize to Rae again for what she has done earlier. Heck, for what she has done the past sixteen years if she were being honest.

So Agatha follows her at a safe distance while rehearsing the apologies in her head.

I’m sorry I panicked.
I’m sorry I’m emotionally constipated.

I'm sorry I didn't know earlier.

I should have known.

She’s just about to speed up and call Rae when she accidentally collides with someone else, making her stop in her tracks.

“Jesus—” Agatha snaps, steadying herself.

“Agatha?”

She knows that voice. Rio.

There she is in casual clothes, hair loose, and a small smile on her lips showing her gap tooth.

Agatha’s brain short-circuits at the thought of the woman before her.

“Oh,” She gasps. “You.”

Rio laughs. “Wow, that’s a warm welcome.”

“What are you doing here?” Agatha asks, which she realizes is stupid after it went out of her mouth.

Rio dodges the questions and points at her scarf and sunglasses insead. “Are you in witness protection?”

“Incognito.” Agatha corrects, removing her eyewear to avoid being rude. “It’s a lifestyle.”

Rio’s smile falters slightly. Not obvious, but Agatha sure notices it.

Then, she remembers the messages.

Agatha crosses her arms. “So, since fate shoved us together, what’s this important thing you wanted to discuss?”

Rio hesitates as her eyes flick past Agatha’s shoulder.

Agatha looks back consciously but sees nothing unusual. “What?”

Rio clears her throat. “It’s just.. maybe this is not the best place to talk about it.”

“Why?” Agatha inquires. “Are you about to confess you’re secretly married? Or part of the mafia? Don't tell me you're a serial killer.”

“No..”

Before Agatha can push past the awkward tension, another familiar voice cuts through the air. “Well, isn't it a small world we live in.”

Rae. Of course. 

Agatha turns slowly, almost ceremoniously, to face her daughter. 

Rae stands there, smirk locked, designer shopping bags dangling from her arms like shiny little trophies. She tilts her head between the adults, her eyes glinting with suspicious delight, the kind of look that says she already knows exactly what chaos she’s stirring.

My kid. Agatha thinks. My actual kid. She’s.. enormous. Not physically, thank God, but somehow she already occupies all the chambers of Agatha’s heart.

“Didn’t expect to see you two bonding.” Rae says, voice sweet but sharp, perfectly timed. “What is this, a crossover episode?”

Agatha opens her mouth, tries to say something, but no single syllable comes out.

Rae steps closer, locking her free arm with Rio’s, and Agatha’s stomach drops.

“This is my mami.” Rae announces. “She’s the one who took me in after you gave me away.”

Her eyes are bright with mischief and challenge as she continues, “You’ve met her, obviously.”

Agatha’s brain explodes in slow motion.

Mami. 

Rae’s mami, is Rio?

Suddenly, it clicked. It's a puzzle piece snapping into place, painfully obvious in hindsight. 

She remembers the first time she met Rio—how tense she had seemed, how she always looked like she was about to say something important but somehow held herself back.

And then, there's Raina.

Jen had said the name. She’d mentioned it casually, and Agatha had been too distracted by the whirlwind of her own emotions to notice. She was too focused to realize that Rae’s real name.. the one buried in papers, was in fact Raina.

The same Raina Rio had been on the phone the other night.

How could she have been so stupid?

Her throat tightens and her lips twitch. She wants to scream, to laugh, to run, and stay still all at once. Meaning, she doesn’t know what to do.

Rio stiffens beside her, and Agatha sees it. The protective weight she carries, the careful boundaries that just shifted a little under Rae’s small hand. 

She’s.. maternal.

“Oh.” Agatha finally breathes. “You have got to be kidding me.”

Rae tilts her head. “Excuse me?”

Agatha laughs. “Nothing. The universe really has jokes set out on me.”

Rio looks panicked. “Agatha—”

“So,” Agatha cuts in, voice steady despite the sudden weight in her chest, “This is why you wanted to talk.”

Her eyes flick back to Rio. The flirting. The soup. The dinner. The way she’d been drawn in without realizing it.

Her daughter’s mother.

Her chest tightens more as time goes on. It feels like someone shoved a fist inside and refused to let go.

Her brain keeps repeating it like a chant. Her daughter’s mother.

Rae’s mami.

Of course the universe has its twist. Because, why wouldn’t the woman she’s been casually flirting with, be the person who raised her kid?

Agatha laughs again, quieter this time, the sound lighter but still tinged with disbelief.

Rio swallows. “Agatha, I didn’t—I mean, I wanted to tell you, I just.. there was never a right moment.”

There is never a right moment to tell someone you’ve been flirting with that you’re their daughter’s adoptive mother, but sure.

Rio steps closer, cautious, like Agatha might spook. “She’s a good kid.”

“Sure.” Agatha says, crossing her arms like she needs the barrier, “You’re rich, you cook, and you raised her. That’s quite the résumé you’ve got there.”

Rio lets out a small, awkward laugh, rubbing the back of her neck. “When you say it like that, I sound like a superhero.”

She straightens her posture as she’s about to say something else—something that might actually matter but Rae steps in front of her like a human barricade.

The way she moves is almost defensive, as if she’s shielding her mami from Agatha.

Agatha tries not to let that get into her head.

“Okay.” Rae says, clapping her hands once. “We’re done here.”

Rio blinks. “We are?”

“Come on, mami.” Rae begins to pull Rio away. “You promised we’d get boba. And I am emotionally unstable without sugar.”

Rio hesitates, eyes flicking back to Agatha, something unsaid hanging between them. “Rae—”

“Mami, please.” Rae insists, yanking Rio’s arm harder. “Let’s leave now before we corrupt our minds by hanging too much with her.”

She shoots Agatha a look. A guarded one, like she’s already built a protective wall between them.

Agatha watches it happen. The casual way Rae leans into her. The way Rio automatically adjusts her grip on the shopping bags so Rae doesn’t have to carry them. The way their bodies already know each other’s rhythms.

Rae meets her gaze. “Don’t get any ideas. This sudden meetup isn’t a weekly thing.”

Agatha forces a half-smile. “Heartbroken already.”

“Good.” Rae replies flatly. “Stay that way.”

Rae pulls Rio away decisively, like she’s afraid staying any longer might mean something. Rio glances back, hesitates, then mouths a small, apologetic bye.

They disappear into the crowd, blending in like every other mother and daughter in the mall. They continue living a life Agatha only knows from a distance.

While Agatha stays where she is, hands in her pockets, sixteen years crashing into her chest all at once.

Back in the quiet comfort of Lilias’ guest bedroom, Agatha finally lets herself stop pretending she’s fine.

Rae is her daughter.

The words don’t feel real yet. They float around her head like something from a bad script she hasn’t memorized. 

She lost sixteen years of her daughter’s life.

Missed birthdays. Missed scraped knees. Missed first crushes and first heartbreaks and every tiny moment in between.

And of course, there’s Rio. The beloved mami. Rae’s mami.

Agatha presses her lips together like she can physically keep that word from sinking in. The way Rae said it is natural and easy, she made it seem like it is the safest word she knows.

And maybe it really is.

She sits on the edge of the bed and stares at her hands. The same hands that once held a newborn she was too scared to keep. The same hands that just hours ago were shoved into her coat pockets while her daughter walked away with someone else.

This is your doing, she tells herself. You chose this.

Her chest aches in a quiet, persistent way. It reminds her that this isn’t something she can joke her way out of.

A few minutes in and her phone buzzes.

Speaking of. She receive a message from Rio on instagram. 

She doesn’t open it right away. She lets it sit, she refuse to look desperate on Rio’s end when she replies quickly.

Eventually, she opens the notification.

riovidal: i know i should’ve told you sooner

riovidal: i’m sorry

Her thumbs hover over the screen as she types, deletes, types again, and deletes again.

Every sentence feels wrong. Frankly, she doesn’t know what to say.

Agatha isn’t sure what she’s feeling toward Rio, and that somehow makes it worse. 

A hint of anger sits there for keeping her in the dark, but it doesn’t burn the way she expects it to. It just simmers quietly as she wonder where to put it.

Why did Rio hide it from her? Does she have hidden agenda? Or was she simply protecting Rae?

Or maybe.. she was protecting Agatha, sparing her from a truth she wasn’t ready to face. 

Agatha turns the questions over in her head again and again. She tells herself that if she finds the right angle, it’ll finally make sense.

And then there’s the flirting. God. It feels wrong now. She crossed a line she didn’t even know existed. 

In the end, she locks her phone and tosses it onto the bed beside her.

She settles with silence. No reply.

Not tonight.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 8: Chapter 8

Chapter Notes

i have made it a task to challenge myself: the next chapter should be longer than the last one. this is longer than the previous chapter so i hope you enjoy this treat (plz do enjoy it. seriously)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

An uneventful week passes since the incident (Or the Harkness reunion, unbeknownst to the people involved except Agatha) occurred.

Rio doesn’t push. And annoyingly, that’s a relief.

Agatha hasn’t heard from her since leaving her on read in those Instagram DMs. She admits she’s sort of surprised to see no follow-ups such as a simple, “Hey, just checking in,” message the morning after.

Agatha honestly thought Rio would be the type to do something small but intentional. From what little she thought she knew, Rio seemed like that kind of woman.

Clearly, she was wrong.

Then again, did she actually know Rio at all? The woman couldn’t even bring herself to say she was her daughter’s adoptive mother. That feels like a pretty major detail to skip over.

Sure. Who’s holding a grudge? Not Agatha. Definitely not her. 

She has proclaimed herself to be an expert when it comes to emotional constipation and betrayal.

She tells herself it’s for the best.

Getting tangled up with Rio would only complicate things. Her relationship with Rae is already hanging by a thread so thin it might as well be nonexistent. The last thing she needs is to step on a landmine by getting involved with her daughter’s mami—especially when said daughter is clearly ready to throw hands if anyone even looks at her mami wrong.

And as much as she seems to enjoy messing with Rae over petty things, she’s well aware that it’s a line she couldn't cross. She will not attempt messing with her mami.

Along with that, she manages to convince herself this is maturity. This is the kind of growth and self-control she must apply in her life more as a functional adult.

But then, that stupid little voice in her head simply would not stop talking: Wow, she dropped you fast. Guess you were forgettable, after all.

Agatha finds offense at that.

She’s Agatha Harkness, for fuck’s sake. She’s anything but unforgettable.

Still.. deny it as she might, it does stings. Just a little. 

She tries to be fair about it. She tries to justify Rio’s actions by putting herself on the other woman’s shoes.

Maybe Rio reached the same conclusion Agatha did, just faster and with less emotional spiraling. Maybe she decided Rae comes first, no matter what. And maybe, through some weird unspoken agreement, they’ve both decided to back off for the kid’s sake.

Unconscious telepathy: coparenting edition, though they’re actually not coparenting in any sense. Still, Agatha finds humor in her situation.

Above all, she’d be lying if she said she didn’t miss it. With the brief time spent together, the easy banters and flirting felt harmless in the moment. For a second there, she’d felt someone saw past the armor she had long created and didn’t immediately run.

Shame it had to end so fast, and shame at herself to have enjoyed it at all.

Rae, on the other hand, had very clearly been avoiding her.

The kid still participated actively in class. She excels as usual, volunteers to be the first to perform at almost every activity—but she only ever directed her attention at Lilia. 

With Agatha, it was strictly professional. They only converse when it’s time for feedback, and even then Rae simply nods or hums at whatever she says. 

Gone are the banter and side comments. She even refuses eye contact longer than necessary. Every time Agatha tried to approach her, Rae drifted away like she’d rehearsed it.

The only time Rae acknowledged Agatha was when she came in late, coffee splashed down her blouse after an incident at the café outside her neighborhood that involves one clumsy barista.

When she arrived, her eyes had met Rae’s across a sea of students. She didn’t miss the way Rae had snickered.

The kid looks delighted. She was absolutely thriving at Agatha’s public humiliation.

Agatha would take that. She’d take anything. Even a verbal assassination, if Rae felt like offering one. At least it meant the kid was still looking at her.

It’s a strange kind of internal shame. Now that she knows Rae is her daughter, Rae seems to find every possible way to slip through her fingers. She keeps distance as if getting close to Agatha might somehow hurt her.

Agatha would never hurt her.. She would never.

She gave her up so Rae wouldn’t be hurt. That was the whole point. It is the logic she clings to and the sacrifice she bleeds from.

Still, it feels odd. To be in the same vicinity with Rae without any sarcastic comebacks does something to her heart. It aches, in a way.

She misses her daughter, she absolutely does.

Not being able to admit that part out loud is a different level of shame.

“Wanda’s the redhead, right?” Jen asks, flipping through music on the radio while Agatha drives, eyes fixed on the road. “Isn’t she the one you said lives a pretentious suburban life with her husband and two kids?”

Agatha scoffs. She did say that, and she wasn’t entirely wrong. “Ex-husband.” She corrects. “The divorce got finalized earlier this year. Or was it last year? Doesn’t matter.”

Wanda had sent her an invite for a small housewarming party. Apparently, she’d just bought a new place, and after finding out Agatha was in town, she made sure to reach out. 

Typical Wanda Maximoff. She’s polite, thoughtful, and always trying to keep old connections alive.

They’d met when Agatha was just starting out in showbiz. Wanda had been a casting director on one of her early films. They bonded over being from the same nowhere town of Westview and their mutual hatred at a certain Tony Starks from the industry.

Agatha wouldn’t say they were tight. Not really. They drifted once Wanda’s kids were old enough for school and her personality-less husband decided they should move back to Westview. 

Wanda became a housewife. She settled into that picture-perfect-pretentious suburban life Agatha loved to mock.

They texted sometimes, never missing each other’s birthdays. Agatha sends gifts to her sons on christmas, which is always money or gift cards. They grabbed lunch whenever Wanda flew to L.A., which wasn’t often. Still, Agatha considers her one of her oldest friends, even with the distance and the years in between.

“I love that for her.” Jen sighs, finally settling back into her seat. “I could never imagine myself with a man. Women, on the other hand, think I’m too difficult. At this rate, I’ll probably die alone with no spouse and no kids.”

Agatha snorts, because honestly? Same. Rae is her daughter, yes, but not technically hers. And tying herself down to anyone in the near future sounds about as appealing as jury duty. 

So really, they’re both doomed in different fonts.

They pull up to the address Wanda sent. They were greeted by a two-story modern house tucked into a quiet neighborhood on the upper side of Westview. Still suburban, just less pretentious now that there’s no husband lurking around.

“Agatha!” Wanda greets them, already tipsy, glass of wine in hand as she rushes out onto the patio. One thing Agatha has always loved about her is that drinking at inappropriate times has never been an issue. “Hon, I’m so glad you made it!”

They share a quick hug. “Happy to be here.” Agatha says, handing over the housewarming gift. It is a basket of supposedly useful nonsense Jen curated. “And if you remember, this is my assistant, Jennifer.”

“Jen.” She corrects with a grin, shaking Wanda’s hand. “Beautiful house, by the way.”

“Thank you!” Wanda beams, then leans in to whisper dramatically, “I think it’s haunted. Got it for twenty percent off the market price. But honestly? As long as people tell me it’s beautiful, I won’t mind living with ghosts.”

They laugh, and Wanda leads them to the backyard where the party is in full swing. A pool, a buffet table, and a balloon arch in blue and pink like someone accidentally booked a baby shower decorator. Knowing Wanda’s whimsy, it was definitely not an accident.

Wanda tries to bring Agatha to meet the twins, but they’ve apparently vanished into the void, so instead she parades her around to other guests who immediately start gushing. Wanda half-heartedly tells them not to smother her, but Agatha secretly enjoys the attention.

As conversations blur together, somewhere between her second glass of wine and a stranger calling her “iconic,” Agatha realizes her phone isn’t with her. 

She probably left it in the car so she excuses herself, leaving Jen happily absorbed in Wanda’s chaotic storytelling.

On her way out, she sees a teen leaning against the front doorway, black scarf wrapped around his neck despite the weather, scribbling in a notebook like he’s drafting his tragic memoir.

There's one of two.

“Well, if it isn’t Bruno..” Agatha says fondly, walking up to him.

The teen looks up, black ink heavy around his eyes, curls falling into his face. Damn. Wanda really raised an emo.

“It’s Billy.” He corrects politely, slipping the notebook into his pocket as he stands. “Nice to see you again, Aunt Agatha.”

Agatha smiles. The twins are a year older than Rae, if she remembers correctly. For a split second, she wonders: if she had raised her.. would Rae be here too?

“No wonder your mom keeps complaining about losing her eyeliner.” Agatha lies. “You clearly stole it all.”

Billy shrugs, grinning. “I appreciate the compliment.”

“Auntie Agatha!” A louder voice calls, followed by its heavy footsteps.

They both turn to see his twin sprinting toward them, sweat all over his body and arms wide open. “Wouldn’t you give your favorite nephew a hug?”

“No.” Agatha deadpans, planting her hand on his face before he can get closer. “God, Timothy. Couldn’t bother changing?”

“I was on the treadmill.” He protests. “And it’s Tommy.”

Agatha knows that. She just enjoys getting it wrong.

The last time she saw them, they were barely eleven. Now they’re towering over her like ungrateful weeds. 

“BTW, the cash you gave me last christmas was fire!” Tommy announces proudly. “Paid for, like, three dates. With three different girls, mind you.”

Agatha winces and looks at Billy instead. “Is something wrong with your brother? You should probably get him checked.”

Billy laughs. “He’s just like that.”

“How long are you staying in town, Auntie?” Tommy asks, rocking on his heels. “We should take you out for dinner. Mom’s friends with this famous chef and her restaurant is absolutely bomb. Reservations are impossible, but we can totally get in. We just have to make sure a certain someone isn’t working when we go.”

Agatha physically shivers at the words chef, restaurant, and reservation. The universe wouldn’t be that cruel, right?

“Yeah.” Billy supplies, eyes widening. “And I think that’s Auntie Rio parking over there.. wait—shit, Tommy. Auntie Rio is here. She’s here!”

And there it is. Auntie Rio. Fuck her life.

Can Westview get any smaller, or is it just actively trying to ruin her?

Agatha follows Billy’s gaze and spots a sleek silver Bentley pulling up on the side of the road. Her stomach drops. It’s been over a week since she last saw Rio, and apparently the universe chose now for their reunion. 

“Wait.. she’s here?” Tommy whisper-screams. “I thought Mom said she wasn’t coming?” His eyes go wide, his face turning pale by the second. “Oh god, Rae is going to kill me.”

That’s when it clicks. If Rio is here.. Rae is probably here too.

“Wait, you know Rio?” Agatha blurts out, suddenly dizzy by the sudden revelation. “And Rae?”

“Heck yeah.” Billy confirms, immediately ducking behind Agatha like she’s a human shield. “Mom’s friends with Rio. We go to school with Rae. This idiot,” He jerks a thumb at his brother, “Dated one of Rae’s friends for two days and then dumped her. Now she’s furious.”

“It was three days!” Tommy looks genuinely traumatized. “The last threat she gave me was that she’d burn my gym equipment and make it look like a freak accident. I’m not letting that happen.”

With that, he bolts. Before Agatha can make a sense of what’s happening, Tommy’s already gone. His survival mode was triggered by the mere thought of Rae.

Agatha presses her palm to her forehead. She can feel a migraine forming. Threats at such a young age further proves that it’s really her daughter, apparently.

“And what did you do?” She turns to Billy.

“Nothing, I swear!” He panics. “But since Tommy messed with her, she says she’s coming after our entire bloodline for hurting her friend’s feelings.”

Agatha stares. “Jesus Christ.”

From the corner of her eye, she sees Rio step out of the car with sunglasses on. She’s looking unfairly calm for someone about to wreck Agatha’s entire nervous system. Might as well include her cardiac, too.

Billy visibly shudders. “Yup. I’m hiding ‘cause I’m afraid even if I’m in the comfort of my own house. I can’t do this.” He backs away slowly. “Nice seeing you, Auntie Agatha!” And with that, he runs away too.

Agatha stands there alone after the twins literally left her, staring at Rio across the driveway, heart pounding like it’s auditioning for the fastest heartbeat in a minute race.

Great. Absolutely fantastic timing, universe.

Rio only notices her when she’s already halfway across the driveway.

Agatha considers sprinting upstairs like the twins just did. Maybe she should lock herself in the bathroom to avoid any interaction, but it’s too late. Rio is only a few steps away now, close enough that Agatha can smell her perfume and regret all her life choices.

“Agatha?” Rio calls, like she’s saying the name just to check if it’s real. “What are you doing here?”

“What are you doing here?” Agatha shoots back.

Rio blinks, clearly thrown, but she recovers immediately. “I know Wanda. Our kids.. well, they go to the same school.”

Of course Rio is the kind of parent who knows other parents. She probably has complete attendance on PTA meetings or doesn't start a petty feud with the bake sales lady for using a boxed mix. 

Agatha should build her a shrine for her moral superiority.

“And you?” Rio asks, sliding her sunglasses off and pushing them onto her head. She pauses, as if realizing something. “Right. Wanda used to be a casting director.”

“Yeah.” Agatha mutters.

They stand there in a painfully awkward silence that stretches for far too long. How do you exactly talk to the woman you flirted with who turns out to be your daughter’s adoptive mother? There’s no manual for that.

Agatha mentally adds to write a handbook to her to-do list.

“Agatha, listen..” Rio starts, her voice softening. “I should really apologize for—”

“Rio!” Wanda’s voice cuts in cheerfully as she appears, holding yet another glass of wine like it’s a personality trait. “I’m so glad you made it!”

“Hi, Wands.” Rio smiles warmly, turning her attention to the host. “Congratulations on the house. It’s lovely.”

“Thank you, hon! It’s haunted with ghosts, but I’m coping.” Wanda chuckles, clearly reusing her favorite line. Then she looks between them. “And you’ve met Agatha! Or perhaps you two already know each other?”

“We do.” Agatha says quickly, before Rio can answer. “Her daughter goes to our workshop.”

“Oh!” Wanda lights up. “Speaking of, where’s darling Rae?”

Hmm, where is Rae?

As much as she would love to see her daughter, Agatha actually prays she’s nowhere near this driveway. Having Rio is one thing. Having Rae is another. She wouldn’t know what to do or how to act around those two, maybe she’d combust on the spot and she really does not want to combust right now.

“She has ballet.” 

“Rae does ballet?!” 

Both Wanda and Rio turn to her when her voice raises a pitch higher.

Well, excuse her for not knowing that. When she looked for Rae’s social media, the kid doesn’t exactly post her hobbies online, which is a good thing to avoid lurking creeps (not Agatha). 

Besides, Agatha can barely dance without spraining something, so forgive the shock.

“Yes.” Rio smiles. “Not as much now as when she was younger. Her old coaches still text her sometimes, and she’ll drop by to help teach kids under ten when she feels like it.”

Huh. Definitely didn’t get that from Agatha.

“She’s one busy kid.”.

“I let her do whatever she loves to do.” Rio informs her. “She says it makes her feel alive.”

Their eyes meet, blue and brown, as if a sense of understanding is being shared. A moment passes that feels heavier than it should. It feels like they’re having a conversation neither of them is brave enough to say out loud.

“Okay!” Wanda suddenly claps her hands, stepping between them. “What if we continue this very intense staring contest in the backyard? There’s food and actual chairs, that should be tempting enough.”

Well, who are they to refuse the lady of the house?
