Agatha pours herself a drink she doesn’t want and takes a long sip anyway. The alcohol burns, reminding her that she is not a tragic character in a badly written soap opera.

“Mind if I join you?” Rio asks with a small smile.

Agatha glances around. The table is boxed in by people, chairs pushed too close, no clean escape route. She is trapped and couldn’t think of a better excuse to run.

The universe is very committed to its bit tonight.

“Free country.”

Rio pulls out the chair in front of her, and for a moment, they just exist there. The air between them is thick but not sharp anymore. It has become cautious, both of them fully aware they’re tiptoeing over a tripmine that might explode any second with one wrong move.

Or, one wrong word.

“Agatha.” Rio starts carefully, “I’m really sorry for not telling you sooner. About Rae. I should’ve said something the moment I realized who you were.”

“Why didn’t you?” Agatha asks quietly.

“Didn’t what?”

“Why didn’t you tell me sooner?” Her voice doesn’t bite this time. It simply asks.

Rio exhales slowly, like she’s been holding this in for days. “I told you but uh.. it’s because I wanted to know you first.” She admits. “A screening process, if you will.”

Agatha raises an eyebrow, clearly unconvinced.

“I’ve always been protective of Rae.” Rio continues, fingers twisting together in her lap. “She’s my baby, no matter how old she gets. And you—” She hesitates, searching for the right words, “You were orbiting close to her life without even knowing it.”

Agatha tries to deliberately keep her face neutral while the other woman speaks.

“We know you on screen.” Rio says, voice wavering. “But we don’t actually know you. At least I don't, and that scared me.”

“I’ve spent sixteen years building something safe for her. A life where she knows she’s loved. Where she doesn’t have to wonder if she’s wanted.” Rio does the thing where she pokes her tongue at the side of her cheek. “I still don’t know you. I didn’t know your reasons back then but I’m sure it is to give Rae chance at a better life, and I will never judge you for what you did for I know what kind of sacrifice you had to make, but..”

She keeps her gaze towards Agatha this time, holding it as long as she can. “I don’t want to open the door to someone who might walk out again.”

Agatha’s chest tightens. Well, that went straight to her vena cava. Ouch.

“I couldn’t risk her getting attached and then getting hurt.” Rio admits. “Not by anyone. Not even by you.” There it is. Raw. Honest. Vulnerable. She’d give her that.

“So I thought.. if I knew you first,” Rio says quietly, her eyes dropping to her hands, “Maybe I could decide for myself if you were someone safe to let into my daughter’s life.”

She lets out a shaky laugh. “That sounds awful when I say it out loud, I’m sorry.”

Agatha doesn’t interrupt. She just listens.

“But you have to understand..” Rio continues, voice cracking, “I had no bad intentions. None. I swear. I just.. I didn’t want her to get hurt. I only want what’s best for her, Agatha. That’s all I’ve ever wanted.”

And the thing is, as much as she hates being lied to—Agatha understands.

She doesn’t like it. She won't forget it instantly, but she gets it. 

Because if the roles were reversed, if someone unknown and unpredictable was drifting too close to her kid, she would’ve done worse than background checks and casual dinner. She would’ve gone full detective mode. 

So yeah, the secrecy stings, but beneath that?

She sees a mother who was scared.  A woman who built a life around protecting one small human and refused to let it crack.

Agatha can’t fault her for that. Not when she would’ve done the same.

“But it turns out I was already too late.” Rio chuckles, trying to ease the tension. “This whole time, you were already in her life. Or, she was in yours. That one is inevitable beyond my control.”

Agatha hums, lifting her glass and studying the liquid like it might suddenly reveal the secrets of the universe. She does what she always does when she doesn’t know what to do.

“You know..” She finally speaks, “I once ghosted my own therapist for six months.”

It’s easier than admitting she understands. Easier than saying thank you for protecting her or I’m scared too or I don’t know how to do this right.

She’s not there yet.

Who knows one day she will be, but that day is definitely not today.

Rio blinks, trying to process what Agatha just said. “That feels.. unrelated.”

“Is it?” Agatha shrugs. “Avoidance is a lifestyle choice, I guess.”

“You’re deflecting.” Rio points out, smiling a little. “But, sure. May I know what happened with that therapist?”

“It’s confidential, I pay to make whatever I say stay between me and her.” Agatha takes another sip. “So, ballet?”

“What?”

“Rae.” Agatha says, suddenly very interested in the condensation on her glass. “You said she does ballet. Which is insane, by the way, because I have the coordination of a malfunctioning squid.”

Rio laughs softly. “She’s actually really good.”

“Of course she is.” Agatha rolls her eyes. “She couldn’t inherit one of my flaws.” That statement made Rio laugh louder.

“Uh, she started when she was little.” Rio begins to explain. “Five, I think. I took her to watch her first Nutcracker show in Paris..”

“She went to Paris when she was five?” Agatha gasps, eyes wide.

Rio ducks her head shyly, rubbing the back of her neck. “It was actually a Europe tour with my parents and sister.”

“Europe?” Agatha repeats, louder now. “She went to Europe when she was five?” The words hit her all at once, and suddenly she’s picturing tiny Rae with a passport bigger than her hand. 

“She’s travelled a lot more than I did when I was a kid, that much I can tell you.”

“God. You really gave her a good life, didn’t you?” There’s awe in Agatha’s voice and a quieter something else. Gratitude. 

Rae got to experience things Agatha never did growing up. Now, equipped with the knowledge that Rae’s world was bigger, brighter, and safer than her own ever was?

That’s a kind of peace she didn’t know she needed.

“I really hope I did.” Rio smiles at her, once again showing her gapped tooth. “So the show was almost five hours and we were really impressed that a young kid managed to go through all that without tantrums. She was just sitting there with her pink tutu and glittery water bottle, absolutely amused by the performances.”

“Let me guess, Clara is her favorite character?”

“You bet.” Rio grins. “When it was over, she begged me for lessons. She said she wanted to do ballet like the ones she just saw and only then she threw tantrums. She cried in the theater when I told her we couldn’t go to Paris every weekend just so she can attend exclusive Nutcracker classes, or whatever it was called.”

Agatha winces. “She cries? That’s new information.”

“Oh, she’ll deny it.” Rio waves. “But yeah. She cried. It was a full dramatic meltdown, I told her she can take ballet classes in Westview and she can buy anything she likes at Disneyland. That deal made her stop effective immediately.”

Agatha snorts. For the hundredth time she’ll ever say it in her head, yep, that’s definitely her child.

“She stuck with ballet for a few years.” Rio adds. “Even when it got hard. Even when the other girls were mean and she becomes meaner. She’d always practiced in the living room and knocks down the same lamp over and over again.”

Agatha grins before she can stop herself. “I would’ve paid to see that.”

“She blamed the cat.” Rio shrugs. “We don’t even have a cat.”

Agatha laughs, real this time, and it surprises her how nice it actually feels to laugh like that.

“She doesn’t talk much about it now since she’s grown up and she has learned to love other things more like acting instead of dancing.” Rio tells her. “But sometimes, she still stretches in the mornings like she’s about to go on stage. I guess being a ballerina will always be a part of her.”

From then on, the conversation slows, but somehow it has become easy. The tension dissipated and the whole world seemed to be block out of sight. They talk more about Rae’s sarcasm, her music taste (she has Olivia Rodrigo’s personal number, apparently), and how she refuses to admit she still binge watches Barbie movies.

“You raised her well, Rio.” 

“I really tried.”

“You didn’t just try.” Agatha says as a matter of fact. “I know that. Rae knows that.”

The words hang between them. Refusing to let another beat of silence pass, Rio clears her throat. “So.. about me.”

Agatha arches a brow at the sudden change of conversation, but she didn’t point it out. Guess she’s not the only one deflecting. “What about you?”

“We’ve covered a lot about Rae.” Rio remarks. “But you don’t really know anything about me. Well, other than whatever google told you about my family’s wealth and that I cook.”

Agatha smirks. “You also flirt aggressively over soup.”

“Hey!” Rio protests. “You flirted back.”

“Regrettably.”

“Liar.”

Agatha surrenders. “Fine. Tell me something tragic about yourself then. I simply enjoy hearing about that.”

Rio thinks for a second, as if her answer will be the trajectory of whatever this is. “For starters, I cry during cooking shows.”

“Why?” Agatha quips. “That is tragic.”

“And..” Rio adds, ignoring her question. “I have nine functional ovens at home.”

“Stop.” Agatha deadpans. “And there I thought you collecting food containers was already tragic.”

“Rae named my most expensive one.” Rio grins proudly. “She calls it ‘Venny.’”

“That’s an awful name.” For a second, Agatha forgets everything complicated about their situation. 

“You should still be mad at me.” Rio says softly, eyes searching Agatha’s. “Again.. I’m really sorry, Agatha.”

Agatha exhales, leaning back slightly. She tries to figure out how to deal with the conflicting emotions in her chest “Honestly? I don’t think I was mad. Just.. upset. I didn’t like being lied to. I mean, who does?”

Rio nods slowly. “I get it. I promise I’m going to be honest with you from now on.”

“From now on?” Agatha repeats, yet again raising an eyebrow.

Rio shifts awkwardly, tucking a strand of hair behind her ear. “Well, if you want any part in Rae’s life, then that means we have to..” She pauses, fumbling for words.

Agatha feels the almost-verbal “co-parent” hovering in the air and stops herself from blurting it out. Instead, she offers, “Be friendly to each other?”

“Yeah. Friendly.” Rio shrugs. “But the decision still rests with Rae. Whatever you want moving forward, it will only happens if she allows it.”

Agatha doesn’t know yet what role she wants in Rae’s life. What she does know is that for now, she’s content to exist in the space she’s allowed without rushing anything.

“Well, if you ladies aren’t getting too comfortable here.” Wanda sing-songs, their almost-private bubble popping as she sashays over with yet another drink in hand. This time, Agatha’s pretty sure it’s beer. “I’ve been watching you for like.. an hour now. You two are deep in a serious conversation! What’s up?”

An hour? Neither of them noticed it had been that long.

“Rio was just telling me about the new infrastructures of Westview.” Agatha lies smoothly.

“And Agatha’s been telling me all about L.A.” Rio adds, playing along. “Erewhon, right?”

Agatha fakes a nod. She hasn’t even stepped foot in Erewhon, but points for effort.

Wanda sets her glass down on the table and loops her arms around both of them, hands slightly damp from condensation. “I’m just so happy to see my two best friends bonding. This is like, healing for me.”

Rio gently pries the drink away. “Okay, that’s enough alcohol for you, hon.”

“Don’t silence me in my own haunted house.” Wanda huffs before she wanders off again, probably to overshare with a stranger or grab herself a different beverage.

Agatha watches her go. “She’s a lot.”

“She means well.” 

Before Agatha can respond, Jen appears out of nowhere like a summoned demon.

“AGATHAAAA.” She barrels toward them, swaying like she’s on a boat. Her eyeliner is smudged, her heels are in her hand, and she smells aggressively like tequila. In a span of an hour Agatha left her to be, this is already the state she found herself in?

“Oh no.” Agatha mutters.

“There you are.” Jen slurs, dramatically gripping the table for balance. “I have been looking for you everywhere!”

That’s a lie. She knows exactly where Agatha is after leaving her alone to deal with Rio earlier.

“How did you got yourself drunk?” Agatha asks in disbelief.

Instead of answering, Jen’s eyes land on Rio. “Ohhhhhh my God.”

Rio stiffens. “Hi?”

Jen leans in way too close. “I know you. You’re the rich girl in town!”

Rio blinks, surprise by the other woman’s bluntness. “I—thank you?”

“Forgive my assistant, she gets cuckoo with every sip of tequila and I presumed she must consumed a lot, though I frankly don’t know how.” Agatha explains. “Okay, pack it up, Jenny. We’re leaving.”

Jen ignores her, her attention fixed on Rio. “Wait.” She gasps loudly upon connecting the dots. “WAIT.”

She spins back to Agatha in an instant. “This is her. This is the woman. The one with the kid. Or, your kid. Whose kid, whatever! She’s your.. What’s the term again?”

Agatha chokes, her eyes wide in fear for what her friend might say next. “Jennifer, don’t you dare.”

Jen snaps her fingers repeatedly, missing every time. “Your.. your.. baby mama!”

Crickets. More, and more, crickets.

Rio coughs after a beat. “I’m sorry?”

Agatha freezes as her brain absolutely short-circuits. Jen really said that out loud. She swears she won't complain if the earth swallows her whole right now.

“Jen.” Agatha warns, “You are drunk. Whatever’s coming out of your mouth is junk.”

“No, I am spiritually sober.” Jen says, wobbling to prove a point. “I am also spiritually aware.”

She points between them casually with her long finger nails. “You had a baby. She raised the baby. Boom! Baby mama.”

Rio’s face turns crimson. “I don’t think that’s.. is that even a thing?”

“Noforgivehershe’sjustdrunkdon'tthinkaboutit.” Agatha mumbles quickly as she is already dragging Jen away, one hand firmly wrapped around her wrist, mentally noting it’s officially time to go before her friend says something that will permanently ruin her social standing.

“We’re leaving!” Agatha calls over her shoulder, voice loud enough to cut through the music.

“Agatha, wait!” Rio calls, attempting to chase after them but Agatha moves fast in a speed of lightning.

Jen, unfortunately, was in her villain era. She was blowing kisses at other guest, loudly complimenting a woman’s shoes, and nearly tripping over a decorative plant. 

They are already in the car when Rio reaches the front door, sighing to have missed the chance of a proper goodbye with Agatha.

“Jen, I am never letting you drink tequila again.” Agatha tells her.

“Tequila and I are soulmates.” Jen slumps to her seat. “We will find each other again, hey! Maybe I will not end alone for the rest of my life after all.”

The ride home is a blur of Jen singing off-key and Agatha massaging her temple, but oddly enough, the day doesn’t feel like a total disaster.

When Jen is passed out on Lilia’s guest bedroom and Agatha is finally alone—her phone buzzes, finally receiving a notification she hasn’t receive for a week.

riovidal: i wasn't able to say goodbye earlier

riovidal: i really hope your friend's okay

agathaharkness: She’s knocked out.                                        

agathaharkness: I should be the one apologizing for what she said, clearly she’s lost her mind.                                                 

riovidal: haha, no worries

Agatha breathes through her nose, a smile she refuses to acknowledge tugging at her lips.

agathaharkness: You are never letting that go, are you?

Three dots appear almost instantly.

Agatha snorts, shaking her head.

agathaharkness: I hate you.

Agatha smiles, unguarded.

She tells herself it’s just because it’s funny.

Definitely not because it’s Rio.

Chapter 9: Chapter 9

Chapter Notes

lemme introduce you to agatha (down bad, emotionally conflicted) harkness!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Lilia claps her hands in a commanding way she always does before class officially starts. Agatha swears she’s Pavlov-trained these kids because the second that beat echoes through the room, they scramble back to their seats like obedient theatre soldiers. 

“Alright, young actors.” Lilia announces, “Today, we’re doing object transformation.”

Agatha grins from her spot. Oh, this is going to be good. 

This is the kind of exercise that exposes the ones who commit way too hard and the ones who freeze like deer in headlights. She can already picture the chaos with kids gripping random junk while desperately trying to convince everyone it’s something else entirely.

“You’ll each choose a random object of your liking.” Lilia explains, pacing slowly in front of the group. “And your job is to turn it into something else. Please refrain from giving me a boring mime, I don’t want to see you pretending. I want to believe you, you have to make me believe you.”

She stops beside a kid in the center aisle. “If you turn a shoe into a phone, I want to see your whole life inside that call. Who are you talking to? Why are you calling them? What happens if they don’t pick up? What’s at stake?”

She spreads her arms dramatically for added effect. “Is it heartbreak? Is it hope? Is it an I know what you did last summer sort of confession? Are you calling the one person you swore you’d never speak to again? Live in it. Breath it. Show me how it's done.”

A few kids buzz in excitement. Someone already looks stressed, someone else smirking while glancing at its watch with probably a few ideas floating in its head at that exact moment.

“Commit.” Lilia tells them with gritted teeth. “I don’t care if it’s messy or ridiculous. I don’t care if it makes you look stupid. I only care that it’s honest.”

Agatha watches from the sidelines, amused. She can’t wait to witness these kids allow their imagination collide with fear and instinct. 

Subconsciously, she glances at Rae’s usual seat. It’s empty.That’s when it dawned to her.. Rae isn’t here today.

She straightens in her chair, scanning the room like she might’ve missed something obvious. Maybe Rae moved to the back, though she knows better. There is absolutely no universe where Rae would willingly choose the back row. That kid lives for being seen.

Agatha counts faces again but even then, there’s no Rae in sight.

That’s.. strange. Rae seems to be the type that doesn’t miss class. She treats the workshop like it’s her personal church, clinging to it as if it’s a religion. She’s always the first to volunteer, the first to argue, and the first to roll her eyes.

On top of that, she excels the most. She adjusts her performance the moment feedback is given, as if learning comes to her the way breathing does. Her absence speaks volume.. or is Agatha biased of her own kid?

“Hey.” Agatha leans in casually when Lilia sits back beside her, trying not to make it obvious that she might be spiraling. “I don’t see Rae anywhere. Did she say she wasn’t coming today?”

Lilia frowns, following Agatha’s gaze. “Right? That kid would’ve jumped up to go first.” She mutters. “I didn’t get a heads-up or anything, but I’ll make sure to ask Kate to contact her later.”

Later feels too far away.

Agatha forces a nods, but her stomach is already tying itself into knots. She’s trying not to jump into conclusions or assume the worst, God forbid something happened.

Before she can overthink it further, she pulls out her phone and opens Instagram. Her fingers hover for a second before she taps Rio’s profile, then sends a short message with her number and a vague “call me.”

Not even two minutes pass when her phone vibrates so she makes her way out of the room before answering the call, paying no attention to the ongoing activity.

Sorry, kids. Mentor Agatha—Mommy Agatha has personal business to attend to. Your make believe objects can wait.

“Agatha?” Rio says from the other line. “What’s wrong?”

“Rae didn’t come to class today.” Agatha blurts. “Where is she?”

There’s a brief pause on the other end, long enough for Agatha’s brain to feed itself with the worst case scenarios. “Really?” Rio asks. “I told her to inform one of the adults in the workshop, she must have forgotten.”

Agatha’s heart is racing. “Is something wrong? Is she sick?”

“No, she flew to Hawaii with my mom.”

“Hawaii?” Agatha repeats, stunned.

“Yeah. My mom has this yearly get-together with her friends, and she insists Rae tags along every time. They’ll be gone for the weekend.”

Only then does Agatha realize she’s been holding her breath the entire time. She lets it out slowly, tension draining from her shoulders. “Oh.”

“Sorry.” Rio adds gently. “I should’ve followed up and made sure she told someone.”

“It’s fine.” Agatha dismisses her. “I was just—” She stops herself from saying the word worried. 

She doesn't want to overstep and claim something she technically has no right to. So instead, she shrugs even though Rio can’t see it. “I just noticed she isn’t here.” 

Agatha tries to hide the part where her chest dropped the second she saw that empty chair. For one awful second, her mind went everywhere it shouldn’t, and she doesn’t like it.

Maybe that’s just what it means to care. Give it to Agatha who holds a bachelor’s degree in the art of deflection. She pushes the thought aside before it can settle and consume her any further.

“Well..” Agatha can hear shuffling movement from the other line. “Rae is very much alive. We were texting an hour ago. Right now, she’s probably bossing her abuela over piña colata.”

“Yeah. That tracks.” She leans against the hallway wall, phone pressed to her ear. “Thanks for calling me back.” She adds reverently.

“Anytime.”

There’s a beat of silence after that, long enough Agatha presumes Rio must have already hung up. “You know..” She murmurs eventually, voice careful, “Yelena Belova is performing in town tonight.”

“Who?” Agatha asks, brows knitting together.

“Yelena.” Rio repeats her name with distinct pronunciation, as if that alone should clear everything up. “The singer? She went viral a while back. She used to live in her car before people discovered her online, she’s kind of a big deal now.”

“I genuinely have no idea who you’re talking about.”

Rio lets out a small laugh. “Okay, that’s fair.” Then she adds, almost like an afterthought, “I could take you so you’d have an idea who I’m talking about.”

Agatha was taken aback. She considers the bad timing and impending terrible circumstances. She doesn’t know if it’s a good idea to go out with Rio, especially with everything hanging over them like a storm cloud.

“Would that even be okay?” Agatha asks slowly.

“Mhm?” 

“Would you.. taking me out,” Agatha clarifies, choosing her words carefully, “Would that be a good idea? I mean, with Rae and everything going on.”

Rio goes quiet, clearly thinking it through. “Right.” She finally admits. “It’s complicated.”

Agatha nods because, of course it is. Nothing in her life gets to be simple anymore. Everything is complicated the way the universe intended it to be.

Maybe that’s the price she has to pay.

“I don’t want to confuse her.” Rio continues. “Rae already has enough on her plate with meeting you and all. I don’t want to add more pressure.”

“Yeah.” Agatha agrees. “She already hates me on a good day. I don’t want to give her additional reasons to hate me even more, if that’s even possible..”

“She doesn’t hate you.”

“Be with us in a room for three minutes and say that again to my face.”

“Do you want me to talk to her?”

“Please don’t.”

Rio hums a small okay before changing the subject. “For starters, I didn’t mean it like a date.” She clarifies. “Not really. I just thought we could go as two adults who simply know each other.”

Simply? More like simply complicated. 

“Wow.” Agatha says dryly. “That’s such a romantic pitch.”

“That wasn’t the goal.” Rio huffs a quiet laugh. “We don’t have to label it.”

“I really don’t want to hurt her.” Agatha lets her vulnerability slip slightly. “I already feel like I’m walking on glass.”

“I know.” Rio replies kindly. “Me too. That’s why I asked instead of assuming.”

Agatha should say no. She knows she should, but she’s tired of always choosing the safe option when everything else in her says otherwise.

“What time?” 

“Eight. Small venue downtown.” 

“Figures.” Agatha mutters. “You hate fancy places as if you don’t already live in one. Or is it six? Be honest.”

“Not true!” Rio protests mildly. “I do not own six houses, Agatha. That’s absurd.”

“Yeah, it’s ‘cause you probably own seven.” Agatha smiles to herself when she hears Rio groaning. “Send me the address and to be clear, this is not a date, no?”

“Yup. Definitely not a date.” Rio must be grinning from the other line.

They hang up. Agatha tells herself it won’t be that bad if it’s not a date because it won’t mean anything. There will be no lines crossed. Hopefully, considering Agatha’s record of flirting shamelessly.

Anyway, what harm could a stroll downtown do, with some singer she’d never even heard of humming in the background? 

That’s fine. She’s fine. They’ll be fine. She pockets her phone and sighs. “It’s not a date, Agatha. You’ll be fine.”

In true Agatha fashion when she has to involve herself in the doings of the public, she shows up looking like a member of a secret spy agency. Cap pulled low, tinted sunglasses on.. at night. There's no sun in sight but frankly, she has zero shame.

Her get up doesn't allow her to be 100% incognito, but it helps. People still stare and she lets them. Fame is weird like that. Sometimes you avoid it, sometimes you lean into it just to feel something. Tonight, she’s doing both.

Rio is already there when Agatha arrives, she's leaning against the streetlamp with her hands in the pocket of her jeans. Agatha stops dead in her tracks when she notices the actual crime.

They’re both wearing long sleeve polos in the same color. It is in different shades of blue, sure, but still. 

Rio has hers tucked casually into jeans, sleeves slightly rolled up. Agatha on the other hand paired hers with a long white skirt, allowing the fabric to flow freely with the breeze of the air.

“Are you fucking kidding me?” Agatha hisses in disbelief, lifting her sunglasses just enough to glare.

Rio looks at her up and down, tongue pressing against her cheek in a way that somehow feels like flirting even when she would swear it isn’t. “Damn. The universe really hates us.”

“This is not funny.” Agatha declares. “We look coordinated.”

“The funniest part..” Rio adds, dead serious, “Is this was not intentional.”

Agatha waves a hand at Rio’s entire fit. “You have to change.”

Rio blinks. “Why?”

“Because I don’t want to be seen matching outfits with you.”

“Yes, but not more than I do.”

“Rio.”

Rio crosses her arms, amusement clear on her face like she's enjoying this entire ordeal. “Okay, why do I have to change? Why don’t you change?”

Agatha opens her mouth to think of an excuse or a rebuttal. When she can't think of any to justify her pettiness, she sighs in defeat. It would really be unfair to make the other woman change.. “Whatever, just don’t walk too close to me.”

She knows that two people wearing the same outfit and walking too close at night is the kind of thing that makes strangers assume they’re a couple. Isn’t that what ordinary couples do nowadays? They coordinate aesthetics by committing to one color palette.

She absolutely does not want that kind of impression.

“Sure.” Rio smirks. “M’lady.”

They start walking, although not quite shoulder to shoulder. They’re close enough to share the same path but far enough to keep a careful distance, blending into the noisy crowd of downtown. 

With every loud music spilling from open bars and food stands with their bright neon signs, Agatha feels like she belongs here. Or maybe it’s just nostalgia messing up with her mind.

Still, as much as she hates the town, she can’t deny the comfort it offers her now. In its own roundabout way, it’s the place that shaped her into who she is today.

The singer won’t be performing until later so Rio brings her to a small birriería tucked between a laundromat and a closed tattoo shop. It looks like it might disappear if you blink too long.

“This place..” Rio points, her eyes almost glinting. “Absolutely changed my life.”

Agatha squints at it. “It looks like it might give me food poisoning.”

“Trust me.” Rio insists, chuckling. “I would never betray you with bad birria.”

“That’s a strong promise.”

They entered the shop and step up to the counter. The guy working there grins at Rio, clearly recognizing her.

“¡Rio!” He calls. “You finally brought your novia!”

Agatha chokes on absolutely nothing. She doesn’t speak Spanish, but from the scraps she picked up in Señora Alma’s class at least two decades ago, she’s fairly certain she knows what novia means. “Excuse me?”

Rio’s eyes widen in panic. “No, no! We're not—”

The guy cuts her off, pointing between them. “Matching fits? Come on. That’s ultimate couple behavior.”

Agatha looks down at her polo, her own choices from earlier betraying her now. “I would like to formally state I did not consent to this.”

Rio laughs nervously, nodding in agreement. “We dressed similarly in pure accident.”

“Uh-huh.” The guy smirks. “Accidentally in love too?”

In love? With her? The woman who raised her kid?

For some reason, that idea made Agatha’s brain forget how to use its respiratory function. To add salt to the injury, her heart is doing that stupid thing where it thumps too loud, clearly demanding for attention. 

Please shut up, she tries to shut it off. This is not the time to deal with feelings.

Agatha turns to Rio. Rio is laughing, but she looks embarrassed. Her cheeks are a little pink, and Agatha hates how she noticed that detail.

“I do not like him.”

Rio hides her face with her hand. “He’s like this with everyone.”

“I’m not.” The guy insists, obviously eavesdropping. “I’m only like this to cute couples.”

Agatha leans in this time, whispering to Rio once again. “If he asks us to share a birria, let it be known I’m leaving.”

The guy grins wider, thriving in their situation. He has such excellent auditory skills to have heard what Agatha said. “Two orders of birria for the lovebirds, then.”

“Stop calling us that!” They protest simultaneously, which only makes it worse.

That became his avenue for teasing them even more. “Relax. Just enjoy the food and maybe you’ll kiss after.”

Agatha can feel her own cheeks burning. At this point, her soul is actually leaving her body. “We will not.”

Rio nods awkwardly. “We really won’t.”

It’s funny when before she knew Rio was Rae’s mother, Agatha had been whining about only getting a hug from her. Now, the very thought of getting a kiss from Rio is enough to make her stomach do cartwheels.

They move away from the counter and find an empty spot to sit nearby. Agatha crosses her legs, pretending she’s very invested in adjusting her skirt when really she’s replaying the guy’s lovebirds and kiss comment in her head like a cursed voicemail she can’t delete.

She clears her throat loudly, the universal sound of I am changing the subject immediately.

“So..” She says too fast. “How exactly do you know about this place?”

Rio was caught off guard by the abrupt shift. “Uh—I guess I enjoyed wandering around to discover hidden little spots to eat. I also pickup tips and notes whenever I could back when I was just learning the ropes in culinary school. A senior once told me that if the menu looks questionable, the food’s probably amazing. I’ve carried that with me ever since.”

Agatha nods way too seriously. “I agree. If the health inspector fears it, expect the flavor to be immaculate.”

Rio chuckles. “Pretty much.”

Agatha keeps going, because stopping would mean thinking, and thinking would mean remembering the unsolicited comments that involves mistaking them for being a couple. “You bring Rae here too?”

“Yep. She pretends she’s too cool for it but she always steals my food.” Rio smiles, and something stirs in Agatha’s chest.

She quickly remind herself that this isn’t a date and she’s far too smart to let a simple smile make her feel anything.

The birrias arrive, and thankfully, the server wasn’t the guy from earlier. Rio watches as Agatha takes her first bite, and Agatha nearly forgets her own name by how spectacular it is, proving Rio absolutely right.

She takes another bite, letting the flavors ground her in the present. She ignores the flutter in her chest whenever Rio looks at her. Instead, she settles on the fleeting sense of calm the food and the company has brought her.

They finish their meal slower than expected, grease-stained napkins piling up between them. Rio jokes that it’s the evidence of a very good decision, and Agatha halfheartedly agrees.

When they leave the place and start walking again, Agatha takes the lead without explaining, cutting through quieter streets and up toward the side of town where the voices thins and the air feels a little less crowded.

Rio notices the change. “You’re walking like someone with a plan.” She notes. “Should I be concerned?”

“I’m not leading you to the forest. This isn’t a true crime podcast.”

“That’s exactly what someone in a true crime podcast would say.”

Agatha grins over her shoulder. “Please. If I were going to commit a crime, it’d be something related to a mass scamming. Homicide is a little too bloody for my liking.”

They stop when a particular structure comes into view. Before them stood a large, slightly weathered public telescope mounted on a concrete platform, pointed toward the sky like it’s been waiting patiently for someone to remember it exists.

Despite the years that had gone, Agatha will always remember its existence even if most people in Westview don’t.

Her expression softens in a way she doesn’t even try to hide. “It’s been here since I was a kid.” She tells Rio. “I used to sneak out just to come up here. I liked pretending I was doing something profound with my life, it’s a NASA dream of mine. ”

Rio steps closer, eyes roaming over the telescope, the platform, and the faint plaque no one ever reads. She observes first before making a statement.

“You’re in Westview’s most under appreciated landmark.” Agatha insists. “Don’t tell me you’ve never been here?”

“Never.” Rio admits, almost sheepish. “I’ve heard of it. People talk about it like it’s a myth, but I never came up here.”

“Ah, yes.” Agatha raises an eyebrow. “Tonight we have the wealthy cultured, well-traveled, and yet tragically deprived of small town astronomy—Rio Vidal.”

“I feel judged.”

“You should.”

Agatha moves to the telescope and adjusts it with practiced ease. The muscle memory kicks in before thought as she gestures grandly, “Behold, the moon!”

Rio leans down and peers through the lens curiously. “I don’t see anything.”

Agatha sighs. “You didn’t even try.”

“I absolutely did. I saw.. darkness, and maybe my own disappointment.”

“You have to adjust it.” Agatha instructs, stepping closer. “Here. Try again.”

Rio bends down once more, eyes squinting. “Still nothing. Is it broken?”

“It’s not broken.” Agatha says patiently. “You just—hold on.”

She reaches out instinctively, hands landing on Rio’s hips to gently guide her forward. It’s meant to be practical, except the second her hands make contact only did she realized what she has done.

Oh. That’s a body. A very real body. Rio’s warm body.

No lines crossed, right? Then why the fuck is she making a move by holding—

She feels Rio stiffen in her touch for half a second, then relaxes. “Am I in the right place now?”

“Shhh,” Agatha shushes her, not wanting to entertain the elephant in the room. “You weren’t, but you are now.”

She steps closer, standing just behind Rio now, adjusting her stance with small, careful movements. One hand stays at Rio’s waist, the other briefly brushing her side as she angles her toward the lens.

Agatha becomes painfully aware of how close they are, of how easily she could rest her chin on Rio’s shoulder, and of how this is absolutely not something she should be thinking about.

She tells herself to get it together and redirect her focus on her real goal. Honestly, she deserves a standing ovation from NASA for this.

“Okay.” Agatha announces after a minute, satisfied with their position. “Now look.”

Rio places a hand on the top of the telescope. She adjusts her view, then gasps. “Oh! I see it. I actually see it!”

“Told you so.”

“It’s really clear from here!” Rio exclaims. “I didn’t think it’d look like that. Bigger, I mean..”

“Yeah. It always does that. It makes you feel small in a good way.” 

Rio glances back at her, their faces suddenly much closer than intended. “You came up here a lot?”

Agatha feels conscious of the space so she finally removes her grip from Rio, taking a step backward. “I come here whenever I needed reminding that the world was bigger than my problems.” She says, then quickly regrets the vulnerability. “Or when I needed dramatic lighting for an existential crisis.”

Rio laughs. “I like that.”

“I’ve always been drawn to the moon.” Agatha adds. “There’s something honest about the way it hangs there in solitude. It’s always been there, its beauty so often overlooked since it appears while most of the world is asleep, and gone again by the time they wake, as if it never waited at all.”

Rio looks at her in quiet awe, listening to every careful word. “I guess.” She says after a moment, thoughtful. “But the sun isn’t so bad either. I like to think its job is to takeover when the moon needs to rest.”

Agatha catches herself looking at Rio—the way her eyes light up when she talks, the way the glow skims across her face. She’s beautiful like this.. no. She shuts that thought down immediately.

She blames the night sky and the telescope for creating such raw moment between them.

She crosses her arms, deflecting as usual. “Anyway. Big rock, very impressive. We should probably—”

“Thank you.” Rio interrupts, gentle but sincere. “For bringing me here.”

Agatha pauses, then shrugs. “Well, everyone deserves to see the moon properly at least once.”

Even if it means standing too close and pretending it didn’t mean anything.

They drift back down toward town proper as the night thickens. Loud music leaks into the streets before the crowd does. The venue is already full of people clustered like moths around warm light. Agatha keeps her cap low again, sunglasses still on because commitment to the bit matters.

They don’t even make it ten steps into the crowd before Agatha feels it, that familiar prickle at the back of her neck. “Agatha? Is that you?” Kate walks up to her, drink in hand.

“Oh no.” Rio whispers beside her. “Friend?”

“More like threat to my peace.”

Kate is already in front of them, eyes bright with recognition. “I knew that was you. I’d recognize that posture anywhere. You walk like you’re trying not to be perceived.”

Agatha pinches the bridge of her nose. “This is not happening.”

Kate squints past her then, finally clocking Rio hovering a polite step away. “Hello. And you are?”

“No.” Agatha warns firmly, stepping half an inch to block the view. “You don’t know her. She doesn’t know you. Let’s leave it at that.”

Agatha has no idea why Kate is even in town on the exact same night she is. Lilia once mentioned her assistant is heaven sent since she preferred staying home and avoiding crowds like she does so this is a surprise to her. She doesn’t ask about the woman's business, tho.

Frankly, she’s not interested in Kate’s life and whatever she does outside of work.

Kate lifts her hands in surrender, fully aware of how terrifying Agatha can get. “Okay, sorry for approaching you. You may now lurk, or whatever this is.” She gives a sloppy salute with her cup and wanders off, already distracted by someone else

Agatha turns back to Rio, who is now openly grinning at her. “You know she’s getting the wrong impression of us, right?”

“Probably.” Agatha shrugs. “But I know she’ll keep her mouth shut.”

They slip into the crowd just as the lights dim. A hush rolls over the space, followed by cheers as Yelena Belova finally reveals herself. There’s a spotlight while she holds a mic in hand, stepping into the middle of the stage.

It's a human sign

When things go wrong

Agatha feels it immediately. That pull. That quiet ache she pretends not to have.

When the first notes of Cold Heart fill the air, the crowd stills. Yelena’s voice is raw. Every syllable laid bare, as if she sings directly to you. 

When the scent of her lingers

And temptation's strong

She risks a glance at Rio. Rio’s watching the stage, but there’s something else there too. Maybe Agatha is in a high, or maybe Rio feels it too. Maybe the song is pressing on the same bruise on two different people.

“She’s good.” Rio murmurs without looking at her.

“Yeah.” Agatha diverts her gaze. “She is.”

Cold, cold heart

Hardened by you

Agatha feels the words land far too close to home, and suddenly she’s aware of everything. What is she even doing?

When did she convince herself that this wasn’t a date, that walking through town with Rio under borrowed moments was somehow harmless? Why did she agree to this at all, knowing how fragile her footing with Rae already is, knowing one wrong step could push her even farther away?

And worse, why does her heart refuse to listen?

Some things looking better, baby

Just passing through

Her mind lays it out cleanly. If she stands by logic, she’d know how complicated and selfish this is. On top of that, she’s standing on dangerous territory.

But her chest aches in a way even logic can’t explain, thrumming with something unknown. It is both reckless and painfully alive. She hates that part of herself for feeling that way, for wanting something she knows she couldn’t reach for.

Shouldn’t reach for. Must not reach for.

And I think it's gonna be a long, long time

'Til touchdown brings me 'round again to find

So why, standing here with Rio, does wanting feel inevitable?

She’s only known this woman for what, less than a month? Why does she keep finding herself drawn to her anyway? And if it’s wrong, why does it feel easy?

Agatha has had her fair share of women. May it be flings or brief distractions, nothing ever lingered long enough to make an impression. Nothing ever made her feel exposed, nothing ever made her question her feelings the way Rio does now. 

It’s confusing and terrifying all at once, and she hates that she can’t push it away.

I'm not the man they think I am at home

Oh, no, no, no

She shifts, suddenly aware of how near Rio is. Their arms brush. This time, neither of them moves away. A shiver runs down her spine, the hairs at the back of her neck standing on end.

“You okay?” Rio asks.

Agatha nods, focusing on the stage and the singer entirely. “She makes me feel things.”

“That’s her whole brand.”

And this is what I should have said

Well, I thought it but I kept it hid

The rest of the crowd blends into a distant hum. 

At some point, Rio’s hand grazes against Agatha’s, lingering just a fraction longer than expected. It doesn’t do anything. It’s just.. there.

Something in that simple touch makes Agatha’s heart skip. Fingers tentative at first, then slowly settling, as if they’ve always been meant to fit together. Before she realizes it, Agatha finds herself intertwining her fingers with Rio’s, holding on a little tighter than she intended, and feeling a warmth bloom through her chest that has nothing to do with the weather.

Agatha’s brain immediately starts screaming at herself for what she did. Don’t panic. This is fine. People hold hands. Friends hold hands. Do they? God, do they?

Rio doesn’t point out their hands. She doesn’t comment on their touch either. She lets it be, as if it’s the most natural thing in the world and somehow, that makes it even harder for Agatha to think clearly, harder to pretend this isn’t exactly where she wants to be.

Cold, cold heart

Hardened by you

Rio squeezes her hand once, firm but gentle, and it grounds Agatha. She looks up at Rio, catching her warm smile.

They settle into shared silence, though Agatha’s feels her lips twitch into a smile anyway, copying Rio’s. Against better judgment, she lets herself sink into the moment, letting everything else fade into the background. 

Their fingers remain intertwined in a kind of quiet promise neither of them fully understand yet.

Something's looking better, baby

Just passing through

They stand there, swaying lightly with the rhythm of the lingering music every now and then. Yelena's performance ends eventually as the crowd erupts with applause.

Not a date, Agatha reminds herself. Definitely not a date.

And yet, she doesn’t let go of Rio’s hand. She doesn’t want to.

Agatha: Hey, it’s Agatha.

Rio: i already have your number saved 

Rio: also, heyyyy

Agatha: That feels alarmingly fast.

Agatha: Might’ve given you my contact way too soon.

Rio: i promise you won’t regret it

Agatha: Well then, thanks for tonight.

Agatha: I actually enjoyed it.

Rio: you’re welcome and thank you for taking me to see the moon, that was really cool

Rio: i’ll take this as a personal achievement

Rio: also, we should sleep. it’s getting really late

Agatha: Sure, grandma. Want me to tuck you in too?

Rio: watch it!!

Rio: i’m a woman of habit, not decay

Agatha: Tomato, tomato.

Agatha: Good night, Rio.

Rio: good night, agatha

Rio: pls don’t ghost me for six months.

Agatha: No promises.

The next morning, Agatha comes downstairs later than usual, hair still damp from the shower. She carries a mug that’s warming her hands. 

Lilia and Kate are already at the breakfast nook with their plates half-full. They’ve obviously been awake longer than she is. With Jen flying back to LA the day prior, the house is back down to its three occupants.

“Good morning!” 

Lilia looks up from her book and studies her with suspicious gaze. “You’re particularly chirpy this morning.” She comments. “And you don’t look like you regret waking up, why is that?”

“I woke up breathing, figured I might as well continue the trend.” Agatha hums, slipping into the extra chair while taking a sip of her coffee.

“Did something nice happen last night?” Lilia asks not in an accusing or teasing way. Just observant. 

Agatha pauses, mug hovering near her mouth. “That’s a loaded question.”

“I didn’t mean it that way.” Lilia clarifies. “I just meant that if something good happened, you don’t have to pretend it didn’t.”

Agatha’s forehead creases. “It wasn’t a date.”

Kate makes a noise that is absolutely a laugh disguised as a cough. Agatha almost forgot about her, so shoots her a meaningful glare. “It wasn’t.”

“I didn’t say it was.” Lilia utters calmly. “I just asked if you enjoyed yourself.”

Agatha finally nods, slow and reluctant without giving anything. “I did. It was fine.”

Lilia doesn’t have to know the details of her complicated relationship with Rio. Not now, at least.

“Fine usually doesn’t make you smile before noon.”

Agatha sets her mug down. “Am I being interrogated, or is this just mandatory breakfast conversation?”

Lilia sighs, not new to Agatha's way of deflecting a topic. “Just checking in.”

A beat passes, then Lilia speaks again. “Actually, speaking of checking in, I was thinking of doing something for the kids once the workshop wraps.”

Agatha looks up. “Mhmm?”

The workshop won’t end for another few weeks but when it does, it means she’ll be headed back to LA. There’s really nothing left for her to do here in Westview. She has no obligations left or excuses to linger on.

And with that comes the weight of reality, she only has a few weeks to figure out what she wants to do with Rae. How to be in her life, how to navigate something she’s never faced before. The clock is ticking, and every moment feels heavier than the last.

She forces herself to redirect her thoughts, pushing the weight of the looming decisions to the back of her mind. For now, she clings to a simpler, almost fragile idea that when Rae returns from Hawaii, she’ll actually talk to her. Genuinely, without the usual bickering and verbal assassinations.

For now, that’s enough hope to hold onto until she has to face the rest.

“I usually treat them to dinner.” Lilia continues. “Nothing fancy. Just somewhere they can eat too much and feel celebrated. Do you know any catering services around here? Or someone local we could trust?”

Agatha’s fingers tighten slightly around her mug.

Catering service? Food? Agatha’s mind immediately drifts to the only name that comes to mind. It’s almost laughable how quickly her thoughts leap there, but then again, some things are hard to ignore.

“I might, actually.” 

“Tell me more.”

Agatha nods. “Rae’s—” She stops herself, then recalibrates. “Rae’s mami is a chef.”

Lilia watches her with interest. “Is she good?”

“The first night we were here, when we saw Rae working at that Puerto Rican restaurant—”

“Yes, you were very rude to young Rae,” Lilia interrupts, clenching her teeth.

“Not my point.” Agatha rolls her eyes. “Anyway, I found out they actually own that place. Or well, Rae’s mami does.”

“I’ve always known that kid is loaded!” Kate exclaims. “One time, I commented on the Van Cleef she was wearing, and she offered to give it to me. I declined out of moral compass, of course.”

“How’d you even know that?” Lilia asks, barely following Kate’s tangent. “How do you know her mom?”

Agatha shrugs, keeping it casual. “She’s just a friend I coincidentally met recently.”

Lilia eyes her suspiciously but doesn’t press any longer. “Do you think she can handle the dinner?”

“I can ask.” 

She quickly texts Rio about it, and the reply comes almost instantly.

Rio: sure 

Rio: anything for my baby mama 🩷

Such a fucking idiot, she thinks—but she smiles anyway.

Chapter 10: Chapter 10

Chapter Notes

next update shall be in the weekend xx this chap is on the shorter side but have fun reading this lil treat nonetheless!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The workshop is located on the first floor of a building Lilia rented along one of Westview’s busier streets. It isn’t big, but it’s wide enough to carve out a space where parents can lounge if they choose to stay for the entirety of the three-hour class, a concept Agatha has learned is less optional than it sounds.

Some helicopter parents, for example, treat the place like a long-term waiting room. 

Gavin’s mom stays throughout, firmly convinced her youngest couldn’t survive without supervision, despite evidence to the contrary. Paisley’s mom remains for different reasons. She’s constantly hovering and doting, as if her daughter might suddenly require emergency lip balm in a moment’s notice.

That’s one of the reasons why, before she ever knew Rio, Agatha found it suspicious that Rae’s parent never stayed during the workshops. Maybe it was because Rae was on the older side and is one independent kid. Maybe because Rio is often too busy. Either way, she can always just ask Rio about it if she’s so curious with this whole ordeal.

Today, Rio is finally visiting the workshop. Lilia invites her over to discuss logistics such as menus, allergies, and all the boring adult stuff Agatha would probably not listen to.

She, however, feels oddly responsible. So she waits by the entrance when Rio texts that she’s pulling over, playing the role of a welcoming host that she pretends to be.

Rio shows up in a black long sleeves cropped tee, a teasing sliver of toned stomach on display which is probably enough to distract Agatha’s entire focus for the day.

Agatha tries not to look because looking is disrespectful and wrong. It takes her a good ten seconds before she peeks again, ever so casually. Damn it. Who is she kidding? Eyes are after all, made for seeing.

“Hi.” Rio greets, adjusting her basketball cap, completely oblivious to her impact on Agatha’s already mushy brain. “I’m not too late, am I?”

“You’re just in time, actually. Class doesn’t start for another hour, but of course you know that.” Agatha replies, stepping forward as Rio follows her inside. “I hope we’re not pulling you away from something important.”

“Not at all. My sous chefs can handle a few hours without me.” Rio says easily. “So this is what Rae’s been gushing about..”

Her voice lowers as she takes in the space, admiring the setup Lilia’s team somehow managed to pull together. Posters line the hallway walls with glossy stills of Agatha’s films and Lilia’s projects. Some frames contains award photos frozen in time.

Rio stops in front of one poster in particular. The title reads: Afternoon Delight.

“That’s the first movie I ever saw you in.”

Agatha feels heat creep up her neck but she keeps her composure steady. “Which means you’ve seen me having pretend sex with a man.”

Rio laughs, a little guilty. “I believe I have.”

“And you’ve seen my butt.” Agatha adds

“You don’t have to be embarrassed. It’s a cute butt.” Rio doesn’t hide it when she checks Agatha out the same way Agatha’s been looking at her toned stomach.

Guess they can call it even.

“Have fun looking at my ass.” Agatha mutters, rolling her eyes as she turns and leads Rio toward the room where Lilia and Kate are waiting.

She’s only mildly aware of the fact that Rio has seen her half-naked on a giant screen. It’s the art of the job, and so what if she did, really? Rio clearly is not the only one who has seen it.

“I’ve also heard your moan.” Rio adds lightly from behind her, obviously not done with the teasing.

Agatha stops abruptly Rio nearly crashes into her. She turns in slow motion, hands planted firmly on her hips.

“That wasn’t even my real moan.”

“Oh?”

“That was acting.” Agatha clarifies, then, without permission from her brain, she blabbers, “My real moan is better. You should hear it.”

They stare at each other in surprise, the air between them suddenly charged. It is far too intimate, perhaps inappropriate for a hallway lined with movie posters.

Agatha realizes the depth of what she said, how it sounded, and how easy it came out of her mouth. Jesus Christ, what is wrong with her?

Rio blinks first, her face unreadable. She was taken aback to the point she is lost for words, which is a rare occurrence.

Agatha clears her throat, already backpedaling in her head. What she said was truly elegant, sarcasm intended. Nothing screams ‘professional workshop mentor’ than offering a live demonstration of—

“Well..” She breaks the silence, her voice almost shaking. “Hypothetically. You know. In theory.” In theory. Sure.

Rio’s eyes flicker over her face, like she’s trying to decide whether to let Agatha off the hook or watch her dig deeper. Agatha prays it’s the first one.

“Harkness, there you are!” Lilia’s voice echoes from down the hall, making them both flinch in surprise.

Agatha closes her eyes for half a second, breathing in relief. Thank God for Lilia’s impeccable timing, she might just be saved by the bell.

“We’re ready for you.” Lilia calls out. “And please tell me you’re not traumatizing our guest.”

Agatha turns back to Rio, hiding her mortification with feign nonchalance. “I don’t traumatize people. I would never!”

Rio laughs under her breath as she finally finds her voice after the wave of a shock Agatha has given her. “Sure you won’t.”

As they start walking again, Rio leans in just enough to murmur. “We can circle back to that conversation later.”

Agatha very nearly trips over nothing.

“It’s nice meeting you, Chef Vidal.” Lilia says when they finally gather in the room, shaking Rio’s hand with genuine warmth. “Rae is such an amazing kid with spectacular talent. You’ve raised her well.”

“My, thank you.” Rio replies. “I hope my daughter doesn’t give you too much of a headache.”

“Never to me! She’s one of the sweetest.” Lilia assures her, pulling out a chair at their makeshift conference table. “Although, we’ve missed her terribly. When is she coming back?”

It’s funny how Rae is sweet as pie to Lilia and a complete menace to Agatha. The kid really did something special to earn Lilia’s devotion, and Agatha surely respects the hustle despite the inconvenience it has brought her.

“They’re flying first thing tomorrow.” Rio answers. “And I’d also like to apologize if she didn’t formally inform anyone she’d be missing class.”

“She actually sent an email.” Lilia says, eyes widening as Kate arrives with a few glasses of water. “Kate didn’t see it until later.”

“I said I was sorry.” Kate mutters and when she glances up at Rio, she freezes. Recognition flashes across her face, her gaze darting to Agatha in a flash. “Hey, weren’t you the one—”

“Chop chop!” Agatha cuts in sharply, shooting Kate a warning look that very clearly states finish that sentence and you’re dead. “We should get to planning. We don’t want to waste the chef’s valuable time, don’t we?”

Kate mimes zipping her mouth shut, afraid of what Agatha might do to her.

They settle into planning Lilia’s event, with Rio and Lilia doing most of the talking. Agatha contributes sparingly, mostly with unnecessary commentary.

“That’s too tacky.”

“A chocolate fountain? Lilia, it’s not 2003.

Lilia shoots her a glare sharp enough to silence her.

Rio, meanwhile, remains unfazed. She is professional throughout, clearly in her element. Agatha finds herself watching despite her best efforts. The way Rio talks through menu options with ease, the thoughtful pauses, and that one particular habit of her tongue pressing into her cheek when she’s thinking deep.

Eventually, they wrap up the meeting with Kate typing final notes into her iPad. The event will be held on the last day of the workshop. Rio generously offers to make the dinner exclusive at Rayo de Sol for the kids, their parents, and the entire team.

“It’s a pleasure doing business with you, Chef Vidal. I appreciate the time and effort.” Lilia thanks her.

“Likewise, Ms. Calderu.”

“Oh, don’t be a stranger, dear. Lilia will do just fine.”

“Lilia, then.” Rio smiles. “Actually, I’d love to invite you three to the restaurant on Wednesday, if you’re free. We’ve got a jazz act coming in from Las Vegas, thought you might enjoy the atmosphere.”

Lilia gasps softly, a hand flying to her chest while Kate’s eyes practically light up. They’d been vocal about how much they loved Rio’s restaurant, though with the demand for reservations, it wasn’t somewhere they could visit whenever they wanted.

“Are you serious?” Kate blurts out.

Agatha crosses her arms, suspicious of this act. “We don’t want to impose.” She states, popping the happy bubble of the two. “We’ve already been firsthand witnesses to how good your food is. You don’t need to prove anything.”

Rio meets her gaze without missing a beat. “Oh no.” She mutters lightly. “I insist.” Her tone is firm yet playful, which makes Agatha’s mouth twitch.

“Well..” Lilia cuts in cheerfully. “It would be rude to refuse such generosity.”

Kate nods far too enthusiastically. “Extremely rude.”

Agatha pinches the bridge of her nose, guess she can’t run away from this one. “Of course you’d both say that.”

Rio laughs, soft and genuine. “Then it’s settled.”

They begin to head out, class time inching closer. Lilia and Kate hang back to discuss schedules, leaving Agatha to walk Rio toward the entrance.

A small cluster of parents waits in the lounge, mostly mothers clutching the newest iPhones and stanleys. If Agatha knew better, she’d assume there’s vodka in at least one of those drinks.

The moment their eyes swivel toward Agatha and Rio, recognition lights up their faces immediately. Agatha catches it and knows the exact reason why.

These women never seem to get tired of her, despite the fact that they’ve already met more than a few times. Maybe it’s the novelty of it all, your kid being part of an exclusive class with the one and only Agatha Harkness.

They’re constantly making an elaborate move to befriend her. Others bring food with the goal of impressing her, may it be homemade pastries or catered boxes. They want to cling to her so bad so that they have something else to boast about on brunch other than their kid’s A+ reports or their husbands latest stock investment.

Agatha is firm about her boundaries. She’s not the type to collect suburban friendships, especially not with women who smile too brightly. She very much knows that they’re also the type to backstab you the moment you stop looking.

She’s seen their kind before, even played the role herself once (spoiler alert: the character went completely off the rails.)

Still, she’d be lying if she said she didn’t enjoy the attention. It never gets old.

For now, she’s prepared to brush them off with practiced ease except, she doesn’t have to because the attention slides right past her.

Every pair of vulture eyes shifts, not lingering on Agatha this time, but landing squarely on the woman beside her.

Rio.

Well, that’s new.

“Chef Vidal!”

They jump up from their usual seats and dash straight toward Agatha and Rio like a bunch of excited puppies being offered a small treat.

Paisley’s mom is the first to swoop in. “I knew that was you. I eat at Rayo del Sol all the time!”

Gavin’s mom follows close behind, breathless. “Me too. Impossible reservation, by the way. I had to wait four months.”

Agatha steps back automatically, shoes clicking against the floor. Rio simply smiles with her hands raised politely in greeting. The rest of the moms descend with the precision of a prey.

Their voices overlap one another with compliments, followed by questions, and unnecessary comments about how amazing Rio is in person. Agatha thinks at that moment that clearly, she isn’t the only celebrity in town.

Interesting.

“I don’t usually gush like this..” Gavin’s mom continues, chuckling nervously, which is a lie because she gushes like that all the time. “But wow! You’re even more charming in person.”

Paisley’s mom nods emphatically. “Honestly? I don’t even like women like that—” She adds, lowering her voice conspiratorially, “But something about you is making me feel things.”

Agatha blinks, couldn’t quite believe what she just heard. Excuse her?

The moms laugh. Rio laughs too, clearly flustered but gracious. “I’ll take that as a compliment.”

They crowd closer, closing the circle around Rio. Someone bumps Agatha’s shoulder, a move that almost knocks her off balance.

“Sorry!” The mom mutters distractedly, barely glancing at her as she squeezes past.

Then, without warning, a heel comes down squarely on Agatha’s foot, its sharpness buried straight to her skin. She bites back a yelp as sharp pain flares in.

She looks down. Of course, her open-toe shoes offer no protection. A trickle of blood runs between her toes, stark against her pale feet. Give it to Agatha to have a fair, easily bruised skin.

Perfect. Just perfect.

“I’m so sorry!” The mom who stepped on her chirps, already turning her back to Rio, completely oblivious to the damage they’ve done.

Agatha voluntarily stumbles half a step back this time to avoid being nudged again, ignoring the sting in her foot and the hint of redness creeping in her face.

She’s commanded sold-out theaters and held audiences in the palm of her hand with a single look. She knows how attention ebbs and flows. It can abandon you the second something shinier walks onstage.

And yet here she is, watching them orbit Rio. The compliments drip endlessly like honey from every direction. She sees hands casually brushing Rio’s arm. She hears a comment about how hot Rio looks, spoken with admiration.

Rio smiles like she often does, accepting every word with ease. Agatha doesn’t exactly know what she feels about that.

Her eyes narrow. Every giggle and whispered compliment from the other moms twists something tight in her chest. She can’t quite put a name to it, but watching how they hover around Rio, how they press close, how Rio meets their attention with that effortless warmth—it hits her all at once.

She doesn’t like it. Not one bit.

She really, really doesn’t like it.

“Alright!” Agatha yells, finally stepping forward. She’s had enough of whatever mass hysteria this is. “Chef Vidal has places to be.”

She pushes through the crowd, purposely nudging women aside as she slides a hand lightly onto Rio’s back. Not possessive but deliberate because, really, what right does she have to be possessive? Why would she even need to be? Who is she in Rio’s life, anyway?

That small act is enough to silently remind everyone in the room who’s really in control here.

“Of course.” Gavin’s mom murmurs. “Sorry.”

Paisley’s mom snickers, still a little breathless. “We just got excited!”

“Understandable.” Agatha replies, tight-lipped with a blank facial expression that leaves no room for argument. “Now, if you would excuse us.”

She steers Rio toward the exit, forcing herself to keep her stride steady. She’s about to drop Rio off at the curb, ready to let her go back to the restaurant or whatever it is she will do next while she deals with the chaos inside but then Rio slows, glancing down.

Her eyebrows raise, just slightly. “What happened to your feet?”

Rio’s wincing at the small trickle of blood against Agatha’s fair, delicate skin. Agatha tries to hide her foot and pretend it’s nothing, but Rio’s not fooled.

“Let’s not do that.” Rio says insistently. “You’re bleeding. We can’t just ignore that.”

Agatha stiffens, pride warring with practicality. “It’s nothing. It’s barely a scratch. I’ll be fine.”

Rio tilts her head, looking at Agatha with a firm look. “You’re not fine.”

“How can you say that?” Agatha snaps.  “These are my feet, not yours—hey!”

She can’t protest further when Rio reaches for her arm, gentle but firm, guiding her toward a direction Agatha has no choice but to follow.

“I have a first-aid kit in my car.” Rio tells her “And don’t even think about running unless you want me to carry you and trust me, I can do that.”

The possessiveness in Agatha’s chest tightens not for herself, but for the thought of someone else caring for her. She’s not used to letting anyone see her weak spots, may it be the smallest of bruise and yet here she is.

Agatha huffs, giving in. “Fine.”

Rio just smiles and brings her to the area where she parked her Bentley. She opens the passenger door and guides her inside. Agatha folds her arms once seated, but she doesn’t resist.

Rio finds a small first-aid kit in the glove compartment. Agatha watches her in the rearview mirror, an unknown emotion coiling in her chest. She knows she should be annoyed that someone else is fussing over her, but instead.. she can’t help the feeling of relief, and something infuriatingly unknown.

“Stop staring at me.” She rolls her eyes again.

Rio doesn’t, not really. She just kneels slightly beside the open car door to tend to Agatha’s foot, her touch careful and precise as if she knows what she’s doing, having done it a couple of times. Probably. 

Agatha feels something rising from her chest. She knows it’s not from pain, but from the awareness that this attention, this care.. is hers.

And hers alone.

Her mind tries to shove the thought away, but it refused to be ignored. This is inappropriate, she tells herself. Completely inappropriate. 

“Rae gets bruises all the time.” Rio says, dabbing a gauze over Agatha’s ankle. “Even from simple bumps. I guess I know where she got it from.”

“Well sorry if I’m so easily bruised. That’s not exactly something I can control.”

Rio laughs softly, the sound warm and teasing. “I know, I wasn’t even blaming you. I was just saying.”

A comfortable silence settles between them as Rio focuses on her feet, cleaning and wrapping with precision while Agatha fights to keep the storm of thoughts in her head from spilling out. 

“You’re quite the celebrity out there.” Agatha lets her observation slip. “I didn’t realize people around here knew you so well.”

“I’m not.” Rio replies, glancing up for a second. “But I guess the moms know me from the restaurant, and some of their kids go to Rae’s school. Imagine what the PTA meetings are usually like.”

Agatha didn’t even attempt to picture it. The thought of even more moms hovering around Rio made her chest ache, a flush of jealousy creeping up her throat. 

There it is. The unnamed feeling, jealousy.

Is she jealous? Of course not. Why would she be?

But then again, how can she explain the way her eyelids twitch when Rio smiled at someone else? And if that isn’t jealousy, then what the hell is it?

“Remember the first time we met?”

“Mhm?” 

“You called me humble, but I think you’re the humble one. It’s more appropriate.”

One corner of Rio’s mouth tugs in amusement. “You’re just noticing now?”

Agatha sighs. “You’re insufferable sometimes.”

“Insufferable?” Rio questions. “I prefer charmingly irresistible.” Agatha rolls her eyes as Rio finishes cleaning her bruised foot. 

She shifts slightly in her seat, leaning just a little forward, angling herself so they can stay this close without standing. Her knee brushed Rio’s thigh, and the heat of the contact shot straight through her chest.

Every inch of proximity makes her heart hammer. She tells herself to stay composed and to act cool, but as Rio meets her gaze with a soft smile, Agatha knew it was over for her.

“You’re testing me.” Agatha’s voice drop, almost in a challenging way.

“And you’re failing.” Rio grins, brushing her fingers lightly against Agatha’s calf as she adjusts the bandage. That simple contact sent an involuntary shiver up Agatha’s spine.

Agatha couldn’t help but recall the earlier moment in the workshop. All the teasing comments and the playful tension that had made her cheeks burn. The memory returns and can she feel her resolve crumbling a little.

Just a bit.

“You know..” Rio murmurs, voice low and teasing. “If I remember correctly, you still owe me a demonstration.”

Agatha freezes yet again. Her eyes locked on Rio’s, and in that moment, the world seemed to stop moving. 

She’s become suddenly aware of the faint antiseptic smell, the quiet hum of the car, the bandage, the way Rio’s fingers rests gently on her ankle—all of it came together into one maddening moment. Her heartbeat thudded audibly in her ears, her skin tingling.

Fuck it.

Her rational mind is gone. She leans forward even more, resting both arms on Rio’s shoulders and pulling her close as her lips clashes with Rio’s in a sudden kiss.

All logic was gone. Every “what if” erased, every limit crossed. Agatha didn’t care. 

She knew the moment she met Rio that she really, really liked her. Liked her more than she had any right to, more than she’d admit to anyone, even herself.

Rio’s eyes widen briefly in surprise, then softens. She doesn’t pull away. Instead, she tilts her head, letting Agatha set the pace.

When she finally gives in to the kiss, it’s slow and easy, with tenderness that makes Agatha’s chest ache and melt at the same time.

Fuck it.

She leans in harder, claiming Rio with a boldness she’s never allowed herself before, pressing her lips firmly against the other woman and letting everything else.. the wrong, the doubts, their situation, even the world—fall away.

When Agatha pulls back, Rio instinctively leans forward again, like she’s not quite ready to let the moment end. Agatha stops her with a single finger to her lips, gentle but firm.

“Now..” She teases, a dangerous glint in her eyes, “Don’t be too greedy.”

Rio blinks in daze. “Your lips are really soft.” She says, the thought escaping naturally before she can stop it. “That was—”

“Don’t mention it.” Agatha cuts in, already pushing Rio away so she can step out of the car. She moves in one graceful motion, as if her pulse isn’t racing. “Thanks for the aid.”

She walks off like she didn’t just knock the air out of another woman’s lungs.

A few steps in, Rio finds her voice. “You didn’t show me the demonstration!”

Agatha stops and grins to face Rio for the last time that day. “Maybe next time.”

Inside the building, the door closes behind her, and only then does the weight of it hit. The resolve she’d carefully stacked all week collapses in on itself. Every boundary she’d sworn to keep is ruined and every sensible thought is gone.

She shouldn’t have done that. She knows that. She really, really knows that but this time, she didn’t hold back.

Not for a second, definitely not in that kiss.

For the infinite time, Agatha thinks, fuck it. 

She’ll leave it to the universe now—and see what it decides to do with her next. 

Now, what do the kids say? Hashtag YOLO?

Well, hashtag fucking YOLO indeed.
