Chapter 11: Chapter 11

Chapter Notes

enjoy your first of the month treat.. or not xx

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“What do you think, chef?” Alice asks eagerly, setting the bowl down with practice carefulness of somebody doing a sacred offering.

Alice is one of Rio’s oldest friends, dating all the way back to college. She’s her partner in crime when testing shady food stands at their 20s turned to her most trusted sous chef in their 40s.

Steam curls up from the surface as Rio grabs a spoon to taste Alice’s variation of a poblano soup, a tweak from an old recipe. Whatever version of a midlife crisis Alice is having, it manifests itself in relentless innovation. Rio, for her part, is nothing but encouraging and supportive.

“It’s really good.” Rio tastes it once. Then again, slower this time as she lets the flavors sit. “But something’s missing.”

She scans the kitchen, eyes moving past stainless steel until they land firmly on the infamous wall where rows of spices lined up like old friends who know her too well, having spent so much time in the kitchen.

They do in fact knew her too well if they simply had minds of their own, each spices earning its honor from years of playing with flavor until it finally made sense.

It always made sense, no matter how hard the process is. That’s just how it goes for Rio.

She moves and reaches for a small bottle of ground coriander. Alice watches closely as Rio sprinkles it in, grabs a clean spoon, stirs, and tastes again.

She pushes the bowl toward her friend’s direction. “Try it now.”

Alice takes a spoonful, her eyes questioning but never skeptical. “Shit.” She mutters. “C'est magnifique!”

Rio laughs, nudging her playfully out of the way. “Best chef in town, remember?” It’s meant as a joke for her, although it just happens to be true for everyone else.

Her entire life, Rio had been handed options in golden trays. As the eldest daughter of Luella and Manolo Vidal, she was meant to inherit ancient legacies of fortune made from vast businesses. 

But even as a kid, she never wanted to pursue career related to all of that. She never let money be the thing that defined her. She barely noticed it most days despite seeing huge infrastructures with her last name stamped on it everywhere she go. 

All she ever really wanted is the kitchen, the food, and the act of cooking itself.

She knew how lucky she was to have parents who didn’t fight her on it. They allowed her to leave for culinary school in France without turning it into a scandal. They trusted her to find her own path, even when it didn’t look conventional.

Her restaurant wasn’t handed to her. Well, restaurants, rather.

She worked first, long shifts in someone else’s kitchen or the family’s hotel chain. She worked through burns and aching feet for paychecks that made enough, but it barely rivaled to what her college allowance had once been.

She saved and yes, she dipped into her trust fund when she decided it was the right time to build a restaurant of her own. She knew her privilege, having more than just a chef’s salary to rely on with other ventures such as investments and she had always acknowledged that.

Rayo del Sol came later. Rae was nine by then, old enough to read the sign and understand the sense of pride at what her mami had built, especially knowing it bore her name. She made sure everyone at school knew it, and she basked in the attention, loving every bit of it.

Speaking of Rae.. “Mami!”

The doors from the main dining room swing open, and Rae comes barreling in fast. “My love—” Rio startles, then laughs, opening her arms just in time for Rae to crash into her. She folds around her instinctively the same way she always does even when Rae was younger. “You’re here!”

“I missed you, mami.” Rae says, pulling back just enough to look up at her. “Were you incredibly sad without me?”

“Absolutely devastated.” Rio mutters solemnly, giving Rae’s hair a quick kiss. “Look at you, you’re sunburned! Did you forget sunscreen again?”

Rae shrugs nonchalantly. Pink dusts her cheeks and the bridge of her nose, glowing with evidence. “I wanted to get tan but considering how naturally pale I am, I’m basically a victim of the sun.”

“Such a tragic tale.” Rio says, cupping Rae’s face gently, thumbs brushing her warm face. “You’re going to peel.”

“Worth it.”

Rio smiles, but something in her chest eases in a way she hadn’t realized was tight in the first place.

She tends to do this. She counts the hours without meaning to and tells herself she’s busy enough not to notice the quiet.

There are a thousand things she could be worrying about. The restaurant. The kiss. Agatha. Rae.. but right now, Rae is here. She is sunburned and grinning and wrapped around her like she never left.

That’s enough to make Rio feel steady again, even if it’s temporary.

“I got something for everyone!” Rae announces happily. “I got you an anklet since you lost yours when we went to Mexico last year. I also brought spices native to Hawaii, I think you’ll love them!”

“That’s very generous of you, my love.” Rio says with adoration, moving a strand of hair behind Rae’s ears. “I hope your money didn’t all disappear.”

“Oh, abuela gave me more, so I got to splurge.” Rio rolls her eyes fondly. Everyone in her family spoils Rae, despite Rio’s constant warnings not to. They ignore her every time, giving her daughter everything she asks for—her mother being the number one suspect.

“I even got Lilia this really cute flowy beach bag.” Rae adds, miming its shape with her hands. “And some shell necklaces for my friends at the workshop!”

“You did?” Rio asks, suddenly hopeful. “Did you get anything for Agatha?”

“For who?”

“For Agatha.” Surely, Rio thinks. She wouldn’t have skipped Agatha when she’d bought gifts for others in the workshop.

Rae chuckles incredulously, as if her mami just told the worst joke she’s ever heard. “Why would I get her anything?”

Rio stills. “Because you said you got something for everyone?”

“Well, she’s not included in that everyone, mami. Don't be silly.” Rae says casually, crossing her arms. “She’s not even anyone.”

“Raina, what did I say about being nice?”

“I am being nice.” Rae pouts. “And what if I say I simply forgot about her?”

Rio sighs. She knows that tone, she’s very well acquainted with that tone. It’s the one Rae uses when she’s already made up her mind about how she feels and dares the world to challenge it. Anyone who does will be given a difficult time.

Rae is nice. Thoughtful, even. She brings gifts, she remembers birthdays, and she shows up whenever she’s needed. With that comes stubbornness in a very specific way.

Rio would describe it as rooted or principled. Once her daughter decides that something matters, she clutches it with unyielding intensity. When she determines it no longer holds weight, she releases it just as fiercely, letting it fall away as though it had never existed. 

“Anyway..” Rae hums, already backing toward the door. “I’ll go say hi to the staff first. Will you be driving me home in awhile?”

“Of course I will.”

Rae smiles, then turns and jogs off toward the other area of the restaurant, calling out greetings as she goes.

Rio stays where she is, watching until Rae disappears completely. The melancholy comes quietly, a whole new different emotion settling in her chest this time around.

She never intended for Rae to feel a certain way of what seemed to be hatred for her birth mother. Or anyone, really. 

From the beginning, Rio had been careful. Honest in ways that mattered. She made sure Rae understood that people don’t always leave because they don’t care. That sometimes, hurtful choices are made out love.

She had defended Agatha long before Rae even knew her name.

But Rae is Rae.

She doesn’t open easily. She listens, but she doesn’t accept without proof. She demands effort and consistency. Words mean nothing to her without action trailing close behind.

And Agatha, for all her brilliance, would have to live with the fact that she was already being measured by a girl who did not make room for excuses.

Rio presses a thumb on top of her temple, moving it in circling motion to avoid impending migraines.

“Honey, I’m here!”

A familiar voice cuts clean through the steady rhythm of the kitchen. A few heads turn from their stations as Wanda enters the room where Rio is.

“Back here.” Rio calls.

Wanda beams when she spots her. “I knew you’d be hiding close to where the knives are.”

“I live here.” Rio answers. “What did you forget this time?”

Wanda chuckles and reaches into her tote, producing a slim baking pan with a sheepish tilt of her head. “Your tart pan. I swear I meant to bring it back last week.”

Rio takes it from her, already grinning. “Say no more. If I had a dollar for every time someone kept my kitchenware hostage, I’d retire.”

“Sure, but you’d still cook.” Rio nods. That part is probably true.

Rae reappears the moment she hears Wanda’s voice, rushing to her aunt in excitement.

“Aunt Wanda!” 

Wanda turns and visibly melts. “Oh my god.” She says, pressing a hand to her chest. “There she is. Every time I see you, you look older, and taller.. and somehow prettier, which feels unfair.”

Rae grins. “You’re contractually obligated to say that.”

“I am not.” Wanda insists. “I do it willingly. I mean, look at you!” Wanda lets Rae give a little twirl for show. She’s always had a soft spot for Rio’s daughter, filling a space she never quite had the chance to on her own.

Rio watches the exchange quietly. She’s seen it a hundred times before, people softening the second Rae enters a room. Rae has always carried that effect, even as a child.

“You didn’t come to my housewarming party.”

“I had ballet, but I’ll make sure to come visit soon!” Rae explains shortly. “Are the twins with you?”

“They’re sitting in the car refusing to get out.” Wanda groans. “They figured you might be here and Tommy is ever so defensive. Perhaps he got it from his father.”

Re’s eyes light up. “Are they actually scared of me?”

“Mortified.” Wanda says fondly. “Billy even locked the doors.”

Rae laughs. “Seriously?”

Wanda sighs and pulls her keys out of her bag, jingling them once before placing them into Rae’s open palm. “Have fun with it.”

“Yes!” Rae giggles, already walking away. “They’ve been avoiding me for the longest time, now they don’t have a choice.”

The kitchen door swings shut behind her, as Wanda watches her go with a soft smile. Then she turns back to Rio, eyebrow arching slightly. “She’s something else.”

“She always has been.” Rio mutters. “You know she’ll torture your sons, right?”

“Most likely.” Wanda waves a dismissive hand. “But they deserve it for giving me a hell of a week. I don’t know what it is with kids nowadays, they can’t even separate clean clothes from the laundry.”

“Thank God I have a girl.” 

They laugh in chorus as Wanda leans against the counter, glancing around the kitchen with an appreciative nod. “Place looks busy.”

“All the time.” Rio confirms. “Though you did came at a calm moment, which means it won’t last.”

“I’ll savor it, then.” Wanda’s gaze lingers on Rio for a beat longer than necessary, a familiar glint appearing in her eyes. “So..”

Rio feels the shift, which signals that Wanda is about to poke at something. “So,” Rio echoes cautiously.

“You and my good friend Agatha Harkness.”

There it is. She’s been anticipating for Wanda to bring this up one way or another. “That’s one way to put it.”

Wanda’s smile turns delighted. “I’m still wrapping my head around it.”

“There’s nothing to wrap.” Rio shrugs. “She’s running a workshop in town. Rae’s enrolled in it. Voila!”

“Yes, Einstein.” Her friend quips. “I know that part. What I didn’t expect was for you two to be that close.”

“We’re not.”

“Nu-uh, my senses says otherwise.” Wanda presses more. “You’re acting suspiciously calm about this.”

“When have you become a busybody?” Rio asks. “Besides, I don’t see the point in dramatizing it. We simply know each other, Wands. That’s it.”

Rio doesn’t like lying, but she also knows this isn’t hers to explain. She isn’t even sure what is happening between her and Agatha—only that they’ve spent a few moments together, shared one kiss, and that somehow, Agatha has lingered in her thoughts since the moment they first met. 

Still, that isn’t something she can hand to Wanda so easily. Or to anyone else, in that matter.

“It’s complicated.” Rio offers just enough to avoid a lie but not nearly enough to satisfy curiosity. She knows Wanda won’t stop prying unless she draws the line here.

Wanda’s grin widens. “Is it?”

“If anything happens, I promise I’ll let you know.” Rio assures her, even though she isn’t entirely sure what she means by that herself.

“Alright. Does Rae know?”

Rio’s stomach tightens in a way that is subtle but undeniable. “Know what?”

Wanda studies her for a moment. “Nothing. Just curious.”

Rio doesn’t respond immediately. She focuses her attention elsewhere as her thoughts drift. Rae bristles at the mere mention of Agatha, a reaction that feels too big to be casual dislike.

She doesn’t want Rae to carry anger she doesn’t fully understand. She also doesn’t want what she has with Agatha (whatever it is) to become a symbol of something broken before either of them has the chance to speak honestly.

Wanda softens, noticing Rio’s demeanor. “You know I’m mostly teasing, right?” Rio nods. “You don’t have to tell me anything, unless you want to.”

Rio mumbles a small, “I know,” as they settle into a different conversation, Wanda happily steering the topic away.

After a few minutes, the door swings open again as Rae reappears, looking absolutely triumphant.

“Honey, please tell me there’s no bloodshed.” Wanda says as Rae hands her back the car keys. “I just got a carwash.”

“I’d never do that to you.” Rae says with a smile, batting her eyelashes in mock innocence. Then she glances between them, perceptive despite her playful tone. “So, what did I miss?”

“Nothing.” Rio says quickly.

“We divulged ourselves in casual adult conversation that is monotonous to you young ones.” Wanda supplies.

Rae’s expressions are transparent, which makes her mood easier to read. She narrows her eyes but says nothing, which works to Rio’s advantage. “Mami, can we go home soon?” She asks instead.

Rio’s answer comes without hesitation. “Whenever you’re ready, my love.”

Wanda watches the two of them, something thoughtful passing over her face. “Well, I should get going before the twins decide the car is their new home.”

“You really should check on them.” Rio winces, mentally noting she should probably ask Rae what new schemes she’s cooked up to scare the twins this time. “And try to return my tart pan a little sooner next time.”

“No promises.” They exchange a quick hug as Wanda squeezes Rio’s arm knowingly before stepping away.

The next day, Rio drives Rae to the workshop earlier than planned, which isn’t unusual. Rio has always preferred arriving early to enjoy the calm before others fill it with noises.

Rae doesn’t complain. She’s seated cross-legged in the passenger seat, humming to herself as her fingers drum lightly against the paper bag resting in her lap. 

When Rio had mentioned hosting Lilia's thanksgiving dinner for the workshop, Rae had lit up immediately. She’d launched into ideas such as theme suggestions, who should sit where, and what dessert would impress without trying too hard. 

Rio listens patiently the entire time, silently savoring Rae’s presence. After a brief vacation, having her daughter back feels like the missing piece has been found. It also serves as a reminder of how quiet her life had been without her.

They pull into the parking lot and step out into the late morning air. Rae is already halfway into the building before Rio even opens the car door.

She follows her daughter into the large room where classes takes place. Only Lilia and Kate are there, seated close together with heads bent in conversation. Agatha is nowhere to be seen, give it to Rio to notice her absence right away.

Huh. She hadn’t come here for Agatha but somehow, she’s searching for her. What does that say about Rio?

“I’ve missed you all!” Rae calls out brightly as she runs forward, nearly tripping over her own enthusiasm.

Lilia looks up and breaks into a wide smile. “Well, here is my star. Finally!” She stands to pull Rae into a hug. “How was Hawaii, sweetheart?”

“Sunny.” Rae says, pointing to her face. “Painfully so. My skin is protesting.”

Kate laughs. “I love your tan, Rae.”

“Thank you.” Rae beams. “I hope I didn’t miss too much.”

“Nothing you can’t catch up on quickly.” Lilia tells her.

Rio remains by the door, hands loosely folded in front of her.

She loves moments like this. Moments where Rae is accepted without question, where her sharp edges are met with warmth instead of resistance.

Rae is kind but she is also firm, adamant when she feels challenged or dismissed. It’s a strength that sometimes makes the world push back harder than necessary.

Seeing her here, surrounded by people who like her as she is settles something in Rio’s chest.

“You’re here.” The voice comes from her left, making Rio jump slightly in surprise. She turns and finds Agatha standing there, having apparently materialized without warning.

To make things worse, she looks.. unfair.

She’s wearing a black button-up, loose enough to command attention as the neckline dips just enough to be distracting. Her hair is in its usual curly state, looking healthier than ever. On top of that, a pair of vintage looking glasses sit low on her nose.

Rio has to actively remind herself where she is and who she’s with.

Get it together, you freak.

“Oh.” She says, the word slipping out lower than intended. “Hi. I didn’t see you come in.”

“Clearly.” She remarks. “Why are you here?” Agatha asks casually, but there’s an undercurrent Rio can’t quite name.

“I have a proposal to discuss with Lilia about dinner.” She pauses, then adds gently, “Rae’s here too, she arrived yesterday.”

Agatha’s expression shifts upon the mention of Rae’s name.

If Rio weren’t looking at her intensely, she wouldn’t have catched the subtle flicker in her eyes. Agatha’s fingers lift instinctively to the necklace resting at her throat, thumb brushing over the pendant in one motion.

“Nice glasses.” Rio points out, hoping to smooth the moment before it hardens.

Agatha glances at her. “They’re for reading.” She replies, already removing them. She sets her glasses carefully on top of her clothes, much to Rio’s quiet disappointment. “I got sent a script last night so I had to look it over.”

“Oh.” Rio mutters once more. “That makes sense.”

They stand there for a moment, neither quite stepping away. Rio is acutely aware of the space between them, the memory of their kiss humming under her skin. 

She likes Agatha. There’s no point denying it anymore. She likes her in a way that feels reckless and grounding all at once, and it scares her.

Liking Agatha doesn’t exist in some separate dimension. It exists here, in the same world as Rae. And Rae.. Rae has mixed feelings toward Agatha which might complicate everything if they decide to act on them. 

That is—if Agatha feels the same way at all.

“Mami!” Rae calls from across the room. “Come here!”

The spell breaks as Rio gestures lightly toward the room. “Come on.” She says to Agatha, already moving.

The paper bag is open now, souvenirs laid out neatly across a table. Rae stands proudly in front of them, hands clasped behind her back.

“This is for you.” Rae announces, pushing one toward Lilia. “I bought you this bag and this scarf because I thought it matched your vibe.”

Lilia laughs, touched. “You remembered me.”

“Of course I did.”

“And this is for you.” Rae continues, handing Kate a small box. “That’s not Van Cleef but it’s a really pretty bracelet.”

Kate’s giggles. “Thank you, Rae.”

“Well..” Agatha steps forward at last, revealing herself to the rest of the group. “If it isn’t Rae. Back so soon?”

“Yes.” Rae replies coolly. “I couldn’t let you keep believing you’re the best actor in the room other than Lilia. Someone has to humble you.”

Agatha smirks. “Bold of you to assume you could.”

Rio stands there, heart caught somewhere between them.

She understands Rae’s defensiveness. She understands Agatha’s restraint. And she hates that she’s the only one in the room who understands both.

This is exactly what scares her.

She wants Agatha. The sharp wit and the quiet moments where Agatha lets her guard slip. She likes how alive she feels around her.

At the same time, she loves Rae. Real love demands care and understanding. That’s what makes it confusing, the conflict of this all.

Rio doesn’t know how to bridge that gap yet. For now, she only knows she’s standing right in the middle of it.

“I know I could.” Rae grins. “I’m young and I haven’t even reached my prime. Imagine what I could do then.”

Agatha turns fully toward her now, hands slipping casually into her pockets. “You know, for someone who missed a few classes, you seem very eager to critique.”

“I had time to reflect.” Rae replies sweetly. “Distance does wonders for clarity. You should try it sometime.”

Rio watches them circle each other with practiced ease. To Kate and Lilia, it probably reads as harmless sparring. A teenager testing boundaries and an actress enjoying the challenge, nothing more.

But Rio knows better. She sees the precision in Rae’s words, the way each sentence lands exactly where it’s meant to. She sees how Agatha never looks away, how her attention sharpens rather than floats away. This is nowhere near casual.

“Alright, children!” Lilia interferes. “Save the dueling philosophies for later.”

“Sorry, Lilia.”

Agatha inclines her head. “Of course.”

Kate gestures to the table. “These gifts are really thoughtful, Rae.”

“They’re souvenirs.” Rae clarifies. “I figured if I was going to be gone, I should come back properly.”

Agatha hums. “Preparedness, another surprise.”

Rae glances back at her. “You seem disappointed.”

Agatha arches a brow. “Should I be?”

“You look like you are, unless I’m mistaken.” Rae mocks, shrugging. “I didn’t get you anything though. I really didn’t thought of you, apparently you have slipped my mind.”

Rio feels it then as she watches Agatha, whose jaw tightens for a fraction of a second before she smooths it away.

“Raina.” Rio says her name, nothing more. But Rae takes it as a warning and doesn’t push further. Brave as she is, Rae has her limits, especially when Rio uses her full name, the one that clearly says don’t be difficult.

“You know, Rae, you’re the only person I’ve met who gets sunburned as badly as Agatha.” Lilia steers the conversation, her tone light. “She suffered through the same thing in Cabo a few months ago, despite all the expensive sunscreen she swears she applied.”

“Lilia, I don’t think they want to hear that story.” Agatha deadpans.

“I’m just saying.” Lilia grits her teeth, giving Agatha a pointed look. “You two are a lot more alike than you’d care to admit, despite all the banter.”

Rio almost chokes on nothing. Lilia says it casually, but all three of them feel the weight behind it: the resemblance, the mirrored stubbornness, the quiet ways they’re drawn together. It’s impossible to miss, and they know exactly why.

Lilia claps her hands once. “Alright, that’s enough. Chef Vidal, why don’t you tell us what you wanted to discuss?”

“Right. Yes. So—” Rio is glad to finally put an end to the tension Rae and Agatha had created.

She recognizes the tension for what it is. They are two people testing strength and measuring each other’s intent. Rae has built a wall while Agatha is holding herself carefully, acutely aware of every misstep.

Rio joins the rest of the adults at the table while Rae lingers nearby, close enough to hear everything without saying much. 

The proposal moves easily. Lilia asks thoughtful questions, Kate chimes in with logistics, and Agatha listens more than she speaks, offering the occasional condescending comments. 

At some point, Agatha shifts in her chair, reaching for her bag, and her glasses slip free. Once it hit the floor softly, both of them move at once.

Rio bends instinctively, already reaching out, and Agatha does the same. Their hands collide, fingers brushing before either of them can pull away. 

Rio stills in her place as Agatha’s breath catches. For a second, the room feels distant, reduced to the space between their hands and the quiet awareness of each other.

Agatha looks up first, sharp blue eyes meeting Rio’s. Rio feels something warm and dangerous settle low in her chest. She likes this.. she likes the closeness, the accidental intimacy, and the way Agatha doesn’t joke her way out of it pronto.

Then Lilia coughs, the moment breaking at once.

Agatha withdraws her hand quickly, straightening her posture in the chair. Rio, whose hands reached the glasses first, passes them to her.

“Thanks.” Agatha takes them carefully, slipping them on calmly rather than tucking them back into her clothes.

“No worries.” Rio replies.

Rae’s gaze flicks between them before she looks away again as if she's bored.

The rest of the conversation wraps itself up without ceremony. Lilia is satisfied and Rio nods along, committing additional details to memory. 

Rio slings her bag over her shoulder and moves toward the door, each step measured. Agatha rises as well, just enough to meet her gaze, a subtle pull that says don’t go just yet. 

Rio stops, caught by the quiet insistence in her posture. “Wait.” Agatha says, voice low, almost hopeful. “I—”

Rae clears her throat behind them, a single note that cuts through the shared space. Rio glances back and sees her daughter standing near the doorway, her presence alone says mami, that’s enough.

Rio sighs slowly. She wants to stay. She wants to step forward, brush a stray curl from Agatha’s face, maybe lean in close enough to hear her laugh. She wants to reach for the warmth she’s felt lingering since the last time they were alone, the faint ache left by stolen glances and an unforgettable kiss. 

However, Rae’s steadying presence keeps her rooted. Rae comes first. Always had, always been, always will. Rio reminds herself of that.

“I have a meeting to go to.” Rio says, her tone apologetic. “I’ll see you some other time?”

She catches the hint of disappointment across Agatha’s face, but the woman masks it just as quickly. “If my schedule permits.” Agatha replies, the calm politeness burying the hope that hides just beneath.

Rio takes it as her cue to leave, offering a final goodbye to the team before letting Rae lead her toward the parking lot.

Once in the car, Rio settles into the driver’s seat, hands gripping the wheel a little tighter than necessary. Her mind keeps drifting back to Agatha’s gaze, that quiet mix of hope and restraint that she can’t shake. She can’t bear the weight of that look lingering unacknowledged, not when she’s trapped in traffic.

Almost reflexively, she pulls out her phone and sends a short message.

Rio: are you okay?

A typing bubble appears on Rio’s screen, and she watches it blink and fade. A full minute passes without a reply. Sighing softly, she sets her phone down, telling herself that Agatha is probably just busy with class, too caught up to respond right now.

That same night, the living room is dim except for the glow of the television. One of Rio’s comfort cooking shows plays softly, the host narrating something about the role of technology in cooking.

Rae is sprawled across her mami’s lap, knees tucked up, Kindle balanced against her chest. Rio’s fingers move through her long hair in slow strokes, the motion as familiar as breathing.

“Mami?”

“Mhm?” Rio hums, eyes still on the screen as her thumb presses the remote, pausing the show.

“Would you ever date again?”

Rio’s fingers still as she chuckles awkwardly. “Where’s that coming from?”

“I don’t know.” Rae says. “Just a question.”

It’s never just a question with Rae. Rio knows this. She’s known it since Rae was little, how her daughter tests the ground before stepping into it. 

Rae is observant and notices everything, she always has. She just chooses carefully what she admits to noticing.

Rio keeps her tone even. “Honestly, I couldn’t say for sure.” She watches the words as she says them, weighing each one. “I’m not closing that chapter of my life. Who knows? Maybe one day.”

Rae doesn’t respond right away. The silence stretches as Rae shifts. She pushes herself upright, turning so she’s sitting and facing Rio properly now. Her Kindle is forgotten on the couch.

“Mami.” She calls again, quieter this time.

“Yes, my love?”

“Does what I think still matter to you?”

Rio’s chest tightens but she doesn’t hesitate. “Of course it does.” Her hand moves to Rae’s cheek, thumb brushing lightly along her jaw. “It always will. You know you’re the most important person in my life, right?”

Rae’s mouth curves into a small smile. “I know, mami.”

She nods once, as if confirming something internally, then adds, “But hypothetically—if you dated someone, and I didn’t like that someone.. would you listen to me?” Rae’s voice cracks just a little. “Would you.. would you even choose me?”

The question lands harder than the others.

She looks at her daughter.. really looks at her. The careful way Rae carries herself, the quiet vulnerability she doesn’t try to hide. The way her eyes search Rio’s face for answers.

Rio understands then, with a clarity that hurts a little.

Rae knows something. Rio doesn’t know what, or how, but she can feel the awareness slipping through the cracks. Rae knows enough to sense the presence of someone new orbiting too close.

Rio feels the conflict rise in her chest because there is indeed someone. Because she is, against her better judgment, already in deeper than she meant to be. 

Rio will cross that bridge when she comes to it, deciding later if she should act on her feelings. For now, she cups Rae’s face gently, grounding herself in the warmth of her skin.

“I will always choose you.” Her voice did not waver. “There is no version of my life where I don’t.”

Rae studies her for a moment longer, as if testing the truth of it. Then she nods, satisfied. “I couldn't be luckier to have you as my mom, mami.”

She turns back and settles into Rio’s lap again, grabbing her Kindle. Rae goes quiet, but Rio’s thoughts refuse to settle so easily. While she continues stroking Rae’s hair, her mind drifts back to Agatha, the someone in question. 

Being around her presence, her voice, to the way her glasses slipped and how absurdly intimate that moment felt. To how alive she’d felt, and how guilty that aliveness now seems.

Rio presses her lips briefly to the top of Rae’s head. She loves her daughter more than anything. That part is simple and non-negotiable.

What isn’t simple is the realization that her heart has started to want something else, and that wanting doesn’t feel like a betrayal, even if it might look like one from the outside.

Rio sits there, holding both truths at once, knowing this is only the beginning.

She can only hope it will make sense one day, just like everything else in her life.

Chapter 12: Chapter 12

Chapter Notes

i think we all need this chapter (at the end of the day, rae is still a babie.. rio’s baby particularly and maybe, agatha’s too?) :p

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha: I’m planning to speak with Rae today.

Agatha stares at the screen a beat longer than necessary before sliding her phone back into her pocket, in case Rio replies late. Or early. Or if she even replies at all, after Agatha left her on read the other day.

She tells herself she doesn’t care—which is a lie, but at least it’s a familiar one.

She has sworn that she’ll finally find the nerve to speak to Rae now that the kid is back from vacation. She’s rehearsed the conversation more times than she’s willing to admit, practiced it in the mirror with different expressions and tones. 

She tried being casual, which seems far too casual for her liking. Detached might make Rae feel like she doesn’t take this seriously. She attempted to be maternal, which she immediately scraps because it looks ridiculous on her.

None of it matters. She knows the second Rae looks at her, the words will disappear all at once. She tells herself that the intention is there, and that has to count for something.

Agatha wants to work it out if Rae will let her. Whatever role Rae is willing to tolerate her in, she’ll take it. She’s not that greedy.

What she can’t fathom is Rae telling her to disappear completely from her life without giving her a chance of being there at all.

It’s not unlikely, considering their history. Agatha prepares herself for the worst. She can only pray that whatever decision the kid makes, hopefully she makes peace with it.. 

Although, accepting it doesn’t mean it won’t hurt.

But what are Agatha Harkness’ awards if she can’t pull a performance? She can smile throughout, take the hit with grace, and walk away pretending her heart isn’t being pulled apart by the simple possibility of it.

Agatha’s fingers curl around the pendant at her throat as her gaze sweeps the room, searching for Rae. She thinks of more reasons to make the kid listen to whatever she has to say later on.

For today’s workshop activity, the young actors are tasked with creating original scenes in groups, allowing them full creative control of their choosing. Rae, of course, has appointed herself the lead, the director, and the writer, of her small army.

Agatha can’t help the secret grin that curves her mouth every time she passes Rae’s group. Rae is bossing everyone around her, issuing instructions with the confidence of someone used to being in charge.

“No, don’t stand there. You’re blocking the light. And don’t do that thing with your face when you deliver the last line, you look constipated.”

She keeps walking, hands clasped behind her back and handing out comments every now and then. Rae doesn’t acknowledge her, at least not directly. 

Agatha sees the way Rae’s attention sharpens whenever she speaks to the room. The way Rae’s head tilts just slightly as she glances over and then looks away too fast when Agatha catches her.

She always pretends she isn’t listening, but she’s the one who takes Agatha’s feedback best.

Truly, Agatha thinks, my daughter.

As she continues pacing the workshop, something finally catches her eye. And no—it’s not Rae’s sunburned cheeks, though Agatha does file that away for later concern and future sunscreen recommendation.

Agatha stops beside Rae’s group.

“Rae, darling..” She says in her most exquisitely condescending tone. “Can you come with me for a minute?”

Every head swivels toward Rae in anticipation while Rae herself raises a brow at her, unimpressed and unbothered.

“We’re busy planning, Ms. Harkness.” Rae replies, dragging out the honorific in spite. “Is it important, or can it wait?”

“It cannot, actually.” Agatha turns on her heel, already walking away. “Unless you’d like me to interrupt your entire production instead. Which, believe me, I’m more than capable of doing.”

She pauses just long enough to glance back over her shoulder.

“Now.” She adds seriously. “Please.”

Rae follows her into the hallway. She makes a whole production of it, feet hitting the floor harder than necessary. Agatha keeps walking, fighting the very real urge to roll her eyes at the theatrics.

“What?” Rae demands the second they’re out of earshot, already looking bored. “Are you sabotaging our performance by removing me from my group? You know they cannot function without me.”

Agatha finally slows, then turns to face her.

The more Rae talks, the more she notices it. There’s a shift in her voice, a faint nasal edge that definitely wasn’t there last time.

“You’re sick.” Agatha says flatly.

Rae blinks. “For caring about my group?” She asks, eyes widening in mock offense. “The bar is low, I fear.”

“No.” Agatha retorts. “Not that kind of sick.”

She studies Rae more closely now. The flushed cheeks. The glassiness around the eyes. The way Rae’s posture is just a fraction stiffer than usual. 

“You’re sick as in you’re not well.”  Agatha clarifies.

Rae scoffs. “Since when did you become a physicia—” She cuts herself off with a sudden sneeze, barely managing to cover her mouth with her hands.

Agatha pauses, deeply satisfied to be proven right. “See? You’re sick.”

“I am not.” Rae insists, blinking rapidly as her eyes water. Another sneeze follows, louder this time.

“You literally just sneezed in front of me, Rae. Twice.”

“It’s dusty out here.” Rae snaps. “Aggressively dusty.”

Agatha doesn’t respond. She steps forward and presses her palm to Rae’s forehead without warning.

Rae stiffens. “Hey—”

Agatha grimaces and pulls her hand back. “God, you’re burning.”

Rae frowns. “I’m fine.”

“You are on fire, not fine.”  Agatha says dryly. “How are you even upright, let alone terrorizing your peers?”

“I am leading them.” Rae corrects. “Someone has to.”

Agatha breathes through her nose, irritation and concern tangling together in a way she very much does not appreciate.

“You’re going to pass out dramatically mid-monologue.” She says. “And while that might be memorable, it’s not the kind of workshop I’m aiming for.”

She tilts her head, eyes narrowing when Rae goes quiet. “How long have you felt like this?”

“I told you, I’m not sick.”

“Tell me that one more time..” Agatha murmurs “And I swear I’m rating your group the lowest possible score should you insist on performing.”

She knows that threatening a teenager is not ideal but sometimes, you do what you have to do especially when the teenager in question is apparently powered by spite.

Rae straightens immediately. “I started sneezing when I got here but it wasn't bad.. just a few here and there. I didn’t notice I have fever, I didn’t know until you pointed it out.” She hesitates, then adds, “I have been more tired than usual. I just thought it was because of traveling.”

Agatha softens almost instantly, irritation giving way to concern. She’s already pulling her phone out, thumb moving on muscle memory alone.

“You’re going home.” 

“What? No, I cannot!” Rae protests. “What about my performa—” She sneezes again, mid-sentence.

“I can’t miss it!” Rae continues stubbornly. “I’ve been working hard the last few hours. Our ship will sink without me and I cannot let that happen.”

“Again,” Agatha says, eyes locked on her phone as she searches for Rio’s contact. “I cannot have you fainting theatrically in my workshop. It sets a bad precedent.”

She finally looks up. “I’ll have your mami pick you up.”

“My mami’s not here.” Rae crosses her arms, clearly pleased with herself. “So, no one’s picking me up which means I get to stay.”

Agatha’s fingers still. “Where is your mami?” She wants to add, why isn't she replying to me? but Rae wouldn't know why.. would she?

“She drove five hours to Northview for a convention.” Rae tells her. “She’s not coming back until tomorrow.”

Agatha closes her eyes for half a second, feeling the problem bloom fully formed in her chest. “Then who are you staying with tonight?”

“Mrs. Davis.”

Agatha opens her eyes. “Who?”

“She used to take care of my mami when she was younger.” Rae explains. “She’s not officially working now, but she comes by sometimes to check on us and help if she can in the house.” Rae squints at her. “Why am I even explaining this to you?”

Agatha ignores that. “Fine. Ask Mrs. Davis to pick you up, then.”

“Why?”

“Rae.”

“I can’t.”

It's Agatha's turn to ask. “And why, exactly, can’t you?”

Rae shrugs, casual again, like the answer is obvious. “She won’t be coming over until dinner.”

Agatha stares at her. Dinner, a few hours from now.

“So..” Agatha mutters carefully. “Your plan is to stay here, visibly feverish, sneeze your way through rehearsal, and then.. what? Walk home?”

“It's not as bad as you think, Meredith Grey.” Rae deadpans. “And FYI, I take uber.”

“That is not a defense.” Agatha grits her teeth. “Must I reiterate that you cannot stay here.”

“And must I reiterate as well that I’m not leaving.” Rae fires back, chin lifting.

There it is. The stalemate. She actually wonders if Rae knows chest, which is not necessary this time but should be a good thing to know for Agatha.

She lowers her phone slowly and looks at Rae, the stubborn set of her mouth that feels.. painfully familiar.

“I cannot have you stay here either.” Agatha’s voice is firm now, leaving no room for argument. “You will risk getting everyone infected with whatever it is you’re brewing, including me.”

She studies Rae again, then adds, almost begrudgingly, “Are your grandparents around?”

“No.” Rae replies. “They travel a lot. Abuela already had plans to go to Fiji right after our Hawaii trip.”

Agatha massages her temple, eyes closing briefly again as if she can will a solution into existence. When she opens them, she looks resigned. “Fine. You’re coming with me, then.”

Rae laughs, startled. “You’re joking.”

“If I were,” Agatha glares at her. “I’d be laughing too.” She turns back to Rae. “Go grab your things. I’m driving you home.”

“Oh my god, you are insufferable!” Rae exclaims. “I’m not letting you kidnap me.”

“Is it kidnapping when I am very clearly informing you of my intentions?” Agatha asks calmly, lifting a brow. “Go. Now.”

Rae plants herself by the door, gripping the handle in case Agatha has plans of physically dragging her away. “I’m not leaving.” She insists. “Not until our performance is over.”

“You are contagious.”

“I can wear a mask.”

Agatha steadies herself. Maybe she can just bargain with this one since intimidation clearly doesn't work..

“You obviously haven’t taken care of a kid.” Rae taunts her. “It’s just a fever and some sneezing. It’s not going to kill me.”

That part, unfortunately, is true. And Agatha supposes taking care of a kid can’t be that different from taking care of an adult. How hard could it be?

“Be that as it may..” Agatha begins, pointing a finger at her. “You are coming with me afterward unless another responsible adult takes over.” Her eyes narrow. “And if I see you feeling even slightly worse in there, I'll pull you out immediately.”

“I’m not weak.” Rae rolls her eyes, sneezing again for the.. honestly? Agatha lost count.

The moment someone hands her a mask, Rae barely makes it five minutes back inside before she abandons her group and collapses into the nearest chair. She’s sweating despite the cold air, shoulders slumped, bravado gone quiet.

She is, in fact, weak. Agatha notices immediately.

Of course she does. She’s looking at her like a hawk.

She watches from across the room as Rae presses her elbows to her knees, head dipping forward, breathing just a little too heavy for someone who insisted she was fine.

“Unbelievable.” Agatha whispers and starts walking toward her.

“Okay, superstar. We’re leaving.” She stops in front of her, blocking her escape.

Rae looks up at her through the edge of the mask. “No, we're not.”

“Raina.”

The name lands between them.

It’s the first time Agatha has ever said it out loud. She’s only heard it from Rio and once from Jen. She never trusted herself with it before until now. 

“I’m not buying any of your excuses.” Agatha continues evenly. “And I’m not negotiating.”

That does it. Rae huffs, muttering something under her breath, but she pushes herself up anyway even if she's reluctant. She follows Agatha as she explains things to Lilia in a low voice. Lilia doesn’t ask questions. She just nods once, understanding quickly, though the look she gives Agatha suggests there will be words later.

Fine. Agatha can take that.

She guides Rae out to the parking lot and toward her car. Predictably, Rae opens the back door instead of the passenger seat and sprawls across it immediately.

Agatha pretends not to notice how exhausted Rae looks. She starts the engine instead.

“You don’t even know where I live.” Rae’s voice is muffled as she stares out the window.

Agatha checks the mirrors, then pulls out smoothly. “Which means now is the perfect time to tell me.”

Rae doesn’t answer.

Agatha sighs. “Or,” She adds lightly. “I can take you straight to a pediatric clinic. Your choice.”

There’s a pause.

Rae sits up just enough to glare at her. “You’re cruel.”

Agatha doesn’t look at her as she signals out of the lot. “I prefer efficient.” Her grip tightens on the wheel, just slightly.

“Address.” She adds. “Now, please.”

The drive goes by quickly. Agatha is a reckless but safe driver, as she insists. Rae complains the entire time, claiming she’ll die in a car crash long before any disease gets to her.

They arrive in the exclusive uphill village in Westview a few minutes later.

When Agatha pulls up, she’s surprised to find a two-storey house that’s modern and warm instead of being aggressively enormous and flashy. It’s built with light stone and dark wood. Wide windows face the front, letting in a lot of natural light.

Big, yes—but not massive. Not the kind of mansion Agatha had half-expected for Rio and Rae to live in. A straight stone path leads up to a solid wooden front door, surrounded by neat greenery.

Agatha will take this house apart later. Right now, she has a groaning kid in the backseat who will not stop sneezing.

“You’re sneezing and you have a fever.” Agatha says, stopping the engine. “What’s next? Coughing?”

“It should be in about an hour.”

Agatha doesn’t argue, she knows better. Sick Rae is more dramatic than usual Rae, and this is not her first rodeo.

She steps out, opens the back door. Rae is slumped sideways, arms crossed over her chest.

“I’m sorry.” Agatha fakes a pout. “Should I be getting you a wheelchair?”

“I want my mami.” Rae mutters. “I’m not going into my own house with only you. What if you do something to me?”

Agatha pinches the bridge of her nose. “What would I even do to you?” She says dryly. “The worst thing I can do is shove a tablet down your throat when you’re too stubborn to swallow it.”

Rae glares before sneezing again. “No.”

“You never grew out of the no phase, did you?” Agatha sighs. “You told me your mami is not going home until tomorrow. What’s your plan here?”

“Call her.” Rae demands. “I want verbal confirmation, I also want someone else to know you were the last person with me if I mysteriously perish tomorrow.”

Agatha stares at the stubborn kid before her and briefly considers screaming. She doesn't.

So to humor Rae, she pulls out her phone and begins to dial.

“You have my mami’s number?!” Rae jolts upright.

“You literally asked me to call her.”

“But why do you have her number?”

Before Agatha can answer—

“Hello?” Rio’s voice cuts in smoothly. “Agatha, I’m driving—can I call you back?”

“No.” Agatha answers. “You’re on speaker. Your daughter is sick.”

“Rae?”

“Yes, Rio. Rae.” Agatha states the obvious. “Unless you’ve been hiding a second one. Would you mind introducing her to the class?”

Rae shoots her a look sharp enough to cut glass. The suggestion of possibly having another sibling is not being taken well. Huh. This kid is really accustomed to the only child lifestyle..

“Are you with her?” Rio asks. “How is she?”

“She’s burning up and sneezing.” Agatha confirms. “I drove her home.”

There’s a pause, followed by a swallow. “She can hear me, right?”

Agatha nods even though Rio can’t see it and angles the phone closer to Rae.

“Rae?”

Rae doesn’t answer. She simply frowns.

“Agatha,” Rio says carefully, “Is Rae really there?”

“She’s here.” Agatha insists. “She's being selectively mute.”

“Mami.” Rae speaks suddenly, snatching the phone from Agatha. “Someone on my flight to Hawaii wasn’t wearing a mask and now I’m clearly infected and sick.”

“Right..” Rio hums, not sounding convinced but choosing peace. “Okay, my love. You know where your medications are, yes? I’ll call Mrs. Davis so she can come check on you. For now, change into your pajamas and drink lots of water.”

“Do I have cough syrup?”

“Yes, I bought you a new one recently.”

Agatha can’t help herself. “Cough syrup for what?”

“For diarrhea.” Rae deadpans. “Of course it's for cough, duh. Let’s use our brains sometimes, shall we?”

“But you’re not coughing.”

“I told you I’d be coughing later.”

“Agatha?” Rio interrupts. “Uh.. Rae gets sick a lot. We’ve been to so many doctors, but they can’t really explain it. When she gets a simple fever, it’s never just a fever. There’s always coughing and sneezing, sometimes nausea and vomiting.”

Agatha’s mouth opens slightly as realization hits. Oh.

If Rae gets sick easily.. is it likely that it’s because of her?

The thought lands heavier than she expects, settling somewhere uncomfortable in her chest. Genetics is something passed down without permission.

Is this her fault?

Rae sneezes again, snapping Agatha out of her thoughts. Unfortunately, the spiraling will have to wait.

“Rio.” Agatha glances at Rae while she speaks. “Tell her she can safely go with me. I can stay until you get here or Mrs.. whoever it was.”

“Mrs. Davis.” Rio supplies.

“Right. Her.”

There’s a pause. “But would that be okay with you?” Rio asks carefully. “We’re not interrupting something, are we?”

It is Agatha’s plan to talk with Rae so staying with her right now is exactly where she needs to be. Besides, what's the worst that could happen?

“I think I can manage a few hours with her.” 

“Thank you.” Rio replies. “You hear that, Rae?”

“If I turn out dead, don’t cry at my funeral, mami.” Rae announces dramatically, finally grabbing her bag and climbing out of the car. She almost shoves Agatha aside in the process, despite being visibly weak.

“She already said her goodbyes.” Agatha mutters into the phone, watching Rae trudge toward the front door, probably deeming inspiration from a doomed Victorian child.

“I’ll be quick.” Rio says. “I’m about twenty minutes from Northview. I just have to drop something, then I’ll drive straight back. Are you sure you can handle her while I’m away?”

Agatha snorts. It’s a sixteen-year-old kid. Yes, a dramatic one. Yes, currently febrile and feral. But still.. a kid.

Her kid.

“I’ll feed her and give her medication.” Agatha purses her lips. “How hard can that be?”

Rae, halfway up the path, turns around after hearing it. “Famous last words.”

Agatha waves her away. “I’ll meet you inside and I will prove you wrong.”

Agatha regrets her confidence approximately thirty seconds after the front door closes behind them.

Rae drops her bag on the floor, kicks off her shoes with all the grace of a toddler, and immediately collapses onto the nearest couch.

“I’m dying.” Rae announces.

“You’re young and full of life.” Agatha clasps a hand over her mouth. “Don’t leave us too soon, oh darling Rae!”

“You’re making me more sick.” Rae glares at her as she stretches her feet. “Now my bones hurt.”

“You’re sixteen.”

“That doesn’t make me immortal.”

Agatha breathes through her nose and looks around the living room. It’s clean, which suggests the presence of a housekeeper or perhaps someone who stress-cleans when she’s worried. Everything is neutral, calm, and has soft edges everywhere. 

Agatha will also dissect the interior and the picture frames hanging on a wall some other time, should she be invited back in. If not, well.. that seems to be a good conversation starter.

“Alright.” Agatha claps her hand, obviously getting the inspiration from Lilia. “Shoes are off. Couch is contaminated. What’s the medicine situation?”

Rae doesn’t answer.

“Rae.”

“I’m conserving energy.” Rae murmurs, eyes closed.

Agatha waits exactly three seconds. “Where’s your medicine?”

Rae groans as she picks up a pillow to cover her face. Okay, copied. She's of no help.

Agatha makes herself at home by following a hallway which leads to the kitchen. She begins opening cabinets like she knows what she’s doing. She does not. 

So far she finds three types of tea, a collection of expensive looking knives, spices she can’t pronounce, and exactly zero medicine.

She pulls out her phone.

Agatha: Where are the drugs?
Agatha: Be specific. Vague instructions stress me out.

The reply comes almost immediately.

Rio: top cabinet next to the fridge on your left. it's in a white box with labels facing out.       Rio: you'll know it's rae’s coz the syrup container is bedazzled.. don't ask why
Rio: thank you for staying with her
Rio: really

Agatha finds the box, grinning to herself while holding two types of syrup and a cup. One is for fever, the other for cough. Looks like Rae is not capable of swallowing a tablet indeed. That's another one to her arsenal.

She holds her phone with one hand as she read the last text for a beat longer than necessary, then types:

Agatha: We’re bonding.
Agatha: Who knows? She might let me braid her hair later or ask for a bedtime story.

She grabs a glass and pours water, bringing the medicine back to the living room by putting it all on top of a plate.

“Sit up.” She instructs, placing the stuff on a coffee table in front of Rae as she starts to open the bottle while reading what's written on it.

Rae removes the pillow from her face as she squints. “Do you even know how much to give me?”

“The recommended amount.”

“That's not the answer I’m looking for.”

“You’re not five.”

“I was once.” Rae grumbles, finally sitting up.

Agatha rolls her eyes, reads the instructions one last time, then pours the exact amount into the cup. No room for error.

She hands it to Rae right away. “Want a lollipop in case it tastes like shit?”

“Shut up.” Rae hisses at her, knocking it back in one go and immediately reaching for the glass of water herself.

Agatha watches her wince. Without a word, she grabs a napkin from the table and hands it over, then leans back against the couch.

“Blanket.” Rae adds.

Agatha looks around and finds one folded neatly over the arm of a chair. 

“Let me—”

“No.” Rae takes it from her grip as she wraps herself up like a burrito and sighs. “My mami does this better.”

Agatha feels that one. “I’m sure she does..” She whispers.

There’s silence for a few minutes. Rae closes her eyes as Agatha watches her from across the couch, her foot bouncing nonstop.

She doesn’t relax. She can’t.

She stands and carefully checks Rae’s forehead with the back of her hand. Too hot. She withdraws like she’s been burned.

She texts again.

Agatha: She's still burning.
Agatha: How hot is too hot?

Rio: thermometer’s in the drawer underneath the tv
Rio: it's the blue one
Rio: don’t panic

Agatha resents that last part deeply.

She isn’t panicking. She refuses to. Still, the worry settles in persistently, even if this is probably routine to Rio—another one of Rae’s episodes, another fever that never comes alone.

Agatha finds the thermometer and wakes Rae carefully. She shows it to her first. Rae barely protests as Agatha slips it under her tongue, too tired to argue.

“Don’t bite it.” Agatha warns.

“I know what to do.” Rae protests. “I'm not a child.”

They wait, neither of them talking to one another.

Eventually it beeps as Agatha takes it from Rae, reads it, frowns, then reads it again.

That’s.. higher than she expected.

Her phone buzzes almost immediately l

Rio: what does it say?

Agatha hesitates before typing the results.

Agatha: It should be fine.
Agatha: I think? It's on the higher end but it should be manageable.

There’s a pause this time.

Rio: okay
Rio: that’s okay
Rio: give her water, keep her cool
Rio: you’re doing great

Agatha stares at the screen.

She is not doing great. She is standing in another woman’s living room, hovering over a child who looks too small under a blanket, feeling guilt crawling up her spine for not knowing what else to do.

Agatha: When do I take her to the hospital?

Rio: if it gets worse

Agatha: How am I supposed to know if it’s getting worse?

Rae shifts on the couch and starts coughing. She hadn’t been lying earlier. The cough really does come later.

Agatha: She’s coughing now.
Agatha: Is she gonna be vomiting next?

Rio: hopefully not
Rio: cough syrup is in the red bottle. 3 ml

Agatha does what she’s told and measures the dose carefully. She shakes Rae gently by the shoulders.

“One more.”

Rae squints at the cup. “That’s disgusting.”

“Drink it anyway.”

“You’re bossy.”

“You’re sick.”

Rae drinks it and immediately gags. “I hate this.”

Agatha watches her swallow. Watches the faint tremor in her hands. It’s barely there yet she doesn’t miss it.

“Do you want your lollipop now?” Agatha asks.

Rae glares at her, then turns onto her side and slumps back down instead.

As comfortable as the couch is, Agatha’s concern Rae might strain her back.

“You should move to your room.” She suggests. “You’ll sleep better in your bed.”

Rae coughs once, dry and stubborn. “No. I like it here.”

Agatha opens her mouth to argue, then stops. She studies Rae for a second longer than necessary.

“Fine.” She resigns. “But if you wake up miserable, I’m saying I told you so.”

Rae mumbles something that might be agreement.. or it might just be exhaustion.

Agatha stays where she is anyway.

The house is quiet now. The kind of quiet that makes Agatha hyperaware of everything. Every breath Rae takes, every tick of the clock, every second Rio isn’t here.

She texts again.

Agatha: She’s asleep.

Rio: that’s good
Rio: i’m stuck in traffic
Rio: but i promise i should be there soon

Agatha doesn’t respond right away.

She looks at Rae. Really looks at her. The curve of her cheek. The stubborn set of her mouth even in sleep. The way she clutches the blanket like it might leave her.

Agatha presses her lips together.

Agatha: Hurry.
Agatha: She pretends she’s tough but she’s not fooling anyone.

Three dots appear almost instantly.

Rio: neither are you

Agatha scoffs, but she doesn’t deny it.

She doesn’t realize she’s drifted off too until her name pulls her back, faint and unsteady, like it’s coming from underwater.

“Agatha?”

“Mhmm?” The sound leaves her before she’s fully awake.

She pushes herself up immediately, the couch protesting beneath her. For a split second she’s disoriented. Where she is, whose house this is—then she’s already moving, crossing the short distance to Rae without thinking.

Agatha presses the back of her hand to Rae’s forehead.

She freezes.

It could be wishful thinking but Rae feels cooler.. somehow. Not normal yet, but better than before.

Rae whispers something, the words slurring together.

Agatha leans closer. “What was that?”

“I said—” Rae opens her eyes briefly, her own blues meeting Agatha’s. “Don’t leave me here.”

Something in Agatha’s chest tightens.

“I won’t.” She answers without hesitation.

It’s not a promise she thinks about. It just comes out naturally.

Rae’s eyelids flutter. She exhales, the tension in her shoulders easing like that was all she needed to hear. Agatha pulls the blanket higher, careful not to wake her fully, tucking it over her chest.

Rae doesn’t protest. She lets it happen.

Agatha lingers there longer than necessary, hand still resting lightly on the blanket, feeling the rise and fall of Rae’s breathing. Counting it. Measuring it. Making sure it stays steady.

She tells herself it’s just being responsible. Just watching over a sick kid until her mami gets back.

But Agatha stays close, even after Rae slips fully back into sleep. She doesn’t move far, doesn’t let herself relax completely either.

And if Rae wakes later—confused, feverish, or afraid.. Agatha will still be there. She would stay the night if she has to, just to prove to the kid that she didn’t leave. That she won’t.

Not again.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha jolts from sleep by a crack of thunder rolling through the house.

She’s still disoriented as she squints, clarity rushing in the moment she realizes she isn’t in her room at Lilia’s. In fact, from what little she can make out in the dim light, she isn’t anywhere in Lilia’s house.

Oh.

She turns her head immediately and finds Rae asleep on the couch beside her, a fever patch pressed to her forehead. Rae looks peaceful—disarmingly so, as if she isn’t capable of verbal attack when conscious.

Agatha pushes herself upright, and only then notices the blanket draped over her body. It definitely hadn’t been there before so in her half-awake state, the realization confuses her more than it should.

For a second, her gaze drifts to the wide windows, where rain hammers down hard enough to compete with the thunder. Typical Westview and its unpredictable weather. More often than not, it is sunny in the morning and it becomes borderline apocalyptic by nightfall.

She yawns and stretches quietly, folding the blanket before setting it aside and moving closer to Rae.

The kid is still in deep slumber, chest rising and falling steadily. Agatha rests a hand carefully against Rae’s arm where it’s slipped free of her own blanket and breathes in quiet relief when she feels only warmth, not heat.

She lingers a moment longer, her hand still resting lightly on Rae’s arm. Just in case.

“You’re awake.”

Agatha startles only slightly. She doesn’t know how long she’s been standing there when the voice sneaks from behind her, but she really shouldn’t be surprised to find Rio emerging from the kitchen hallway.

“Hi!” Rio says, that familiar tooth-gap smile soft and unguarded as she stops beside Agatha. “You were snoring. I didn’t want to wake you when I got here.”

Agatha lifts a brow. “I don’t snore.”

“Well then, that must’ve been Rae.” Rio shrugs, entirely too pleased with herself. “I made french onion soup. You should eat while it’s hot.”

Agatha’s gaze drifts from Rio to the rain streaking down the windows, then to the watch at her wrist. It’s already past seven. “How long was I asleep?” She asks.

“I got here around six.” Rio replies. “You were already out by then.”

Agatha sighs, rubbing a hand down her face. “Well. You’re here now, and Rae seems better.” She straightens. “I should get going.”

Rio’s smile fades just enough to be serious. “Not in these conditions, you’re not. It’s pouring out. The roads are slippery.”

Agatha scoffs. “I’ve driven through worse.”

“I’m sure you have,” Rio says gently. “That doesn’t mean I’m letting you.”

Agatha turns to her, scandalized. “I cannot possibly stay at somebody else’s house without permission. What would my father say?”

Rio laughs. “I’ll explain it to him kindly.”

“You say that with alarming confidence.”

“You know my charm’s a gift.”

Thunder rolls again, closer this time. 

Rio softens. “Seriously. Please stay, at least until the rain dies down.”

Agatha hesitates. She doesn’t like imposing. She doesn’t like needing. But she remembers the promise she made and she really doesn’t want to break it.

“Fine.” Agatha mumbles at last. “But I’m not sleeping over.”

Rio’s smile turns victorious. “Of course not. The princess forts are not built yet, anyway.”

They move toward the kitchen together. Agatha pulls out her phone, typing a quick message to Lilia informing her of her whereabouts before slipping it back into her pocket.

Agatha sits at the dining table while Rio moves around the kitchen. She rests her chin in her hands, elbows planted, watching the other woman work. Rio moves easily in the space, it’s almost like a habit. Drawers opening without hesitation and pots set down with practiced certainty.

Agatha notes all of it. She always does.

“I’m surprised you don’t live in a castle.” She comments aloud.

Rio laughs. “We don’t. It’s just the two of us so if we lived in a castle, we’d probably lose each other for days.”

“Your house is beautiful.” Agatha compliments, eyes drifting to the arches and the warm tones. “The interior is very.. mediterranean.”

“Thank you.” Rio replies with a smile. “It’s still new, relatively. We moved here about three years ago.”

So that means there’s another place. Another version of home for Rae. “This isn’t Rae’s childhood house?”

“It’s not.”

Agatha tilts her head, suspicious. “Now, don’t tell me she grew up in a castle.”

Rio chuckles again. “I don’t think there are castles in Westview.”

Pity, Agatha thinks. She’d have ruled one. She’d lead a fine monarchy—at least in theory. In practice, her sharp tongue and sour attitude would have the townsfolk chanting for her execution and have her head on a spike by morning before the crown even settled.

Rio sets two bowls of soup in the table. Steam curls upward, carrying the scent of onions and herbs.

“I drove to Northview for a supposed cooking convention. Panels, tastings, networking.. all that kinds of stuff.” Rio says casually, wiping her hands on a towel. “It’s an annual thing.”

“And yet,” Agatha notes mildly. “You’re here.”

Rio shrugs. “What’s a mother gotta do?”

One thing is certain: she’s a great mother to Rae. That was never in question. Agatha has a lifetime ahead of her to thank Rio for everything she’s done, especially for all the moments Agatha wasn’t there to do it herself.

She clears her throat. This isn’t the time to get mushy or sentimental. It must be the weather, or whatever excuse keeps her from sounding like a fool.

She moves a bowl closer to her as she takes a spoonful of soup. As usual, it’s perfect. When had Rio ever disappointed her with food?

“You didn’t have to come back.” Agatha mutters.

“I wanted to.” Rio replies simply. 

“Do you really think I couldn’t take care of her on my own?”

“Oh, I know you can.” Rio says calmly, like she’s stating a fact. “I’m just afraid of the attitude you two will throw at each other. Someone needs to interfere and stand as referee, you know?”

Agatha rolls her eyes. That’s fair. She’s only considered being in the same proximity with sick and vulnerable Rae, who knew what kind of chaos they’d unleash once the kid feels better and goes back to her usual self.

She could almost hear the words Rae would utter to get under her skin, and she would, of course, respond in kind.

Rio occupies the chair in the middle after offering Agatha a glass of juice. “Do you have plans tonight?”

“No.”

“Then maybe you should just stay.” Rio suggests. “I don’t think it will tame anytime soon.”

Thunder rolls again, rain drumming insistently against the windows. Agatha glances toward the hallway, where Rae sleeps soundly.

"But what about the princess forts?" She asks in sarcasm.

“Something to look forward to next time, then.” Rio's voice softens, almost faltering, as if she just realized how forward she sounded. “I mean.. if you want to. Only if you want to.”

Agatha keeps quiet, taking another sip of her soup. Rio on the other hand doesn’t want to settle on silence tonight, it seems.

“What do you usually do on your free nights here in town?” She asks, casual but curious. “Are there.. perhaps, I don’t know, dates?”

Agatha’s brow lifts slowly. Ah. So this is where this is going. “I limit myself to one woman only.” She deadpans. “Per area.”

Rio looks at her, openly amused. “And am I the lucky woman of Westview?”

“Bold of you to assume that..” Agatha stirs her soup with exaggerated focus.

She doesn’t have to confirm or deny anything. She doesn’t want to give Rio the satisfaction and the boasting rights.

“What about you, then?” Agatha questions her instead, glancing up. “Anyone keeping you busy outside of cooking and child-rearing?”

Agatha didn’t miss the way Rio flushed, nor that little habit she had of pressing her tongue against the side of her cheek.

“I’m too busy to date.” Rio shrugs. “The last serious relationship I was in didn’t last long.”

Agatha points an accusing utensil towards her direction. “Is that a you problem?”

Rio presses a hand to her chest, pretending to be offended. “Ouch.”

Agatha doesn’t look away. “Well?”

Rio laughs, shaking her head. “We just don’t share the same values.”

“Sure.” Agatha settles back, staring at her over the rim of her spoon. Sure. “But surely, there are other women?” She doesn’t have to specify, Rio knows exactly what she means.

Rio nods. “Occasionally.” Then, catching Agatha’s judgy expression, she quickly adds, “I have needs too. I’m not a robot.”

She couldn’t argue with that. She understood, truly. Besides, no one should shame a woman for her desires. Sexual or otherwise, it’s not the 1700s.

After a beat, she speaks again. “Is it true Rae gets sick a lot?”

“She has a weak immune system.” Rio hesitates, then adds gently, “Did she maybe inherit that from you?”

Agatha recoils theatrically. “Don’t accuse me of weakness!” A pause. “…Yes.” She admits, quieter.

Rio laughs fondly. “I was just kidding.”

“I’m not.”

Agatha shifts in her seat. This is the part she usually avoids, the part where humor stops working.“Her other parent..” She starts, then stops.

Rio looks at her, attentive. “Yeah?”

“I don’t know her.” Agatha admits. “It was a one-night stand at a bar. There was too much alcohol and my hotel room was only a few minutes a way.” She shrugs. “I kicked her out first thing in the morning.”

Rio doesn’t interrupt.

“Female to female pregnancies are rare but the chances are never zero. Give it to me to be one of the lucky winners. When I found out I was pregnant..” Agatha continues, staring into her soup, “I remember thinking, I can only hope my child doesn’t inherit anything awful. Some hidden disease or genetic time bomb, per say.”

She laughs bitterly and adds, “Unfortunately, she got my immune system, so I suppose the universe has a sense of humor.”

Rio offers a small, reassuring smile. “Could be worse.” Then, “For what it’s worth, she definitely got her talents from you.”

Agatha snorts. “And her attitude.”

“Also you.” Rio agrees easily. “Definitely you.

She sighs, but there’s no real bite to it. “Apparently.”

“When the workshop is done..” Rio’s gaze is set at Agatha, hopeful in a way she’s clearly trying to disguise. “Uh—are you..?”

“Am I what?”

“Are you going back to where you live?”

“I’m from L.A.,” Agatha answers. “And for that question, I don’t know. Honestly.”

Because the truth is, it isn’t really her decision. It’s Rae’s.

She doesn’t know how she’s supposed to make it work—her job, the filming schedules, the fact that her entire life is anchored thousand miles away. Her residency is in L.A., her calendar is brutal and unyielding. Despite all that, the options forms anyway, stubborn and inconvenient should Rae want her to stay.

She’ll figure it out.

Rio nods slowly, like she understands more than Agatha’s said aloud. She opens her mouth again. “Do you want to—” She stops.

Footsteps sound from the hallway, soft but uneven. Both women turn at the same time.

Rae stands there, blanket draped around her shoulders. Her hair is a mess and her eyes are almost red. She looks smaller like this. Disoriented, less sharp-edged than usual.

“Mami..” Rae whispers, her voice hoarse as she shuffles forward.

Rio’s expression changes instantly. She stands and crosses the space in two steps, hands already out, guiding Rae into her arms.

“Hey,” Rio says softly. “Hey, I’ve got you.”

Agatha stays where she is, watching the way Rae leans into Rio without hesitation, the way Rio presses a kiss to her hair like it’s a routine. It probably is.

Rae blinks, then glances past Rio, eyes landing on Agatha. “You’re still here.”

Agatha reacts on instinct. The familiar armor slides neatly back into place as she raises a brow, feigning nonchalance. “You asked me to stay.”

I wanted to stay, she didn't say.

Rae squints at her, suspicious even through the haze of fever and sleep. “Did I?”

Agatha doesn’t miss a beat. “Does this come with mild amnesia, or is that just a bonus symptom?” She turns toward Rio, gesturing vaguely with her spoon. “You know, she even asked for a lullaby.”

Rio snorts before she can stop herself while Rae’s face immediately turns red. “I did not.”

Agatha shrugs lightly and takes another spoonful of soup, infuriatingly unbothered. “I’m pretty sure you did, hon.” She hums thoughtfully. “It’s a very moving request, actually. You said something about my soothing presence, so who am I to refuse such?”

Rae mutters something under her breath, rolling her eyes so hard it’s a miracle they don’t get stuck.

“Maybe you’ll remember when you’re more.. put together.”.

Rio steps in smoothly, placing a gentle hand at Rae’s back as she guides her toward the table. “You should eat now, my love.”

“I want to sleep more.” Rae complains, voice dragging.

“And you will.” Rio tells her calmly, already ladling soup into a bowl. “After you put something in your stomach.”

Rae opens her mouth to argue, then closes it again when Rio gives her that look. She has no choice but sigh dramatically and slump into the chair across from Agatha, with Rio settling neatly between them like a human buffer.

“Can I have cereal instead?” Rae tries.

“No.” Rio replies without missing a beat. “You eat what’s served to you.”

“Ohhh!” Agatha claps once, delighted. “I didn’t know you could be stern.”

Rio glances at her. “Do you know my daughter?

Agatha shakes her head, considering. “I’m beginning to.”

“You have to be stern with this one.”

“Mami..” Rae groans. “I’m literally right here.”

“And still dramatic.” Rio says fondly, nudging the bowl toward her. “Eat.”

Rae pokes the soup suspiciously with her spoon. “I have no appetite.”

“Other children are starving, Rae.” Agatha supplies. “You should consider yourself lucky, with a roof on your head and food in your table, all that.”

Rae shoots her a look. “Remind me again, why are you talking and why are you still here?”

“My love, she can’t possibly drive in this condition.” Rio answers for her. “It’s pouring out.”

Rae sighs, then finally takes a bite. She chews slowly, clearly exhausted. “So she’s staying the night?”

Agatha shrugs. “I’ll leave once the rain stops”

“But, what if it doesn’t?” Rae stares at her, fully awake now. “Our guest room is not ready for guests.”

“It is, actually.” Rio butts in automatically.

“It’s not.” Her daughter insists, chin lifting.

Agatha blinks between them. Interesting. A domestic contradiction. 

“Well,” She mutters lightly, batting her eyelashes. “I can always stay in your room, then.” She turns her head at Rae. “I can sing you more lullabies later, if you want more.”

Rae hisses. “I never asked you that!”

She didn’t. Agatha just finds it deeply enjoyable to pretend she did and tease her about it.

“You’re not welcome in my room.” Rae snaps. “Actually, you’re not even welcome in my wing.”

Agatha turns slowly to Rio, eyes wide with mock awe. “She has a wing of her own?”

Rio waves a dismissive hand. “No, she doesn’t.” She sighs. “Our rooms are on opposite ends of the house and she likes calling her side her ‘wing,’ even though it isn’t.” She looks at Rae. “Right?”

Rae crosses her arms, frowning. “It’s still my wing.” She insists. “And a certain someone is not welcome there.”

Agatha fakes a pout to match her expression. “So where, pray tell, am I supposed to sleep if the rain never stops?”

“That’s not my problem.” Rae says flatly.

“Is it not? I’m here in the first place because of you.”

“No.” Rae shoots back immediately, pointing an accusing finger. “You’re here because you insisted I was sick and you wanted to drive me home. I’m not responsible for your decisions.”

Agatha stares at her for a beat, then laughs. Not loudly, just a short, surprised sound. God help her, this kid really doesn’t know how to back down.

“Oh, I like you.” Agatha tells her. “You’re exhausting.”

“Mami,” Rae says, turning to Rio. “You’re not seriously considering this.”

Rio exhales slowly, the way she does when she’s already made up her mind but knows there’s going to be resistance. “It’s still raining.” She states. “I just checked and the forecast says it won’t stop for hours.”

“So?” Rae demands. “She can—”

“—Stay.” Rio finishes gently but firmly.

Rae’s jaw drops. “What?”

“She can stay.” Rio repeats, leaving no room for debate. “I’m not sending someone out into a storm.”

Rae looks between them, betrayed. “You’re really letting her stay?”

Agatha grins, pleased at the situation. “I think you should be more like your mami. She’s sensible.”

Rae glares at her. “You’re not welcome here.”

“But I’m already here.”

Rae opens her mouth again, clearly prepared to argue further, but Rio cuts her off with a warning “Raina.”

That hushes her. She’s not happy about it, but clearly it was effective.

Rae slumps back against her chair, mumbling, “This is unbelievable.”

Agatha leans slightly closer, lowering her voice conspiratorially. “For what it’s worth..” She whispers. “I think your wing sounds very exclusive.”

“Don’t talk to me.”

Agatha smiles, unoffended. “Good night to you too, hon.”

Meanwhile, Rio shakes her head without saying anything, unsure what to do with the endless banter the two women carry on in front of her.

They sit like that for a few more minutes. The rain is steady outside, thunder roaring occasionally. Rae eats slowly but steadily, leaning back in her chair, eyes half-lidded. Agatha finishes her own bowl and doesn’t immediately move away.

At some point, Rae’s head starts to dip.

“Hey.” Rio calls her attention. “Don’t fall asleep mid-spoon. You’ll hurt yourself.”

“I’m fine.” Rae mutters, pushing her bowl away. “Can I go back to bed now?”

Rio studies her the way only a parent can. Her eyes scanning, hand hovering, instinct doing a full systems check. “Do you feel better?”

“Yes.” Rae admits, then adds, “But my nose feels kinda stuck.”

Rio hums. “I’ll wake you up for another dose in about..” She glances and starts pressing something in her smart watch. “Four hours.”

Rae clutches her blanket like a shield and shuffles away down the hallway, shoulders slumped, footsteps dragging. She pauses once, just long enough to glance back.

Agatha raises two fingers in a lazy salute. “Sleep tight, Your Highness of the East Wing.”

Rae didn't say anything more as she disappears into the second floor.

The house settles into a quieter vibe once she’s gone. The kitchen light feels warmer without Rae’s sharp commentary cutting through it.

“Well..” Agatha breaks the silence. “At least she won’t be sleeping on an empty stomach.”

Rio chuckles. She stands and starts clearing the bowls, so Agatha follows to help, but Rio waves her off.

“You’re a guest.” 

“I don’t believe in that concept.” Agatha replies. “I believe in being useful, that’s just basic etiquette. And, that makes it less awkward.”

Rio glances at her, amused. “You don’t strike me as someone who feels awkward often.”

Agatha smirks. “I’m an Emmy winning actress, after all.”

“What..” She croaks, which comes out more like a haunted wheeze buried below than a word. “Do you want?”
