Walk 'em like a dog

Walk 'em like a dog, sis, walk 'em like a dog

Agatha freezes, her soul leaving her body on the spot. She stares at the open door from where she stands, livid. “What,” She whispers hoarsely. “The fuck.”

Her brain does several things at once, none of them helpful. Why does Rae know that song? Why is it playing out loud? Is she making videos? Who is she with? What is happening in this household?

Agatha’s heart rate spikes. She spins on her heel and marches down the staircase, calling for, “RIO.”

She finds Rio in the kitchen, calmly chopping vegetables. “Rio,” Agatha says again, storming in. “We need to talk. Pronto.”

Rio looks up, startled. “You’re awake.”

“That is not the point.”

Rio sets the knife down carefully and glances her way with puzzled looks. “Did you feel worse?”

“No.”

“Better?”

“Yes.”

“Okay—”

“Your daughter is making videos. Tiktoks, I think.” Agatha blurts.

Rio blinks. “Yes.”

“With a friend.” Agatha adds, pointing emphatically back toward the hallway.

“Yes.”

“To Walk ’Em Like a Dog.”

Rio pauses and Agatha sees the way Rio tries to suppress her laughter. “…Okay.”

Agatha stares at her in disbelief. “That’s it? Okay?”

“What would you like me to do?” Rio shrugs. “Confiscate the phone? Ground her? Stage an intervention?”

“She’s sixteen!”

“Yes, I am aware.” Rio purses her lips. “Were they doing anything unsafe? Anything more dangerous than listening to that music?”

“I didn’t stay long enough to find out, obviously.” Agatha admits. “I value my sanity.”

Rio hides a smile by reaching for the pot on the stove. “They’re just making tiktoks.”

“To that song.”

Rio raises an eyebrow. “You seem very invested.”

“I am concerned.” Agatha insists. “Isn’t she too young for whatever, pray tell, she is doing?”

Rio turns to face her fully now. “You should take a sit.”

“I don’t—”

“Sit.” Rio repeats firmly, pulling out a chair.

Agatha hesitates but she does what she’s told anyway, folding her arms like a petulant cat.

Rio slides a glass of water toward her. “You’re still sick.”

“I am recovering.”

“Okay, if you say so.” Rio nods. “Rae’s friend is staying for a few hours. They’re supervised with doors open. No nonsense, although I should have to talk with her for using the sound you heard.”

Agatha eyes her. “You’re far too lax about this. I’d assume you’d be otherwise.”

“Nah, I trust my kid.” Rio says simply.

That lands heavier than Agatha expects. She looks away. “Well, I don’t trust the internet.”

“That’s fair.” Rio agrees. “I monitor her social media accounts so she doesn’t post or see anything inappropriate.”

Agatha sighs, rubbing her temple. “I thought she was.. I don’t know. Studying? Memorizing lines for fun? Rotting in bed?”

“She feels better. Besides, this is her version of fun. I just let her.” Rio finishes plating the soup and sets it down in front of Agatha with unmistakable finality. “Eat.”

“I’m not a child.” Agatha whispers, but she still picks up the spoon, taking one spoonful. 

Rio watches her with arms crossed and a sheepish grin. “You know..” She begins, “For someone who keeps insisting she’s fine, you sure let me feed you a lot of soup.”

“I’m humoring you.” Agatha replies, sniffing. “For morale.”

“Mhm. Sure. That explains why you’re already halfway through the bowl?”

Agatha pauses mid-bite, scowls, then pointedly takes another spoonful. That action made Rio laugh. 

“Who’s with Rae?” Agatha finally asks, squinting toward the hallway as if the answer might physically emerge from it. “Who is possibly with her that she’s making tiktoks to that sound with?”

“America.” Rio answers easily.

Agatha's forehead creases. “America.”

“Yes.”

“The country?”

“The girl.”

“A girl..” Agatha repeats faintly.

“Uh-huh.” Rio smiles, completely unbothered, leaning her hip against the counter. “I think she’s courting Rae.”

Agatha’s soul almost left her body for the second time that day. “COURTING WHAT?” 

Rio winces slightly. “Indoor voice.”

Agatha ignores her. “Rae.. she’s—is she really?” She gestures vaguely with both hands, words failing her. “She's into girls?”

Rio hums.“Yes.”

Whoever or whatever Rae ends up liking, Agatha knows, with a certainty that she’d accept and support it. 

Rae’s femininity catches her off guard a little not because it’s wrong, but because it’s so intentional. However, Agatha doesn’t read it as a stereotype, she reads it as a choice. Rae knows who she is and she’s proud to know her daughter wears it comfortably.

Hearing that she likes girls barely registers as a shock. Agatha is just glad Rio takes it the same way, no questions asked as if it's the most simplest thing in the world.

“America lives close by. They’ve been friends since what? Grade school?” Rio supplies.

“She would..” 

“She would what?”

“Be the kind of girl who pulls the slow-burn friends-to-lovers nonsense.” Agatha continues. “That’s Rae’s brand.”

Rio laughs, nodding. “It kind of is.”

“And Rae’s making her wait?”

“Absolutely.” Rio confirms. “Rae’s stubborn. I don’t know how long she’ll keep America in the ‘just friends’ zone, but the girl’s patient. Persistent, even.”

Agatha hums, thoughtful. “Good.”

Rio glances at her. “Good?”

“Yes. It does build character.” She pauses upon realizing something, “Hey, Rio?”

“Yes?”

“I’m not meddling..” Agatha says quickly, which is usually how you know she is. “But have you, I don’t know, had the talk with Rae?”

Rio considers her. “Which is?”

“The birds and the bees.” Agatha clarifies. “Sex talk.”

“Yes, I have, actually.”

“And?”

“She handled it like a champ.” Rio shrugs. “She asked smart questions and if I remember correctly, she only rolled her eyes at me twice.”

“That tracks.”

“I gave her options, resources, boundaries—all that stuff. She told me she values her first time and isn’t rushing into anything.”

Agatha narrows her eyes. “Really?”

“Really.” Rio says without hesitation. “I also take precautions. Just like I mentioned earlier, the door always stays open when she has someone over. I also track her location when we’re not together so that's an added bonus.”

“Hence the tiktok trauma.” Agatha sighs, dragging a hand down her face. “Honestly? I feel better.”

“Do you?”

“Yes. I’ve heard kids act out when they’re deprived.”

Her own mother has always defined sexual intimacy as sins so severe they might as well be murder. Such desires rot your soul and send you screaming into hell if you so much as thought about them for too long. Being told otherwise didn’t soften Agatha. In fact, it did the opposite.

It made her curious. She was reckless in the way only a person raised on fear can be. She had to learn about biology and her options through television or educational pamphlets she'd seen around.

Rio nods sympathetically. “My parents did the same to me when I was younger. They were very honest and thorough. They even scared me half to death with pregnancy horror stories.”

“And?”

“I didn’t lose my virginity until I reached my twenties.”

Agatha smirks. “So high school was just making out?”

“Pretty much.”

“I lost mine when I was seventeen.” Agatha shares. “Well, as far as someone else's fingers go.”

Right on cue, Rae appears in the kitchen with her mystery friend in tow.

America looks exactly like the kind of kid who never learned to shrink herself. She has dark hair and wears a worn leather jacket slung over a plain tee. She takes one look at Agatha, bundled in borrowed clothes—and stops dead.

“Agatha Harkness! Rae wasn't kidding when she said you're here.” The girl moves forward, her eyes wide with excitement. “Hi! I’m America Chavez, Rae’s friend.” 

At least the kid has manners. Good for her.

“Hi. I’m Agatha.” She repeats, as if the name hasn’t already detonated in the room.

“It’s really nice to meet you.” America’s grin flickers into something softer. “My mother is a huge fan of your filmography. We watch some of them together.”

“My thank you, hon.” Agatha’s flattered. “Would you like an autograph for your mother?”

Rae watches this exchange with visible dread and speaks before America does. “Why are you still here?” She asks flatly, eyes on Agatha. 

Agatha scoffs, turning to her now. “Eager much?”

“You were supposed to leave.” Rae presses. “Like, hours ago.”

Rio, from the counter, offers gently, “She wasn’t feeling well, my love.”

“I’m feeling better now.” Agatha corrects reflexively because she refuses to be perceived as weak by a sixteen-year-old who inherited her attitude.

America glances between them as if she’s watching a tennis match. “You guys talk like—”

“Don’t finish that sentence,” Rae warns her.

Agatha bats her eyelashes in a mocking way. “Like family?”

Rae’s glare could peel paint. “No.”

America chuckles anyway, hands shoved into her jacket pockets. She looks comfortable here and she seems nice. That's a good thing. Agatha doesn't know what she knows about Rae being her biological daughter but if Rae did tell her, then that means she trusts her friend enough.

Rae turns toward the pantry. “We’re just grabbing snacks.”

“Disappointing.” Agatha mutters. “I was looking forward to spending more time with you.”

The teens disappear down the short hallway, voices trailing behind them. Rio silently watches her from across the kitchen, shrugging to herself.

A few minutes later, footsteps return alongside the crinkle of snack wrappers. Rae reappears with a bag of chips under one arm while America is balancing a handful of chocolate bars and a few canned drinks.

“Okay,” Rae stops short again. “You’re still here. Why?”

Agatha doesn’t even look up. “I might just stay another night.Who knows?”

“Please don't.” Rae frowns.

America speaks, getting herself in the middle. “It was really nice meeting you.”

Agatha meets her gaze. “Be a good influence to her, I think she really needs a role model.”

America nods without hesitation. “Always.”

“Stop talking to her.” Rae groans once more.

“Truly, your hospitality is unmatched.”

Rae shoots her a look. “You’re annoying.”

“And you’re a kid.” Agatha shoots back easily. “We all have our burdens.”

“Raina.” Rio says, calm but unmistakably firm. She doesn’t raise her voice, she never needs to. “That’s enough. That’s not how we talk to guests.”

Rae mutters something under her breath that sounds suspiciously like whatever. She adjusts the grip on the snacks and jerks her head toward the hallway. “Come on.”

America hesitates for half a second, glancing back with an apologetic little smile before following Rae. Their footsteps fade as they head back up to Rae’s wing.

Clearly Rae's not in the mood for a conversation so Agatha will try again next time. 

Agatha watches them go, then clicks her tongue. “She’s delightful.”

Rio sighs. “I’m sorry for that. I’ll make sure to speak with her.”

Agatha doesn't reply as she shifts in her seat, rolls her shoulders once, testing. The ache in her muscles is still there but it's no longer unbearable. Additionally, her head feels clearer. Her nose is still stuffy to no one's surprise, but she’s survived worse on far less.

“I’m better.” Agatha says, already pushing herself upright. “I really should leave now.”

Rio doesn’t respond right away. She steps closer instead, hand pressing gently to Agatha’s forehead before Agatha can protest.

Agatha freezes. “I didn’t consent to this examination.”

“Hush. Humor me.” Her hand is grounding as she frowns just a little. “You’re still hot.”

“I’m always hot. I maintain my figure through an active lifestyle and curated diet.”

“You are, but that's not the kind of hot I was referring to.” Rio smiles.  “I can drive you home.”

Agatha waves the suggestion off immediately. “No. Absolutely not.”

“Agatha—”

“I can drive.” She insists. “I’m not incapacitated and you’ve already done more than enough.”

Rio studies her, searching for cracks. “You’re sure?”

Agatha meets her gaze, steady. “I am.”

A beat passes. Then Rio nods, reluctantly. “Alright then.”

She gathers her things from the guestroom quickly without lingering any second longer. Downstairs, Rio is waiting by the door. They step outside together, the rain now a soft mist that clings to the environment. Westview feels almost polite this morning in contrast to the previous night.

Rio walks her to the car parked in the garage, keeping pace without crowding her. Agatha reaches the door, one hand on the handle, and feels Rio’s presence beside her. Close enough to feel, distant enough that she can pretend she isn’t noticing.

“Well,” Agatha breaks the ice. “This is where you tell me to text you when I get home.”

Rio’s amusement becomes evident. “Text me when you get home.”

“Predictable.”

“And you’ll do it anyway.” Rio doesn’t hesitate this time around.

She steps in, closes the distance, and presses a gentle peck to Agatha’s cheek. It’s enough to make Agatha’s breathing catch in the most irritating way.

Rio pulls back just far enough to look at her. “Drive safe.”

Agatha stares at her for a beat too long, then scoffs, flustered and annoyed at herself for it. “You know..” She says, opening the car door. “For someone so gentle, you’re alarmingly good at following orders.”

Rio winks. “Funny. I was thinking the same thing about you.”

Agatha pauses, one foot already inside the car. She glances back over her shoulder, smirking dangerously. 

“Oh?” She drawls. “Careful, Chef. Keep that up and people might get the wrong idea.”

Rio just lifts her brows, curious “What idea would that be?”

“That I tell you to jump..” Agatha grins, “And you’ll say how high.”

Rio taps the roof of the car once, a playful smile on her lips. “Text me.” She reiterates, closing the door herself.

Agatha smirks, leaning slightly out of the window as she starts the engine. “Thanks for the shelter, the food, and for putting up with me being a germ factory.”

“Anytime.” Rio replies, shrugging as if it’s no big deal, though the glint in her eyes says otherwise.

Agatha rolls the window up just a bit, her voice low. “Don’t let it get to your head.”

Rio laughs. “Too late.”

Agatha shakes her head with a small, reluctant grin and pulls out of the garage. She glances in the rearview mirror, catching Rio’s wave one last time. 

Somehow, she already knows she has a reason to come back or see the other woman soon. She’s still wearing Rio’s clothes, and she’s definitely not ready to stop thinking about her until then.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 15: Chapter 15

Chapter Notes

the amount of times i've written and rewritten this chapter for the past two weeks is painfully embarrassing and while editing the final draft, i wasn't able to save it so i had to edit again.. i legit wanted to cry but lo and behold! here she is (finally!!!) longest chapter thus far i believe ~

See the end of the chapter for more notes

2009 - Westview, New Jersey

“Agatha?”

It comes from just outside the cubicle. From where she’s hunched over, Agatha can make out the shadow of someone lingering.

“Are you okay?” Maria Hill’s voice echoes through the four cornered room.

She’s new. Six months in, maybe less. A senior case coordinator who’s always trying to be friendly to Agatha. She brings extra coffee and persistently attempts small talk. She carries the sort of politeness that passes for goodwill in a place like this.

Agatha knows better than to trust what lives on the surface.

She straightens, smooths her blouse, takes a steadying breath, and opens the door. She nearly collides with Maria, who hops back a step. She looks apologetic enough for merely being in Agatha’s way.

“Why wouldn’t I be?” Agatha says casually, as though her stomach isn’t staging a full-scale rebellion even after taking all its contents out and flushing it down the drain.

She moves past the other woman to the sink, as she turns on the faucet and lets the cold water run before washing her hands. She takes some to gargle, noting in mind about the menthol strips she bought specifically for moments like this.

In the mirror, Maria remains where she stands. She wears that look people get when they think they’re being kind, yet they’re really just prying. She watches in silence a second too long.

“I’ve been noticing some things.”

Agatha lifts a brow as she loosens her hair, fingers combing through it. She knows what’s coming next so she’s holding herself together by habit alone. “Congratulations. However, that concerns me how?”

“Shouldn’t I be the one congratulating you?” Maria lets out a quiet laugh and steps closer. She then lowers her voice, “I don’t want to assume. I really don’t, but we work together all the time and I cannot help it. Everything that’s happening.. it’s textbook definition.”

Agatha feels her eye twitch. Actually twitch. She keeps her face blank out of spite and not to give anything away through her expressions. “Textbook what?” She asks.

Maria hesitates for a second, then she goes for it. Although Agatha would have preferred if she stayed hesitant instead. “How far along are you?”

There it is.

Agatha turns fully, her cold gaze meeting Maria’s own. “Excuse me?”

“I mean—” Maria glances toward the door, as if afraid someone might come in unexpectedly. “You can’t be more than three months. You were drinking vodka at the firm party and that was three months ago, right? I remember because Tom made a speech and—”

Two months.

Agatha knows exactly how far along she is. She also knows better than to say it out loud. Not here. Not to her.

“I’m not pregnant.” Agatha grits her teeth, each word precise. “If that’s what you’re implying.”

“Oh.” Maria smiles, small and careful. “Okay. Of course. I just thought—well. If you ever need help with anything, you know I’m here.” She sounds genuine but again, Agatha knows better than that.

Maria nods once and finally leaves. The door clicks shut behind her, and only then does Agatha release the breath she’s been holding.

People are noticing. The nausea, the dizziness, the way her hand drifts to her stomach as if instinct alone might protect what’s growing inside her.

She knows the nausea hits hardest in the first trimester, eventually it will ease. If she begins to show, she can mask it with looser clothes. She doesn’t need forever, anyway. She just needs enough time.

Harkness & Associates looms around her like a mausoleum made of glass and steel. Her mother’s firm which means her mother’s rules. Agatha took business administration in college. Almost poetic, really, considering she could’ve chosen other pre-law courses, something vaguely relevant to the circus she’s running at the firm.

Not that it mattered. Any pre-law course she might’ve taken would’ve gone to waste since Evanora wouldn’t permit her pursuing law school, no matter how desperately she begged.

Even she, a lawyer herself, couldn’t stomach the idea of Agatha following a path that in any other family would’ve been passed down, generation to generation. Agatha likes to think her mother was just terrified that she might actually outdo her and all that she has done. Honestly.. who could blame her?

Still, Agatha tells herself it’s only a few months more, then she’s gone. Gone from this town. Gone from this building. Gone from the sight of the woman who made her life hell.

A few months more before she meets the child she never planned for—but wants so fiercely it almost frightens her.

She hadn’t known she was capable of loving someone like this. Someone she hasn’t even met yet. The feeling crept in quietly, filling spaces inside her she didn’t know were empty but yet capable of being full.

And it terrifies her, a little, how easily it happened. How certain it feels.

Agatha has spent most of her life convinced love was something she did not deserve and will never have, but this is different.

For the first time, she thinks maybe she could do it right. Maybe she's capable of loving someone else and give it her all.

Not a week later, Evanora finds out about the pregnancy. At the same time, Maria Hill gets a promotion.

Agatha decides she’s done postponing it. Or, more accurately, she decides she’s done pretending postponing it is a strategy instead of fear.

There’s no manual for how to talk to the daughter you had to give up sixteen years ago. If there was, Agatha would’ve read it twice and highlighted significant parts the same way she does when she’s handed exclusive scripts. 

Unfortunately, all she has is instinct and the talent to act fine when she clearly isn’t fine to begin with. Still, she’ll push through. She has to. Deflection has carried her far, but even that has limits she cannot drag any longer.

Inviting Rae to stay at the workshop after class might be a terrible idea. It would raise questions, even invite suspicion from looming eyes. Agatha wouldn’t want Rae to be interrogated by her own peers.

What they need is a neutral territory. Just the two of them and whatever wreckage the truth leaves behind.

The odds aren’t great, that much is obvious given their relationship. Rae could say no. Rae would be right to say no. Rae is definitely saying no.

But Agatha has to try, although, how do you exactly ask a teenager if there’s room for you in her future over a cup of coffee? Maybe Rae prefers tea. Perhaps dinner is a better time?

How do you ask if you’re allowed to stay—when leaving has been the only thing she has known you for?

For today’s activity at the workshop, Lilia proposes a game that every kid in the room has probably played at least once at sleepovers when the lights were dim.

“Two truths and one lie.” Lilia announces, pacing slowly in front of the class. Her hands are clasped neatly behind her back as her voice carries the careful cadence she uses whenever she’s about to turn something simple into a philosophical exercise. “You’ll give us all three statements. The rest of us will listen and maybe provide guesses along the way.”

A few of the kids straighten in their seats almost immediately, a quiet buzz of excitement rippling through the room. The game is familiar enough to be interesting, and interest is usually enough to wake up a group that has been sitting through acting drills for the past hour.

“This exercise..” Lilia continues, pausing now and then as she slowly circles the room for added flare, “Is about your ability to blur the line between acting and real life. I want to see how naturally you allow a lie to sit in your body and how easily you can let the truth exist without decorating it. Remember what they say that subtlety matters while good acting hides effort. The best performances make the audience forget there was effort at all.”

Agatha, who has been leaning back in her chair with one leg crossed over the other, can’t help the quiet snort that escapes her.

Lilia always does this, takes something small and wraps it in layers of poetic explanation. It probably makes sense on some level. In fact, Agatha suspects it makes perfect sense to the kids who look up to her mentor, but that doesn’t stop the amusement that bubbles up every time Lilia slips into that tone.

Lilia turns toward her slowly, already smiling in a way that suggests she noticed the interruption long before the rest of the room did.

“Which,” Lilia says pleasantly, “Is why you’ll start.”

Giddy laughter spreads across the class as Agatha exhales and pushes herself up from her chair, resigned to her fate. If there’s one thing Lilia enjoys other than teaching, it’s putting Agatha directly under the spotlight whenever possible.

She did not deserved to be treated this way (she does in fact deserved that).

Agatha walks to the center of the room with the kind of confidence that only comes from years of standing in front of audiences who paid good money to watch her pretend to be someone else. 

“Well,” She begins lightly as she studies the room, “This feels like a sleepover.”

A few of the kids giggle immediately, the tension easing now that Agatha has shifted the energy away from Lilia’s philosophical tone and into something far more casual.

“I’m Agatha Harkness.” She crosses her arms over her chest. “Though frankly, I believe we’ve reached the point in my career where introductions are deemed unnecessary.”

She lets the words settle. If her smugness inspires these kids to strive harder until they too won’t have to introduce themselves in front of a huge crowd, then so be it.

“Age I refused to disclose.” She adds with a small shrug. “But I’m confident at least three of you could Google it faster than I can blink.”

The laughter grows louder now, a few students already pulling out their phones in exaggerated gestures as if to prove her point.

Agatha’s gaze drifts across the room while the noise fades, lingering briefly on each student in turn before eventually landing on Rae.

Rae sits perfectly still in her usual spot, her expression completely neutral. Tough crowd. Though, technically speaking, that crowd in question appears to consist entirely of Rae.

Tough Rae.

“Alright.” Agatha says at last, beginning to pace slowly across the floor that suspiciously mirrors Lilia’s earlier movements. Apparently, the theatrics are contagious. “First, crying is the easiest thing for me to do in terms of acting.”

She can see a few heads nodding in agreement.

“Second,” She raises a finger to count, “I prefer stage acting to film because there’s less room for error.”

That earns a stronger reaction from the room. Agatha has always known there’s a quiet notion among actors that stage work is the more difficult craft since there are no cuts or  careful editing to smooth over a mistake. Once the curtain rises, whatever happens belongs to the moment.

She’s always liked that part of it.

On stage, every breath and tremor in your voice exists in real time. You cannot break the fourth wall and ask for a retake if you falter.

Not that she’s done much of it. Compared to the endless catalog of films attached to her name, her theater work is small. It consists of brief returns to the stage between bigger projects. Still, the few times she’s stepped into that world, she can’t help but admit how she’s always loved it a little more.

“And third..” Agatha smiles. “I do not believe the tabloids when they say I was robbed of an Oscar in 2023 for my role as Emma.” As much as it pains her to admit, Olivia Coleman deserved that golden statue more than she did no matter what the critics say.

The room immediately buzzes with reaction as they all try to clock her tea. 

Lilia steps forward, reclaiming control of the exercise. “Which one do you think is the lie?”

Hands shoot up all around the room before she even finishes speaking.

“You cry insanely well so the first thing you said was definitely the truth.” One kid says confidently.

“That Oscar thing was fake, you gave a better performance in my opinion! Even reddit users said so.” Another supplies..

“No way you prefer stage over film, should that be true you could have done way more theater projects now.” Someone else insists.

Agatha allows the debate to unfold for a moment, her expression unreadable as she listens to the increasingly passionate arguments forming around her. Her gaze flicks briefly, almost unconsciously, toward Rae again.

Rae hasn’t raised her hand. She looks uninterested to say the least, as though this is all a waste of her precious time.

After a moment, Agatha lifts a finger over her mouth, and the room quiets almost instantly.

“The lie is that crying comes easily.” She admits. “It doesn’t. It never did, it never will. I loathe crying scenes with utmost passions because they take so much toll on me.”

A chorus of protests erupts immediately.

“That’s not true!”

“But you’re amazing at it!”

“I literally studied your breakdown scene from Dawn!”

She exhales through her nose before adding, a little less flippant this time, “Just because you’re good at something doesn’t mean it comes easily. And it certainly doesn’t mean it doesn’t cost you every single time.” The words settle over the room heavier than she intended.

Agatha immediately ruins the moment by shrugging. “But if any of you figure out how to cry on command without emotionally destabilizing yourselves, do let me know. It would save me an embarrassing amount of therapy.”

A few kids laugh again, tension easing. Then Agatha adds, almost absentmindedly, “Also, for the record, someone once told me I look like I’m having a stroke when I cry, so there's that.”

The reaction that follows is immediate and loud.

“That’s horrible!”

“Who said that?”

“They’re lying!”

Agatha chuckles softly, though her eyes drifts back toward Rae for just a moment. Her face remains carefully blank, but there’s a tightness in her shoulders that gives away more than she probably intends.

Agatha refocuses her attention back to the group. “Anyway,” She waves a dismissive hand, “If you ever feel discouraged about your acting abilities, just remember—somewhere out there, someone probably thinks you’re unwell.”

“Thank you.” Lilia says at last. “That was instructive, my dear.”

Agatha returns to her seat, the humor sliding off her expression the moment she turns away.

“Who’d like to volunteer next?”

The energy shifts immediately. Several students suddenly become deeply fascinated by the floor upon hearing the idea of one of them going up next.

No one wants to follow Agatha, well, except one hand that rises cleanly through the silence.

“I’ll go.” Rae is already standing before Lilia can respond.

Lilia beams instantly at her volunteer, looking proud as Rae comes near. She says she doesn’t play favorites but anyone with an eye can quickly tell who her favorite student is. “Go ahead, sweetheart.”

Rae stands tall without apology and smiles warmly before speaking. “So my name is Raina Andreia—”

“Your name is Raina Andreia?” Agatha blurts out, disbelief cutting straight through the moment.

The room immediately stiffens as Rae stops mid-sentence and turns slowly, one eyebrow lifting in a way that feels painfully familiar.

“Yes.” She says firmly, obviously not amused for being interrupted. “Do you have a problem with that?”

“No..” Agatha gestures vaguely, already regretting opening her mouth but unable to close it now. “I just—Andreia?”

She’s heard of Raina, even spoke of it once.. But Andreia? How can she not possibly known of her own daughter’s second name?

Rae crosses her arms now, a defensive measure. “You can’t seriously think my name is just plain old Rae, do you?”

“I’m just saying—”

“Well, the more you know.” Rae cuts in. “Rae is just a nickname, obviously.”

Agatha blinks once. Then again, slower this time. Her gaze scans around the room in the hopes of someone else sharing her sudden yet reasonable surprise.

“Why do I not know this?” She asks, the question slipping out before her better judgment can intervene. She gestures lightly between Rae and the rest of the class. “Am I the only person in this room who was apparently not informed that Rae comes with an extended edition?”

A couple of the kids glance at each other. One of them shrugs, this being the least shocking development of the afternoon.

Agatha turns toward Lilia, then Kate, expecting backup. Instead, both women are looking at her with the same faintly puzzled expression, the kind usually reserved for people who’ve just reacted a little too strongly to something extremely casual.

And that’s when it hits her.

Oh.

Right.

She might be sounding.. suspiciously invested in a teenager’s second name.

“I mean—” Agatha thinks of ways to retreat. “I’m simply saying that if someone introduces themselves to you with one name, you begin to assume that’s their only branding.”

“Honey, most kids go by nicknames in this class.” Lilia intervenes patiently, gesturing toward the back of the room. “Coby, for instance.”

Coby raises a hand in acknowledgment. “My name’s actually Constantine.”

Agatha begins to realize more she may have, perhaps, slightly overreacted to a perfectly normal piece of information.

Rae, meanwhile, clears her throat softly. It isn’t loud, but it cuts cleanly through the lingering chatter, pulling everyone’s attention back toward the front where she still stands.

“Anyway,” Rae hums, reclaiming the floor. “Since we’ve apparently established that people in this class have more than one name, let’s pick up where we left off.”

All attention returns to Rae. The room quiets almost instinctively, curiosity hanging thick in the air as everyone waits for what she’ll say next.

“First, I’ve traveled to sixteen countries.” Several kids nod immediately.

That part tracks. Everyone in the room knows who Rae’s family is. Her surname alone is plastered across half the buildings in Westview so really, she can’t be questioned when it comes to her wealth.

“Second,” Rae continues, “I failed my driver’s test multiple times. Apparently my one flaw is sitting behind the wheel.”

“Same.” Someone mutters from the back as chuckles erupt through the room.

Agatha doesn’t move a muscle, because Rae looks at her then. Not just a simple glance, no. She can almost see the mischief looming behind those ocean blue eyes that mirror her own.

Rae eventually smiles at her. No. Not a smile. A grin, rather. A taunting one to be more specific.

Rae is about to do something reckless and impossible to undo. Oh no.

“Lastly,” Rae mutters, never breaking eye contact, “I am related to Agatha Harkness.”

The room detonates as every single head turns toward Agatha. She can only pray that they don’t overhear her heart pounding in her ears.

“Rae.” Presley calls, already shaking her head, “You could’ve made it less obvious.”

“Yeah.” Debbie agrees. “There’s no way you’re related to Agatha.”

Agreement hums through the room, but Rae doesn’t rush to answer. She doesn’t even gloat.

Agatha sits perfectly still on the other hand. Years of training take over before instinct can betray her. Her posture stays relaxed, one leg crossed neatly over the other, expression composed in that effortless way cameras have always loved.

If she moves wrong, if she breathes wrong, this becomes a spectacle.

And she absolutely refuses to let that happen here.

“The lie is that I actually travelled to eighteen countries, not sixteen.” Rae clarifies, a little too pleased with herself. 

The beat drops when realization lands slowly. Voices pile over each other as eyes swing back to Agatha and Rae back and forth.

“Hold on..” Lilia interjects, still clearly in disbelief herself. “If that’s the lie, then all this time you’re telling me you and Agatha are related to each other?”

The room goes quiet as they all wait for the answer.

Agatha meets Rae’s gaze and holds it. She tries to keep her face neutral, but the moment stretches into a telepathic challenge between them. One daring the other, one not backing down.

If Rae says yes, then Agatha has some explaining to do. Frankly, it wouldn’t be the easiest thing in the world, but if that’s what her daughter wants—

“Okay, wow.” Rae giggles, raising both hands slightly. “Relax. You’re all so serious. That one’s not real either.”

The room blinks.

“I was bluffing.” She adds nonchalantly, like the whole thing is obvious. “I actually said two lies. Congratulations, you all got played!”

“That’s not how the game works!”

“Sure it is.” Rae insists. “You just have to commit.”

“So you’re not—”

“Not related to her.” Rae repeats, nodding once toward Agatha. “Sorry to disappoint.”

A few people laugh, the tension dissolving almost instantly now that the mystery has an easy answer. Across the circle, Agatha smiles. It’s perfectly timed and casual.

“Well.” Lilia looks like she just breathed the biggest sigh of relief. “Next time we’ll clarify the rules before someone rewrites the entire premise of the game.”

The group laughs again, the moment already slipping away as someone volunteers to go next.

Raw retreats back to her seat like nothing happened, barely bothering to give Agatha any more of her attention.

And just like that, they move on.

Later that night, Agatha sends Rae a message for the first time before she can overthink it any further.

Agatha: Hi, Rae.

Agatha: It’s Agatha.

The reply almost comes instantly.

Rae: who gave you my number?

Agatha: Your mami did.

Rae: why?

Agatha: I wanted to invite you over for lunch.

Agatha: Or, whatever time works best for you.

A beat passes by.

Rae: again.. why ?

Agatha: Don’t you want to spend more time with your mommy?

Rae: don't ever text me again

Ouch. Okay, note taken. Rae’s clearly not in the joking mood tonight.

Agatha: I’d like to talk.

Rae: about what?

Agatha stares at the blinking cursor as if it could give her the right words. She can feel her heart trying to push her thumb away, telling her this is the point most people chicken out.

She doesn’t.

Agatha: About you being my daughter.

Three dots appear. Disappear. Reappear.

Agatha’s stomach twists. Rae is going to say no, isn’t she?

Agatha: And everything that comes with that.

Agatha: Which is a lot, I’m aware.

Rae: that's it?

Agatha: Yes. If it’s okay with you.

Another pause. Agatha starts composing an apology she hasn’t even been asked for, a reflex she can’t stop.

Rae: lunch where?

Agatha blinks in disbelief. Is Rae actually considering this?

Agatha: You’re not saying no?

Rae: i'm not saying yes either.

That sounds like Rae. Still, hope sneaks in, curling around her ribs.

Agatha: Uptown. Open area, but not too open.

Agatha: I’m not trying to trap you. I don’t want you to feel that. Emotionally or otherwise.

Rae: so, public humiliation is off the table

Rae: sucks

Rae: tomorrow?

Agatha nearly drops her phone.

Agatha: Can you make it tomorrow?

She waits and tries not to read too much into it, but how can she not?

Rae: ok

Agatha: Okay.

Agatha: I’ll let you know where.

Agatha: Thank you. Rae.

She stares at the screen long after it locks, her mind scrambling to catch up. She hadn’t expected agreement this easily. But she’s relieved, impossibly so. Finally.

She’s finally going to talk to Rae and maybe, they’ll start to shed some light on this mess of a relationship, together.

The next day, Agatha treats getting ready as though she’s preparing for a covert operation. Which, frankly, isn’t new territory.

The outfit is neutral to the point of anonymity. She stares at her reflection, fixing her beige coat then adds a scarf. Sunglasses follow, large enough to hide half her face and most of her dignity.

Rae had been clear about one thing: absolutely not their restaurant.

Agatha hadn’t argued. Neutral ground had been her idea in the first place, somewhere uptown, far from familiar staff, further from questions that start with Isn’t that—. They will meet at a place where two people could sit across from each other and pretend this was just lunch.

Casual, harmless lunch.

She arrives early. The hostess leads her to a small table for two by the window. The kind of place where people speak in low voices and pretend not to stare. Agatha sits, folds her hands, then immediately unfolds them.

She checks her phone for any messages or updates from Rae. There’s none so she waits patiently instead.

Ten minutes pass.

She asks for water, then changes her mind and orders coffee instead. She settles for black without sugar. If she’s going to spiral, she’ll do it caffeinated.

Agatha: I’m here.

Agatha: Let me know if you’ve arrived.

Twenty minutes in and she decides to give Rae a text all the while not sounding too desperate.

The waitress checks in, polite smile in tact.

“Is someone joining you?”

“Unfortunately,” Agatha says, then winces. “I meant to say yes. Hopefully.”

Thirty minutes.

Humiliation is starting to creep in. In addition to her waiting, a couple of people has made obvious glances towards her way.

She tells herself Rae is late because she’s a teenager. Teenagers are constitutionally opposed to punctuality.. right?

This is fine. This is normal. This is not a sign.

Forty-five minutes.

Another waitress appears, probably concerned of the space Agatha has occupied when there’s a long waiting line outside with actual guests.

“Would you like to order while you wait?”

Agatha smiles tightly. “No. I shall wait for my companion.”

The woman nods albeit hesitant. She didn't linger any longer so thank God for that.

An hour.

Agatha’s phone remains stubbornly silent. There has been no cancellation or any form of presence from Rae.

A familiar ache settles in her chest, and Agatha can’t quite tell if it’s worry, irritation, or some dangerous cocktail of both. Why wouldn’t Rae have given her a heads-up? 

She forces herself not to spiral into worst-case scenarios because imagining what could’ve happened to Rae, even for a second, is the kind of self-inflicted torture she’s sworn off. Still, the pit in her stomach refuses to lighten.

She tells herself to give the kid the benefit of the doubt. Maybe something genuinely came up. Maybe Rae’s just.. busy. Or distracted. Or.. testing her patience, because apparently that’s a hobby now.

Agatha glances at her phone, thumb hovering over Rio’s number. Maybe she can try asking her. Not that she’s about to admit panic, of course. That would be far too dramatic. But a little intel wouldn’t hurt, just enough to confirm that Rae is alive and not secretly plotting the world’s most elaborate way to frustrate her somewhere.

She exhales a sharp hiss that feels like it’s trying to punch the air itself. A few months ago, her life had been a predictable routine. Red carpets, Beverly Hills brunches, book clubs where people wore too much perfume and too little sense.

Now? Now it’s a tight knot of anxiety, waiting for a sixteen-year-old to decide whether she’ll show up or blow her off on a random Sunday afternoon.

She lets herself accept the fact Rae isn't coming and prepares to leave instead, until the room shifts.

It was subtle at first. Heads turning in anticipation not toward her table, but toward the entrance. The low murmur of conversation rises and someone lifts a phone. Then another.

Agatha frowns, tugging her scarf higher. Great. Because nothing screams ‘inconspicuous’ like a forty something woman trying to hide behind a fabric tube.

That’s when she hears it. Her name. Not spoken or whispered, no. It was something else.

She looks up just as the front doors swing open. Not Rae. Not even a hint of civility. Just a cluster of people with cameras already raised, flashbulbs stuttering and voices overlapping in a chorus of chaos.

“Agatha! Over here!”

“Is it true you’re working on a new project?”

“Agatha, can you confirm—”

Her stomach drops. She mutters, mostly to herself, “Oh, you have got to be kidding me.”

More people pour in as curious diners crane their necks, desperate to witness the spectacle. The quiet restaurant dissolves in seconds, leaving her acutely aware that sunglasses are basically a suggestion at this point, not a disguise.

The hostess rushes forward, flustered. Security trails behind too little, too late. Agatha stands, chair scraping loudly against the floor. 

“Agatha, who are you meeting?”

“Is this a secret lunch?”

“Agatha—Agatha—”

She doesn't know how these vultures managed to track her down, until it made sense.

Rae.

The realization lands heavy. Of course. Of course the kid had agreed so easily because she doesn't have plans to show up in the first place. She’d been outmaneuvered before even saying hello.

She scans the crowd, half-expecting Rae to be peeking from some corner, soaking in the chaos she orchestrated without moving a single muscle. But no, she’s nowhere near.

The flashes keep coming relentlessly and their buzzing noises are starting to hurt her ears.

Agatha straightens, spine locking into place. Her armor of confidence slides back on. If she’s going to be ambushed, she’ll at least do it with grace. She refuse to look like a startled cat in a silk scarf, even if that’s what she actually feels.

Still, beneath the practiced composure, something aches. She’d shown up. She’d waited. And somehow.. she admits this to no one, not even herself—she’d been outplayed. 

Agatha doesn’t remember exactly how she gets out of that situation.

One moment she’s boxed in by cameras and noise, flashes bursting against her vision; the next, there’s a firm hand at her elbow, security cutting a narrow path through the crowd. It's a mercy she didn’t ask for but desperately needed.

She keeps her head down, scarf pulled high, sunglasses doing nothing to stop the burn behind her eyes.

By the time she’s in the car, her hands are shaking.

She drives on instinct alone, fury and heartbreak blurring together until they’re indistinguishable.

Rayo del Sol looms ahead before she consciously decides to go there.

She parks badly and storms inside as though she belongs there which, at this point, everyone seems willing to accept.

The staff freeze when they see her. A few look startled, a few look concerned. One thing they did in common is not stop her.

There’s an unspoken understanding by now: if Agatha Harkness is moving with purpose, you clear the way and deal with the fallout later.

"Is Rae here?" She asks a waiter.

"Uh.." He was hesitant at first. "She's over there."

Agatha barrels into the end part of the restaurant, not minding the employees only sign.

Her eyes lock on the one thing she’s been hunting for: Rae. There she is, sleeves rolled up, back bent over some flower arrangements near the prep area, casual clothes at odds with the sharp uniforms of the staff around her. 

“Raina.” Agatha keeps her voice low but firm.

Rae freezes in place, and slowly lifts her head. Surprise flickers across her face for a moment, but she covers it as quickly as a thief hides a stolen glance.

“What are you doing here?” Rae's voice is clipped, obviously startled by Agatha’s sudden arrival.

“You left me waiting.” Agatha accuses her. “And yet you had no intention of showing up. You even sent the paparazzi after me. If you weren’t coming, you could’ve just said so.”

Rae smirks, tilting her head. “Where’s the fun in that?”

Agatha swallows, teeth clenching. How do you reason with someone who is fueled by hatred? 

“Rae,” She mutters her name, hands gesturing helplessly, frustration and longing threading through the motion. “I’m trying here.”

Rae’s eyes narrow. “Are you really? You didn’t even know my name.”

Point taken. Agatha inhales sharply, the weight of sixteen years pressing down. “How would I know if you wouldn’t tell me? If you wouldn’t listen to what I have to say? If you won’t even give me the chance to know you at all?”

“Why would I want to do all that?” Rae’s voice is cold. “Who are you in my life, anyway?”

Agatha’s chest tightens. She wants to say the truth that matters—I’m your mother. But the words stick. Even if she had given birth, even if she had lived through every late-night tear for this child, Rae doesn’t see her that way.

Maybe she never will.

“I’m..” Agatha falters, searching for words, her throat tight. Rae leans back slightly, arms crossed, challenging her without saying a word.

“See?” Rae says, a mixture of accusation and amusement in her tone. “You don’t even know who you are.”

Rae then adds, “Why would I give you a chance if, in the first place, you didn’t want me?”

Agatha’s eyes blaze. “It’s not true,” She hisses, every word a spark. “I wanted you. Don’t you dare say I didn’t.”

Rae crosses her arms, challenging. “If you did, then why—”

“Because I had to!” Agatha cuts in, and the whisper turns into a growl, raw with sixteen years of unsaid words.

“Why?”

“I love you and wanted you more than anything in the word but above else, I wanted to keep you safe. To give you the life I couldn’t give then!” Agatha’s voice rises, shaking with the edge of desperation. “So don’t you ever say that. You don’t know what I went through. You don’t know anything."

For a moment, Rae’s usual armor wavers. Her voice drops now, almost fragile. “Then why.. why did you give me away?”

Agatha swallows, the words thick and heavy in her throat. “I.. I had to do what I thought was best then. If being away from me is the safest you'll ever be then, so be it.”

Rae studies her, the hardness in her eyes softening just a fraction. It’s almost as if curiosity is mingling with confusion. Agatha dares a breath, letting herself hope again that maybe, her daughter might understand it this time around.

“Safe from who?” Rae presses, unrelenting. “Who were you trying to protect me from?”

“I—” Agatha starts, but her words are cut short by the soft footsteps of someone approaching.

“Uh.. excuse me?” A staff member interjects, voice hesitant. “Sorry to interrupt, but Rae, someone’s here to see you.”

“Who?” Rae asks wary, turning slowly.

“Surprise, babe!” A chirpy voice rings out as Rae freezes, eyes widening in instant recognition.

A woman appears from the corridor that leads toward the dining area, stepping enthusiastically into their line of sight.

She’s holding a bouquet of flowers wrapped in neat paper. The gesture feels almost absurd in the middle of the emotional wreckage Agatha and Rae had been building only seconds ago.

Agatha barely registers her presence at first. Her attention is still caught on Rae, still caught on the conversation that had cracked open something raw between them, it is both fragile and unfinished.

Then the woman steps forward, and that’s when Agatha’s eyes land on her face. She knows this woman. 

Well. That’s unfortunate.

The universe clearly woke up today and decided Agatha Harkness hadn’t suffered quite enough emotional whiplash for one afternoon.

Standing there, smiling like she hasn’t aged a day, is none other than Maria Hill.

Of course it is.

“Maria!” Rae blurts out immediately, the surprise in her voice becoming obvious by the minute.

Before Agatha can even process what’s happening, Rae crosses the distance between them and throws her arms around the woman in a tight hug.

“You’re here!”

Agatha watches it happen from a few steps away, and an unexplainable ache twists in her chest. It’s an instinctive reaction, the kind she wishes she could pretend she doesn’t have.

After all, she doesn’t get to claim any rights here. Not really. Not technically. Not legally. Rae has a mother. Rae has a life. Rae has people she runs to like that.

Still, watching your daughter hug someone else so comfortably when she can barely look at you does something unpleasant to your heart.

“Of course I’m here to see my favorite girl,” Maria says warmly, pulling back just enough to look Rae over. “How have you been? Your hair has gotten so long! Should we have girls’ day out asap?”

Rae laughs, and Agatha feels that same small, traitorous ache again.

Then Maria’s attention drifts as her gaze slides past Rae and lands directly on Agatha.

There’s a brief pause, just a second of confusionbefore recognition slams into place.

Maria’s eyebrows lift. “Wait..” She says slowly, then her eyes widen. “Agatha Harkness?”

Agatha nods stiffly. “Maria Hill.”

Rae looks between them, “You two know each other?”

“Oh, we do.” Maria replies brightly, already moving toward Agatha before she can object.

Before Agatha can step away, Maria wraps her in a hug. A full hug.

The audacity.

Agatha stands there like a statue, arms awkwardly half-raised, trying to decide whether shoving her away would make the situation better or significantly worse.

“Agatha, it’s been forever!” Maria gushes when she pulls back. “God, how have you been?”

Amazing! Truly incredible!

Apparently, Maria has decided there isn’t a complicated history between them. It was as if  Agatha didn’t spend years suspecting that Maria was the one who tipped off Evanora about a certain pregnancy back when everything fell apart.

It was never proven, but Agatha has always believed it to be true.

“Dear God.” Agatha says through gritted teeth.

Maria either doesn’t notice the tone or chooses to ignore it. “I used to work at her mother’s firm.” She explains to Rae, gesturing between them in a cheerful little reunion kind of way. “Back when Agatha was still pretending she enjoyed corporate law.”

Rae blinks, absorbing the information.

“So, how do you two know each other now?” It is Maria’s turn to ask.

The question did not land well. Rae and Agatha share a knowing look as the silence stretches.

There is no version of the truth that fits comfortably into polite conversation such as this one.

“We—”

“Maria?”

The voice cuts through the moment.

Rio appears looking flustered in her chef’s uniform, wiping her hands on a towel.

She stops dead when she sees them.

“Wait—Agatha? You’re here too?”

“There she is!” Maria beams.

Before Rio can react, Maria crosses the room and pulls her into a hug the same way she did with Agaha.

“If it isn’t my favorite ex.”

Agatha’s brain catches on that word instantly.

Ex. Ex? As in ex girlfriend?

For fuck’s sake.

Rio freezes halfway through returning the hug, her own confusion practically radiating off her.

“What are you doing here?” She asks carefully.

“Mami, that’s not the real question.” Rae tells her smoothly, stepping forward.

Everyone turns to look at her.

“You know how I’ve always liked Maria for you.” Rae continues, far too casually. “And even after you broke up, we stayed in touch.”

Agatha’s brain stops working. Rae likes Maria.. for Rio? Her mami?

What? What.

Rio looks equally as confused as Agatha, if not more.

“You did?”

“Of course we did.” Maria confirms, waving a hand. “Rae’s the sweetest. She invited me over and I thought I’d surprise her too since I just got back from Vienna.”

She beams at them all. “So, surprise!”

Agatha stares at the scene before her. She’s watching a play she was never given the script for, so let’s review.

She used to work with Maria Hill, who once probably (most likely) snitched on her.

Maria is Rio’s ex-girlfriend.

Rae clearly adores Maria.

Maria is currently touching Rio’s arm like she still has every right to do so.

Rio looks like she’s trying to understand how she got dragged into this circus.

And Agatha—Agatha is absolutely not fuming with jealousy.

Wait, jealousy? Is that even the right emotion?

Why would she be jealous? Maybe annoyance is more appropriate. To say she’s jealous would be ridiculous.

“Why don’t we all go to lunch?” Maria suggests, looping her arm through Rae’s. “Like old times.”

Old times. Agatha nearly chokes at that.

“Agatha—” Rio starts, stepping forward, but Rae intentionally shifts just enough to block her path.

“Agatha’s my mentor at the acting workshop,” Rae explains, looking at Maria. “She stopped by to give me some notes since we have a performance coming up next week.”

Agatha stares at her. That’s the story? That’s what they’re doing now?

Should they really pretend the emotional meltdown that just happened five minutes ago never existed?

“Is she now?” Maria mutters thoughtfully, studying Agatha with a look that’s just a little too curious. “Agatha always was dedicated to her work. Nice to see she still is.”

Agatha’s head is starting to throb.

“Well yeah.” Rae agrees quickly. “She’s actually just leaving.”

Then she looks directly at Agatha as if speaking again through telepathy. “Isn’t she?”

She doesn’t want to get tangled in whatever this is so if she must leave, well.. “I am, actually.”

“Too bad.” Maria states. “I was hoping we could catch up.”

“You and me both.” Agatha forces a smile, heavy on the sarcasm.

“But it’s nice seeing you again!” Maria adds.

“You too.” Agatha lies.

Rio hesitates as she stares at her,  “I’ll walk you out—”

“Mami, no.” Rae insists. “Why don’t you show Maria around first? She hasn’t been here in years. A lot’s changed.”

Rio looks uncertain, but Maria is already dragging her away.

“Come on, chef.” She beams. “Show me what you’ve done with the place.”

Rio throws Agatha one last worried glance as she disappears down the hall with her ex girlfriend.

Agatha doesn’t react initially. She waits until they’re gone, right as Rae turns back to her.

“Rae—”

“We can talk another time.” Rae suggests quietly. “I won’t leave you hanging. I promise.”

Agatha studies her face carefully. It’s a surprise Rae offered and really, even if she’s still hurt for what happened earlier, who is she to refuse that?

“Well..” She whispers finally, “I’ll hold you to that.”

Rae gestures toward the exit. “I’ll walk you out.”

They leave the restaurant together in silence. No snide comments or meaningful looks. It’s just the sound of their footsteps and the low hum of the restaurant.

Agatha walks to her car alone. She sits there for a moment before starting the engine.

She lets her hand settle over her chest, feeling the steady throb beneath her palm. It’s slower now, but still there—like her heart hasn’t quite realized the fight is over.

Agatha exhales quietly. She’ll try again with Rae next time. Mothers don’t just give up on their children that easily.

Rae can hate her for now. Agatha can live with that.

Rio, on the other hand.. Well.

Maria is very clearly there to keep her occupied, hovering close in that way exes do when they’re trying to look casual but aren’t fooling anyone. If Rio decides to get back together with her, then fine. Wonderful. Agatha doesn’t care at all.

She really doesn’t.

Although she will be extremely spiteful about it.

Her mouth tilts into a faint, crooked smirk as she drops her hand from her chest.

“Who doesn’t care now, huh?” she mutters under her breath.
