Chapter 16: Chapter 16

Chapter Notes

in honor of the mother gothel announcement, i hereby give you a surprise chappy! i hope you enjoy this treat ✨

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“Mama, please don’t. I prohibit you from buying a Porsche for my daughter.”

Rio massages her temples as she balances her phone against the fruit bowl on the table, the screen glowing with her mother’s face during their early-morning video call. Breakfast sits half-touched in front of her—an açaí bowl that’s slowly melting while this conversation refuses to end.

“Well, why couldn’t I?” Luella asks from the other end, acting oblivious.

The video shakes slightly as Luella adjusts her phone. The background reveals exactly where she is: the salon. It’s barely eight in the morning, and somehow the place has opened early just for her. 

“My Rae asked for it,” Luella insists, matter-of-factly. “She needs it.”

Rio stares at the screen, dumbfounded.

“No, she doesn’t need it.” She grits her teeth, pushing the bowl aside with mild irritation. “She doesn’t even have a license to begin with. Do you hear how absurd that sounds? Buying her a car she literally cannot use?”

“She can keep it in the garage until she’s capable enough to drive.”

“No. Absolutely not.”

Reasoning with her mother has always been difficult, but the moment Rae becomes the topic, logic practically flies out the window.

Rio will admit she gives Rae a lot, maybe even more than she should though she really tries to do it with moderation. 

Luella, on the other hand? One single pout from Rae and the woman is ready to rearrange the entire world for her nena.

Of course Rio is grateful. She truly is. Having parents who love Rae as much as she do is a blessing but sometimes, it becomes.. this.

“Hija, please.” Luella pleads. “She really wants a Porsche.”

“And she’ll get one when she can buy it herself.” Rio states calmly. “She’s been working extra shifts at the restaurant. Give her.. I don’t know, a decade. She’ll have enough savings and maybe by then she’ll also know how to drive.”

Luella gasps softly, offended. “Why make my nenita suffer when I can already give it to her?”

Rio pinches the bridge of her nose. “I know that, Mama.” She mutters patiently. “But your nenita has to learn what it’s like to work for something. We’ve given her everything her whole life and I’m starting to realize now that’s not doing her any favors.”

Rio knows she’s not perfect at this either. She’s slipped more times than she can count when Rae asks, but wanting the best for your child and actually teaching them how to be a good person aren’t always the same thing.

Luella sighs dramatically. “I understand that.. It’s just that I recently bought Sophia a Porsche and I don’t want Rae to feel neglected.”

Rio blinks. Now, that’s why.

Sophia is Rio’s niece who’s only a few months younger than Rae. For a moment, she just stares at her mother through the phone. “She won’t feel bad, Mama.” Rio assures her. “Trust me.”

“How do you know that? I care about my granddaughters deeply. I want them treated equally.”

Rio understands where this is coming from.

When Rae was still a baby, Rio had been extremely careful about one thing: making sure Rae never felt like an outsider in the family. She had asked everyone to treat Rae with extra care, extra love, and extra reassurance.

Looking back now, maybe they all took that instruction a little too seriously.

“Just trust me on this.” Rio says, reaching for her smoothie and taking a sip. “Also, I know you’ve been giving Rae money.”

Luella suddenly becomes very interested in the hairdresser working behind her signature perm.

“Mama.” Rio warns.

“Well..”

“Would you please stop?” She requested, raising an eyebrow. “Or at least reduce it. I’m trying to teach her financial independence.”

Luella gasps again as if Rio has personally insulted her. “So now I cannot spoil my granddaughter. Wonderful. What’s next? Am I forbidden from seeing her too?”

“Don’t be dramatic. I’m just saying fifty dollars is acceptable. A weekly allowance of one thousand on the other hand? Yeah, maybe tone it down.”

A few months ago, Rae had lost a ring Rio gave her. A very expensive ring. Recently, Rae shows her the same exact jewelry, claiming she bought it as compensation for what she has lost.

Rio knows how much Rae earns from picking up extra shifts at the restaurant. She’s proud of her for working harder lately, but even with that income? There’s absolutely no way Rae could afford something like that on her own.

Which leaves only one logical conclusion..

Rio gives her mother a knowing look through the screen. “How much money have you been giving my daughter?”

On the other end of the video call, Luella’s perfectly applied fake eyelashes flutter, her hand flying to her chest as if Rio has just accused her of something deeply offensive. Again. “I do not know what you’re talking about!”

Rio can only sigh. It’s the kind of sigh that comes from years, even decades of knowing exactly how these conversations go and still having them anyway.

“Alright, then. Just keep in mind what we talked about and–” She cuts off mid-sentence. “There you are!”

Rae freezes in the kitchen doorway. Apparently, she had been hoping to slip in quietly, grab something, and disappear before Rio noticed her.

Unfortunately for Rae, Rio has the eyesight of someone who has spent sixteen years keeping track of a very clever and resourceful child.

“Mama, I’ll call you back.”

“But we still haven’t talked about tomorrow’s event!” 

Rio is already reaching for the red button. “I love you. We’ll talk again soon.”

The call ends. Rae, meanwhile, is already retreating.

“Oh heyyy, Mami.” Rae greets her, backing toward the hallway. “I was just leaving. Bye!”

Well.. Now Rio can say with full confidence that someone is definitely avoiding her.

“Not so fast.” She reminds her, pushing her chair back as she stands. “Come back here, young lady.” Rae stops as Rio actually sees her take a deep breath.

Then Rae turns around slowly and walks back toward the table, clearly accepting that escape is no longer an option.

“I’m meeting my friends.” Rae gestures vaguely toward the hallway. “Can this wait?”

“It cannot.” She folds her arms across her chest. “Did you ask your grandmother to buy you a Porsche?”

“No.” Rio says nothing. She just looks at her and it only took Rae approximately three seconds before she takes that one back. “Okay fine, yes.”

“Why?” Rio asks. “You can’t even pass your driver’s test and now you’re asking for a car?”

“But Mami..” Rae tries to reason out, suddenly animated as she leans against the counter. “It’s called manifestation.”

“Manifestation?”

“Yes!” Rae nods enthusiastically, as if this explains everything. “Think of it like motivation. If I already have the Porsche, I’ll be more motivated to pass my test so I can finally drive it.”

Rio looks at her daughter with genuine horror. Is this what teenagers believe now? “Honey..” Rio massages her temples. “You cannot be getting a Porsche even with that manifestation bullshit.”

“But Sophia got one from abuela!”

“That’s because Sophia knows how to drive.”

“I know how to drive.”

“You don’t.”

Rae stomps her foot, then she pouts.

Rio presses her lips together, fighting the urge to laugh at her daughter’s defensive reaction. This is supposed to be a serious parenting moment.

“So if I get my license first, then I can get my Porsche too?”

Rio smiles. “Nope.”

“Mami, why?” Rae groans loudly.

“We have three cars here.” Rio attempts to prove a point. “You can use one of mine. You’ll get your own car when you can afford to buy it with your hard earned money.”

Rae goes quiet and Rio can practically hear the gears turning in her head, which is why Rio immediately adds, “And no, you will not be getting financial assistance from your abuela. I know she’s been giving you money.”

Rae groans in frustration but quickly gets up from her theatrics.

“Okay..” She’s definitely going to negotiate at this point. “You’re using the Bentley, so maybe I could take the Tesla?”

To make the negotiation more probable, she adds a sweet smile and an even sweeter tone to the mix. “Please, Mami?”

“No.” Rio mirrors the same sweet expression. “You’re getting the SUV, though. That’s still a win.”

“NOOOO!” Rae whines immediately, collapsing against the counter in betrayal. “Mami, do you hear yourself? No one my age drives an SUV.”

“Then you’ll be the first.”

“Mami, please.” Now Rae pulls out the real weapon–those big blue puppy eyes she’s been using since she was five years old. She even steps closer until they’re nearly face to face.

Rio studies her. She still can’t believe how much this tiny human has grown.

Once upon a time Rae barely reached her waist and lived permanently attached to Rio’s hip, now she’s only a few inches shorter than her mami. Give it a few years and Rae will probably be taller than her.

Rio reaches forward and lightly bops Rae’s nose. “I’ll think about it.”

Rae grins instantly. “I can work with that.”

“But do not ask your abuela for a Porsche.”

“What if she offers?” Rae asks innocently. “It’s rude to refuse a gift, you know.”

“Say no politely then.”

“Fine.” Rae sighs in defeat. “Now can I go?”

Rio raises a single finger, clearly savoring the small power she has in this moment. “Not yet.”

Rae groans softly, the sound carrying equal parts frustration and resignation. She had thought that she was out of the woods, free to retreat to her world of friends.

“Why are you in contact with Maria?” Rio finally asks. “And why is she here?”

Rae’s expression shifts.

For the first time this morning, she looks a little guilty. “She said she was in town..” Rae answers carefully. “And I thought I could invite her over considering we’re friends.”

Rio raises an eyebrow. “You are not friends. She’s my ex.”

“Yes.” Rae shrugs. “But what does that have to do with our friendship?”

Rio studies her carefully. Over the years, only two girlfriends have been introduced to Rae. None of them stuck, of course.

Rae had always been polite but she’s more distant and unimpressed. Maria was the only one Rae actually seemed to like.

Which is suspicious.

“She’s nice.” Rae continues. “She works on some legal team for Rhode and sometimes, she  sends me free PR stuff.”

Rio remembers dinner last night with Maria being very friendly. Their breakup had been mutual which leaves no bad blood between both sides but still, exes are exes for a reason.

“Is this about Agatha?” Rio asks quietly.

Rae stiffens in an instant. “About who?” 

“You heard me.” Rio holds her gaze. “Is this about your mother?”

“You’re my mother.” Rae corrects immediately. “And, no. This has nothing to do with her.”

Rio watches her closely.

Sometimes she can tell when Rae is lying. She doesn’t know how, she just can.

Maybe it’s the way Rae’s eyebrows lift just a little too high. Or the tiny crease that forms between them.

“Have you talked to her?” She inquires more. “Agatha.” She adds as clarification in case it isn’t clear enough.

“No.”

A pause.

“But did she try talking to you?”

Rae shrugs. “I mean, in a way, yes.”

Rio leans forward slightly, interested. “So? How did it go?”

Rae shrugs again. “I don’t know.”

She has tried very hard not to let Rae build resentment toward her biological mother, long before they knew it was Agatha. So wherever this wall is coming from, Rio doesn’t quite understand it.

Or maybe.. she just hasn’t fully accepted yet that the little girl in ballet tutus is now old enough to form her own opinions.

“I think she’s trying.” Rio tells her gently. “Maybe you should give her a chance.”

For a moment something real flickers across Rae’s face, then the mask of voidness returns. “Maybe.” Rae mumbles. “Now can I go? I really don’t want to be late.”

Rio hesitates, then nods. “Text me where you are.”

“I will, Mami.” Rae tiptoes forward and presses a quick kiss to Rio’s cheek. “I love you.”

Rio watches her spin around and head toward the hallway, already moving with that easy, careless energy she always has when she thinks she’s escaped a conversation.

Rio can only hope Rae actually considers what she said.

Later that day, Rio runs a few errands, one of which includes dropping something off at the workshop. She’s hoping, though she doesn’t dare say it out loud, that she might catch a glimpse of Agatha.

As if the universe were listening, she spots a familiar figure stepping out of the building. Her heart gives a little jolt, and without thinking, she taps the horn once.

Agatha pauses on the sidewalk, brows arching slightly as she turns toward the car. The recognition comes a second later, followed by that small, curious tilt of her head she does when she’s trying to figure out why Rio Vidal is suddenly appearing in unexpected places.

Not totally unexpected, but the gist is there.

Rio rolls the window down and leans slightly toward the open space, resting her elbow casually against the door.

“Hey.” She greets with an easy smile. “Going somewhere?”

“I’m heading home.. or well, back to Lilia’s place.” Agatha's eyes narrow faintly in curiosity. “What are you doing here?”

“I dropped something off for Lilia.” Rio explains shortly. “But Kate met me outside, so I didn’t have to go in.”

She studies Agatha for a moment and adds, “I didn’t know you were here.” 

It’s probably a silly assumption, Rio realizes immediately. Agatha technically works here for the time being so it’s not unusual for her to be at her own workplace. Still, the workshop doesn’t have classes today, so Rio had figured the building would be mostly empty.

“A mutual director friend came over from Chicago.” She tells her. “He wanted to see the place and me apparently so, voila.”

Rio nods thoughtfully as her eyes flick briefly to the dashboard clock glowing softly inside the car.

She looks back at Agatha, the idea already forming before she fully thinks it through. “If you don’t have plans tonight, would you like to grab some dinner with me?”

“Rio..” Agatha looks puzzled. “It’s barely six p.m.”

“Early dinner, then.” Rio is unfazed. “My treat. And no—I’m not taking you to my restaurant. I’d rather not risk you getting tired of my food.”

Agatha considers it for a moment, clearly weighing the offer.

Then she gestures to herself. “You can’t possibly bring me anywhere public. I don’t have my scarf or sunglasses. How am I supposed to go incognito?”

Rio smiles a little wider.

That part of Agatha’s life still fascinates her—the quiet little dance required anytime she’s out and about.

“You can borrow my cap.” Rio offers, pointing to the one currently sitting on her own head. The faded lettering reads be cool. “And I’ve got extra sunglasses somewhere..”

She leans over and pulls open one of the compartments in the center console, rummaging for a moment before producing a Ray-Ban case the same way a magician revealing a prop. “Here.”

Agatha glances at the case, although still hesitant. “But I already booked an Uber…”

Rio waits, then Agatha sighs.

“You know what, never mind.” She reaches for the passenger door. “I’ll cancel it and pay him extra.” 

Rio can’t help the little smirk that slips onto her face.

“We’re having Japanese.” Agatha insists as she makes herself comfortable in her seat. “I really want sashimi.”

“I know a really good place.”

Agatha is now buckling her seatbelt as she speak, “And you’re paying.”

Rio glances over at her as she starts the car.

“That’s what I said.”

Rio pulls the car into traffic while Agatha settles beside her, adjusting the borrowed sunglasses slightly lower on her nose. Even half-hidden like that, she still looks unmistakably like herself.

Rio suspects she could wear a paper bag and people would still recognize her somehow. The sunglasses and scarf get up is definitely just for show.

“So..” Rio begins casually as she merges onto the main road, “Why are you leaving early if your friend just got there?”

Agatha scoffs. “I told Lilia I wasn’t feeling well. She might have been suspicious of my bluff but I’m too good of an actress at faking a cough.”

Rio glances over, amused. “Why would you do that?

Agatha turns toward her slightly, utterly unrepentant. “He’s one of those directors who believes every sentence he says deserves applause.” Agatha explains dryly, annoyance obvious in her tone. “You know the type. Smug, full of himself, literally kind of person who says ‘process’ every five minutes.”

Rio laughs. “I already can’t stand him.”

“Exactly.” Agatha is satisfied. “I lasted thirty minutes out of courtesy. That’s more than generous.”

Rio hums thoughtfully. “I’m impressed. I usually tap out at fifteen.”

Agatha smiles faintly at that statement before turning the conversation back. “What about you?” Why aren’t you at the restaurant?”

“I take time off sometimes. Even I deserve a break from my own kitchen.” Rio admits. “The ship will do just fine with an anchor in tow.”

“What anchor?”

“My sous-chef.” Rio clarifies. “Her name’s Alice and she’s a close friend of mine. She keeps everything steady when I’m not around.”

“That’s good because if the ship sinks while you’re gone, that would be very embarrassing.”

“Devastating, honestly.” Rio agrees solemnly.

Agatha laughs softly as Rio pretends to keep her eyes on the road.

Pretends. The truth is, having Agatha Harkness sitting in the passenger seat of her car is a dangerous situation for her focus.

The streetlights pass across Agatha’s face in warm flickers as they drive, illuminating the curve of her cheekbones, the soft lines near her eyes when she smiles, and the slight part of her lips when she’s listening.

Rio has seen her on screen plenty of times, but the camera doesn’t get it right. It doesn't do it much justice.

It captures her beauty, sure—but it misses the texture of it.

The way her expressions change every few seconds. The warmth in her eyes when she’s relaxed. The effortless charisma she carries even when she’s doing absolutely nothing.

And the laugh. Dear God.

Rio doesn’t remember when exactly it happened, but somewhere along the way she became embarrassingly aware of how much she enjoys hearing Agatha laugh.

They reach the restaurant just under twenty minutes later.

It’s tucked along a quieter street near downtown, the soft glow of lantern lights spilling onto the sidewalk outside. The entrance is modest but elegant with its wooden panels, sliding doors, and the faint scent of grilled fish and soy sauce drifting out every time someone walks in.

Rio parks nearby and turns off the engine. “This is it.” She reaches up and pulls the cap off her head, immediately hands it to Agatha. “Use it.”

Agatha takes it, but before putting it on, she flips down the visor mirror.

She begins tying her hair back into a loose ponytail and Rio instantly regrets having functioning eyeballs. Now she’s watching the other woman shamelessly. Again.

Agatha hums a tune softly under her breath while gathering her hair, her movements casual and unselfconscious. The streetlight through the windshield casts a warm glow over her skin, highlighting the natural pink in her cheeks.

Rio doesn’t even try to look away.

Agatha pulls the tie tight, then glances sideways. “What?”

Rio blinks like she’s been caught committing a crime. “You’re beautiful.” She utters before she can stop herself. It comes out completely sincere, almost hypnotized. “Like.. really beautiful.”

“If you’re trying to swoon me,” Agatha teases, “You’re going to need more vocabulary than beautiful.” She slides Rio’s sunglasses on and studies herself in the mirror. “This should be good.”

Rio notes that dutifully. “Oh, you’ll hear more words other than beautiful soon enough.” She promises as she begin to unbuckle her seatbelt. “Ready?”

Agatha opens the door. “Always.”

Their flirting has always hovered on the surface, but Rio knows she wants to say more eventually. She wants Agatha to hear it and she wants to be completely free of guilt when she says it.

And maybe, it won’t be as complicated as she’s been telling herself. Maybe Rae will earn to understand it eventually..

They step out of the car and walk toward the restaurant side by side.

Inside, the atmosphere shifts immediately. It has dark wood panels and paper lanterns hanging from the ceiling. The gentle clink of ceramic plates and quiet conversation filling the room.

A hostess greets them and leads them upstairs to the second floor.

The space up there is calmer, the tables arranged with a little more privacy. A few couples sit in low conversations while a group at the far corner shares sushi platters.

Agatha looks around with a satisfied smile. “Oh, this is nice.”

“Told you.

They settle across from each other at the table. Menus arrive eventually and Agatha barely needs one. She only came here for one thing. “Sashimi. A lot of it.”

“You weren’t kidding.”

Agatha looks up, unapologetic. “I deserve this.”

Rio orders a few additional dishes—miso soup, tempura, grilled salmon, a sushi platter. Agatha adds two more things to the list just for fun and to make full use of Rio’s generosity.

When the server leaves, the quiet settles comfortably between them.

Agatha leans back slightly in her chair as Rio studies her across the table.

The cap shadows her face just enough to keep her hidden from casual attention, but Rio still sees everything—such as the small smile playing on her lips.

And Rio realizes, not for the first time tonight, that she could probably sit here for hours just looking at this woman.

Which is a mildly terrifying thought, but also a very nice one.

Their food hasn’t arrived yet when Rio finally asks the question that’s been silently sitting between them. “Have you spoken to Rae?” She ponders. “About.. you know.”

Agatha nods, although the sunglasses make it harder for Rio to read her expression, which is mildly frustrating. Agatha’s eyes are naturally very honest even when the rest of her isn’t.

“I tried.”  Agatha answers shortly, her hands moving to hold the pendant she frequently wears. It's a habit at this point, from what Rio has observed.

“And?”

“She called the paparazzi on me.”

Rio is taken aback. “She what?!”

“I was attacked by those vultures and when I was about to confront her and we were about to talk, your ex showed up.” She continues.

Rio straightens immediately. “Wait, what?” She blurts in disbelief, leaning forward even more. “Did that happen yesterday? Why didn’t you tell me?”

Even behind the sunglasses, Rio can recognize that look on Agatha’s face. It’s subtle, just a small tightening around her mouth and oddly enough, it reminds Rio a lot of Rae.

That same flash of guilt that appears right before one of them tries to downplay something.

“I didn’t want to make it a big deal.” Agatha says with sincerity. “Besides, weren’t you busy entertaining that woman?”

“I was not entertaining her.” Rio shakes her head to deny it. “Tell me what happened.”

Agatha protests but Rio is pretty much insistent so she ends up recounting the whole thing anyway.

The lunch she was supposed to have with Rae, how Rae never showed up, and how instead paparazzi appeared out of nowhere.

Rio feels her stomach drop somewhere around that part.

Agatha continues—how they were finally supposed to talk at the restaurant.. until Maria walked in, then Rio herself.

Rio physically winces at that. Jesus.

From Agatha’s perspective, that must have looked like a coordinated ambush.

She presses her fingers tightly against her temple, trying to absorb the entire story without visibly spiraling into parental horror.

Because.. wow. Rae can be sarcastic. Occasionally a little mean in that teenage way where humor and cruelty sometimes blur together.

But calling paparazzi on someone after agreeing to meet up with them?

That’s.. new. And not in a good way.

When Agatha finishes, Rio sits quietly for a moment, living with it all. Then she apologizes. “I’m sorry. I don’t know what’s going on with that kid.” She means it. She really does.

Rae has always been spirited. A little dramatic often but she’s also kind. Sweet, even.

She's the kind of kid who used to leave sticky notes on Rio’s coffee mug that said drink water today so hearing about this version of her daughter, the one setting paparazzi traps and playing emotional chess with people—Rio doesn’t quite know where that girl came from.

“I’m moving on.” Agatha announces. “Besides, she promised we’ll talk again.”

Rio nods slowly although she doesn’t ask the question that briefly crosses her mind, which is why Agatha gave Rae up?

It’s not her story to pry into. And if Agatha ever decides she wants to share that with Rio, she will.

With that.. even knowing Rae inherited a good portion of Agatha’s personality including the stubbornness, the sharp tongue, and the love for dramatic flair—what Rae did yesterday was still unacceptable.

Rio traces the rim of her cup quietly. “I’ll talk to her.” No matter how complicated this situation is becoming, one thing Rio knows for certain is this: Rae must to understand that hurting people on purpose is not how you deal with complicated feelings.

Especially when those feelings involve someone who is trying, however clumsily, to be part of her life.

The server returns before Rio can say anything else.

A wooden tray appears between them, and suddenly the table fills with color of ruby slices tuna, pale salmon marbled with fat, and thin cuts of yellowtail arranged like petals. Steam curls from the miso soup while tempura crackles softly on a ceramic plate.

The smell alone makes Agatha’s mood change entirely. “Fuck, I’m already salivating.”

Rio seconds the motion, completely forgetting about the heaviness of what they're dealing with.

Agatha immediately reaches for her chopsticks. She looks like someone who has been waiting all day for this exact moment. She picks up a slice of tuna, studies it with exaggerated seriousness, and dips it in soy sauce.

Rio watches as Agatha takes a bite, her eyes almost rolling to the back of her head.

“You're forgiven.” She concludes after chewing thoughtfully. 

“For what?”

“For kidnapping me”

Rio chuckles. “That wasn't kidnapping.”

Agatha points vaguely with her chopsticks. “Well now I have sashimi, so you’ve temporarily secured my goodwill.”

Rio shakes her head, smiling as she takes a bite of salmon. Across the table, Agatha has already moved on to the next piece as though she’s conducting a tasting.

Agatha's cap and sunglasses don't hide the way she beams when she likes something. Or the small vein that appears on her forehead when she's feeling such specific emotions.

It’s ridiculous, honestly.

Rio has known plenty of beautiful women, but Agatha Harkness has this special ability to make beauty feel.. distracting. Hypnotizing, almost.

Especially when she’s relaxed like this.

“You’re staring again.” Agatha mutters without looking up.

“I’m admiring the sashimi.”

“Sure you are.”

“Chef’s privilege. I’m simply evaluating the quality of the fish.”

“I am no chef but I believe the fish passed inspection.” Agatha utters skeptically. “Or you can simply just say you're watching me..”

Rio sets her chopsticks down. “Well..” She starts slowly, “How can I not? Your smile is captivating.”

Agatha pauses so Rio continues, voice considerate. “And you have this thing where you lift one eyebrow when you’re about to say something sarcastic and your laugh is.. loud. In a good way.”

The other woman stares at her for a second longer. Then she laughs, which made Rio feel a little stupidly pleased for being proven right.

Agatha eventually rests her elbow on the table, studying Rio. “It's always nice to hear some feedback.” Then, she changes the topic. “So, how does someone become a chef?”

Rio wipes her hands with the napkin. “Very slowly.”

Agatha gestures for her to continue.

“I grew up around food and that alone is a privilege. My family’s always cooked. Big gatherings, loud kitchens, too many people giving opinions.”

“That explains a lot.”

Rio narrows her eyes. “What does that mean?”

“You’re very calm for someone who runs a restaurant.” 

“Years of practice.”

Agatha presses more. “And you like it?”

Rio doesn’t hesitate. “I love it.”

Something soft crosses Agatha’s expression and of course, Rio notices it immediately. She notices a lot of things about Agatha now.

The way her fingers tap the table when she’s thinking. The way she leans forward when she’s interested in a conversation. The way her whole face lights up when she laughs.

And Rio suddenly realizes they’ve already finished half the food.

Agatha glances down at the plates. “Oh.”

“What?”

“You ordered all this and I ate most of it.” Agatha gestures at the empty dishes, looking bashful.

Rio laughs. “I planned for that.”

Agatha points her chopsticks at her again. “You’re very confident.”

“Only when I’m right.”

Rio feels something warm settle quietly in her chest and for the first time all evening, neither of them mentions Rae.

It’s nearing the end of their dinner when Rio hears her name from somewhere behind her.

“Rio?”

She recognizes the voice immediately. Both she and Agatha turn at the same time just as a familiar figure approaches their table.

“Lia!” Rio exclaims, pushing her chair back as she stands.

Emilia Vidal—Lia to everyone who knows her, looks so much like Rio that strangers sometimes assume they’re twins. Same browm hair, same striking features, though Lia carries herself with a sharper sort of composure. Where Rio moves easily through a room, Lia walks like she owns it.

“I thought I heard your voice.” Lia says, smiling as they lean in for a beso on the cheek.

Rio squeezes her arm briefly. “What are you doing here?”

“I was meeting a client downstairs.” Lia explains casually before giving Rio a pointed look. “You weren’t at Yvette’s birthday lunch last week.”

Yvette is the youngest of three sisters. If Rio is the one who wandered off the expected path and Lia the one who stayed firmly on it, Yvette somehow balances both worlds effortlessly.

“I had something to take care of, but I took her out for dinner the day after, so I’m forgiven.”

Lia nods once, seemingly satisfied. Then her attention shifts, her gaze sliding past Rio and lands on Agatha.

Agatha, who has been watching the exchange with quiet curiosity, lifts her head slightly to be acknowledged.

“And who are you with tonight?” Lia asks, tone polite but observant.

Rio opens her mouth, already preparing some vague explanation, something that won’t invite too many questions, but Agatha beats her to it.

To Rio’s surprise, she stands. In one smooth motion, she removes the sunglasses and offers her hand. “Hi, I’m Agatha.”

For a brief moment. Lia simply stares. Rio actually watches the realization happen in real time.

“Agatha Harkness?” Lia whispers, her voice full of genuine surprise. “My goodness. You really are here in Westview.”

Agatha remains polite. “Well. Yes.”

Lia takes her hand, still looking slightly stunned. “It’s a pleasure to meet you, I’ve seen a lot of your work.”

Rio suppresses a small smile. Lia rarely sounds impressed by anything so this is a huge deal.

“And you’re acquainted with my sister?” Lia continues, glancing between them. “Rio hasn’t mentioned that.”

Rio clears her throat. “It's because—”

Agatha speaks first, perfectly calm. “We’re friends.”

Rio feels something flutter briefly in her chest at how naturally Agatha says it.

Lia studies them both a little longer than necessary. Rio knows her sister too well to recognize that look.

There’s curiosity there and a secret second thing. A quiet sort of evaluation, perhaps?

Rio and Lia have always had that between them.

Growing up as the two eldest daughters in a family like theirs meant expectations were never evenly distributed. Rio had been the firstborn—everyone assumed would inherit the family empire, until she didn’t.

Instead she walked away from it all to become a chef.

Everyone was surprised. Everyone except Lia. Lia had stepped into the role without hesitation, becoming everything their parents expected.

And though she’s never said it to Rio directly, she once overheard Lia telling their mother years ago, “Sometimes I feel like a spare.”

Lia had always been the one interested in their family’s business, even as children. Which meant that feeling probably came from the quiet understanding that everything she has now belonged to Rio if Rio had simply decided she wanted it in the first place.

Now Lia looks back at Agatha again. “So how do the two of you know each other?” 

Rio opens her mouth but Agatha answers first, beating her through it. Again. “We met through Rae.”

The name lands softly but heavily in Rio’s chest.

“Rae?” Lia repeats as her eyes flick briefly, calculating something Rio can’t quite name. “It’s certainly not every day I run into my sister having dinner with a movie star.”

Agatha smiles while Rio notices the way Lia keeps glancing at Agatha although not in admiration, exactly. More like.. interest. It can also be curiosity.

It’s ridiculous, really, but Rio has known her sister her whole life and Lia has always had a habit of wanting to measure and question the things Rio chooses for herself.

“Would you like to join us for a moment?” Agatha offers before Rio can stop her. “It's really nice meeting Rio’s sibling.”

Lia considers that, although she's already shrugging her head, “Oh, I wouldn’t want to intrude.”

But she doesn’t leave immediately either, instead she lingers beside their table a moment longer. Her actions contradicts her words.

Rio knows her enough to assume her sister can't leave quickly without prying for more, especially that curiosity has already rooted her in place. 

“Are you sure you don’t want to sit?” Agatha asks again, half teasing now.

Lia glances at the empty chair, then at Agatha. “Fine, only for a minute.”

She pulls the chair out and sits with graceful composure, crossing one leg over the other as the other two went back to their respective chairs as well.

“So..” Lia says, folding her hands together as she glances at Agatha, still in awe, “I have to say this is quite surreal.”

“Meeting your sister here?”

“No, meeting you here.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “Please don’t start.”

But Lia is already grinning warmly at Agatha. “I’ve seen almost all of your films.” She admits. “My daughter is actually obsessed with you.”

“You have a daughter too?”

“Yes.” Lia nods proudly. “She’s turning sixteen next week.”

“If it isn't that great an age.” Agatha’s expression softens instantly.

With Rae and Sophia being almost the same age—just like Rio and Lia, Rio can’t help the stray thought that slips into her mind for the first time. She wonders if there's something brewing between the girls too?

Rae has been unusually adamant about wanting a Porsche from her abuela, and Rio is trying to figure out where that sudden insistence even came from.

The girls are close, that much is true. Sophia’s gentle sweetness has always balanced Rae’s sharper edges in a way that somehow works, but closeness doesn’t always mean simplicity.

Rio had never noticed any real competition between them before. Then again.. people rarely see rivalry when it’s still quiet, when it’s buried under smiles and shared sleepovers.

After all, she and Lia look perfectly fine on the surface too.

“Oh!” Lia suddenly exclaims, turning fully toward Agatha. “My daughter’s birthday party is next weekend, it would be an absolute honor if you came.”

Rio nearly chokes on her saliva. “Emilia—”

But Lia continues, earnest and enthusiastic now. “She would lose her mind if she met you. Truly. I don’t normally ask things like this but, if you happened to have the time..”

Rio gazes at Agatha, already preparing herself for the polite refusal.

Agatha is many things. Attending a random teenager’s birthday party for someone she just met? That seems unlikely.

Agatha only shrugs, “If I’m still in town next week, I don’t see why not.”

Rio’s head snaps toward her as she chokes up a small, “Really?”

“Sure.”

Lia actually claps once, delighted. “She’s going to be so excited!”

Rio glances at Agatha, searching for any sign of reluctance, but there’s none. If anything, Agatha looks like she truly wants this.

“I won’t keep you both any longer.” Lia tells them as she stands up, smoothing her dress. “I'll make sure to send the details through Rio.”

She leans down to kiss Rio’s cheek again and points at her in an accusatory way. “Don’t forget this time.”

“I won’t.” Rio promises.

Lia gives Agatha one last grateful smile. “It was wonderful meeting you.”

“You too.” Agatha replies warmly.

And just like that, Lia disappears down the stairs. Rio watches her go, then turns back slowly toward Agatha.

“You just agreed to attend a sweet sixteen”

Agatha reaches for the last piece of sashimi. “Yes.”

“You don’t even know my sister, nor my niece”

Agatha eats the sashimi casually as if she didn't just made a plan she might not want to do in the first place. “This is my avenue of spending more time with Rae.” She reasons out and winks at Rio. “And you.”

Rio chuckles, shaking her head. “You have no idea what you just walked into.”

Agatha truly looks like she’s not worried at all.

By the time they leave the restaurant, the night air has cooled. The city lights reflect softly against the car windows as Rio starts the engine.

Agatha settles into the passenger seat, both cap and sunglasses discarded at this point,

Rio glances at her. “You really didn’t have to say yes to that.”

“It’s a birthday party, Rio. Not a blood oath.”

Rio nods as she pulls onto the road.

Still, she can’t stop thinking about the way Lia had looked at them earlier.. That quiet measuring glance? That means trouble.

“You know she was testing you.” Rio says after a moment.

“Hmmm?” Agatha hums. “Testing me?”

“My sister.. She likes to evaluate people.”

Agatha raises a brow. “And did I pass?”

“I think you managed to impress her.”

Agatha is smirking now. “I wouldn't expect anything less.”

They drive for a few minutes in silence. Streetlights pass in soft intervals and Rio finds herself glancing at Agatha more than she should every now and then.

Rio has to forcefully drag her attention back to the road, forcing out a deep breath to calm her insides.

“So, do I get extra points for agreeing to attend a child’s party for you?”

“You didn’t do it for me.”

“Maybe I did.”

Rio doesn’t answer that. Instead she pulls the car to a stop outside Lilia’s house. They sit there for a moment, neither moving.

Agatha fixes her shirt and Rio feels that familiar distraction hit her again.

“You’re staring again.” Agatha mutters. “Can you possibly make it less obvious?”

“How can I not?”

Agatha looks at her with something close to amusement in her eyes. Then, without a word, she leans across the center console. Rio barely has time to process it before Agatha’s lips press gently against hers.

The kiss is soft—barely more than a peck, but it’s enough to send the butterflies in Rio’s stomach into a frenzy, fluttering wildly into chaos.

When Agatha pulls back, Rio is still blinking in surprise. “That’s for the sashimi.”

Rio lets out a quiet huff, still a little stunned. “Just the sashimi?”

Agatha opens the door. “We’ll see about the rest later.”

She steps out of the car, giving Rio one last glance before heading toward the house.

Rio sits there for a little while after she disappears inside. Her fingers tap once on the steering wheel, and she realizes she’s smiling like a complete fool.

When Rio arrives home, Mrs. Davis is in the living room, curled up with her iPad and an HBO show playing quietly in the background. 

Her old nanny has a routine which includes coming over a few nights a week, sometimes stay the night, keep herself busy. Rio doesn’t ask her to clean or do chores; she’s offered Mrs. Davis a kind of retired freedom, letting her live life however she wants. But the woman, stubborn as always, prefers to keep moving, keep her joints working, and keep her mind occupied.

“You’re home.” Mrs. Davis says upon spotting her. “Would you like me to heat up some dinner for you, dear?”

“No thank you. I already ate.”

“You already ate?”

“Yes. I had dinner with a friend.” Rio replies, feeling warmth curl in her chest.

Mrs. Davis watches her with keen eyes. “Well, you’ve got a nice smile going on there.”

“Do I?” Rio asks, raising an eyebrow, though she already knows the answer.

“Please. I’ve taken care of you since you were a child.” Mrs. Davis tells her, laying a hand over her heart. “I’ll recognize that toothy grin anywhere.”

Rio simply shakes her head as she starts heading toward the stairs. “I’m going up to check on Rae.” She informs her. “Don’t stay up too late!” She calls back, knowing full well Mrs. Davis will most likely stay up late using electronics.

Instead of going directly to her room, Rio decides to go to Rae’s wing first. She knocks, then hears Rae’s soft voice saying, “Come in.”

The room is spacious and immaculate, done in soft beige tones. A queen-sized bed sits neatly made, a study nook with an R shaped lamp glows gently, and the walk-in closet is huge, perfectly organized. On the walls hang large framed photographs: Switzerland, Italy, snapshots of faraway adventures.

Rae sits in front of her desk, her laptop open, her pink matching pajamas soft against her skin. Her hair is rolled up in the morning curlers, the kind that promise effortless waves by sunrise.

“Hey, Mami.” Rae greets her, looking up.

Rio leans against the doorframe, arms crossed casually. She doesn’t speak immediately, just watches. The soft glow of the lamp and the quiet hum of Rae’s humidifier fills the space between them.

“What?” Rae asks, a little self-conscious. “Did I do something wrong?”

“I know about what you did to Agatha.”Rio’s voice is gentle but firm. “That wasn’t right, my love.”

Rae’s eyes widen for a fraction, then she masks the surprise quickly. “I’m sorry.” She whispers, her voice small.

“Don’t apologize to me. Apologize to her.”

Rae goes mute as Rio continues, “You know, I thought I gave you everything. Even taught you the things you know. I thought I made you understand. But I guess.. I’m missing something.”

Her daughter rises from her chair and takes a cautious step toward her. “Mami, no, that’s not it.” She attempts to soften the blow, but Rio gently raises a hand, stopping her.

“She’s still your mother, Rae. And so am I. Both things can be true at once.” Rio explains, her tone soft but unyielding. “If you don’t want to treat her as such for some reason, that’s your choice to make. But please.. treat her like a human being, above all else, when it’s hard to treat her like your mother.”

Rio inhales slowly and allows herself to smile despite it all. Her heart swells at the sight of Rae, who means more to her than she can articulate. 

Sometimes, all a mother can do is guide and let go.

“I..” Rae struggles for words. “Are you mad at me?”

“I’m not.” Rio answers quietly, placing a gentle hand over Rae’s shoulder. “I’m just disappointed.”

The weight of that word lands on Rae, heavier than anything else. All her life, she’s tried not to hurt her mami, and hearing her disappointment stings.

“If you’re old enough to pull a stunt, I’m sure you’re old enough to fix it yourself.” Rio continues, her voice steady but kind. “I told you I’d be supportive, no matter what your decision is, but support doesn’t mean tolerating bad behavior. There’s a difference, Rae. I hope you understand that.”

Rae nods slowly, a soft blush coloring her cheeks. She doesn’t speak, but her eyes convey everything: understanding, remorse, and that tender spark of love for the woman who raised her.

Rio stands, brushing back her hair, and gives Rae one last glance before she quietly exits the room while her daughter stays there, a little breathless, staring at the door.

At the end of the day, that’s her little girl. She wants Rae to make her own decisions, to grow and learn, but never at the expense of others.

Rio lets herself linger in the hallway for a beat, feeling the quiet satisfaction of having set the boundaries. She wants to guide Rae toward a better path, one where mistakes are lessons meant to be learned.

She turns and finally heads to her room, praying that even in the midst of teenage rebellion, her little girl is still there.

And somewhere deep in her chest, Rio knows that patient and unyielding love—will always guide that little girl home.
