Chapter 17: Chapter 17

Chapter Notes

come come, meet the vidals :p

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“Ms. Harkness?”

Agatha’s gaze shoots up immediately the moment she hears one particular voice calling her name.

Rae stands before her, tote bag slung over one shoulder and a pink iPad case clutched in the other hand. She looks shy, almost aloof, as she approaches the table Agatha shares with Lilia and Kate.

Rae being described as.. shy? That’s new information.

“Yes?”

“Can I speak with you?” Rae asks and adds, “In private, preferably.”

Agatha points at herself and then looks at the other two people beside her in surprise. Speak with her? In private? Her? Agatha Harkness?

What the fuck is going on.

“You want to speak with me?” Agatha clarifies, still unable to believe Rae would be the one making the first move. “Me?”

“Dear, I believe you’re the only Harkness in this bunch.” Lilia announces without looking up from the notebook she’s scribbling in. She waves a hand dismissively, as if shooing Agatha away.

“Right now?” Agatha questions again, giving Rae the opportunity to perhaps reconsider this idea.

For today’s class, they did some acting drills and rehearsed a few scenes for the performance they’ll be doing in a few weeks.

Rae, front and center as usual, has been notably pale and out of sorts. She arrived late and even missed a few lines and cues—something that never happened before, especially for someone like her.

Agatha had meant to ask if everything was okay, but she never got the chance to catch Rae alone. And frankly, there was a high chance the kid would’ve snapped at her for even breathing near a fraction away.

Still, Rae being off her game like this? It’s not on brand.

“Yes.” Rae nods to confirm. “If you can spare some time.”

Of course Agatha can spare—will spare some time. That’s literally her kid asking for the first time. Who is she to deny?

She stands up albeit reluctant, excusing herself to the others before leading Rae out into the hallway. Most of the students have already gone home, leaving the workshop quiet.

Agatha can’t help the suspicion creeping in as she places a finger under her chin, studying Rae with exaggerated curiosity. “Are you calling the paparazzi on me again?”

Rae visibly cringes, immediately avoiding Agatha’s gaze. “No.”

“Then we’re off to a great start.”

Rae doesn’t fire back with a rebuttal, which is alarming in itself. Agatha is genuinely starting to worry now. What happened to the strong-willed sixteen-year-old she met? Because honestly, the kid in front of her looks like she’s one inconvenience away from a full emotional breakdown.

“What do you want to talk about?” She asks gently, persuading Rae to start talking.

Rae takes a deep breath, fiddling with her fingernails. The kid looks bothered, as if the weight of the world is on her shoulders right this moment.

Eventually, she speaks. “I’m sorry.”

Agatha’s ears almost buzz upon hearing it. Well, that’s unexpected. She stares at Rae for a long second, blinking slowly.

Either the universe just shifted on its axis, or someone slipped something into her milk this morning.

“I didn’t quite catch that one.” She says slowly, straightening her posture. “Would you repeat it for me?”

Rae bits her lower lip as she lifts her head to meet Agatha’s eyes. “I said.. I’m sorry.”

Agatha blinks again. Right. She actually said she’s sorry so she did hear that correctly.

She crosses her arms, looking at Rae as though she’s some rare, endangered species that just wandered into the building. “This is new.”

Rae frowns. “What is?”

“The apology.” Agatha gestures vaguely between them. “Usually when we interact, it’s more of casual public humiliation. Maybe a light paparazzi ambush here and there. You know, the classics.”

Rae did not say anything although Agatha can tell she’s guilty of all those things based on her facial expressions.

“You’re really apologizing?” Agatha tries to clarify, testing the sentence out or else it might explode if handled incorrectly.

Rae’s mouth tightens into a small twitch. “Yes.”

“Voluntarily?”

Rae exhales through her nose, clearly already regretting this entire interaction. “Yes. Voluntarily.”

Agatha studies her more with suspicion. “Should I be checking the ceiling for hidden cameras? Is this some sort of elaborate social experiment?”

“There are no cameras and this is certainly not a prank.”

“Mhmm.” Agatha narrows her eyes. “Because if Jimmy Kimmel jumps out right now, I swear to God—”

“Agatha.” Rae firmly calls her name. “I’m actually being serious for once.”

Agatha sighs dramatically since she really means business. “Fine, ruin my fun.”

She crosses her arms, leaning her shoulder against the wall, trying very hard to look unimpressed instead of whatever the hell she’s currently feeling because Rae apologizing is approximately as likely as a solar eclipse happening indoors.

“So.. you’re sorry.”

“Yes. How many times must I reiterate that?

“Don’t snap at me. You’re supposed to be apologizing, remember?” Agatha reminds her. “Is the apology for the paparazzi ambush or the general emotional terrorism?”

Rae grimaces, being reminded of what she has done. “All of it.”

Agatha watches her carefully now. The sarcasm is still there, perched on her tongue like it always is, but something in Rae’s face makes her swallow the harsher version.

The kid looks bothered and painfully would prefer to be somewhere else but she’s stuck here instead. Rae shifts her weight, gripping the strap of her tote bag tightly. “I shouldn’t have done that. It was really immature of me.”

Agatha’s brows arch. Immature. Look at that, personal growth and character development this early on. Miracles do happen, after all.

“Also,” Rae adds stiffly, clearly forcing the words out one by one, “Tipping the paparazzi was excessive.”

Agatha lets out a small hum. “You only realized that now?”

The kid hesitates again before adding quietly, “I didn’t think you’d actually show up.”

That catches Agatha off guard. Her expression softens before she can stop it. “Of course I’d show up. Why wouldn’t I?”

The tension in Rae’s shoulders loosens just a little even if she doesn’t answer that question.

Silence settles between them for a moment and as Agatha continue to look at her, she really can’t deny that the resemblance between them is uncanny. Not just the face, no. It includes the attitude and personality on top of everything else.

If Agatha didn’t know better, she’d say the universe plagiarised her homework.

“What brought this on?” Agatha says after a beat, refusing to allow awkwardness envelop them into a suffocating hug.

Rae hesitates again, then shrugs. “Mami talked to me.”

Agatha huffs out a quiet laugh under her breath. “Well, remind me to send her a fruit basket as gratitude.”

She wonders what exactly Rio said or did to this kid to make her march over here and apologize without so much as a dramatic eye roll. Whatever it was, it clearly worked.

Honestly, Agatha half expects the ceiling to collapse from the shock of it. She never would have expected Rae to apologize without a fight but now, as she looks closer, she can see that Rae actually seems.. genuine.

Agatha clears her throat, softening her tone just a notch. “What exactly did she say to you that has you going around issuing public apologies?” She asks, trying to keep the question light.

Rae’s gaze drops to her hands. “She said she’s disappointed in me.”

Agatha hadn’t expected that, which is why she straightened her posture when Rae said it, sensing the heaviness in the kid’s voice. Apparently it is that serious.

Rae fiddles with her fingers again, shoulders drawing in just a little. “I don’t want to be a disappointment to Mami.” She says quietly. “That’s the last thing I ever want to be. I really try to do everything right so she’ll be proud of me. I don’t want her looking at me like that ever again.”

Agatha exhales slowly. So all of this is because Rae doesn’t want to disappoint Rio, and while Agatha understands that, there’s still a small ache in realizing the kid is doing it for her mami—not for Agatha herself.

But she’ll take the win. At least they’re starting somewhere.

“I’m pretty sure she’s proud of you. I mean, look at you. You’re talented and capable of orchestrating paparazzi ambushes before you can legally vote. Most mothers would be amazed by that kind of range.”

Rae frowns at the casual dig against her.

“But..” Agatha adds, raising a finger, “Actions against other people might slightly damage that otherwise impressive résumé so, take it easy.”

“I know.” Rae grits her teeth. “That’s why I’m saying sorry now.”

As much as Agatha would enjoy this, the kid looks miserable enough already. There’s no need to pile on so she gives a small smile instead. “Okay. Apology accepted.”

“Really?”

Agatha nods. “Oh yes, I don’t like seeing you being all..” She gestures pointedly toward Rae, “Sad and emotionally responsible. It’s unsettling, I’m actually getting goosebumps standing next to you.”

“You’d rather I be mean to you?” Rae raises a brow.

“I’d rather you be yourself.” Agatha replies, then she smirks. “And for the record, I can absolutely be meaner. I’m just letting you off the hook since, you know.. you’re younger and much fragile.”

“Aww.” Rae fakes a pout, finding her footing. “Are you saying you’re old?”

“No, I’m simply saying you can’t level with someone who has years of expertise.”

“So basically, ancient.” Rae concludes. She tilts her head, pretending to think. “How was Noah’s Ark, by the way? Was it a five-star cruise or more of a budget situation?”

Agatha blinks at her at her for a moment before a small chuckle slips out. “Wow, mocking my age and biblical history in one sentence. Impressive!”

For the first time that day, Rae smiles. It’s small, but it’s surely there.

Agatha, being deeply allergic to prolonged emotional vulnerability, clears her throat. “Is there anything else you’d like to talk about before we both pretend this heartfelt exchange never happened?”

Rae looks like she’s about to say something. She hesitates, starts to speak, and stops. Then finally says, “No.”

Fair enough. Discussing the complicated history of secret adoptions in a hallway probably isn’t ideal anyway.

“Alright then, you should head home, Rae.” She waves a hand casually. “Try not to terrorize any Uber drivers on the way.”

Rae nods and without saying anything more, starts to turn her back against Agatha. When Agaha herself was about to return to the room, Rae calls her name again.

“Agatha?” The voice is softer this time.

She turns back immediately, a flicker of something hopeful crossing her face. “Yes?”

“When you said you wanted me..” Rae murmurs, voice barely above a whisper. “Is that true?”

Agatha doesn’t even let a beat drop as she answer immediately. “Of course it is.”

“Okay..” Rae responds, as if it’s more of a conviction to herself. “Okay. I just wanted to hear that again.”

For a moment, they simply stand there, staring at each other and for the first time since they crossed paths, it doesn’t feel like a battlefield. 

Rae turns and walks down the hallway, officially heading toward the exit while Agatha stands there for a second longer than necessary, her fingers clasp firmly against her pendant.

Weekend arrives, and it’s Rio’s niece’s sweet sixteen celebration. Agatha still isn’t entirely sure why she agreed to come in the first place.

Part of her insists it’s because this means getting to know Rae’s family—the people she grew up with, the village that helped raise her when Agatha couldn’t. Those are the people who were there for her kid during the years Agatha wasn’t, and perhaps in some quiet, unspoken way, she wants to thank them.

For loving Rae, for keeping her safe, and for giving her a home.

That’s the official reason why she’s coming. The other reason, of course, is Rio Vidal.

Agatha is apparently completely, embarrassingly enamored with Rio. It’s humiliating, really, to have your eyes set on a woman you can have should the situation be different.

Maybe she can still have her. If she does, will she be Rae’s mommy or step-mommy? How does that even work? That's the least of her worries as of now but she'll definitely cross the bridge when she gets there.

After roughly a hundred outfit changes and a brief existential crisis involving three different brands, Agatha finally settles on a perfectly tailored cream suit. It looks effortless, which is the vibe she's going for.

She's wearing a fitted turtleneck sitting underneath, the fabric soft against her skin. Wide trousers fall neatly to her ankles, and a belt pulls the entire thing together. Gold jewelry glints just enough to be noticed while her hair falls in loose waves around her shoulders, intentionally imperfect.

She’s not trying to impress anyone with her look, her presence alone does that, but what's the harm in a little added polish?

Agatha also isn’t trying to impress Rio. That would imply effort. She could show up half put-together at best, and Rio would still look at her like she’s the most interesting thing in the room. The problem with that is Rio’s not even pretending to be subtle about it.

Rio sends her a text message when she’s outside Lilia’s house.

They’d agreed Rio would pick her up, and luckily the universe shows mercy because Lilia and Kate both have errands to run. This means no interrogation on how suspiciously long Agatha spent getting ready or why she's hanging out with the Vidals in the first place.

She takes one final look in the mirror and thinks she’d do herself so with that, she grabs a sleek clutch and a small gift bag before heading outside.

Rio’s Bentley is parked neatly at the curb. Agatha reaches for the passenger door then pauses in action upon seeing the sight behind the wheel.

Suddenly, Agatha forgets how oxygen works.

Rio wears a soft brown dress that drapes loosely over her body, the fabric thin enough that it moves naturally with every breath. Which also means it becomes painfully obvious she didn’t bother with a bra. Agatha surely notices that, and then tries very hard to pretend she didn’t.

Bold move. Very bold move.

“Hey.” Rio greets. Dark sunglasses cover her eyes, giving her that untouchable look. Her wavy hair falls freely over her shoulders, slightly tousled as if she didn’t try very hard with it.

Small gold hoops catch the light when she turns her head, and a few delicate necklaces rest against her collarbone, which is somehow impossible not to stare at.

Even sitting there casually, she carries that calm confidence that makes people orbit around her without realizing it. “We look like a latte threw up on us.” Rio adds with a grin.

Agatha glances down at herself, then back at Rio.

“If we’re going to resemble a beverage, I’m glad it’s at least something I would drink.” She says smoothly as she slides into the seat.

Rio laughs softly, and Agatha has to pretend again the sound doesn’t make something warm bloom in her chest.

The theme is clearly beige and brown, something Agatha will never fully understand about teenagers and their strange devotion to muted color palettes.

Still, it works because Rio looks ridiculously good in it.

Agatha takes another glance. Then another. Then she immediately looks away before she gets caught.

Too late. Rio grins slightly. “See something you like?”

Agatha scoffs. “Oh please, I’m just surprised you decided to attend a family event dressed like a walking distraction.”

Rio lifts a brow. “And you showed up in a cream suit like you’re about to close a million-dollar deal.”

“What can I say? I like to look competent.”

Rio studies her for a moment as she starts the engine. “You look really beautiful, Agatha.”

Agatha freezes for half a second but she manages to recover quickly, leaning back in the seat with a casual shrug. She’s unwilling to let Rio win this game, whatever deeply consequential game this has become.

“So do you.”

“Do I?” Rio asks in a playful tone, eyes focused on the road.

Agatha hums, tilting her head just slightly as she glances at her from the corner of her eye, carefully at that, because looking directly would be a mistake, and Agatha does not want to make that kind of mistake.

“I’ve only ever seen you in tank tops and casual fits.” She points out her observations. 

Her gaze betrays her for half a second—dipping lower at Rio’s chest before snapping back to the road as though nothing happened.

“This is a very effective reminder that you have money.” She continues, gesturing loosely in Rio’s direction without looking at it.

Rio lets out a quiet snort. “I always prefer comfortable clothes.”

“Of course you do.”

“But I do enjoy dressing up sometimes.” Rio adds, lips curving faintly. “Otherwise, where exactly would I spend all this money for?”

Agatha rolls her eyes, though the faint pull at her mouth ruins the effect. “Ah, yes. The burden of wealth.”

Rio laughs as Agatha shifts slightly in her seat, crossing one leg over the other, “Where’s Rae, by the way?”

“She already spent the night there.”

Agatha nods once, absorbing that. “And is she aware I’m coming, or am I continuing my streak of unannounced appearances in her life?”

Rio glances at her for a quick moment, “You’re not gatecrashing, Lia announced that the great Agatha Harkness is invited the moment you said yes in our family GC so she's very much aware.. so is everyone, apparently.”

“At least I’ll be welcomed properly.” She mutters, smoothing her sleeve.

“They’re really excited to meet you.”

Agatha raises a brow. “Rich people gush over celebrities now?”

Rio is unfazed. “Not just any celebrity. It turns out my family has a particular fondness for you.”

Agatha doesn’t respond immediately, as if that didn't boost her ego up. She just looks out the window as the scenery begins to shift. A few minutes of driving and she can already see wider streets and bigger houses. There is more distance between each property, as though even proximity is a luxury here.

Rio’s house is already in a wealthy part of Westview. Where they're heading to now is another wealthy part of the town. It's exclusive in a way that doesn’t need to announce itself.

“Why don’t you live near your family?” Agatha asks, gaze still outward.

“We used to live a few blocks away.”

“And then you escaped?”

“Something like that. I decided I wanted more space.”

“From weekly dinners and brunches or Sunday board games except you count who has more riches?” Agatha guesses in sarcasm.

Rio didn't specify what and only says, “Exactly.”

Agatha lets out a quiet breath. “It must be nice having a big family.”

Rio glances at her although this time, there’s something more careful in it. “You don’t?”

“No.” She admits. “I don’t think I ever really had one, my mother was just a cunt who raised me. May her soul never rest in peace, though I fear she's very much alive.”

There’s a brief pause, then to her surprise, Rio snickers. Agatha feels something in her chest loosen upon hearing that, appreciating no form of pity from the other woman. “That’s the appropriate reaction.”

“I’ve been told I’m very supportive.”

Not long after, they reached their destination. Massive silver gates open before them, and the car rolls forward into the Vidal estate.

Agatha straightens slightly as the house comes into full view. Mansion might be more of an appropriate word to describe it.

Three stories of stone and glass, clean lines softened by warm lighting that spills from within. The driveway curves in an elegant arc, already filled with cars.

It’s fascinating but it’s not cold, as most wealthy people's houses are. It feels lived in, and honestly that's an impressive observation even for Agatha who have been to many estates such as this.

“I see where the ‘spend all your money’ philosophy went.” Agatha murmurs as Rio parks.

“Keep in mind that this is my parents’ house, not mine.” 

They step out together, and it’s only when Agatha gets a proper, unobstructed view that she realizes Rio isn’t wearing a dress.

Instead, she's wearing a two-piece. Her choice of clothing shifts with movement, clings just enough to be distracting without being obvious.

Agatha looks. Then immediately looks away. Then looks again, because apparently self-control is optional tonight.

Looking and not looking has almost become a habit and she doesn't like it one bit.. she really wants to look without looking away—get it?

“Something wrong?” Rio asks, noticing her behavior.

“Nice drip.” Agatha says smoothly, clearing her throat.

Rio only smiles like she knows exactly what that means. They move in tandem, a few people whispering as Agatha walks past.

“Do you always cause this kind of reaction?” Rio murmurs.

“I’m not causing anything, people simply recognize excellence when they see it.”

Rio bumps her shoulder playfully. “Right.”

They move through the house easily, and Agatha notices the difference immediately. It’s grand, yes, but not in a suffocating way.

There are people everywhere and Rio points at them as they weave through the crowd, knowing all of their names or where they're from. Mostly it's just family and young friends of the celebrant themselves.

“Birthdays are usually here. Or any big celebration, really. My parents’ place is bigger than all our houses.” Rio explains.

“It is really huge.” Agatha says, glancing around.

“We all kind of gather here all the time.” Rio continues. “This used to be my great great grandparents house. They came from Puerto Rico, built everything from scratch when they moved here. It's passed down from generations until it's refurbished to keep up with time.”

Agatha turns slightly, “Were you born in Puerto Rico?”

“I was born here, but we visit there yearly to be one with our roots, as what mama says.” Rio answers. “Most of the distant family from my parents are there so it's always exciting times.”

They step out into the backyard, where string lights cast everything in gold. There’s a section arranged almost like a function hall—tables, a dance space, music threading through the air.

Agatha takes it in quietly, eyes moving from detail to detail. It isn’t the scale that stands out, but the atmosphere. People move easily, families gathered in small groups, teenagers drifting between them.

She’s been to enough parties to expect something louder, designed to impress before anything else. This isn’t that. The wealth is there, obvious in the details, but it settles in a way that it has nothing to prove.

She watches them for a moment, something quiet settling in her chest. Rae grew up here, surrounded by this kind of people and the warmth they bring.

There’s relief in knowing that Rae didn’t grow up in something cold. She wasn’t left to figure everything out on her own, and that should be enough but there’s something else underneath it.

Because yes, Rae growing up like this also means she didn't grow up with Agatha.

“Rio..” Agatha starts but another voice calls out, much louder than her’s.

“Rio!” A woman approaches, pulling Rio into a quick embrace before she can react.

“Finally, you have shown yourself.” She says, then turns to Agatha, eyes lighting up. “And this must be—oh my god, it is you.”

There’s something familiar about her face. She has this warmth in her eyes and the same kind of smile that feels kind. She might look older but undeniably cut from the same place as Rio.

“You’re Agatha Harkness.” She points out, as though it’s both a statement and a small victory. “I knew it.”

Agatha tilts her head, faintly amused. “Its a pleasure to be here, Mrs. Vidal.” Agatha smiles. Of course she knows who she's speaking to. Google has offered its fair share of information about the matriarch of the Vidal family.

“So you really now my daughter.” Luella grins. Then, without hesitation, “You have the most beautiful blue eyes I’ve ever seen.”

Agatha blinks. That was—unexpected.

Luella pauses, then adds quickly, almost apologetic, “No. Second, actually. I’m a little biased.”

Agatha’s brow lifts, intrigued despite herself. “I was hoping for first place.” She jokes.

“First place belongs to her beloved granddaughter.” Another voice slips in, and Agatha turns just in time to see—well, another Rio variant.

They're not exactly identical, but close enough to make her pause. They have the same facial features, although this one looks sharper at the edges, like the softer parts haven’t had time to settle yet.

“I’m Yvette.” She introduces herself, stepping forward. “The youngest of three.”

Agatha hums, glancing between them. “I’m Agatha.”

The comment about blue eyes lingers somewhere in the back of her mind, but she doesn’t quite follow it—doesn’t make the connection. Not when there are too many versions of the same face standing in front of her.

“You do have beautiful eyes.” Yvette supplies, studying her with open curiosity. “You know, Mama and I watched your Italia film in Italy. She’s sort of a fan.”

“That feels appropriately on brand.”

“Well, I love my celebrities every now and then.” Luella adds, entirely unhelpful.

“Let’s not overwhelm her.” Rio cuts in, moving closer, tone light but pointed.

“Oh, don’t start.” Yvette waves her off, giving her sister a playful glare. “Why have you been gatekeeping her from us? We didn’t even know you were friends with a literal A-lister.”

“We only met.” Rio defends quickly. “She’s uh—Rae’s mentor.”

Her eyes flick to Agatha’s. It’s brief, but there's an understanding sitting just beneath the surface of the words. Something only the two of them are aware of, carefully held in place.

Agatha meets her gaze, just as fleeting. “Something like that.”

“Well, my guest is here!” Another voice joins their circle.

Agatha turns just in time to see Lia approaching, champagne in hand. “Agatha, it’s really nice to see you here!”

Agatha smiles, the kind that lands exactly where it needs to. “It’s a beautiful party.”

It is. She won’t say that twice.

Lia lights up like she’s been personally validated. “I’m so glad you think so. I wasn’t sure you’d actually show up but here you are!”

“I do try to exceed expectations occasionally.”

That earns a laugh and just like that, she’s absorbed into it.

Vidal women, apparently, don’t do anything halfway. They gather seamlessly, as if this was always going to happen the second she stepped foot into their orbit.

“So you're Rae’s mentor, huh?”

Agatha doesn’t miss the way Rio stills just slightly when Yvette asks,

 “Among other things.” She replies vaguely. 

“Mm..” Yvette hums, “I hope our darling Rae isn't giving you much of a headache.”

“She would never!” Agatha has to take her acting skills to use. “Rae is an absolute sweetheart.”

Luella leans in, “Of course she is.”

Lia, however, has no interest in staying on that thread. “Well,” She cuts in, already redirecting the spotlight, “My daughter is just as sweet. Have you met Sophie?”

“Alright!” Rio cuts in before Agatha can answer. “That’s enough interrogation for one evening.”

“But we’re just getting started!” Yvette protests.

“No, I’m saving her.” Rio says smoothly.

“From us?” Luella laughs.

“Exactly.”

Agatha lifts a brow. “I wasn’t aware I needed rescuing.”

“You do.” Rio tells her lightly, already guiding her away with a hand at her back. “Once they start asking questions they won't be able to stop.”

Agatha allows it. Of course she does so they both excuse themselves, stepping out for a moment.

“I am trained at answering questions.”

“I'm sure you are.” Rio agrees. Then, a little quieter, just for her, “But first—we're eating. I am in fact starving.”

“Fine.” Agatha sighs, long-suffering. “Lead the way.”

Rio leads Agatha toward the buffet table, and Agatha can barely contain herself. The spread is mostly Puerto Rican dishes, and she’s already plotting to try everything. The aroma hits her first as she inhales deeply, the tiniest spark of excitement lighting her chest.

“Trust me,” Rio nudges her gently. “Start with the empanadas. You’ll thank me later.”

Agatha beams, surveying the table with excitement. “I don’t know whether to eat first or cry with joy.”

Rio laughs. “You can do both.”

They finally settle at one of the tables, plates piled high. Agatha is mid-bite into a pastelito when a small, hesitant voice cuts through.

“Tia?”

Agatha freezes, fork halfway to her mouth.

“Sophie!” Rio beams, standing to greet the young girl and sweeping her into a warm hug. “Happy birthday, hon.”

“Thank you, Tia!” Sophia says softly, glancing at Agatha. Her eyes widen, the kind of wide that’s equal parts awe and disbelief. “Holy shit! You’re Agatha!”

Rio rolls her eyes playfully. “Here we go again.”

Agatha sets down her fork and stands, extending a hand. “And you must be Sophia.” She says smoothly. “Happy birthday.”

The girl takes her hand eagerly, and Agatha can’t help but notice the excitement radiating off her. “Thank you! I’ve seen so many of your films! And your guesting on the Drew Barrymore show—chef’s kiss! The insights you shared were amazing!”

Agatha is definitely amused. Sophia is in a simple tulle dress with a golden sash across her chest:Birthday Girl, glittering like it has its own spotlight. 

“Aren’t you nice?” Agatha mutters, letting a small smile slip.

“I try to be.” Sophia replies shyly, then turns to Rio with the excitement only a birthday girl can muster. “Tia, you have to see my Porsche! Abuela bought it for me, and it’s in my favorite color!”

Agatha suppresses a brow raise. Porsche for a sixteen-year-old? She’s not about to question it. Some things are better left unchallenged.

“I can’t wait to see it, hon.” Rio says, smoothing the sash on Sopha’s dress. “Where’s your cousin?”

“She’s with our friends.” Sophia answers, bouncing slightly on her toes.

Agatha lets her gaze linger on Sophia for a moment, noting the spark of pure enthusiasm and the wide-eyed admiration.

Sophia leans closer, almost conspiratorial. “Do you like chocolate empanadas? They’re my favorite.”

Agatha can’t help the smirk that curls at her lips. “Sweet tooth approved though at my age, I prefer mine with a side of sarcasm.”

Sophia giggles as Rio chuckles softly, glancing between the two of them. “Be nice, Agatha. You might set unrealistic expectations.”

“Unrealistic? Me?” Agatha deadpans, taking a careful bite of empanada. “Never.”

Sophia squeals quietly, eyes sparkling, and Agatha has to admit—her giddiness is kind of contagious.

“Sophia, your friends are looking for you.” Another girl says, passing at their table. “Something about cake and very strong opinions on frosting.”

Sophia gasps like this is a crisis. “I have to go.”

“Yes, you do.” Rio laughs.

Sophia turns back to Agatha quickly. “Please don’t leave yet!”

“I won’t.” She assures her, then, almost as an afterthought, she reaches for the small gift bag she’d set aside earlier. “This is for you.”

Sophia blinks. “A gift? For me? From you?”

Agatha nods, holding it out. “You only turn sixteen once.”

That earns a bright giggle, and Sophia takes it carefully, as if it might disappear if she moves too fast. “Okay, this is amazing.” She gushes, already peeking inside. “I will be back to interrogate you more—fair warning. Thank you so much!”

“I look forward to it. I’ll prepare my defenses.”

Sophia beams at her, clutching the bag like it’s the highlight of her night before spinning off again.

Once Sophia leaves, Agatha relaxes. “She’s really nice.”

“She is pretty sweet.” Rio agrees, taking a slow sip of her iced tea. “She and Rae.. well, they’re growing up fast.”

“Speaking of Rae,” Agatha begins, “Where is that kid?”

“I honestly do not know.” Rio replies casually, not the slightest hint of worry in her tone.

“And you’re not even looking for her?” Agatha asks, brow raised.

“She’ll show herself when she’s ready.” Rio’s voice is full of nonchalance.

Agatha hums thoughtfully. “You know, she apologized to me. Said she did it because you were disappointed in her. Or at least you said something about disappointment for the first time.”

Rio’s expression softens just a fraction. “She really did apologize?”

Agatha nods, “She did. And as much as I enjoy tormenting kids, especially one like Rae, I really hope you’re not mad at her. It’s all good on my end.”

Not once had Agatha expected to be tolerant of teenage nonsense. She prided herself on being unforgiving when necessary. But when the teen in question is yours—and when you have years to make up for, you learn to take whatever crap they throw your way. 

And somehow, it’s not just tolerance that creeps in. It's a mixture of pride and relief, including a stab of guilt that she hasn’t been there as Rae grew into herself.

“That’s really good to hear.” Rio finally concludes, a relieved smile touching her lips. “Though I hope you’re not upset at me.”

“For what?”

“For how she’s been raised.”

She doesn't think Rae has been raised wrong. You can’t fix everything. Nature has its own stubborn streak, and Rae certainly inherited most of Agatha's. 

But Rio.. she’s done right by her. She’s given her roots while letting her fly. As much as Rae drives her up the wall, Agatha can’t deny it, she’s proud of her. 

For all the attitude, the sharp tongue, and the constant defiance—Rae turned out good. Better than Agatha ever expected, if she’s being honest. Smart, capable, a little too brave for her own good, and somehow still kind in ways Agatha never quite learned how to be.

“I think nature has got to play its part alongside nurture. You can only do so much.” Agatha tells her, letting her gaze rest on Rio’s calm face.

Rio smiles, eyes meeting hers in quiet acknowledgment. “That’s fair.”

Agatha allows herself a small, rare grin, turning the thought over in her head. “She’s lucky.” She mutters, her voice lighter, teasing. “You’re doing right by her, even if she’s going to make you pull your hair out sometimes.”

Rio chuckles. “She definitely keeps me on my toes.”

“And you wouldn’t have it any other way.” With that, Rio just shakes her head, knowing that’s exactly right.

Agatha takes a sip of her own drink and lets herself relax into it, a rare quiet settling over her. For once, she doesn’t feel the weight of absence or the sting of lost years. She's here now and she won't be going anywhere anytime soon.

The party continued around them but it felt distant, like they’d stepped just slightly out of it. Agatha noticed the way Rio moved through it all with quiet confidence, greeting family and friends with warmth that didn’t require effort. They were here together, in a bubble of their own making, and Agatha found herself enjoying it more than she expected.

They talked easily, Agatha asking about Rio’s father, who was out of town, and learning she wouldn’t be meeting the patriarch anytime soon. Conversation drifted toward Rio’s childhood—growing up in this house, being the eldest of three sisters, the responsibilities and privileges of it all. Agatha listened, amused and intrigued, noting the way Rio’s eyes lit up with memories, the corners crinkling as she spoke.

“Come, let me show you something.” Rio stands and extends her hands toward Agatha after what feels like an hour.

“Show me what?” Agatha questions, but accepts Rio’s hand either way, letting herself be led.

“Where’s the thrill in telling?” Rio teases while wiggling her brows.

They weave through the crowd, stepping out of the warm buzz of the party and onto a winding stone path that led to the other side of the estate.

They stop at a garden, where a soft maze of blooms in every color imaginable, benches tucked beneath arched trellises, and a fountain in the center spraying gentle splashes of water that caught the light and glittered like diamonds. 

Stone archways framed the scene, ivy creeping along the edges, creating a quiet, almost enchanted seclusion.

Agatha paused, taking it all in. Her gaze sweeps over the flowers, the gentle curves of the fountain, the benches, the lights hitting the water just right. 

“I grew some of the flowers myself.” Rio reveals proudly, pointing to one particular bloom, orange and vibrant.

Agatha steps closer, nodding. “Hibiscus. That’s beautiful. I thought they mostly grew in tropical climates.”

“Not if you have a green thumb.” Rio shrugs, a teasing lilt in her voice.

Agatha quirks an eyebrow. “Uh, smug.”

“Not when I can be.” Rio sneaks a tongue out and brushes a strand of hair from her face.

Agatha’s eyes linger longer than necessary, tracing the line of her jaw, the curve of her cheek, and the way her lips catch the light. 

Rio turns slightly, adjusting a flower in the garden, and Agatha finds herself moving imperceptibly closer, drawn by something electric in the space between them. 

Her internal monologue had gone from casual observation to full-blown plotting.

Rio catches her gaze—or maybe she just notices the lingering stare. A small smile tugs at her lips, mischievous and knowing, like she can read Agatha’s thoughts from across the garden.

“Thinking about stealing a flower, or just admiring mine?” Rio teases softly, voice low enough that the surrounding garden seemed to shrink around them.

Agatha smirks, fighting the urge to reach out. “Depends. Are you offering, or warning?”

Rio moves just slightly closer, and for a moment, the sound of the fountain and the rustle of leaves were all that existed. Agatha’s heartbeat picks up, and she can feel the electric pull of it—the almost dangerous fun of being this close.

Rio’s gaze drops just briefly to Agatha’s mouth and that's all it takes.

Agatha leans in first, as though she’s been thinking about it for longer than she’ll ever admit. She’s decided, very suddenly, that she’s done waiting.

Their lips met and the kiss isn’t rush at all. It isn’t hesitant, either.

It's more so curious at first—testing, but it doesn’t stay there for long.

Rio exhales softly against her, one hand coming up, hovering for a second like she’s giving herself a chance to stop.. she doesn’t.

Her fingers curl lightly at Agatha’s waist instead, pulling just enough to close whatever space was left between them.

Agatha hums under her breath, something inevitably smug, but it melts into something warmer when Rio’s hand stays at her waist, caressing whatever she can hold.

The world narrows and the noise from the world fades into nothing.

Agatha cages her in without quite touching, as Rio’s fingers tighten just a fraction.

“We should go back.” She breathes between kisses, but there’s no urgency in it.

Agatha doesn’t move. “Eventually.” She agrees.

Neither of them does anything about it. Not yet.

They in fact, did not go back to the party. 

The next thing she knows, Agatha is being yanked, practically levitated through a crowd of confused partygoers and up what feels like a hundred-year-old staircase.

Her heels clack a frantic rhythm against the worn wood, sharp and unsteady against the distant thrum of bass from below.

Rio is a whirlwind ahead of her, dark hair and determined eyes. She didn't slow down until she finally pushes open a door on the third floor. It reveals a surprisingly pristine bathroom, untouched by the chaos of the party below.

The door slams shut behind them, the sound swallowed by a sudden, heavy silence.

Agatha barely has time to register the antique claw-foot tub before Rio is on her—hands everywhere, urgent and unrelenting. Their mouths collide with a sharp, breathless intensity, the kind that feels inevitable after a night of tension stretched too tight.

“Hmmm.” Agatha let out a breathless moan as Rio’s fingers tangled in her hair, pulling her head back just enough for a deeper, more punishing kiss.

Agatha, never one to be out-maneuvered, pushes Rio against the cool tile wall. A low hiss escaped Rio's lips, but it was quickly devoured by Agatha’s own mouth. 

Agatha’s hands, agile and hot, travel over Rio’s clothes, tracing the curve of her waist to the swell of her hip. A shiver ran through Rio’s spine.

"Took you long enough." Rio murmurs, pulling back just an inch, her voice a husky whisper. 

Rio’s eyes, dark and intent, are locked with hers. Every glance feels like a current pulling Agatha closer, and she couldn’t resist leaning in. Their hands brushed, fingers tangling for a heartbeat too long, and a quiet yet shaky breath escaped Rio that makes Agatha’s pulse spike.

The rest of the world fades into background static. Agatha had imagined this moment countless times, the thrill of just being this close to Rio, and now it is intoxicatingly real.

In the midst of touching and kissing, Rio’s phone buzzes sharply on her pocket, breaking the spell. Twice.

Agatha groans softly, stepping back just far enough to watch Rio scramble for the device. “That’s honestly doing wonders for my libido.” She mutters breathless, a teasing smile tugging at her lips.

“Sorry! Sorry!” Rio is flustered, fumbling with the phone. “I’m turning it off—oh, it’s about Rae.”

“What’s wrong?” Agatha asks quietly, eyebrow raised.

Rio shakes her head. “I don’t know. Mama said they need me downstairs.”

In an instant, the intimate tension dissolved, leaving both of them slightly flushed and very aware of the world creeping back in.

They took a moment to straighten themselves, Rio smoothing her hair while Agatha adjusts her clothes, both silently pretending nothing had happened.

They make their way downstairs together, weaving through the party, careful to keep their closeness casual.

And as they descended, Agatha allowed herself one more stolen glance, a hint of the thrill from the garden lingering, knowing that this little moment was theirs alone even if it had to end abruptly.

Voices begin to overlap as they near the party, a cluster of people gathers near the center of the room, movement that doesn’t match the easy rhythm from before.

Agatha stops. “Well,” She says dryly, eyes narrowing slightly as she takes it in. “That’s never a good sign.”

Rio’s posture straightens immediately, her attention snapping toward the commotion. “Excuse me.” She murmurs, already moving forward.

Agatha follows, slipping easily into step beside her, curiosity piqued despite herself.

“What happened?” Rio’s voice cut through the chaos, commanding attention.

Someone steps aside, and then that's when they see it. Of course. 

There she is finally, Rae. Front and center as always, chin up, eyes flashing just enough to be defiant without tipping into theatrics.

Behind her, a small army: Luella, Yvette, and the ever-watchful shadow of family expectation.

“I didn’t do it!” Rae snaps, voice strong but laced with frustration. “I swear!”

“Sure you didn’t.” Lia spat, pointing a finger that seemed to shake from sheer indignation. Sophia clutches her tiny bouquet of nerves behind her, wrapped safely in the arms of someone Agatha assumed was Lia’s husband. 

“You were the only one standing close to it.” Lia adds, venom dripping from every syllable.

Rae let out a short, disbelieving laugh, “Yeah, because I was merely standing there. That’s not a crime.”

“You were alone.” Lia insists. “And then it was scratched.”

Rae squares her shoulders, a subtle rebellion that speaks volumes. “So that automatically makes it me?”

“I’m just saying—” 

“No,” Rae cuts her off, sharper now. “You’re implying.”

Sophia sniffles, little tears brimming, looking between the bickering people and clearly overwhelmed by whatever is happening.

“But aren’t you technically jealous of Sophie, Rae?” Lia accuses, though she’d discovered some ultimate truth.

Rio’s body shifts automatically, moving to stand in front of Rae like a dam holding back a flood. “What happened here?” Her voice questions, low and firm. “There are people watching, Lia.”

Lia points accusingly at Rae. “Your daughter scratched Sophie’s new car!”

“Lia, you don’t have evidence.” Luella interjects, trying to mediate, though her voice lacked bite.

“Oh, Mama, hush it!” Lia snaps at her. “That’s why that kid is too comfortable—because all you guys do is spoil her. We all know she did it!”

“We don’t, Lia.” Yvette insists.

“Then who else would do it? She’s the only one who’s jealous—”

“Emilia.” Rio murmurs, eyes sharp and warning. “Do not cross a line.”

“What line? I’m just trying to protect my daughter on her special day!” Lia’s voice rises to hysteria. “Honestly, Rio, you should keep your daughter in check!”

Rio didn’t even acknowledge that comment, instead turning her full attention to Rae. Agatha feels herself caught in the pause, her usual sarcasm failing her entirely. She had nothing to throw into this storm—except sheer surprise for Rio’s composure under fire.

“Did you do it?” Rio asks, her voice deadly calm.

Rae lifts her head, meeting her mami’s gaze. “Of course I didn’t.”

Rio nods once, then turns her attention back to Lia, all steel and quiet fury. “She didn’t do it, Lia. Stop this fuss. Maybe we can talk calmly—”

“No!” Lia explodes. “I’ve always been patient with that kid, who clearly has some sort of secret animosity toward Sophie. I will not let this pass!”

“Emilia, do not make a scene.” Luella warns her.

“No. Enough is enough!” Lia hisses more, face red. “I will not let that daughter of yours who feels entitled to everything when she’s an outsider who got adopted and is nothing but a stray ca—”

The words barely leave her mouth when a loud, sharp sound cuts through the air. Agatha’s jaw drops—along with everyone else’s.

Rio’s palms meet Lia’s cheeks. The fury in her eyes is palpable, terrifyingly electric in its quiet control. The entire courtyard freezes. Even Lia’s hands fly to her face in shock.

“Say that again about my daughter, and that’s not all you’ll be getting from me.” Rio's voice is authoritative and equally dangerous. Every guest around them seems to hold their breath at once.

Agatha’s mind almost blanks by the situation at hand.

“Let’s go, Rae.” Rio mutters more softly now, reaching for her daughter’s wrist. Rae, speechless, lets herself be led away, too shocked to react.

As they pass Agatha, Rio’s eyes meet hers and she gives a single, brief nod. Follow. Agatha obeys without a word, falling into step behind them, leaving the stunned family and party guests behind in a sea of open mouths and hushed whispers.

So much for this being a warm, family gathering.

The three of them walk in silence all the way to the parking area, the noise of the party fading into something distant and irrelevant. Rio’s grip on Rae’s wrist stays firm but careful, protective without crossing into force, while Agatha follows just behind, acutely aware of the tension thickening the air.

When they reach Rio’s Bentley, Rio finally looks back at them, and something in that glance shifts. Agatha has always seen her gentle before—but this is different. This is something wrapped in love. A mother’s armor, if you will.

“Rae..” Rio starts softly, though the tremor in her voice betrays everything underneath.

Rae flinches. “I didn’t do it.” She grits her teeth, her voice tight.

“I know..” Rio murmurs, barely above a whisper now. “Are you okay?”

Rae doesn’t answer right away. She lifts her head slowly, looking at Agatha, then back at Rio—eyes clearly hurting.

“I don’t want to come home with you.”

Agatha catches the flash of pain in Rio’s eyes, quick but unmistakable. Gods..

“What?” Rio asks, her voice cracking despite herself.

“I don’t want to come with you.” Rae repeats, refusing to unyield.

“My love, I don’t—”

“Please, Mami.” Rae’s voice breaks, small and brittle, and Agatha feels something twist sharply in her chest.

Rio’s jaw tightens, a tremor passing through her shoulders. She takes a breath, trying to hold herself together, trying to make space for Rae even when it hurts. “Okay.. okay,” She tells herself. “Would you want to stay with Abuela or Tia Yvette? I can call—”

“No.” Rae’s refusal is immediate. “Not them.”

Rio’s expression softens, though the hurt doesn’t leave. “Then where do you think you’d like to be?”

“I’ll come with her.” Rae points at Agatha.

“Me?” Agatha blurts, caught off guard.

“Yes.” Rae’s voice is final.

Rio looks at Agatha then, something vulnerable in her gaze now—trust, maybe, or something close to it. “Would that be okay? Can Rae stay with you?”

Agatha’s mind races for a second. Logistics, questions, the reality of having Rae under her roof—but all of that fades under the weight of what’s actually being asked. 

“I.. I think so.”

Rae crosses her arms, resolute.

“Are you sure, my love?” Rio asks gently.

“Yes.”

Rio nods slowly, swallowing hard. The hurt in her expression doesn’t disappear still—it just settles somewhere deeper.

They get into the car, Rae slipping into the backseat while Agatha takes the passenger side. Rio makes a quick call, arranging for Rae’s things, but her eyes keep flicking to the rearview mirror, stealing glances at her daughter. Rae just stares out the window, obviously unreachable for now.

The drive is quiet and filled with everything none of them say.

When they arrive at Lilia’s house, Rae is out of the car first, already moving and putting distance where she can. Agatha watches her go before turning back to Rio.

“I don’t know why she’s mad at me.” Rio admits quietly, the words sitting somewhere between confusion and hurt.

“She’s just upset.” Agatha whispers. “I think.”

Rio nods, exhaling. “Are you sure you’ll be okay with her?”

“We’ll be fine.” Agatha offers a small smile, convincing both herself and Rio.

“I’m sorry, Agatha.”

“For what?”

“My family, they don’t usually treat Rae that way.”

“I know.” Agatha replies, steady. “I know that. Sometimes.. things happen.”

Rio’s lips press together, something grateful flickering through her expression. “You should get going. We’re all tired.”

“Alright.” Agatha unbuckles her seatbelt. “Drive safe.”

They stay for a moment, neither quite moving until Agatha got the hint. She gets out of the car as Rio rolls down her window slightly to say goodbye to Rae for the last time tonight.

“Good night, my love.” 

Rae only gives a small nod, refusing to respond in words.

Rio takes it anyway, her smile tight, holding more than it shows.

Agatha watches as the Bentley pulls away, its tail lights fading into the night.

Behind her, Rae stands just outside with her arms crossed. Agatha glances back at her, then toward the empty street, and sighs slowly.

“Come on inside, Rae.” Agatha tells her, stepping aside to let her in. She doesn’t want to rush nor crowd her. 

Rae follows quietly, shoulders still tight and choosing not to speak.

Lilia and Kate are in the living room, halfway through a show, but both of them look up the second the door opens.

“Agatha—what?” Lilia rises immediately, eyes landing on Rae. “Rae?”

“I’ll explain later.” Agatha’s tone is stripped of its usual bite. “Can she use the spare room? Just for tonight.”

Lilia doesn’t hesitate. She only smiles, noticing the weight in Agatha’s voice. “Of course, my dear.”

There are no more questions after that.

Kate quietly gets up, already heading to gather extra toiletries without being asked, while Lilia guides them down the hall. Rae says nothing, just follows, smaller somehow than she was earlier, as though the fight has drained out of her and left only the aftermath behind.

The room is prepared quickly, leaving just the two of them in it.

Agatha lingers by the door, unsure for once. “Do you want to talk about it?” She offers.

Rae doesn’t look at her. “No.”

There’s no attitude in it, it’s simply exhaustion.

Agatha nods once. “Alright.. do you want me to stay? Keep you company?”

“No.” Rae says again, quieter this time. “I’d rather be alone.. if that’s okay.”

Agatha swallows whatever instinct she has to push. “Of course it’s okay.” She responds. “I’ll just be in the next room, if you need anything.”

Rae nods, already sitting on the edge of the bed, staring somewhere distant.

Agatha takes that as her cue. She steps out, closing the door gently behind her, giving Rae the space she asked for.

The house is quieter now. Lilia is already in the kitchen, pouring water into glasses as if she’s been waiting.

“Lilia..” Agatha starts, preparing her explanation.

“It’s late, dear.” Lilia mutters gently. “We can talk tomorrow.”

Agatha exhales in relief, something in her loosening. “Thank you.”

Lilia smiles, but then pauses, studying her just a moment longer. “Though, there’s one thing.”

Agatha lifts a brow, tired but curious. “Hmm?”

“Rae.” Lilia says her name carefully. “Is she yours?”

Agatha doesn’t even think about it as she replies a steady, “Yes.”

Lilia’s expression softens, something warm settling in her eyes. She places a hand on Agatha’s shoulder for comfort. “That’s all I needed to hear.”

She gestures to the pitcher and glass on the counter. “Bring this to her. She might wake up thirsty.”

And just like that, she leaves it there with quiet understanding.

Agatha stands alone in the kitchen for a moment, staring at the water, at her own reflection faintly caught in the glass.

Eventually, she moves. She takes the pitcher and glass, walks back down the hall, and knocks softly.

“Rae?” She calls.

No answer. She pushes the door open just slightly, and stops in her tracks.

Rae is already asleep. Curled into the bed like the weight of the night finally caught up to her. Shoes still half on, breathing uneven but steady enough.

“Of course.” Agatha murmurs under her breath.

She steps inside carefully, setting the glass down on the bedside table without a sound. Then she crouches slightly, fingers moving with surprising gentleness as she slips Rae’s shoes off, setting them neatly aside.

The blanket is still folded at the foot of the bed and Agatha hesitates for only a second before pulling it up over her, adjusting it just enough to make sure she’s warm.

Rae doesn’t stir.

For a moment, Agatha just stands there looking at her daughter.

Peaceful, finally. Not arguing, not hurting out loud, not carrying the world on her shoulders like she had been just hours ago.

Agatha’s chest tightens. There’s so much she missed. So much she doesn’t know. So much she wants to fix and can’t.

But she’s here now. Agatha lets out another  quiet breath, something fragile settling into place.

“Sleep.” She whispers, barely audible. “I’ve got you.”

She stays a second longer, just enough to make sure Rae doesn’t wake, before stepping back and turning off the light.

And as she closes the door behind her carefully once more, she realizes something—for the first time, she isn’t outside of Rae’s life looking in.

She’s finally inside it.
