Chapter 18: Chapter 18

Chapter Notes

i may have poured my entire heart in this chapter so i really hope you like it ❤️‍🩹

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“Good morning, dear.”

When Agatha barges into the kitchen early that morning, Lilia is already settled at her usual breakfast nook. A cup of half-consumed coffee sits in front of her, still faintly steaming. It's a quiet sign that she has been awake far longer than anyone else in the house.

Agatha pauses for a second, eyeing the scene. Whatever this woman does before sunrise doesn’t really interest her—but there’s a small, inconvenient part of her that’s curious anyway.

“Why do you always wake up so early?” She asks, pulling her robe tighter around her chest. “Is that some sort of self-indulgent behavior I should know about?”

Lilia chuckles, entirely unbothered. “It’s a habit of mine ever since I was young. Clearly once you start doing it, it’s very hard to stop eventually.”

Agatha nods, turning toward the pantry instead. She decides that understanding Lilia and her many antics is a problem for another lifetime.

“I’m making us breakfast.”

“Excuse me?”

“I said,” Agatha repeats, already rummaging through their stock with growing determination. “I’m making us breakfast.”

She heard the snickering as soon as she said those words.

Agatha slowly peeks out from the pantry just enough to glare at Lilia, who very quickly straightens her face, suddenly very invested in taking her seriously.

“In the years I’ve known you, not once have I ever seen you hold a pot.”

“You will now.” Agatha replies firmly, already gathering eggs, pancake mix, cereal—anything remotely edible that might pass as breakfast for a sixteen-year-old. She pauses, scanning her inventory. “Do we have bacon?”

“There’s some in the fridge.” Lilia supplies, watching her with open curiosity now. “You’re going to cook us a feast?”

Agatha drops everything onto the counter with a soft thud and heads straight for the fridge, pulling out bacon and a box of waffles on her way. “I’m going to cook whatever survives my effort.” She mutters. Then, more softly, “Rae’s going to wake up hungry.”

Agatha doesn’t need to look to know Lilia's choosing her next words carefully, weighing them, filing through whatever questions are lining up in that head of hers.

And really, she can’t blame Lilia. You don’t just walk into someone’s house with a teenager in tow and casually announce, by the way, that’s my daughter, as if it’s been common knowledge all along.

“Go on.” She encourages, although she doesn't look back. “I can practically hear the questions forming. Might as well let them out before they start haunting the kitchen.”

“How long have you known?” Lilia finally asks. “About the kid being yours.”

“Not long enough to win any awards for motherhood, apprently.” Agatha replies, keeping her voice casual.

“Was it on our first night here?” Lilia asks gently. “When Rae was the one serving at the restaurant?”

Agatha pauses to register that. She doesn’t know if it’s obvious, or if Lilia simply has her.. ways of putting things together, but she manages a small, “Yes.”

“Well, there you have it.” Lilia murmurs, as if that answer alone settles something for her.

It doesn’t fool Agatha for a second. That woman has a whole inventory of queries, neatly lined up and waiting.

Agatha sighs as she cracks an egg into the pan, watching it spread as the heat catches, “Let me save you some trouble.”

And just like that, she starts talking.

It comes out in pieces at first, a casual recalling of her previous encounters with Rae while she continues to move around the kitchen. She flips eggs, adjusts the heat, opens a drawer she doesn’t need just to close it again. Anything to keep her hands busy while she fills in the gaps.

She tells Lilia how it happened. How her life changed the moment Rae entered in it. How everything she thought she had control over quietly unraveled the second things started making sense.

To her credit, Lilia doesn’t interrupt, not even once. She listens, her expression neutral that gives nothing away. Agatha can’t tell if she’s being judged. If she is, Lilia is doing an excellent job  hiding said judgement.

Well, what do you expect from a veteran actress? Keeping her face perfectly still is as easy as blinking, and it’s not even because of botox.

Agatha keeps going anyway, finishing the story the same way she told Jen. By the time she’s done, there’s already a full spread laid out across the dining table as the scent of breakfast fills the space. 

It’s not gourmet per se, but what she made can pass as edible. Rae will eat it. Probably. And if she doesn’t—well, whatever that kid does to bruise Agatha’s ego at this point, she’s fairly certain she’s built an immunity to it.

She glances at Lilia, who’s still in her nook. “Well?”

Lilia stands, pulling her scarf over her shoulders as she walks closer, inspecting the spread with quiet interest. “I think they look amazing.”

“That’s not what I mean.” Agatha can’t help but roll her eyes. “What I meant is—now that you know, do you think I’m more of a selfish bitch? Or am I just a generally terrible person for leaving my daughter behind?”

“Dear, I’d always think you’re a bitch.” Lilia replies easily, a teasing smile following right after. “But it’s not because of that, no.”

Agatha exhales, some of the tension easing from her shoulders.

Lilia’s gaze softens as she looks at her more carefully now. “What you did wasn’t abandonment in the way you’re trying to punish yourself for. I don’t think you walked away because you didn’t care. You walked away because, at the time, you knew you couldn’t give her the life she deserved.”

Agatha doesn’t move, but she listens—because that’s exactly what she’s been trying to tell Rae. Lilia is surely hitting every point with unsettling precision.

“You chose the harder path. Not for Rae, but for yourself. You made a decision with her future in mind. That includes her safety and her chance to grow up with things you didn’t have, or couldn’t offer then.”

A pause settles between them before Lilia speaks again.

“And that doesn’t make you selfish, it makes you a mother who understood her limits, even when it broke her to admit them.” She places a hand on Agatha’s shoulder, and Agatha lets it stay, which is her version of accepting comfort. “You didn’t leave her because you wanted to be free of her. You let her go because you wanted her to have more.”

Agatha swallows quietly, eyes dropping to the breakfast spread she barely remembers making. She finds herself hoping that the rest of the world might be half as understanding as Lilia, who takes it all in stride without making her feel like she has to defend every choice she’s ever made.

“And now..” Lilia finishes, gentler still. “She’s here, and so are you. That has to count for something.”

Agatha wiggles her brows. “I don't think she likes me very much.”

“So you’ll settle with that?” Lilia crosses her arms over her chest. “The Agatha I know wouldn’t let anything or anyone stop her—not even a teenager who looks and acts exactly like her.”

When Agatha opens her mouth to respond, the sound of footsteps makes them both snap their heads toward the hallway. As if the universe itself decided to summon her, Rae appears in front of them, a small storm of disheveled hair and last night’s clothes. 

Agatha blinks, momentarily seeing her not as a sassy, sharp-tongued teenager. Instead, she looks like a lost kid, a little unsure of where she is or why she’s here in the first place.

“Sorry..” Rae mumbles, glancing first Agatha, then at Lilia. “Am I interrupting something?”

“No, no.” Agatha says quickly, caught off guard. Her usual bite feels useless here as she looks at her daughter. “Did you have a good sleep?” 

“Uh.. yeah.” Rae nods, then hesitantly places a hand on her stomach. “Is there something I can possibly eat? I’m starving.”

“You’re just in time, dear.” Lilia beams, gesturing at the dining table. “Come, sit. Agatha prepared all of this for you.”

Rae eyes immediately scan the spread, and if Agatha reads her correctly, there’s a flicker of excitement in her eyes mixed with the usual teenage skepticism. She hopes the food pass Rae’s standards, as basic as it is.

“Great.” Rae mutters, stepping closer but stopping short of Lilia. “Ms. Calderu, I apologize if I wasn’t able to talk to you last night.” Her voice carries that careful tone, as if she just remembered the previous evening’s drama.

The older woman’s face softens, almost teary. She straightens her back, giving Rae her full attention. “Nonsense. You are always welcome here, my dear.” Lilia says warmly, eyes wide with genuine affection. “Now, will you come and give nana a hug?”

Nana? Before she can intervene, Rae leans forward and hugs Lilia without second thoughts. Agatha freezes mid-step, feeling that familiar tug in her chest—the mix of envy and disbelief.

Here is this girl, her daughter, offering a side of her Agatha hasn’t earned yet.

It’s painfully humbling, but Agatha can’t deny the small relief within her. Lilia is on her side, a part of her life. If Rae can trust Lilia, perhaps she can trust Agatha next. 

Agatha lets herself linger on that thought, clinging to the tiniest flicker of hope that one day, Rae’s guarded warmth will extend her way too.

“You know.” Rae murmurs between the embrace. “Can I really call you nana?”

“If you like.” Lilia shrugs, stepping back and cupping Rae’s chin gently. “You look so much like your mother.”

Agatha winces at that. Lilia hasn’t been briefed enough on Rae’s nuanced feelings toward her, and she really doesn’t want that kid to interpret that statement otherwise.

To her surprise, Rae simply shrugs, as though she’s long accepted the fact that she really does look like her mother. “Do I?”

“Yes, dear. Now sit, before all of this gets cold.”

Agatha moves first, reaching for a plate and utensils, setting them down in front of Rae with more care than she’ll ever admit out loud. Lilia follows, already at the fridge, pulling out a carton of milk and a pitcher of orange juice.

“Do you mind eating that?” Agatha asks, nodding toward the spread with a hint of suspicion. Knowing Rae, she’s already bracing herself for criticism before it even comes.

Rae barely looks up as she pulls a chair out and starts helping herself. “Sure. What do you think I eat, human flesh?”

Agatha scoffs, crossing her arms. “Honestly, I wouldn’t put it past you.”

Rae hums, already reaching for the pancakes. “I only bite when provoked.”

“Well..” Agatha gestures vaguely at the table. “I just assumed you eat caviar for breakfast. Maybe imported, served with a personal butler and a small orchestra playing jazz.”

Agatha knows none of that actually happens, it’s just far too entertaining a narrative to let go of. If anything, it makes for a perfect excuse to taunt the kid.

“I eat caviar for dinner.” Rae corrects her without missing a beat, piling food onto her plate. “Breakfast is where I lower my standards.”

Agatha presses her lips together. This is the Rae she knows and honestly, Agatha would gladly take a full-blown verbal sparring match because she knows at least then, Rae is being her usual self. “How generous of you.”

Lilia lets out a chuckles as she settles into the seat beside Rae. Agatha lingers for a second, then moves to the chair directly across from them, lowering herself into it with a quiet exhale. From there, she has a full view of Rae, her plate, and every reaction that comes afterwards. 

Rae picks up a pancake drenched in syrup, the thing practically surrendering under the weight of it, and takes a bite.

Agatha watches her while keeping herself on high alert at the same time. There’s a whole defensive speech lined up in her head should Rae so much as twitch in disapproval.

“Wait..” Rae says suddenly, her expression shifting. She freezes after swallowing, eyes widening just a fraction. “Is that.. honey?”

“Yes.”

Rae suddenly bolts for the glass of milk, but stops halfway, her breath catching in a way that is immediately, unmistakably wrong.

“I—I can’t—” Rae gasps, a hand flying to her chest. “I can’t have honey. I’m allergic—I can’t!”

Both women are on their feet instantly as chairs scrape loudly against the floor. “YOU’RE WHAT?” Agatha’s voice spikes. “What do you mean you’re allergic?”

Rae is already struggling, continuing to gasp for oxygen. “I—I can’t—” She chokes out, her face paling as panic sets in.

Lilia lays steady hands on the kid’s shoulders, looking equally as worried as Agatha. “Breath, dear. Slowly. Look at me.”

Agatha, meanwhile, goes completely cold. Her stomach drops so fast it almost makes her dizzy.

She didn’t know.

Of course she didn’t know. What kind of mother doesn’t know something like that?

Her hands are already shaking as she fumbles for her phone. “I’m calling 911.” Her voice is tight while her eyes locked on Rae as though she might disappear if she looks away. “Rae, just—just hang on, give me a second.. Hello?”

Agatha’s chest tightens. She cannot have this kid die in front of her. Not like this. Not over breakfast. Not because of something she made.

There’s response from the other line and before Agatha can explain the situation, Rae suddenly stops. A beat passes, and then..

“And scene.”

Agatha freezes, phone still pressed to her ear while Lilia goes completely still beside Rae.

Rae claps her hands, looking completely fine. A slow smirk spreads across her face while her eyes glint with mischief. “Did I do good?”

In the midst of recovering from the almost heart attack, Agatha glances at Lilia, who is already staring at Rae with absolute horror. They both can’t fathom that this kid had the nerve to pull something like that right under their noses, commit to it, and stick the landing.

“I’m not allergic to honey, by the way.” Rae adds, acting entirely too pleased with herself.

Agatha has her gaze set on the kid. The relief hits first knowing that she’s not killing this kid afterall, but it immediately follows by something far less forgiving.

“You are unbelievable..” Agatha mutters, lowering the phone slowly, her voice dangerously calm. “I almost had paramedics on standby for your performance.”

Rae only grins wider. “So convincing, then?”

Agatha doesn’t know what to say. She’s mad, she’s definitely mad—but does she even have the right to reprimand her? Or is that just going to push Rae further away?

She doesn’t know where she stands yet. Not really. But wrong is wrong, and to be frank, she doesn’t care if Rae gets upset at her. Someone has to say something for what she did, that kid cannot just—

“Rae, dear..”

Lilia cuts in before Agatha can spiral any further. Her tone is soft as she reaches out to brush a strand of hair away from Rae’s face. There’s a smile on her lips, too.

Agatha knows that smile. That is not a kind smile.

“You will reach great heights, that I’m sure of. Acting comes very naturally to you.”

Rae lights up at that, clearly caught off guard by the praise, her mouth already opening to respond but Lilia lifts a finger, signifying she’s not done talking yet.

“But if you ever pull a stunt like that in front of me again,” She continues, her voice dropping just enough to turn the air colder. “I will personally call every director and producer I know and make sure you never set foot on a set before your career even starts.”

Rae goes very still. The confidence drains just enough to make room for something else—realization. Maybe even fear. She knows Lilia isn’t bluffing, especially not with the kind of connections she has.

“I don’t care if you’re Agatha’s daughter. What you did was not acceptable. Do you understand me?”

Rae swallows, then nods. “Okay.. nana. I won’t do it again.”

“Very good.” Lilia says, just as easily, as if she hadn’t just issued a career-ending threat. “Now, sit and eat your food.”

Rae obeys immediately, sliding back into her chair and reaching for her plate with far less theatrics this time. Rae settles into her seat without another stunt, even going as far as to mumble a quick “thank you” to Agatha between bites. 

Lilia straightens, then steps past her, pausing just long enough beside Agatha. “That child is one hundred percent yours.” She murmurs under her breathe.

Agatha exhales slowly, dragging a hand down her face. “I fear she’s taken the worst parts.” She mutters. Then, a reluctant smile tugs at her lips. “Or the most entertaining ones.”

Agatha: Your daughter scared the shit out of me.

Agatha: She pretended to have allergies to honey and did one dramatic performance.

Rio: so i take it she’s back to her usual self, then?

Rio: also, sorry about that. she’s done that to me more times than i can count

Rio: she does not, in fact, have any allergies

Agatha: Such a menace.

Agatha: Have you spoken to her?

Rio: she texted me this morning, actually

Rio: said she “woke up and magically felt better”

Agatha: Of course she did. Convenient timing.

Agatha: Are you picking her up?

Rio: oh

Rio: do you want me to pick her up?

Agatha: I asked you first. Don’t repeat the question to me.

Agatha: She can stay as long as she wants, obviously.

Agatha: I’m just preparing for the eventuality.

Rio: don’t worry, agatha

Rio: she’ll tell you when she’s ready

Rio: and i don’t think she’s ready just yet 😉

Agatha stares at the message, brows raised. As she’s about to type a reply to Rio, there comes a knock at her door and before she can even say “come in,” the knob twists on its own and Rae barges in without warning.

“I’m ready!” She chirps.

After breakfast, the kid had gone upstairs to shower. An hour passed or two, and now she’s back, looking refreshed. She’s changed clothes, and her hair which was once a complete disaster, is now neatly tied into an updo.

Rae has an innocent face with her pink cheeks and long lashes. Agatha privately takes credit for those angelic features with a satisfied sort of pride. Although no one would ever guess, looking at her, just how capable she is of emotionally terrorizing adults.

“Ready for what?” Agatha’s voice unintentionally turn a pitch higher. “Also, when you knock, you’re supposed to wait until the person inside tells you to come in. You can’t just come crashing in like you did.”

“In my defense, you were taking too long to respond!”

“You didn’t even give me a chance to respond!” Agatha snaps back, exasperation slipping through her composure. She watches as Rae starts scanning the room, her expression far too critical for someone who was just offered breakfast and sanctuary. “See something you don’t like?”

“For a person like you who thinks highly of herself, your room is pretty bland.” Rae comments flatly.

Agatha opens her mouth, ready to retort that this isn’t even her main residence and Rae should really take a look at her own space in L.A.—but she stops herself mid-thought, inhaling slowly instead. Breath. You are the adult here, she reminds herself.

“And where, may I ask, are we going?” She questions instead, tone regaining its usual sharp edge.

Rae grins, as though she’s been waiting for that question. “We’re going for snow cones.”

Agatha didn’t exactly expect her day with Rae would go like this, but it did anyway. She finds herself at a snow cone drive-thru, much to Rae’s insistence.

The drive here hadn’t come easy. They were already bantering the moment they got in the car when Rae refused to sit in the passenger seat, again. And of course, it continued the entire ride, especially when Agatha failed to follow the GPS Rae had so confidently dictated, turning left instead of right.

How they arrived in one piece is a mystery known only to them.. and God.

“Hi, what can I get started for you?”

Agatha adjusts her sunglasses, glancing at Rae through the rearview mirror, only to find her already leaning out of the car window. “Hey, can I get a medium wedding cake, please?”

“Sure. Would there be anything else?”

Rae turns to look at Agatha. “What do you want?”

Agatha isn’t entirely sure she wants a snow cone. She hasn’t had one in years so even if there’s a menu, she doesn’t really know what to get. “I’ll have the same thing you did.”

Rae grins, then leans back out the window again. “Let’s add a medium Spider-Man to that. That’s all.”

A medium what? That’s not what she ordered for herself—so why is Agatha getting a Spider-Man instead of what Rae’s having as well?

“That’ll be 10.58. Will you pay by cash or card?”

Rae glances at Agatha again, and before she can ask, Agatha is already reaching for her card and handing it over the counter.

“Thanks! Your orders will be coming right up.”

As soon as the card is swiped and the girl moves to prepare their shaved ice, Agatha turns back toward Rae, removing her sunglasses with a pointed look.

“What the hell is a Spider-Man?” Agatha winces at the name. It’s probably gonna taste ridiculous as much as it sounds. “I told you to get me the same as yours.”

“I wanted to be unique. I don’t want you copying mine.” Rae reasons, sticking her tongue out. “Spider-Man is really good though, don’t worry.”

Thankfully, the place is practically empty, so when their orders arrived, Rae doesn’t hesitate to hop out and lead the way to one of the small outdoor tables near the shop. Agatha follows, still half-expecting Rae to do something else unpredictable, but the kid simply plops down across from her as though this is a perfectly normal situation.

The two sit under the shade, the quiet hum of the place surrounding them. The soft scrape of spoons against crushed ice begins as they dig in. It turns out, Spider-Man is just flavors of cherry and blue raspberry mixed to look, quite literally—like Spider-Man’s colors.

Agatha watches Rae for a moment before finally taking a bite of her own snow cone. The sweetness and the cold hit immediately, it’s a little overwhelming, but not unpleasant.

Rae, meanwhile, is already deep into hers, looking far too pleased for someone who just caused mild confusion over a fictional snow cone name.

“I haven’t had these in years.” Agatha takes another bite, her own words coming out lighter than she expects. “Back in my time, you could barely taste the syrup. It was mostly crushed ice.”

“Yeah, this place is really good. They’re very generous with the portions.” Rae replies. “Mami’s friend owns this shop. I usually get them for free when I come here, no matter how many cones I ask for.”

Agatha looks at her, brows lifting in disbelief. “Then why did you make me pay?”

Rae shrugs, wincing slightly—likely from brain freeze. “For fun.”

Agatha exhales through her nose, shaking her head as she goes back to her snow cone. Of course. She needs to start accepting that reasoning with this child is less of a conversation and more of an exercise in patience she did not ask for. 

That’s what she tells herself but she knows she doesn’t really mind it as much as she should.

A quiet settles between them for a moment, until Rae finally speaks. “You gotta start talking.”

Agatha doesn’t look up right away. “About what?”

“About why you left me.”

The words land cleanly as Agatha’s hand stills slightly around the cup. When she finally looks up, her blue eyes meet Rae’s own. “Is that why we’re here?” 

“Sure.” Rae adds casually, taking another bite. “Unless you don’t want to.”

Agatha lets out a small breath, setting her cup down for a moment as if giving herself the space to actually answer instead of deflect.

Of course she wants to. That’s the whole point. That’s been the point since the moment Rae walked into her life.

“No.. no, I do.” Agatha insists, more firmly this time. “I just don’t know where to start.”

Her fingers tap lightly against the side of her cup before she steady them, as if grounding herself. Agatha Harkness has never been short on words. She’s built a life on knowing exactly what to say and how to say it.

But this?

Sure, she has practiced what she would say—but now that she’s here, sitting across from the person she walked away from, trying to explain a decision that still echoes in places she doesn’t always want to revisit, she finds herself at a loss for words.

She glances at Rae again, who looks genuinely interested in what she’s about to say next. “Starting is the hardest part.” She admits, almost to herself. “But.. I suppose it would be unfair to ask for your patience without offering you the truth.”

Rae nods, as if organizing the conversation in her head. “You can start with the conception. That’s where it usually begins, right?”

A smile tugs at Agatha’s lips despite herself, some of the tension easing just a fraction. “I don’t think you’d like to hear about my one-night stand with a woman whose face I don’t even remember—”

“So it is a woman!” Rae cuts in excitedly, as if she’s been proven right. “Thank God. Before I knew you, I used to imagine my birth parents were two women. I refuse the idea of having a man’s DNA in me. That’s just.. icky.”

“Of course it’s a woman. I wouldn’t be caught dead with a man.” Agatha says, rolling her eyes. I should apologize in advance, though. If you ever wanted to know who she is, I don’t have any information to give you.”

“I’m not interested.” Rae shrugs, taking another bite of her snow cone. “Frankly, I’m not even that interested in you. But the questions started piling up, so.. here we are.”

That makes sense.

Rae continues, more matter-of-fact than cruel, “I couldn’t care less about the other person involved in making me. They’re already out of the picture, so.. what’s the point?”

Agatha nods once. There’s something oddly grounding about Rae’s bluntness and her surprising maturity to sit through a conversation like this without immediately taking a dig at her.

Agatha chooses not to comment because knowing Rae, the second it’s acknowledged, she’ll snap right back into sarcasm just to prove a point.

“Let me tell you about my mother.” Agatha gets right into it, deciding this is the way to start. “Her name’s Evanora, and she’s a total cunt.”

She stops in her tracks when she remembers something. “Remind me—am I allowed to curse in front of you, or do I need to start censoring myself for your delicate ears?”

“I’m sixteen.” Rae deadpans. “I have my own share of fuck yous and middle fingers every now and then.”

Agatha huffs out a quiet laugh, remembering the time Rae gestured her the finger. “Good. That’ll make this easier.”

She shifts slightly in her seat, eyes drifting somewhere past Rae, as though she’s pulling something old and buried to the surface. “My mother wasn’t warm. She didn’t believe in it. She says thought and affection made people weak. She says I am weak.”

A small pause. Agatha presses her tongue against the inside of her cheek before continuing. “I think her goal was to raise me to become useful. Not happy. Not loved. Just.. useful.”

Rae doesn’t interrupt. She just sits there and listens.

“There was a time, I couldn’t have been older than ten—I messed up something small. I don’t even remember what it was. Probably forgot to do my chores, dropped something, breathed incorrectly. And she just..” She trails off, shaking her head slightly. “Maybe yelling at me or hitting me would’ve been easier.”

Her lips press into a thin line. “She ignored me for days.”

Rae’s brows pull together just slightly.

“No talking. No looking at me like I exist. She made me feel I wasn’t even worth the energy it took to be angry.” Agatha lets out a humorless chuckle. “You’d be surprised how effective that is on a child. You start thinking—maybe if I were better, she’d notice me again.”

She picks at the edge of her cup, not really eating anymore as the ice begins to melt.n“And when she did notice me..” Agatha adds, quieter now, “It was usually to correct me. Fix me. Remind me that whatever I was, it wasn’t enough yet.”

A beat.

“I got very good at performing.” She says, a hint of dry humor slipping back in. “You don’t survive someone like her without learning how to become exactly what they want. Or at least convincing them you are.”

Her gaze flickers back to Rae. “But here’s the thing, no matter how good you get.. it’s never enough for people like that. There’s always something else to take, something else to reshape. You stop being a person and start being.. a project.”

Rae shifts slightly in her seat, her usual sharpness dimmed, replaced by something more serious.

“There were nights, where I’d lie awake and think—if I ever had a kid, I wouldn’t do that to them. I wouldn’t make them feel like they had to earn being loved.” Her jaw tightens slightly after she says it, as though the words taste strange coming out now.

“Then, the universe decides to be funny and does what it does. It throws you into situations you’re not prepared for and suddenly you’re faced with choices that don’t have a right answer. Just less terrible ones.” She looks at Rae. “That’s when I got pregnant with you.”

The memory lands heavier.  Agatha's gaze becomes unfocused as it slips into the past..

Evanora stands across from her, perfectly composed and perfectly still. She has that look on her face, the one that always meant 'You’ve disappointed me, again.'

“You will take care of it.” Her mother tells her, voice calm in a way that made it worse.

Agatha remembers standing there, younger, angrier, but already tired. “No.”

A pause. Evanora moves her head slightly, studying her as if she’s something inconvenient. In Evanora’s life, she really is an inconvenience.

“Don’t be foolish.” She snaps. “You’re not equipped for this. You’ll ruin everything you’ve worked for.”

“I didn’t ask for your approval.”

That had been a mistake. Agatha can still hear the soft exhale that follows.. one meant for disappointment that Agatha heard her entire life. 

“If you insist on keeping it,” Evanora’s steps closer, her voice dropping just enough to regain authority. “Then understand this—your life will become very difficult.”

Another step. “And that child of yours?” A faint, almost amused tilt of her lips appears. “Even more so.”

Agatha remembers the way her stomach had twisted. It’s not even out of fear for herself, but for something that hadn’t even been born yet.

Back at the table, her fingers still against the cup as she catches her breathing. “She didn’t scream at me. My mother didn’t need to raise her voice to make a point.”

Her jaw tightens. “She just made it very clear that if I kept you.. she would make sure both our lives were miserable.”

Her eyes finally lift to Rae’s again. “I knew what she was capable of, I’d lived it my entire life. I wasn’t going to let you grow up under that. Or worse.. become another version of me, trying to earn something that was never going to be given.”

Rae remains unmoving as she sits there, her spoon forgotten in her hand. Her eyes are fixed on Agatha as she absorbs every word.

“So when I say I made a choice, it wasn’t because I didn’t want you.” Agatha smiles bitterly. “It was because I knew exactly what would happen if I kept you in that world.”

Agatha carries the story forward more quietly now, the sharpness in her tone easing into something heavier. She tells Rae about the months she spent trying to prepare in secret—saving every bit of money she could, cutting corners, convincing herself that if she just planned carefully enough, she could outrun her mother’s reach.

At the time, she was still working at her mother’s firm, which should have meant stability. She has steady income which means she has something she could rely on. 

But the moment she refused to get rid of the pregnancy, that disappeared too. Evanora didn’t fire her—not outright. She simply had Agatha cut off from her salary, buried under technicalities and decisions that were perfectly legal.

Sure, she had her fair share of savings tucked away, but she had to think bigger and far ahead. It wasn’t enough for her and the baby, not in the long run. She didn’t allow herself to dwell on the exhaustion. She treated it as a necessity, something she must push through if she wanted even the slightest chance at making it out of here.

So Agatha adapted. She had to. She picked up whatever work she could find—late-night shifts, waitressing, anything that would pay enough to keep her going.  Every tip, every small earning went straight into an account she guarded so carefully. 

And for a while, despite everything, she lets herself believe it might actually work.

Once she’s saved enough, the plan is simple: take everything she has and leave Westview without looking back.

She sets her sights on Spain. Far enough, she thinks. Far enough that Evanora wouldn’t bother chasing her across continents. 

Unfortunately, the evil cunt finds out about Agatha’s savings. She has her ways and when Rae asked how, Agatha explains it that her mother, being a lawyer, knew exactly how to maneuver through systems.

She knows how to make things disappear without ever looking like she touched them. The account Agatha had built quietly is suddenly inaccessible. It’s been frozen and just like that, she has been drain of everything. 

Every bit of security she had tried to build vanishes overnight.

By then, she is nine months pregnant and already living on borrowed time. The apartment she thought was hers turns out to be another illusion Evanora is more than capable of dismantling.

A conversation here, a payment there, and suddenly Agatha is no longer welcome. There had been no argument nor concrete explanation. She’s simply been kicked out of her own space without prior notice.

She’s left with nothing: no savings, no place to stay, and no one willing to step in. Not because they don’t care, but because they're afraid. Everyone who knows Agatha knows Evanora, and no one wants to be caught opposing someone with that kind of reach and control.

With that, Agatha finds herself alone, heavily pregnant, and entirely at the mercy of a woman who has already made her intentions clear. 

But Agatha persists because she really, really wants the child. Not out of defiance, but from something deeper, an instinct she doesn’t question and a certainty she clings to even when everything else is being stripped away from her. 

She has already lost so much control over her own life, but this is the one thing she refuses to surrender. The desire to be a mother becomes less of a hope and more of a promise she keeps to herself, carried through every suffering that comes her way.

One day, her body gives in before her plans do. It wasn't even her due date but she starts to feel contractions and everything moves too fast after that. There comes pain, panic, and the rush of unfamiliar urgency as she’s taken to the hospital, her carefully constructed future suddenly narrowed down to sterile rooms and hurried footsteps.

The room is too bright.

Agatha can’t remember when the lights were turned on, or if they ever were turned off. Time has lost its edges, slipping in and out between contractions that steal her breath and leave her gripping the sheets because they’re the only solid thing left in the world for her right now.

A sharp wave hits as she gasps, head tipping back. A strained sound escapes her throat as her body tightens while the monitors beep steadily beside her, indifferent to the way her entire existence seems to fold inward with each surge of pain.

“Just breath, can you do that for me?” A nurse says gently somewhere to her left.

Agatha tries. She really does, but breathing feels like something she has to relearn every time the pain comes back.

In the midst of the pain, the door of the room opens. Agatha doesn’t need to look to know who it is. The air changes, turning cold in a way that has nothing to do with temperature and everything to do with presence.

“Mother..” Agatha exhales, her voice strained, barely above a whisper.

Heels click softly against the floor as Evanora steps into view. Her posture is perfect as her eyes lands on Agatha with the same clinical assessment she might give a case that has gone poorly.

The nurse shuffles to exit the room, leaving them both to themselves.

“This is what you’ve reduced yourself to. What a shame.”

Another contraction hits. Agatha inhales sharply while gripping the bed rails this time, her knuckles turning white. “Not.. now.” She manages through clenched teeth, more to herself than anyone else.

Evanora doesn’t react to the pain her daughter feels. She simply observes, not having the smallest amount of care to the world.

“Have you reconsidered?” She asks after a beat, as though she’s continuing a conversation that was never interrupted. “It is still not too late to correct this. You have a chance to give this up and continue living your life the way you used to.”

Agatha lets out a terrified breath, shaking her head weakly. “No, I.. I don’t want that.”

Evanora’s gaze sharpens, just slightly. “You are making a mistake, one that will follow you for the rest of your life.”

Agatha laughs despite the pain out of absurdity. “You think this—” She pauses, another wave of contractions breaking through her words, forcing her to inhale before continuing, “This is a mistake?”

Silence stretches between them and suddenly, the room feels smaller. It feels like Agatha is being deprived of oxygen more as the minutes goes.

“I’m not changing my mind. Not now, not ever.” Agatha’s voice wavers, stripped of its usual edge but the message stays the same.

Evanora studies her for a moment longer, confirming something she already knows. “Then you are choosing consequences you do not fully understand.”

Agatha’s eyes flicker shut briefly as another contraction passes. When she opens them again, there’s something different glinting other than fear and hurt itself.

“Please, mother.” She whispers. The word comes out quieter than anything she’s said so far, it almost doesn’t sound like her. “Please.. just—stop asking me to do that. Please let me keep her.. Please—please let me have my child.”

It’s the first time she’s ever asked Evanora for something without armor. It’s the first time she begged not only for herself, but for her child as well.

Her mother doesn’t move. Not one ounce of sympathy can be seen in her face and she doesn’t hesitate when she says, “No.”

Agatha exhales, the word landing heavier than any raised voice could.

“I can’t..” Agatha continues, her voice trembling now. “I can’t lose this too.”

Evanora’s expression remains unchanged. “You will recover.” She insists. “You are resilient when you choose to be.”

“That’s not what I want!”

Another contraction hits harder this time, and Agatha cries out. Her grip tightens as her body curls with pain. Her breathing turns uneven, words coming out in fragments between gasps.

“I want this—” She manages. “I want her my child.. Please, mother. Please let me have this.”

Evanora turns slightly, already preparing to leave, as if the conversation has reached its conclusion. “You should not have been placed in a position you cannot handle yourself.” She says calmly, not daring to look back at her daughter.

Agatha’s voice follows her, weaker now, but persistent. It carries something she hasn’t said out loud before. “Why do you hate me?”

The question hangs in the air. Evanora stops at the door and for a brief moment, there is silence.

Then, without turning around, she answers with her voice void of any emotions. “Because you should not have been born.”

The door closes abruptly behind her.

“What an ugly, fucking bitch.” Rae murmurs under her breath as Agatha finishes speaking, her tone low but edged with something fierce. “Seriously. What a fucking cunt—she deserves the deepest, darkest parts of hell. Shouldn’t she have replaced Satan herself?”

Agatha hadn’t even realized the tears had started until one slips free, trailing quietly down her cheek. She lets out a breathless chuckle anyway, wiping at her face with the back of her hand.

“Alright..” She says gently, voice still a little unsteady but laced with that familiar dry humor. “Maybe we dial the cursing down just a notch.”

Rae glances at her, then shrugs, though her expression softens.

“But you’re not wrong. She’s an ugly, fucking—well.. you get the idea. Good thing our looks didn’t come after her genes.”

“Right.” Rae nods, a small pause settling between them before her expression shifts, curiosity replacing the earlier fire. “So.. how did you end up giving me for adoption?”

Agatha’s breath catches slightly as the memory settles in, the present fading just enough for the past to take its place. 

Hours after her labor, her mind finally floats somewhere between relief and disbelief. She holds her baby in her arms, latching just enough to be fed. 

She’s small, warm, and unmistakably real in her arms. Agatha remembers looking at her tiny face and she can’t help but feel immediate recognition that this little person is hers. That despite everything, something in her life has finally come into focus. 

For a fleeting moment, it feels like the universe has allowed her one fragile, perfect thing to keep.

However, that feeling doesn’t last, as most of them do. The door opens again.

Evanora returns, composed as ever, her presence cutting through whatever softness the moment had tried to hold onto. She doesn’t quiet significance of what has just taken place. She didn’t even bother to glance at the baby Agatha was holding.

Her attention goes straight to her daughter, as though the outcome is already understood and the next step merely needs to be enforced.

“You’ve done what you insisted on doing.” Evanora says calmly, her tone carrying no trace of approval. “Now we proceed.”

Agatha tightens her hold on her baby instinctively, her body reacting before her voice does. “No.” She insists, though it comes out weak, more reflex than resistance.

“This is not a negotiation.” Evanora replies evenly. “You have two options. You will either relinquish the child voluntarily, or I will ensure it is taken from you without your cooperation.”

Agatha’s breath stutters, her grip on the baby tightening just slightly as her gaze lifts, meeting Evanora’s without the usual deflection she might have managed before.

“You wouldn’t.” Agatha mutters, though there’s less conviction in it than she wants.

Evanora’s expression remains unchanged. “I would, and I will make certain it is handled in a way that leaves no room for reversal.”

Evanora’s gaze finally drifts to the baby, and Agatha wishes more than anything that she hadn’t. There’s something about the way her eyes settle, followed by a barely concealed flicker of displeasure that lingers just long enough to be noticed.

“You will not win this by holding on.”

Agatha’s arms tremble faintly around her baby as the weight of the words settles in, not as a threat alone, but as a confirmation of power she has felt her entire life and never been able to escape.

And that is where the memory ends—not with a decision made out loud, but with the understanding that no choice at all had truly been left to her.

“I only had you in my arms for two days.” Agatha's voice doesn’t waver now, though something underneath it still fractures with each word. “Soon as we left that hospital, Evanora was right there beside me when the adoption went through. She never left.”

A faint, bitter smile tugs at her lips as she glances down, then back at Rae. “And because I did my part of the deal, I made her promise one thing—she wouldn’t interfere with your adoption process.”

Rae swallows, her fingers fidgeting with the hem of her shirt.

“Honestly, it’s a surprise she kept her word. I’m just glad you ended up with someone as caring as Rio, and well—you grew into exactly who you are now, life full of love behind and ahead of you.”

In her mind, the memories overlap. She remembers signing the papers, the ink feeling heavier than it should have been. There’s also the quiet exchange with the mother superior when Evanora wasn’t watching. 

Agatha had tried to ask for something a mother can only hope, she wants to ensure her baby would be placed somewhere safe, somewhere kind, somewhere better than the life she had been forced to navigate herself. 

It wasn’t a formal request she could control, just a desperate, whispered plea offered in the margins of a moment she could barely endure.

Leaving her baby behind is the hardest decision of her life, feeling like a piece of herself is gradually removing from her own body. But even in that loss, there had been a fragile kind of clarity: letting go was the only way to protect her baby from the cruelty of Evanora. 

She knows that if the baby had stayed with her, Evanora wouldn’t have let them go easily. She would’ve made their life suffer even worse than she did to Agatha alone. Even if they try to run or escape, Evanora will always find a way to find them.

So, it was the only path that gave her daughter a chance at something Agatha herself had never been allowed to fully have.

She draws a slow breath, grounding herself back in the present. “Anyway, I left eventually.” She leans back a little, gaze drifting as she recalls the aftermath. “One of my acquaintances took pity on me. She lent me enough money for a plane ticket and a chance to start over anywhere, really. I chose Chicago.”

Agatha still remembers the relief of finally being out of Evanora’s grasp, but that relief never came alone. Freedom had been hers, but so had the absence of the one thing she had held closest, the one thing she had chosen to let go of so it could have a better life. 

“I built something there, brick by brick. I kept things quiet, changed what I needed to change. I worked as a cashier at a cinema for a while, it pays enough for rent and cover for groceries.” She glances at Rae again, her expression softening at the edges. “Then one day, a casting call opened up. I was only meant to be an extra, but one of the casts members saw something she liked. She fought to give me a chance and more acting gigs. It was Lilia.”

Agatha shrugs lightly, playing with her empty cup. “And the rest is history.”

She’s glad Rae stays through it all, listening to everything she has to say. There’s no sharp remark or sarcasm this time. If anything, Rae even looks.. empathetic. It seems like the weight of Agatha’s decisions is only now settling in, piece by piece.

“If she was so adamant about making your life miserable, then why did your mother let you go?” Rae asks, her voice quieter now.

“Because she knew she’d already won.” Agatha answers. “There was nothing left to take from me. No punishment that could ever match what she forced me to do.”

Rae nods slowly, absorbing that. Her fingers fidget again before she speaks. “And.. did you ever..” She trails off, searching for the right words. “Did you ever think about going after me? Secretly, behind her back?”

Agatha exhales, shaking her head faintly. “She had eyes on the orphanage. I couldn’t just take you back, not without it turning into something worse.”

She looks at Rae, trying to decipher what’s going on in that brain of hers.

“But of course I thought about it, more than once.” She admits “Then about a month later, I got word you’d been adopted. That you were in good hands. That was my sign to stop looking back. That’s when I finally left for Chicago.”

Rae stays quiet for a few minutes before she finally speaks again. “This is too much for me.” She admits. “If I had known what you went through, I wouldn’t have been so mean to you. I just.. I don’t know what else to say.”

Agatha doesn’t let the silence stretch long. “Oh, it’s alright.” She comforts her. She wants to take the weight off Rae before it settles too heavily. “You don’t have to say anything, I’m not expecting you to. I know it’s a lot.”

Rae nods faintly, biting her lip before finally looking up at her. “Thank you.” She whispers. “And.. I’m sorry. Can you—uh.. can you drop me off back at my house?”

Agatha feels it—that instinct to hold onto the moment just a second longer, but she lets it go just as quickly. Rae showed up, listened, and stayed. That’s already more than she had hoped for.

“Of course.”

The drive home is calmer, a complete opposite to what transpired in the morning. Rae still chooses the backseat, and Agatha doesn’t comment on it, only stealing brief glances through the rearview mirror every now and then to make sure the kid is okay.

Rae leans her head against the window, watching the world pass by, her reflection faint against the glass while Agatha grips the steering wheel a little tighter, then relaxes her hands, reminding herself not to overthink it.

They arrive at their place sooner than she expects. Agatha had sent a quick text earlier to say they were on their way, and true enough Rio was already waiting outside for them.

“We’re here.” She announces, pulling up to the curb.

Rae blinks, like she’s being pulled out of somewhere far away. “Oh.. right.” She gathers her things slowly this time for she’s not entirely in a rush to move. Then she pauses, hand on the door, before turning back. “Agatha?”

“Hmm?”

Rae studies her for a second. For once she looks as though she’s choosing her words carefully—something she rarely does. “I think you’re really brave.”

Agatha lets out a small breath she didn’t realize she was holding, a smile breaking through before she can stop it.

“Thank you, Rae.”

The car door opens before Rae even reaches it. Of course Rio wouldn’t let Rae walk in alone after all that.

Rae barely makes it halfway out before her mami pulls her into a tight embrace without hesitation. Rae melts into it after a second, her shoulders dropping, her hands clutching at Rio’s shirt as Rio whisper words to Rae.

From her spot, Agatha quickly looks away not out of disinterest—but out of respect. That moment isn’t hers to watch, let alone intrude on. 

She leans back slightly in her seat, eyes drifting toward the windshield instead, giving them space without making it obvious she’s doing so.

They talk quietly. Agatha can’t hear the words, only sees the way Rio cups Rae’s face, checking her, making sure she’s alright. Rae nods, says something back.

After a moment, Rae glances back toward the car and Agatha pretends she wasn’t already looking.

The girl hesitates, then jogs back over, stopping just outside the driver’s window. Agatha lowers it with a small hum of the button.

“Hey,” Rae says, a little awkward now, as though she’s not used to this version of herself.

“Hey.” Agatha echoes, one brow lifting slightly. “You forgetting something? Or did you come back to critique my driving one last time?” She decides going back to their usual banter might ease the awkwardness between them.

Rae huffs out a quiet laugh, rolling her eyes. “Please, you’re only a few drives better than me.”

“Remember, I have a license and you don’t.”

That earns her a small smile. “Thanks for today. And for, you know.. everything.”

Agatha makes sure to mirror Rae’s smile. “Anytime, kid.”

Rae stays for half a second more, like she wants to say something else—but doesn’t. She just gives a one last nod before turning and heading back toward Rio.

Agatha watches her go this time.

Rio says something to Rae and presses a kiss to the top of her head right after. She can see Rae nodding again before walking the patio as Rio moves toward Agatha’s direction.

Agatha already has her windows down, so she rests her arm casually against the frame.“Everything okay?

“Everything’s.. getting there.” Rio grins.  “Thank you for letting her stay the night.”

Agatha shrugs one shoulder, trying for nonchalance. “Please. I only almost killed her once today. I’d say that’s progress.”

Rio lets out a soft laugh, shaking her head. “I believe that.”

“We also had a good talk over snow cones.” Agatha supplies. “I’d tell you about it, but I figured you’d like to spend this time with her now so maybe, next time.”

“Next time.”

There’s a brief moment where neither of them moves, until Rio moves closer. Agatha barely has time to register it before the other woman leans in, pressing a quick, warm kiss to her lips.

Agatha freezes for exactly half a second before Rio pulls back, just enough to meet her eyes, a hint of something playful evident in her expression. “Thanks for taking care of our daughter.”

And just like that, she steps away, turning back toward the house before Agatha can fully recover. “Drive safe!” She manages to call out before she complete disappears of her sight.

Agatha sits there for a moment. Engine running. Hands still. Brain and heart… not functioning properly.

Our daughter.

She exhales slowly, blinking once as she shifts into drive.

“Well..” She mutters under her breath as she pulls away from the curb.

Rio’s words echo in her mind. That’s new—and the smile tugging at her lips gives her away, because annoyingly enough, she likes the sound of it.

Our daughter.
